Q1. Chemistry does not play a major role in:
    (A) Explaining superconductivity   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Large scale production of a variety of fertilizers.
    (C) Design and synthesis new materials having specific magnetic, electric and optical properties.
    (D) Explaining ozone depletion.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Chemistry does not deal with explaining superconductivity.
*In superconducting materials the characteristics of superconductivity appear when the temperature is lowered below a critical temperature.
*The onset of superconductivity is accompanied by abrupt changes in physical properties which are more related to phase transitions of the material.
These aspects of studies in properties of materials are better related to studies in the fields of Physics, even though principles involved in Chemistry & Physics go hand to hand.

Q2. Matter can be classified at the macroscopic or bulk level as:
    (A) Solids and liquids
    (B) Elements and molecules
    (C) mixtures or pure substances   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Atoms and molecules
    Answer: C
    Explanation: At the macroscopic level, the matter is classified as a mixture or pure substances. A mixture contains two or more components (in any ratio ) present in it, for example -- sugar solutions in water, tea, air, alloys like brass, bronze, etc. Pure substances (viz. copper, silver, gold, water, glucose, etc.) have a fixed composition. The constituents of pure substances can not be separated by simple physical methods.

Q3. In a homogeneous mixture, the components are:
    (A) do not mix with each other and its composition is not uniform throughout.
    (B) do not mix with each other and its composition is uniform throughout.
    (C) completely mixed with each other and its composition is uniform throughout.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) completely mix with each other and its composition is not uniform throughout.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In a homogeneous mixture,
 the components are mixed together completely.
 has a uniform composition throughout.

Q4. Which of the following statements about pure substances is correct?
    (A) Pure substances have fixed composition.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pure substances are elements only.
    (C) Pure substances are compounds only
    (D) Pure substances do not have fixed composition.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Pure substances have a fixed composition. These may be both (i.e. either elements or compounds). The law of constant composition holds good for such substances.

Q5. Particles of compounds are:
    (A) heterogeneous mixtures
    (B) atoms
    (C) molecules of two or more atoms of different elements   <-- CORRECT
    (D) homogeneous mixtures
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Compounds are made when, atoms of two or more different elements combine together in a fixed ratio to form molecules (viz. water, ammonia, carbon dioxide, glucose, etc. ). Thus the particles of the compound consist of molecules.

Q6. Fill up the blanks with a suitable word in the statement, " Physical properties are those properties which are measured or observed ________ changing the identity or the composition of the substance ."
    (A) after
    (B) without   <-- CORRECT
    (C) by
    (D) with
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A substance is identified by its composition, hence for measuring physical properties of a substance its identity must be retained, (or should not be changed) Hence, the given statement, " Physical properties are those properties which are measured or observed without changing the identity or composition of the substance." is correct.

Q7. SI units for Base Physical Quantities of length, mass, and current are:
    (A) meter, kilogram, candela
    (B) decimetre, kilogram, ampere
    (C) meter, gram, ampere
    (D) meter, kilogram, ampere   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The International System of Units ( abbreviated as SI ) is a modern form of the metric system and is the most widely used form of measurements.
It comprises of a coherent system of measurement built of seven base units.
The base units for length, mass, and current in this system of measurements are, " meter, kilogram, ampere" symbolized respectively as m, kg, A.

Q8. SI unit of density is:
    (A) kg m^-3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) kg m^-2
    (C) kg ^-1m^3
    (D) kg m^3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Since density = mass / volume and SI unit of mass is kg and that of the volume is $m^3$.
$\therefore$ using these SI units the unit of density is derived through dimensional analysis:
density = mass / volume
= kg / m^3 
or, = kg m^-3

Q9. The Kelvin scale is related to celsius scale as:
    (A) K = °C + 212
    (B) K = °C + 273.15   <-- CORRECT
    (C) K = °C + 100
    (D) K = °C + 32
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The relation between the Kelvin scale & Celcius scale of temperatures is -
K = °C + 273.15
Such a relationship is based upon the experimental findings and subsequent conclusion of Charle's law.
The Kelvin scale is also termed as an "absolute scale of temperature."
It is interesting to note that temperature below 0^oC ( ie. negative values ) is possible in the Celcius scale but in Kelvin scale, the negative temperature is not possible.

Q10. In scientific notation for numbers, any number can be represented in the form, N $\times$ 10^n where,
    (A) n is an exponent having positive or negative values and N can vary from 10 to 100.
    (B) n is an exponent having positive or negative values and N can vary from 0 to 1.
    (C) n is an exponent having positive values only and N can vary from 1 to 10.
    (D) n is an exponent having positive or negative values. N represents a number that can vary from 1 to 10, but not 10 itself.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Scientific notation is conveniently used to represent extremely large or even very small numerical values. It is an exponential notation in which any number can be represented in the form, N $\times$ 10^n, where n is an exponent having positive or negative values and N can vary between 1 and 10, but not 10 itself.

Q11. Precision and Accuracy refer to _______ of various measurements for the same quantity repeatedly and agreement of particular value to the _________ of the result, respectively.
    (A) minimum , true value
    (B) closeness, the true value   <-- CORRECT
    (C) closeness , other values
    (D) maximum , true value
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Precision means the closeness of all the data values measured while accuracy means the closeness of a particular value with the real value.
For example,
when the reported values are 2.01, and 1.99 gas the result and its true value is 2.00 g.
These values are both precise and accurate.

Q12. Significant figures are:
    (A) digits before the decimal point
    (B) meaningful digits which are known with certainty   <-- CORRECT
    (C) digits after the decimal point
    (D) first three digits after the decimal point
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Significant digits are certain digits that have significance or meaning to certain digits in a number. Such digits help scientists to use them with more precise information about measurement and other numeric data. These digits also help them in rounding off a very large or very small number

Q13. According to Gay Lussac’s Law of Gaseous Volumes, " when gases combine or are produced in a chemical reaction they do so in a ______ ratio by volumes provided all gases are at the same temperature and pressure."
    (A) equal
    (B) uncertain
    (C) inverse
    (D) simple   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Gay lussac’s law states that when gases combine or are produced in a chemical reaction they do so in a simple ratio by volume provided all gases are at the same temperature and pressure.
Mathematically, the law is expressed as,
[V/n] = k
where V represents the volume of the gas, n denotes the number of moles of the gas & k is the proportionality constant.
Thus, the volume ratio must be related to the relative number of molecules.
This relationship was crucial in establishing the formula of simple molecules at a time when a distinction between atoms and molecules was not clearly understood.

Q14. According to Avogadro Law, equal volumes of all gases at the same temperature and pressure should contain _______ number of molecules.
    (A) unequal
    (B) equal   <-- CORRECT
    (C) similar
    (D) different
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Avogadro's law states that " equal volumes of all gases at the same temperature and pressure contain an equal number of molecules."

Q15. Molecular mass of a compound is the ________ of atomic masses of elements present in a molecule.
    (A) average
    (B) maximum
    (C) sum   <-- CORRECT
    (D) lowest
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Molecular mass is the sum of atomic masses of the elements present in a molecule.
For example ; Molecular mass of CO_2 = $\Sigma$ atomic mass of one carbon atom & atomic mass of two oxygen atoms
= [ 12 + 2(16) ]u
= 44u.

Q1. One mole is the amount of a substance that contains as many particles or entities as there are atoms in:
    (A) exactly 12 g (or 0.012 kg) of the $^{14}C$ isotope
    (B) exactly 14g (or 0.014 kg) of the $\ ^{14}C$ isotope
    (C) exactly 12 g (or 0.012 kg) of the $^{13}C$ isotope
    (D) exactly 12g (or 0.012 kg) of the $^{12}C$ isotope   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: One mole is the amount of a substance that contains as many particles or entities as there are atoms in exactly 12 g of the $^{12}C$ isotope.
A mole of a substance always contains the same number of entities, no matter what the substance may be. In order to determine this number precisely, the mass of carbon -12 atom was determined by mass spectrometer and found to be equal to 1.992648 $\times$ 10^-23g. Knowing that one mole of carbon weighs 12g. the number of atoms in it is equal to: 6.0221367 $\times$ 10^23

Q2. A given compound always contains exactly the same proportion of elements by weight. This law is stated by:
    (A) Dalton
    (B) Avagadro
    (C) Proust   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Gay Lussac
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The observation was first made by French chemist Joseph Proust, based on certain experiments conducted between 1798 and 1804. Proust made the above statement known as " Proust's law" or "Law of definite composition" or " Law of constant composition".

Q3. Avogadro's constant is the number of entities (viz. atoms, molecules or ions) present in ________ mole of a substance.
    (A) 0.50
    (B) 0.25
    (C) 1.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.01
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Avagadro's constant represents the number of entities (viz, atoms, molecules, or ions ) present in 1 mole of a substance.
The constant is denoted by N = 6.022 $\times$ 10^23

Q4. An empirical formula represents the simplest
    (A) ratio of masses of various elements present in a compound
    (B) whole number ratio of various atoms present in a compound   <-- CORRECT
    (C) average fractional ratio of various atoms present in a compound
    (D) whole number ratio of the elements present in a compound
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In chemistry, the empirical formula of a compound is the simplest positive integer ratio of atoms present in a compound.
However, this differs from the chemical formula which expresses the number of atoms in each molecule of a compound.
An empirical formula makes no mention of the arrangement of atoms in a compound.
It is standard for many ionic compounds like CaCl_2 or for macromolecules such as silicates etc.

Q5. Molecular formula represents:
    (A) average fractionall ratio of various atoms present in a compound
    (B) whole number ratio of different types of atoms present in a molecule of a compound
    (C) the exact number of different types of atoms present in a molecule of a compound   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ratio of masses of various atoms present in a compound
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Molecular formula is the exact no. of atoms present in a molecule of a compound.
Molecular formula of a compound is related with its empirical formula as,
Mollecular formula = (Empirical formula)_n
where n represents a positive integer.

Q6. According to the law of conservation of mass, a balanced chemical equation:
    (A) the same number of electrons of each element on both sides of the equation
    (B) the same ratio of atoms of each element on both sides of the equation
    (C) the same number of protons of each element on both sides of the equation
    (D) the same number of atoms of each element on both sides of the equation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: According to the law of conservation of mass,
Total mass of reactants = total mass of product
$\therefore$ The number. of atoms of each element in reactants = number of atoms of that element in products.

Q7. Molarity is defined as:
    (A) the number of moles of the solute in 1 litre of the solution   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the number of moles of the solute in 1 m^3 of the solution
    (C) the number of grams of the solute in 1 litre of the solution
    (D) the number of moles of the solvent in 1 litre of the solution
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Molarity is the most widely used method of expressing the strength or concentration of a solution.
It is denoted by ' M '.
Molarity is defined as the number of moles of solute present per litre of solution.
Mathematically,
Molarity (M) = Number of moles of solute / Volume of solution in Litres

Q8. The calculation of masses or, (sometimes volumes also) of the reactants and the products involved in a chemical reaction is called:
    (A) normality
    (B) stoichiometry   <-- CORRECT
    (C) molality
    (D) molarity
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Stoichiometry is a method to express quantitative aspects of a chemical reaction.
Usually, the masses of reactants as well as those of products in a chemical reaction are calculated using a corresponding balanced chemical equation.
It is convenient and hence desirable to calculate volumes of gaseous reactants and products.

Q9. Molecular mass of glucose (C_6H_12O_6) is
    (A) 192.162 u
    (B) 180.162 u   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 206.162 u
    (D) 198.162 u
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The molecular mass of Glucose is calculated using the relation:
Molecular mass
= $\sum$ (6*atomic mass of C, 12* atomic mass of H, 6* atomic mass of O) u
$\therefore$ substituting the respective atomic masses we get,
The molecular mass of glucose ( C_6H_12O_6)
= [6(12.0107) + 12(1.008) + 6(15.9994)]
= 180.162 u.

Q10. Choose the most appropriate answer amongst the options given below for the statement - A solution of the desired concentration is prepared by diluting _______.
    (A) solution of known higher concentration.
    (B) solution of known lower concentration.
    (C) stock solution   <-- CORRECT
    (D) from a serially diluted solution.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Stock solution can best be described as a concentrated solution of known accurate concentration that will be used for future laboratory use.
Since large amounts of solutes are used for preparing stock solution a more accurate concentration of it can be achieved quite easily, and as such the chances are slim to get erroneous results of the related experiments.
In addition, stock solutions are generally more stable as compared to a working solution since they usually do not support bacterial growth.
Multiple working solutions can be prepared by dilution of stock solution using easy calculation and process.

Q11. The number of moles of solute present in 1 kg of a solvent is called________.
    (A) Molality (m)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ppm
    (C) Normality( N )
    (D) Molarity (M)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Molality is defined as no. of moles of solute present per kg of solvent. It is denoted as " m ". Mathematically,
Molality (m) = [number of moles of the solute] / kg of solvent
Since this mode of expressing the strength of a solution involves (weight/weight) relationship of solute and solvent, the molality of the solution is not affected by variation in temperatures of the solution.

Q12. Molality (m) of 3 M aqueous solution of NaCl is: (Given: Density of solution $=1.25 {~g} {~mL}^{-1}$, Molar mass in ${g} {mol}^{-1}$ : ${Na}-23, {Cl}-35.5$)
    (A) 1.79 m
    (B) 2.79 m   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0.79 m
    (D) 2.09 m
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since Molarity represents a number of moles of solute per litre of solution.
$\therefore$ moles of solute = 3 mols.
As, density of the solution is given
= 1.25 g/ mL
$\therefore$ Mass of solution = 1250g
Mass of solvent = [1250 - 3 (58.5)] g
= (1250 - 175.5) g
= 1074 .5 g
= 1.0745 Kg
Molality
= Number of moles of solute / Kg of solvent
$\therefore$ Molality = $(\frac{3 mol}{1.0745 kg})$ = 2.79 m

Q13. Amount of sodium hydroxide present in 500ml of 0.2M solutions is :
    (A) 8gm
    (B) 40gm
    (C) 4gm   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 80gm
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Molarity of a solution
(M) = $\frac{mass of solute}{molar mass of solute } \times $$\frac{1000}{volume of solution in mL } $ 
∴0.2​$=\frac{w}{40 } \times $$\frac{1000}{500} $
so, w = 4gm.
Amount of sodium hydroxide present in 500ml of 0.2M solutions is 4 gm.

Q14. A solution is prepared by adding 2 g of a substance A to 18 g of water. Mass percent of the solute is _______.
    (A) 1 2.11%
    (B) 20.5 %
    (C) 10 %   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 11 %
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Since , mass % =[{(mass of solute) $\times$) / (mass of solution ) } $\times$100]
$\therefore$ Substituting the given values we get,
Mass per cent
= [ ( 2 g ) / { (2 g of A ) + 18 g of water } ]
= [ ( 2 /20 ) x 100 ]
= 10%

Q15. Consider the equation, Fe + H_2SO_4 $\rightarrow$ Fe_2(SO_4)_3 + H_2
This equation can be balanced by inserting the following in blank spaces.
    (A) 2,3,1,3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2,3,3,2
    (C) 2,1,3,3
    (D) 2,2,3,3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A balanced equation represents the same number of atoms of each element on both sides (i.e. LHS & RHS) of the equation. The balanced equation is complied by introducing the coefficients as (2, 3, 1, 3) respectively. Thus the balanced equation for the given reaction is
2Fe + 3H_2SO_4 $\to$ Fe_2 (SO_4)_3 + 3H_2

Q1. Consider the chemical equation, ----- KOH + ----- H_3PO_4 $\longrightarrow$ ----- K_3PO_4 + ----- H_2O.
The equation can be balanced by inserting the following in blank spaces.
    (A) 3,2,1,2
    (B) 3,1,2,3
    (C) 3,1,1,3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 6.1.2.3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The given equation gets balanced by inserting the coefficients (3,1,1,3) in blank spaces from LHS to RHS. Thus, the balanced equation for the given reaction is 3KOH + H_3PO_4 $\longrightarrow$ K_3PO_4 + 3H_2O.

Q2. Consider the chemical reaction gven as,
--CO (g) + -- $H_2$(g) → -- $C_8$H_18(l) + -- $H_2O$.
This equation can be balanced by inserting the following in blank spaces
    (A) 8,2,8,17
    (B) 8,17,1,8   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8,8,1,17
    (D) 8,2,1,17
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The balanced equation for the given equation is,
8CO(g) + 17H_2(g) $\longrightarrow$ C_8H_18(l) + 8H_2O

Q3. Consider the unbalanced chemical equation ,
-- Al + -- $O_2$ → -- $Al_2O_3$.
The equation for the above reaction can be balanced by inserting the following in blank spaces.
    (A) 2,3,3
    (B) 2,3,1
    (C) 4,3,2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4,2,3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The unbalanced chemical reaction is 
Al(s) + O_2​(g) $\longrightarrow$ Al_2​O_3​(s)
Balance Al atoms by adding 2 to Al on LHS
2Al(s) + O_2​(g) $\longrightarrow$ Al_2​O_3​(s)
Balance O atoms by adding $\frac 32$​ to O_2​ on LHS
2Al(s) + ​$\frac 32$O_2​(g)$\longrightarrow$ Al_2​O_3​(s)
Multiply the whole equation with 2.
4Al(s) + 3O_2​(g)$\longrightarrow$ 2Al_2​O_3​(s)

Q4. ^-- $Ba_3N_2$ +^- $H_2O$ → ^-- Ba $(OH)_2$ + ^-- $NH_3$ .
The above equation can be balanced by inserting the following in blank spaces from LHS to RHS respectively.
    (A) 1,6,3,6
    (B) 1,3,6,2
    (C) 1,6,3,2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2,6,1,2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The given equation gets stoichiometrically balanced when the coefficients ( 1, 6, 3, 2 ) starting from LHS to RHS are inserted in given blank spaces.
Thus, the balanced equation for the reaction is,
Ba_3N_2 + 6H_2O $\longrightarrow$ 3Ba(OH)_2 + 2NH_3

Q5. The gram molar mass of CO_2 is:
    (A) 78 g
    (B) 44 g   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 46 g
    (D) 88 g
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Molar mass of CO_2 = $\Sigma $ (atomic mass of C, 2*atomic mass of O)
= [12+2(16)] u
Since gram molar mass
= Molar mass expressed in gms.
$\therefore$ gram molar mass of CO_2
= 44 g

Q6. The molar mass of Al_2O_3 is:
    (A) 92 u
    (B) 42 u
    (C) 82 u
    (D) 102 u   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Molar mass
= $\Sigma$ [ 2 $\times$ (atomic mass of Al) 3 $\times$ (atomic mass of O)]u
= [(2 $\times$ 27) + (3 $\times$ 16)]u
= ( 54 + 48 ) u
= 102 u.

Q7. The molar mass of C_6 H_10 O_5 is
    (A) 182 u
    (B) 172 u
    (C) 282 u
    (D) 162 u   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Molar massof C_6 H_10 O_5
= Sum of the atomic masses of six C atoms , ten H atoms & six O atoms
thus , substituting the required atomic masses of
 C= 12 ,
H = 1 , &
 O = 16 ,
 we get ,
Molar mass of C_6 H_10 O_5 
 = [ 6(12)+10(1)+5(16) ] u
= (72 + 10 + 80 ) u
=162 u

Q8. Atomicity of glucose is ________.
    (A) 24   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 48
    (C) 12
    (D) 36
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Atomicity is defined as the number of atoms contained in 1 molecule of the compound. As glucose contains 6 carbon atoms, 12 hydrogen atoms, and 6 oxygen atoms, thus the atomicity is 24.

Q9. The molar mass of AgBO_3 is
    (A) 159.9 u
    (B) 165.9 u   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 179.9 g
    (D) 189.9 amu
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Molar mass of AgBO_3 = [atomic mass of Ag + atomic mass of B + 3 (atomic mass of O))] u
Substituting the atomic masses of Ag, B & O as 107.9, 10 & 16 respectively. we get -
Molar mass of AgBO_3 = [107.9 + 10 + (3 $\times $ 16)]u
= 165.9 u

Q10. How many atoms of Oxygen are there in 18g of water? (Hint: Avogadro’s Number = 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 atoms/mol)
    (A) 6.02 $\times$ 10^23   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 8.02 $\times$ 10^23
    (C) 10.02 $\times$ 10^23
    (D) 7.02 $\times$ 10^23
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The problem is based upon the concepts of Avogadro's law. Accordingly, one mole (ie 18g) of water contains
= 6.02 $\times$ $10^{23}$ molecules of water
Again, since the number of oxygen atoms in one molecule of water (H_2O)
= 1 atom 
$\therefore$ the number of oxygen atoms in 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 molecules of water
= 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 atoms

Q11. Given that Avagadro’s Number = 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 atoms/mol, the number of hydrogen atoms in 18g of water is.
    (A) 1.204 $\times$ 10^23
    (B) 1. 204 $\times$ 10^24   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3. 204 $\times$ 10^24
    (D) 2. 204 $\times$ 10^24
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since,18g H_2O
= 1mol water containing 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 molecules of water (H_2O) & the number of H atoms in 1 molecule of hydrogen (H_2) = 2
$\therefore$ the number of H atoms in 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 molecules
= (6.02 $\times$ 10^23 $\times$ 2)
=1.204 $\times$ 10^24.

Q12. There are _____m in 2000 mm?
    (A) 2 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.002 m
    (C) 0.02 m
    (D) 20 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Since 1 m = 1000 mm.
or, 1 mm = $\frac{1}{1000} m$ 
$\therefore$2000 mm = [ $\frac{1}{1000} \times 2000 $ ] m = 2m

Q13. There are ____ L in 0.05 ml?
    (A) 5.0 liters
    (B) 0.00005 L   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0.0005 liters
    (D) 0.50 L
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since , 1L = 1000mL 
or , 1mL = $\frac{1}{1000} L$ .
$\therefore$ 0.05mL = $\frac{1}{1000} \times 0.05 L$ = 0.00005 L .

Q14. The molarity of NaOH in a solution prepared by dissolving its 4.0 g in enough water to form 250 mL of the solution is,
    (A) 0.02 M
    (B) 0.002 M
    (C) 0.4 M   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.04M
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Since Molarity = $[ \frac { moles of solute * }{ volume of solution( mL ) } \times 1000 ] M $
$\therefore$ substituting the given values, we get -
Molarity (M) = $\frac{ 0.10 }{ 250 } \times 1000 M$ = 0.4M
* moles of solute ie. NaOH = $\frac{4}{40} $ mole
= 0.1mol

Q15. Choose the most appropriate option to complete the statement - " Whenever there is a rearrangement of atoms which makes or breaks chemical bonds __________."
    (A) reactants disappear
    (B) products appear,
    (C) a chemical reaction takes place   <-- CORRECT
    (D) catalysts are produced.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The occurrence of a chemical reaction is always associated with the breaking and formation of bonds of the reactant and products along with rearrangement of their atoms, hence the statement at option 1 is most appropriate i.e. " Whenever there is a rearrangement of atoms which makes or breaks chemical bonds a chemical reaction takes place."

Q1. We have to prepare a Litre solution of 0.2 M NaOH from the available 1M solution. What volume of 1M NaOH is required to be taken?
    (A) 0.2 mL
    (B) 20 mL
    (C) 200 mL   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2 mL
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Since the total strength of a given solution = total strength of the prepared solution
$\therefore$ Apply the relation -
M_1 $\times$ V_1 = M_2 $\times$ V_2
where , M1= molarity of solution given= 1.0M ,
V_1 = volume of solution given= ?
& M_2= molarity of solution to be prepared = 0.20 M (given)
V_2 = volume of solution to be prepared = 1000 mL (given)
Substiuting the given values we get ,
1.00M $\times$ V1 = 0.20 $\times$1000
V1= ( 0.20 $\times$ 1000)/1.00
V1 = 200 mL

Q2. There are ____ cms in 0.101 mm?

= 1 cm.

 ~ = 161.44 g / mol

Q11. A person is suffering with fever with a high temperature of 104 °F. What will be his body temperature in °C?
    (A) 28 .10 °C
    (B) 18.68 °C
    (C) 32.38 °C
    (D) 40 °C   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: 104°F − 32) × 5/9 = 40°C

Q12. 20 °F can also be written as
    (A) 206.5 K
    (B) 266.48 K   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 169.5 K
    (D) 300.00 K
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Step 1:
Convert the given temperature in ^oF into ^oC using expression,
F = [(°C $\times$ $\frac {9}{5}$)+ 32} 
20 = [1.98 (^oC ) + 32]
or, 1.98 (^oC ) = -12
 ^oC = $\frac{ -12 }{ 1.98 }$ = -6.66 ^oC
Step 2: Convert the temperature in ^oC into K using relation,
K = ( 273.15 + ^oC )
= [273.15 + (-6.66)]
= 266.48
Thus, 20^oF = 266.48 K

Q13. In centigrade scale, -40 °F becomes
    (A) -40 °C   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -25 °C
    (C) 24 °C
    (D) -20 °C
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Calculations:-
Since , °F
= [ (°C $\times$ 9/5 ) + 32 ] 
Substituting the given value of temperature in ^o F ,we get
-40^o F 
= (^oC$\times$1.8)
$\therefore$ ^o C
= - (72 / 1.8)
= -40^o C

Q14. -122 °C in Fahrenheit scale is
    (A) -187.6 °F   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 237.6 °F
    (C) -237.6 °F
    (D) 187.6 °F
    Answer: A
    Explanation: °F = [ (°C $\times$ 9/5 ) + 32 ]
Substituting the given temperature in ^o C we get,
$\therefore$^ oF = [( -122°C $\times$ 1.8 ) + 32]
= ( -219.6 + 32 )
-122°C = - 187.6 °F

Q15. 27 °C is equal to________K?
    (A) 246.15 K
    (B) 300.15 K   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 289 K
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since, 0^o C = 273.15 K
$\therefore $ 27^o C = (273.15 + 27) K = 300.15 K

Q1. The mass of 1 molecule of O_2 is
    (A) 4.32 $\times$ 10^-23g
    (B) 5.32 $\times$ 10^-23g   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 6.32 $\times$ 10^-23g
    (D) 7.32 $\times$ 10^-23g
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since, as per Avogadro's law,
1 mole of oxygen contains 6.023×10^23 molecules.
the mass of 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 molecules of O_2 = 32 g
$\therefore$ mass of 1 molecule of O_2 = $\frac{ 32 }{ 6.022 \times 10^{23}} g$ = 5.32 $\times$ 10^-23 g

Q2. The mass of 1 mole of O_2 is _________.
    (A) 8.0 g
    (B) 32.0 g   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 6.02 g
    (D) 16.0 g
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Calculations:
Mass of 1mole of O_2
= the mass of 6.022 $\times$ 10^23 molecules of O_2 (as per Avogadro's law)
= molar mass of O_2 in grams (i.e. gram molar mss)
= 32.0 g

Q3. For the reaction
2C_4H_10 (g)| + 130_2 (g) $\rightarrow$ 8CO_2 (g) + 10H_20(l) 300 g of C_4H_10 is burnt in 1000 g of O_2.
The yield of H_2O and the limiting reagent in the reaction are
    (A) 480 g and C_4 H_10 (g)
    (B) 432 g and O_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 455 g and C_4 H_10 (g)
    (D) 442 g and O_2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Calculations 
Moles of C_4H_10 given
= $\frac{300}{58}$
= 5.172 mol 
Moles of O_2
= $\frac{1000}{32}$ moles
= 31.25 mol.
As per stoichiometry of the reaction,
since, 2 mol of C_4H_10 requires 13 mol of O_2 
so 5.172 mol of C_4H_10 require mol of O_2
= $\frac{5.172X 13}{2} $ moles 
= 33.618 moles 
O_2 we have is only 31.25 mol which lesser amount (ie. 33.618 mol ) than what is required, and hence would be consumed first.
Thus, O_2 is is limiting reagent.
Again, 13 mol of O_2 gives 10 mol of H_2O 
$\therefore$ 31.25 mol will give$\frac{ 10 \times 31.25 }{13} $ mol of H_2 O
= 24.038 mol of water
= (24.038 $\times$ 18)g of water
$\approx$ 432 g of water.

Q4. How many molecules of H_2O are there in 18g of water? (Hint: Avagadro’s Number = 6.02 $\times$ 10^23 atoms/mol)
    (A) 6.022 $\times$ 10^23   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 6.022 $\times$ 10^24
    (C) 8.02 $\times$ 10^23
    (D) 7.02 $\times$ 10^23
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Since, the number of molecules contained in one mole of a substance
= Avogadro's number (N)
= 6.022 $\times$ 10^23 molecules, and, gram molar mass of water = 18 g 
$\therefore$ 18g H_2O = 1mole water = 6.022 $\times$ 10^23 molecules of water

Q5. For the reaction Fe_2O_3 + 3CO $\longrightarrow$ 2 Fe + 3 CO_2 the volume of carbon monoxide required to reduce one mole of ferric oxide is:
    (A) 67.2dm^3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 97.2 dm^3
    (C) 11.2 dm^3
    (D) 44.8 dm^3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Based on the given equation it is clear that 1 mole of Fe_2O_3​ i.e ferric oxide is reduced by 3 carbon monoxide.
1 mole of any compound occupies 22.4l of volume. 
So, the volume of carbon monoxide required to reduce one mole of ferric oxide is = 3 $\times$ 224.4dm^3 = 67.2dm^3.

Q6. For the reaction
Fe_2O_3 (s) + 3 CO (g) $\rightarrow$ 2 Fe (g) + 3 CO_2,
224 g of CO is available to react with 400 g Fe_2O_3, the yield of iron and CO_2, are ----------- and ------------respectively:
    (A) 210 g , 279 g
    (B) 210 g ,290 g
    (C) 225 g , 279 g
    (D) 279 g , 330 g   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Calculations :
 Convert the amounts given into number of moles , 
 Moles of CO
 = ($\frac{224}{28}$) 
 =8 moles
 Moles of Fe_2O_3
 = ( $\frac{400}{159.69}$ ) 
 = 2.50 moles.
 Stoichiometric calculations ,
 3 moles of CO is needed for 1 mole of $Fe_2O_3$
 $\therefore$ 8 moles of CO will require
 = $\frac{8X1}{3}$ = $\frac{8 \times 1}{3}$ mole
 = 2.66 mole of Fe_2O_3,
 Thus it is inferred that a lesser number of moles of Fe_2O_3 has been taken to react & hence Fe_2O_3 is limiting reagent.
 Again , 1 mole of Fe_2O_3 produces 2 mole of Fe
 $\therefore$ 2.5 mole of Fe_2O_3 will produce
 = ( 2.5 $\times$ 2 ) moles of Fe
 = 5 moles of Fe
 = ( molar mass of Fe $\times$ 5 ) g
 = $( 55.845 \times 5 ) g$
 = 279.23 g of Fe
 or $\approx$ 279 g of Fe.
 Further , 1 mole of Fe_2O_3 produces 3 mole of CO_2
 $\therefore$ 2.5 mole of Fe_2O_3 will produce
 = ( 3 $\times$ 2.5 ) moles of CO_2]
 7.5 mole of CO_2 
 $\therefore$ mass of CO_2 
 = ( 7.5 $\times$ molar mass of CO_2 ) g
 = $\ ( 7.5 \times 44 ) g$
 =330g.of CO_2

Q7. For the reaction
2N_2H_4(l) + N_2O_4(l) $\rightarrow$ 3N_2 (g) + 4H_2O (l),
Which is the limiting reagent for this reaction?
    (A) H_2O
    (B) N_2O_4   <-- CORRECT
    (C) N_2
    (D) N_2H_4
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For the given reaction,
2N_2H_4 (l) + N_2O_4 (l) $\rightarrow$ 3N_2 (g) + 4H_2O (l)
as per its stoichiometry, if only the right and exact amount of N_2O_4 is taken, the reaction may not go to completion. As such it would be consumed first & is, therefore, the limiting reagent.

Q8. For the reaction, 2 N_2H_4 (l) + N_2O_4 (l) $\to $ 3N_2(g) + 4H_2O(l), if 160 g of N_2H_4 is mixed with 160 g N_2O_4, the yield of H_2O is:
    (A) 105.0 g
    (B) 124.56 g   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 115.0 g
    (D) 120.5 g
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Calculations:
Moles of N_2H_4
=$\frac{160}{32}$ 
= 5 moles 
Moles of N_2O_4
= $\frac{160}{92}$
= 1.739 moles
As per stoichiometry of the given reaction,
2 moles of N_2H_4 require 1 mole of N_2O_4,
$\therefore$ 5 mole of N_2H_4 will need 2.5 moles of N_2O_4
. But we have only 1.73 mole of N_2O_4 so it would be consumed first.
Thus N_2O_4 is the limiting reagent for this reaction.
Again, since 1 mole of N_2O_4 yields water
= 4 mole of water
$ \therefore$ 1.73 mole of N_2O_4 will yield water
= 6.92 moles
$\equiv $ (6.92 $\times$ 18) g
= 124.56g of water

Q9. How many atoms of hydrogen are in 67.2 L of H_2 at STP?
    (A) 5.612 $\times$ 10^24
    (B) 4.612 $\times$ 10^24
    (C) 1.8066 $\times$ 10^24   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2.612 $\times$ 10^24
    Answer: C
    Explanation: One mole of any gas at STP has a volume of 22.4 L.
The number of moles = $\frac {67.2} {22.4}$ = 3 moles of H_2
One mole of any substance contains Avogadro's number of atoms = 6.022 $\times$ 10^23 atoms.
So multiply the number of moles $\times$ number of atoms/mole = 1.8066 $\times$ 10^24 atoms of H_2.

Q10. Chemistry does not play a major role in:
    (A) Large scale production of a variety of fertilizers.
    (B) Explaining superconductivity   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Explaining ozone depletion.
    (D) Design and synthesis new materials having specific magnetic, electric and optical properties.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chemistry does not deal with explaining superconductivity.
*In superconducting materials the characteristics of superconductivity appear when the temperature is lowered below a critical temperature.
*The onset of superconductivity is accompanied by abrupt changes in physical properties which are more related to phase transitions of the material.
These aspects of studies in properties of materials are better related to studies in the fields of Physics, even though principles involved in Chemistry & Physics go hand to hand.

Q11. SI unit of density is:
    (A) kg ^-1m^3
    (B) kg m^3
    (C) kg m^-3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) kg m^-2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Since density = mass / volume and SI unit of mass is kg and that of the volume is $m^3$.
$\therefore$ using these SI units the unit of density is derived through dimensional analysis:
density = mass / volume
= kg / m^3 
or, = kg m^-3

Q12. Molecular formula represents:
    (A) whole number ratio of different types of atoms present in a molecule of a compound
    (B) ratio of masses of various atoms present in a compound
    (C) average fractionall ratio of various atoms present in a compound
    (D) the exact number of different types of atoms present in a molecule of a compound   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Molecular formula is the exact no. of atoms present in a molecule of a compound.
Molecular formula of a compound is related with its empirical formula as,
Mollecular formula = (Empirical formula)_n
where n represents a positive integer.

Q14. The molar mass of AgBO_3 is

    (C) 189.9 amu
    (D) 159.9 u

Q15. One mole is the amount of a substance that contains as many particles or entities as there are atoms in:
    (A) exactly 12g (or 0.012 kg) of the $^{12}C$ isotope   <-- CORRECT
    (B) exactly 14g (or 0.014 kg) of the $\ ^{14}C$ isotope
    (C) exactly 12 g (or 0.012 kg) of the $^{13}C$ isotope
    (D) exactly 12 g (or 0.012 kg) of the $^{14}C$ isotope
    Answer: A
    Explanation: One mole is the amount of a substance that contains as many particles or entities as there are atoms in exactly 12 g of the $^{12}C$ isotope.
A mole of a substance always contains the same number of entities, no matter what the substance may be. In order to determine this number precisely, the mass of carbon -12 atom was determined by mass spectrometer and found to be equal to 1.992648 $\times$ 10^-23g. Knowing that one mole of carbon weighs 12g. the number of atoms in it is equal to: 6.0221367 $\times$ 10^23

# Structure of Atom  (5 tests)

========================================================================
STRUCTURE OF ATOM Test-01  (id 3780) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Chemistry > Structure of Atom
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. According to Dalton’s atomic theory
    (A) Atoms are made of electrons and protons
    (B) Atoms are indivisible   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Atoms are made of electrons, neutrons and protons
    (D) Atoms are made of neutrons and protons
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Dalton’s atomic theory stated that:
 All the matter is made of atoms which are tiny particles and indivisible.
 All the given atom of the element is identical in mass, size, shape, and in other properties.
 All different elements have different types of atoms and also different in their mass, size, shape, and in other properties.
 All the atom of an element cannot be made or destroyed.

Q2. Cathode rays or cathode ray particles are:
    (A) neutrons
    (B) electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (C) protons
    (D) muons
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cathode rays - In 1897, British physicist J. J. Thomson showed the rays were composed of a previously unknown negatively charged particle, which was later named the electron.

Q3. The total energy of an electron in the first excited state of the hydrogen atom is about −3.4 eV. What is the kinetic energy of the electron in this state?
    (A) -3.4 eV
    (B) +1.7 eV
    (C) +3.4 eV   <-- CORRECT
    (D) +6.8 eV
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Total energy of the electron, E = −3.4 eV
Kinetic energy of the electron is equal to the negative of the total energy.
K = −E = − (− 3.4) = +3.4 eV
Hence, the kinetic energy of the electron in the given state is +3.4 eV.

Q4. Charge on the electron was determined by
    (A) x-ray tube experiments
    (B) R.A. Millikan's oil drop experiment   <-- CORRECT
    (C) cathode ray discharge tube experiments
    (D) Electrical discharge carried out in the modified cathode ray tube
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In 1909, Robert Millikan and Harvey Fletcher conducted the oil drop experiment to determine the charge of an electron. They suspended tiny charged droplets of oil between two metal electrodes by balancing downward gravitational force with upward drag and electric forces.
The experiment helped earn Millikan a Nobel prize in 1923

Q5. In the Thomson Model of Atom:
    (A) electrons swarm like flies around nucleus
    (B) electrons oscillate about the nucleus
    (C) electrons are embedded in a positively charged pudding or water melon   <-- CORRECT
    (D) electrons move in circular orbits around nucleus
    Answer: C
    Explanation: J. J. Thomson, who discovered the electron in 1897, proposed the plum pudding model of the atom in 1904 before the discovery of the atomic nucleus in order to include the electron in the atomic model.
 In Thomson's model, the atom is composed of electrons surrounded by a soup of positive charge to balance the electrons' negative charges, like negatively charged "plums" surrounded by positively charged "pudding".
 The 1904 Thomson model was disproved by Hans Geiger's and Ernest Marsden's 1909 gold foil experiment.

Q6. Rutherford’s $\alpha$–particle scattering experiment supported the discovery of:
    (A) radioactivity
    (B) electron
    (C) nucleus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) proton
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Rutherford's model of an atom: Ernest Rutherford was interested in knowing how the electrons are arranged within an atom. Rutherford designed an experiment for this. In this experiment, fast-moving alpha ($\alpha$)-particles were made to fall on a thin gold foil.
On the basis of his experiment, Rutherford put forward the model of an atom, which had the following features:
 There is a positively charged centre in an atom called the nucleus.
 Nearly all the mass of an atom resides in the nucleus. The electrons revolve around the nucleus in well-defined orbits.
 The size of the nucleus is very small as compared to the size of the atom.

Q7. The correct expression for mass number A is:
    (A) A = number of protons (Z)+ number of neutrons (n)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) A = number of nucleons (Z) + number of neutrons (n)
    (C) A = number of protons (Z)+ number of electrons(n)
    (D) A = number of electrons (Z)+ number of positrons (n)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mass number. The mass number (symbol A), also called atomic mass number or nucleon number, is the total number of protons and neutrons (together known as nucleons) in an atomic nucleus.
mass No. = no. of protons + no. of neutrons.

Q8. Isobars are the atoms with
    (A) same atomic number but different mass number
    (B) same mass number but different atomic number   <-- CORRECT
    (C) same atomic number but different number of neutrons
    (D) same number of neutrons but different mass number
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Isobars are atoms (nuclides) of different chemical elements that have the same number of nucleons. Correspondingly, isobars differ in atomic number (or a number of protons) but have the same mass number.

Q9. Isotopes are the atoms with
    (A) same mass number but different atomic number
    (B) same atomic number but different number of electrons
    (C) same atomic number but different mass number   <-- CORRECT
    (D) same number of neutrons but different mass number
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The atoms of a chemical element can exist in different types. These are called isotopes. They have the same number of protons (and electrons), but different numbers of neutrons. Different isotopes of the same element have different masses.

Q10. Photoelectric effect established that light
    (A) behaves like waves
    (B) behaves like magnetic fields
    (C) behaves like rays
    (D) behaves like particles   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The emission of free electrons from a metal surface when light is shone on it is called the photoemission or the photoelectric effect. This effect led to the conclusion that light is made up of packets or quantum of energy. Einstein already associated the light quantum with momentum. This strongly supported the particle nature of light and these particles were named photons. Thus, the wave-particle duality of light came into the picture. Einstein won the Nobel Prize for Physics not for his work on relativity, but for explaining the photoelectric effect.

Q11. Emission spectrum of a material results from the material's (atom or molecules)
    (A) transition from normal to excited state
    (B) radiating a continuous spectrum
    (C) transition from excited to normal state   <-- CORRECT
    (D) radiating an inverted spectrum
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The emission spectrum of a chemical element or chemical compound is the spectrum of frequencies of electromagnetic radiation emitted due to an atom or molecule making a transition from a high energy state to a lower energy state. The photon energy of the emitted photon is equal to the energy difference between the two states. There are many possible electron transitions for each atom, and each transition has a specific energy difference. This collection of different transitions, leading to different radiated wavelengths, makes up an emission spectrum.

Q12. Absorption spectrum, seen as dark lines in an otherwise continuous spectrum, for the given material results from the material's (atom or molecules):
    (A) absorbing selected wavelengths from an input of continuous spectrum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) absorbing all wavelengths from an input of continuous spectrum
    (C) absorbing selected wavelengths and returning to normal ground state
    (D) absorbing all wavelengths and returning to normal ground state
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In an absorption spectrum, portions of a continuous spectrum (light containing all wavelengths) are missing because they have been absorbed by the medium through which the light has passed; the missing wavelengths appear as dark lines or gaps. Black lines indicating where no light gets through to the element.

Q13. When an electric discharge is passed through gaseous hydrogen, the H_2 molecules dissociate and the energetically excited hydrogen atoms produced emit electromagnetic radiation of discrete frequencies. The hydrogen spectrum consists of
    (A) several lines named after their discoverers
    (B) a continuous spectrum that reduces to zero at small wavelengths
    (C) a continuous spectrum that reduces to zero at large wavelengths
    (D) several series of lines named after their discoverers   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The emission spectrum of hydrogen consists of several series of sharp emission lines in the ultraviolet (Lyman series). in the visible (Balmer series), and in the infrared (Paschen series, Brackett series, etc,) regions of the spectrum. These series are named after their discoverer.

Q14. Correct expression for all series of lines in the hydrogen spectrum is (n1 = 1, 2, 3... and n2 = n1 + 1, n1 +2, ... , and is the wavenumber)
    (A) $\overline{v}=109,677\left(\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{1}^{4}}-\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{2}^{2}}\right)$
    (B) $\overline{v}=109,677\left(\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{1}^{3}}-\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{2}^{2}}\right)$
    (C) $\overline{v}=109,677\left(\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{1}^{2}}-\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{2}^{2}}\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\overline{v}=109,677\left(\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{1}^{2}}-\frac{1}{\mathrm{n}_{2}^{3}}\right)$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In an amazing demonstration of mathematical insight, in 1885 Balmer came up with a simple formula for predicting the wavelength of any of the lines in atomic Hydrogen in what we now know as the Balmer series.
Three years later, Rydberg generalized this so that it was possible to determine the wavelengths of any of the lines in the hydrogen emission spectrum. Rydberg suggested that all atomic spectra formed families with this pattern (he was unaware of Balmer's work).
It turns out that there are families of spectra following Rydberg's pattern, notably in the alkali metals, sodium, potassium, etc., but not with the precision the hydrogen atom lines fit the Balmer formula, and low values of n_2 predicted wavelengths that deviate considerably.
Rydberg's general equation is as follows:
$\overline \nu = {1\over \lambda}=R_h\left ({1\over n_1^2}-{1\over n_2^2}\right)$
where
 R_H is the Rydberg constant and is 109,737 cm^-1
 n_1 and n_2 are integers (whole numbers) with n_2>n_1

Q15. Consider the ground state of Cr atom (Z = 24). The numbers of electrons with the azimuthal quantum numbers, l = 1 and 2 are, respectively:
    (A) 12 and 4
    (B) 16 and 4
    (C) 12 and 5   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 16 and 5
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Azimuthal quantum number l = 1 is for p and l = 2 is for d.
Now Cr has configuration $1s^2, 2s^2, 2p^6, 3s^2, 3p^6, 3d^5, 4s^1 $
Hence there are 12, p-electrons and 5, d-electrons

Q1. Mg^2+ is isoelectronic with:
    (A) Na^+   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cu^2+
    (C) Zn^2+
    (D) K^+
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Isoelectronic species refers to the elements that have the same number of electrons.
Mg^2+ is 10 electron species $(1s^2, 2s^2, 2p^6)$. Its configuration is like that of Ne.
Thus it is isoelectronic with any element having 10e^- or we can say 8e^- in its valence shell.
Atomic number of Sodium (Na) is 11 after loosing one electron it became Na^+ and have 10 electrons.
Thus Mg^2+ is isoelectronic with Na^+.

Q2. According to the Heisenberg uncertainty principle, in dealing with milligram-sized or heavier objects:
    (A) the associated uncertainties are very important
    (B) the associated uncertainties are unacceptable
    (C) the associated uncertainties are hardly of any real consequence   <-- CORRECT
    (D) there are no uncertainties at all
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The effect of the Heisenberg uncertainty principle is significant only for motion of microscopic objects, it is negligible in case of macroscopic objects. For example, we apply the concept of uncertainty to an object of mass 1 milligram.
$\Delta x \times \Delta v_x = {h\over 4\pi m}$
$={ 6.626\times 10^{−34}\over 4\times 3.1416\times 10^{−6}}≈10^{−28}m^2s^{−1}$
The value of $\Delta x\Delta v_x $is very small and insignificant in this case. Therefore, when we deal with heavier objects the associated uncertainties have no real consequences and can be neglected.

Q3. Quantum mechanics is a theoretical science that deals with the study of the:
    (A) motions of the macroscopic objects that have only particle like properties
    (B) motions of the macroscopic objects that do not have both observable wave-like and particle like properties
    (C) motions of the microscopic objects that have only particle like properties
    (D) motions of the microscopic objects that have both observable wave-like and particle-like properties   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Quantum mechanics, science dealing with the behaviour of matter and light on the atomic and subatomic scale. It attempts to describe and account for the properties of molecules and atoms and their constituents—electrons, protons, neutrons, and other more esoteric particles such as quarks and gluons.

Q4. According to the quantum-theoretical model of an atom, each orbital is designated by three quantum numbers labelled as n, l, and ml. These are referred to respectively as:
    (A) Azimuthal quantum number or orbital angular momentum, Principal quantum number, and spin quantum number.
    (B) Azimuthal quantum number or orbital angular momentum, Principal quantum number, and Magnetic orbital quantum number.
    (C) Principal quantum number, Azimuthal quantum number or orbital angular momentum and spin quantum number
    (D) Principal quantum number, Azimuthal quantum number or orbital angular momentum and Magnetic orbital quantum number.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Quantum numbers designate specific shells, subshells, orbitals, and spins of electrons. This means that they describe completely the characteristics of an electron in an atom, i.e., they describe each unique solution to the Schrödinger equation, or the wave function, of electrons in an atom.
There are a total of four quantum numbers: the principal quantum number (n), the orbital angular momentum quantum number (l), the magnetic quantum number (m_l), and the electron spin quantum number (m_s). The principal quantum number, n, describes the energy of an electron and the most probable distance of the electron from the nucleus. In other words, it refers to the size of the orbital and the energy level an electron is placed in. The number of subshells, or ll, describes the shape of the orbital. It can also be used to determine the number of angular nodes.
The magnetic quantum number, m_l, describes the energy levels in a subshell, and m_s refers to the spin on the electron, which can either be up or down.

Q5. According to the quantum theoretical model of an atom, each orbital is designated by three quantum numbers labelled as n, l, and ml. The values these can take are:
    (A) n = 1,2,3..
 l= 0,1,..n-1;
 m = 0,1..l-1, l
    (B) n = 1,2,3..
 l= 0,1,..n;
 m = -l,-l+1, ..0,1..l-1, l
    (C) n = 1,2,3..
 l= 0,1,..n
 m= -l,-l+1, ..0,1
    (D) n = 1, 2, 3..
 l = 0, 1,.. n-1;
 ml = -l,-l+1, ..0,1..l-1, l   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: n (Principal quantum number) value tell about the shell to which the electro belong, Ex, If n=1 electron belongs to the first shell (K) around the nucleus
l (Azimuthal quantum number) tell about angular momentum, and shape of the orbitals, and it designates the subshells to which the electron belongs to. For a given value of 'n', 'l' can have a value ranging from 0 to n-1. Ex, If n=2 then, the value of 'l' will be 0 and 1 (0 to n-1).
m_l ( Magnetic orbital quantum number) determines the number of preferred orientations of the orbitals in the subshell, which are defined by given 'l' value.
Ex if 'l'= 2 then m_l = 2l+1 =2*2 +1= 5 m value ie., m=+2,+1,0,-2,-1.

Q6. Spin quantum number with two spin states of the electron represented by two arrows, $\uparrow $ (spin-up) and ↓ (spin down) was introduced to account for:
    (A) the splitting of emission lines in a Magnetic field   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the splitting of emission lines in an electric field
    (C) the splitting of emission lines in vacuum
    (D) to account for uncertainty in electron states
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In 1920, Otto Stern and Walter Gerlach designed an experiment, which unintentionally led to the discovery that electrons have their own individual, continuous spin even as they move along their orbital of an atom. The experiment mentioned above by Otto Stern and Walter Gerlach was done with silver which was put in an oven and vaporized. The result was that silver atoms formed a beam that passed through a magnetic field in which it split in two.

Q7. According to quantum mechanics $ψ^2$(r) the wave function squared gives:
    (A) probability density of finding a proton
    (B) probability of finding a neutron
    (C) probability of finding an electron
    (D) probability density of finding an electron   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Probability density of finding an electron at a point within an atom, it is possible to predict the region around the nucleus where the electron can most probably be found.
${{\psi }^{2}}$ has no physical significance while $ψ^2$ represents the probability density of finding an electron.

Q8. Due to the presence of electrons in the inner shells, the electron in the outer shell will not experience the full positive charge of the nucleus (Z_e). This is known as:
    (A) shielding of the outer shell electrons from the nucleus by the inner shell electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (B) charge stealing by outer shell electrons from the inner shell electrons
    (C) charge stealing by inner shell electrons from the outer shell electrons
    (D) shielding of the inner shell electrons from the nucleus by the outer shell electrons
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Shielding effect can be defined as a reduction in the effective nuclear charge on the electron cloud, due to a difference in the attraction forces of the electrons on the nucleus. It is also referred to as the screening effect (or) atomic shielding.

Q9. The Aufbau principle states that in the ground state of the atoms, the orbitals are filled in order of:
    (A) their increasing energies   <-- CORRECT
    (B) their increasing radius
    (C) their decreasing radius
    (D) their decreasing energies
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The Aufbau Principle states that in the ground state of an atom, an electron enters the orbital with the lowest energy first and subsequent electrons are fed in the order of increasing energies. The word 'aufbau' in German means 'building up'. Here, it refers to the filling up of orbitals with electrons.

Q10. According to Pauli’s exclusion principle:
    (A) All electrons in an atom can have the same spin numbers
    (B) Any two electrons in an atom can have the same set of four quantum numbers
    (C) No two electrons in an atom can have the same set of four quantum numbers   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Any two electrons in an atom can have the same spin numbers
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The Pauli Exclusion Principle states that, in an atom or molecule, no two electrons can have the same four electronic quantum numbers. As an orbital can contain a maximum of only two electrons, the two electrons must have opposing spins.

Q11. Daltons atomic theory could not explain one of the following:
    (A) Discovery of sub-atomic particles   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Law of conservation of mass
    (C) Law of constant composition
    (D) Law of multiple Proportions
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Daltons theory said atom is indivisible in nature so it doesn't explain the existence of subatomic particles.
The indivisibility of an atom was proved wrong: an atom can be further subdivided into protons, neutrons, and electrons.

Q12. Oil drop experiment is for determining the:
    (A) number of electrons
    (B) charge on the electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (C) deviation of the electron.
    (D) mass of the electron
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The oil drop experiment was performed by Robert A. Millikan and Harvey Fletcher in 1909 to measure the elementary electric charge (the charge of the electron). The experiment entailed observing tiny electrically charged droplets of oil located between two parallel metal surfaces, forming the plates of a capacitor.

Q13. How many neutrons and protons are there in the $^{13}_6C$ nucleus?
    (A) 0, 13
    (B) 8, 6
    (C) 7, 6   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 8, 5
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Number of protons = Atomic number =6
Number of neutrons = atomic mass - no of protons = 13-6 = 7

Q14. Cathode rays are discharged under one of the following conditions:
    (A) only when the rays become negatively charged
    (B) at very low pressure and high voltage   <-- CORRECT
    (C) when a certain type of gas is used
    (D) when a certain type of electrode is used
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Production of cathode rays: Cathode rays are produced in the discharge tube (by low pressure and high temperature) by applying the following conditions:
 A high potential difference (>1200 V) is applied across the two aluminium electrodes.
 The length of the tube is 30 cm and the diameter is 3 cm.
 The pressure inside the tube is maintained below 0.01 mm of Hg.

Q15. One of the following scientists was the first to discover electron
    (A) Ernest Rutherford
    (B) James Chadwick
    (C) J.J. Thomson   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Robert Hooke
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Electron was discovered by J. J. Thomson in 1897 when he was studying the properties of the cathode ray. J. J. Thomson won Nobel Prize in 1906 for discovering the elementary particle electron.

Q1. Experiments on electrical discharge through gases ultimately lead to the discovery of ________.
    (A) nucleus
    (B) neutrons
    (C) protons
    (D) electrons   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Towards the end of the 19th century, Joseph J.Thomson (1856-1940) was studying electric discharges. It was known that the discharge and the glow in the gas were due to something coming from the cathode, the negative pole of the applied high voltage. Thomson made a series of experiments to study the properties of the rays coming from the cathode. He observed that the cathode rays were deflected by both electric and magnetic fields - they were obviously electrically charged.
Thomson's result was $\frac{e}{m}=1.8\times {{10}^{-11}}$ coulombs kg
The particle that J.J.Thomson discovered in 1897, the electron, is a constituent of all the matter we are surrounded by. All atoms are made of a nucleus and electrons. He received the Nobel Prize in 1906 for the discovery of the electron, the first elementary particle.

Q2. Television pictures result due to
    (A) fluorescence of protons on the television screen
    (B) fluorescence of canal rays on the television screen
    (C) phosphorescence of protons on the television screen
    (D) fluorescence of cathode rays on the television screen   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Cathode rays (also called an electron beam or e-beam) are streams of electrons observed in vacuum tubes. If an evacuated glass tube is equipped with two electrodes and a voltage is applied, the glass behind of the positive electrode is observed to glow, due to electrons emitted from and traveling away from the cathode (the electrode connected to the negative terminal of the voltage supply).
Cathode ray tubes (CRTs) use a focused beam of electrons deflected by electric or magnetic fields to create the image in a television set.

Q3. The mass of an electron is
    (A) 1.758820 $\times$ 10^11 kg
    (B) 9.1094 $\times$ 10^-31 kg   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1.672614 $\times$ 10^-27 kg
    (D) 1.67492 $\times$ 10^-27kg
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The electron is a subatomic particle, symbol e^− or $\beta^-$ , with a negative elementary electric charge.
The electron has a mass that is approximately $1\over 1836$ that of the proton.
So mass of electron = ${1\over 1836}\times 1.6726219 × 10^{-27}$ = 9.1094 $\times$ 10^-31 kg

Q4. The formula E= h$\nu $is used to calculate:
    (A) energy of quantum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Energy of the ejected electrons
    (C) wave number
    (D) radiation emitted by a black body
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Max Planck theorized that energy was transferred in chunks known as quanta, equal to $h\nu$. The variable h is a constant equal to 6.63 $\times$ 10^-34 J·s and the variable $\nu $represents the frequency in 1/s.
This equation allows us to calculate the energy of photons, given their frequency.
If the wavelength is given, the energy can be determined by first using the wave equation$ (c = \lambda \times \nu) $to find the frequency, then using Planck’s equation to calculate energy.

Q5. Wavenumber of yellow radiations having a wavelength of 5800 $\overset{\circ }{\mathop{A}}\,$ is:
    (A) 1.72 $\times$ 10^2 m^-1
    (B) 1.72 $\times$ 10^3 m^-1
    (C) 1.72 $\times$ 10^6 m^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1.72 $\times$ 10^5 m^-1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Wavenumber is defined as the reciprocal of a wavelength.
$\bar \nu ={1\over \lambda}$
where, $\lambda $ = wavelength = 5800 Å = 5.8 $\times$ 10^-7 m
So, $\bar \nu ={1\over 5.8\times 10^{-7}}= $ 1.72 $\times$ 10^6 m^-1.

Q6. What will be the Electronic configuration of the element having atomic number 24?
    (A) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^3 3s^2 3p^6 3d^5 4s^1 4p^3
    (B) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^6 3d^4 4s^1 4p^1
    (C) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^3 3d^5 4s^1 4p^3
    (D) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^6 3d^5 4s^1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The atomic number 24 is of Cr. Due to half-filled orbital stability, it does not follow the Aufbau rule so its electronic configuration is 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^6 3d^5 4s^1.

Q7. The electronic configuration $1{s^2}2{s^2}2{p^1}$ belongs to
    (A) Boron   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Carbon
    (C) Beryllium
    (D) Lithium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Boron is a chemical element with symbol B and atomic number 5. So electronic configuration of boron is $1s^2 2s^22p^1$

Q8. Around 10^15 Hz corresponds to the region of the electromagnetic spectrum
    (A) visible light
    (B) microwave region
    (C) ultraviolet region   <-- CORRECT
    (D) infrared region
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A frequency of $10^{15} {~Hz}$ primarily corresponds to the ultraviolet (UV) region of the electromagnetic spectrum. The UV region spans frequencies between $10^{14} {~Hz}$ and $10^{17} {~Hz}$. While visible light falls within $4 \times 10^{14} {~Hz}$ to $7.5 \times$ $10^{14} {~Hz}$, a frequency around $10^{15} {~Hz}$ is near the upper limit of visible light and is generally considered to be part of the UV spectrum. Thus, $10^{15} {~Hz}$ most accurately belongs to the ultraviolet region.

Q9. Radio frequency region of the electromagnetic spectrum is used for broadcasting. It is
    (A) Around $10^6$ Hz   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Around $10^{13}$ Hz
    (C) Around ${{10}^{15}}$ Hz
    (D) Around $10^{10}$ Hz
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Radiofrequency (RF) is any of the electromagnetic wave frequencies that lie in the range extending from around 3 kHz to 300 GHz, which include those frequencies used in radio communication or radar. RF usually refers to electrical rather than mechanical oscillations.

Q10. One of the orbitals is non-directional
    (A) f- orbital
    (B) s- orbital   <-- CORRECT
    (C) p- orbital
    (D) d- orbital
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Orbitals with subshell quantum number l = 0 are called s orbitals. All s orbitals are spherical in shape and have spherical symmetry. This means that the wave function will depend only on the distance from the nucleus and not on the direction.

Q11. Find the energy of the photons which correspond to light of frequency 3 $\times$ 10^15 Hz (Hint: h = Planck’s constant = 6.626 $\times$ 10^-34 Js)?
    (A) 1.308 $\times$ 10^-18 J
    (B) 0.988 $\times$ 10^-18 J
    (C) 2.988 $\times$ 10^-18 J
    (D) 1.988 $\times$ 10^-18 J   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: We know Planck's equation is
E = hv
where E is energy, h is Planck’s constant and v is frequency.
E = 6.626 $\times$ 10^-34 $\times$ 3 $\times$ 10^15 = 1.988 $\times$ 10^-18 J

Q12. Find the energy of the photon which has a wavelength of 0.50 $\mathop A\limits^ \circ $?
(Hint: h = Planck’s constant = 6.626 $\times$ 10^-34 J)
    (A) 0.98 $\times$ 10^-15 J
    (B) 1.98 $\times$ 10^-15 J
    (C) 2.98 $\times$ 10^-15 J
    (D) 3.98 $\times$ 10^-15 J   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Energy (E) of a photon having wavelength ($\lambda$) is given by the expression, $E={hc\over \lambda}$
where, h = Planck’s constant = 6.626 $\times$ 10^-34
c = velocity of light in vacuum = 3 $\times$10^8 m/s 
Wavelength $\lambda = 0.50 A^° = 0.50\times 10^{-10} m$ $\lambda$ = 0.50 Å = 0.50$\times$ 10^-10 m
Substituting the values in the given expression of E:
$6.626\times 10^{-34}\times 3\times 10^8\over 0.50\times 10^{-10}$ = 3.98 $\times$ 10^-15 J

Q13. Energy of an electron in stationary state is given by the formula
${E_{{n^m}}}{R_H}\left( {1 - \frac{1}{{{{\text{n}}^2}}}} \right)$
where n = 1,2,3........ In this equation, R_H is called
    (A) Rydberg’s constant   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Proportionality constant
    (C) Planck’s constant
    (D) Avagadro’s Number
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The Rydberg constant, symbol $R_\infty$ for heavy atoms or R_H for hydrogen, named after the Swedish physicist Johannes Rydberg, is a physical constant relating to atomic spectra, in the science of spectroscopy.

Q14. Lines in the hydrogen spectrum which appear in the ultraviolet region of the electromagnetic spectrum, then they are called as:
    (A) Lyman series   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Pfund series
    (C) Balmer series
    (D) Bracket series
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The Lyman series is a hydrogen spectral series of transitions and resulting ultraviolet emission lines of the hydrogen atom as an electron goes from n $\ge $ 2 to n = 1 (where n is the principal quantum number), the lowest energy level of the electron.

Q15. Lines in the hydrogen spectrum which appear in the infrared region of the electromagnetic Spectrum, then they are called as
    (A) Paschen series   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Hydrogen series
    (C) Balmer series
    (D) Hydrogen line series
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The Lyman series lies in the ultraviolet, whereas the Paschen, Brackett, and Pfund series lies in the infrared.

Q1. Lines in the hydrogen spectrum which appear in the visible region of the electromagnetic Spectrum, then they are called as:
    (A) Bracket series
    (B) Balmer series   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Lyman series
    (D) Paschen series
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The Balmer series or Balmer lines in atomic physics is the designation of one of a set of six named series describing the spectral line emissions of the hydrogen atom. The Balmer series is calculated using the Balmer formula, an empirical equation discovered by Johann Balmer in 1885 Balmar series lies in the visible region of the Electromagnetic spectrum.

Q2. The commonly occurring isotopes of carbon atoms are: _6^12C, _6^13C, _6^14C . They contain:
    (A) 6, 7 and 9 neutrons and 6 protons
    (B) 6, 8 and 9 neutrons and 6 protons
    (C) 6, 7 and 8 neutrons and 6 protons   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 7, 8 and 9 neutrons 6 protons
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Isotopes are atoms with the same number of protons but that have a different number of neutrons.
Atomic number of carbon = 6
So number of protons in each isotope = 6
Number of neutrons in $^{12}_6C$ = 12 - 6 = 6
Number of neutrons in $^{13}_6C$ = 13 - 6 = 7
Number of neutrons in $^{14}_6C$ = 14 - 6 = 8

Q3. How many protons, neutrons and electrons are in $^{56}F{e^{3 + }}$?
    (A) 26 protons, 30 neutrons, 26 electrons
    (B) 26 protons, 30 neutrons, 23 electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 23 protons, 33 neutrons, 20 electrons
    (D) 23 protons, 33 neutrons, 26 electrons
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Atomic number of iron (Fe) = 26
So, number of protons = 26
Number of protons = number of electrons
But To gain 3+ charge it should loose 3 electron. So number of electrons present = 26-3 = 23
Now atomic mass = 56 (Given).
Number of neutrons = atomic mass - number of protons = 56 - 26 = 30

Q4. Give the number of electrons in the species, $O_2$ and $O_2^+$.
    (A) 16 and 8
    (B) 16 and 14
    (C) 16 and 15   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 32 and 16
    Answer: C
    Explanation: atomic number O has atomic number = 8 so number of electrons in $O_2$ = 16
while in $O_2^+$ there is one unit positive charge so no. of electron =15.

Q5. An atom of an element contains 29 electrons and 35 neutrons. The number of protons are:
    (A) 30
    (B) 35
    (C) 32
    (D) 29   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In an atom no. of protons = no. of electrons i.e. P = E while this is not true in case of ions.
So the number of protons in the given atom is 29.

Q6. Values of e/m (charge/mass) in the categories alpha particle ($\alpha$), electron (e) and protons (p) increase in the order:
    (A) p < e < $\alpha$
    (B) e < $\alpha$ < p
    (C) $\alpha$ < e < p
    (D) $\alpha $ < p < e   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\alpha $-particle (He^2+) has a very high mass compared to proton and electron, therefore very small $e\over m$ ratio. Proton and electron have the same charge (magnitude) but former is heavier, hence has a smaller value of $e\over m $.

    (D) ${}_{17}^{35}Al$

    Explanation: Chlorine has atomic number 17 and atomic mass 35.5u.

Q8. An atom of an element contains 29 electrons and 35 neutrons. The electronic configuration of an element
    (A) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p 4s^2 3d^6 4s^2 4p^2
    (B) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^6 4s^1 3d^10   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p 4s^2 3d^8 4s^2
    (D) 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^5 4s^1 3d^9 4s^2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Number of electron (29) = Number of protons (29) 
So electronic configuration = 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^6 4s^1 3d^10

Q9. In an atom, an electron is moving with a speed of 600m/s with an accuracy of 0.005%. Certainty with which the position of the electron can be located is (h = 6.6 $\times$10^-34 Js)?
    (A) 5.10 $\times$10^-3m
    (B) 1.92 $\times$10^-3m   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3.84 $\times$ 10^-3m
    (D) 1.52 $\times$ 10^-4m
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Velocity = 600m/s
Accuracy = 0.005%
so,uncertainty in the velocity = ${600 \times 5 \over 1000 }={3000\over 1000 }$= 3 m/s
$∆x $ = ?
Using the Heisenberg uncertainty equation, we have
$Δx \times Δp ={ h\over h\pi }$
$\Rightarrow \Delta x = {h\over 4\pi m \Delta v}$= $6.634 \times 10^{-34}\over 4 \times 3.14 \times 9.1 \times 10^{-31 }\times 3 $ = 1.92 $\times$10^-3m

Q10. Maximum number of electrons in a subshell with l = 3 and n = 4 is _____.
    (A) 12
    (B) 16
    (C) 14   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 32
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Here l = 3 means the subshell is f. 
n = 4 means it is present in the 4th orbit. Finally, it is a 4f subshell.
The number of orbital in f sub shell = 2l + 1 = 2 $\times$ 3 + 1 = 7
Each orbital can accommodate 2 electrons = 7 $\times$ 2 = 14 electrons.
Therefore, the maximum number of electrons in a subshell with l = 3 and n = 4 (4f) is 14 electrons.

Q11. Calculate the energy required for the process He^+(g) $\to$ He^2+(g) + e^- (Hint: The ionization energy of the lowest state, also called as the ground state is 2.18 $\times$ 10^-18 J atom^-1).
    (A) 3.72 $\times$ 10^- 18J atom^-1
    (B) 7.72 $\times$ 10^- 18J atom^-1
    (C) 8.72 $\times$ 10^- 18J atom^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 5.72 $\times$ 10^- 18J atom^-1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: He^+ ion is a single electron species which resembles like hydrogen. Therefore, the energies of the stationary states of hydrogen-like ions are given by the expression
$E_n ={ 2.18 \times 10^{-18} }\times { Z^2 \over n^2 }$
Here n = 1 and Z = 2
$E_n = {2.18 \times 10^{-18}}\times {2^2\over 1^2}$ = 8.72 $\times$ 10^- 18J atom^-1

Q12. The electrons are ejected from the metal surface when the light of certain frequencies strikes the surface is called ________.
    (A) Photoelectric effect   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Thomson model for electron
    (C) Faraday’s cathode ray discharge model
    (D) Planck's quantum theory
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Electrons are ejected from the metal when the light of a certain frequency strikes the surface of a metal, This phenomenon is known as the photoelectric effect and the ejected electrons are called photoelectrons.

Q13. Which transition in the hydrogen spectrum would have the same wavelength as the Balmer type transition from n = 4 to n = 2 of He^+ spectrum
    (A) n = 1 to n = 3
    (B) n = 1 to n = 2
    (C) n = 3 to n = 4
    (D) n = 2 to n = 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: For He^+ ion,
We have
${1\over λ }= Z^2R­_h{[{1\over n_1^2 }-{1\over n_2^2}] } $$= 2^2R_h{ [{1\over 2^2} – {1\over 4^2}]}$$=\frac{3}{4}{{R}_{h}}$ ….(i)
Now for the hydrogen atom
${1\over λ }= R_h{ [{1\over n_1^2 }-{1\over n_2^2}] }$….(ii)
Equating equation (i) and (ii), we get
${1\over n_1^2} -{1\over n_2^2 }= {3\over 4}$
Obviously, n_1 = 1 and n_2 = 2
Hence, the transition n = 2 to n = 1 in hydrogen atom will have the same wavelength as the transition, n = 4 to n = 2 in He^+ species.

Q14. 2 $\times$ 10^8 atoms of carbon are arranged side by side. Find the radius of carbon atom if the length of this arrangement is 2.4 cm.
    (A) 6.0 $\times$ 10^-11 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 5.7 $\times$ $10^{-11}$ m
    (C) 1.2 $\times$ 10^-11 m
    (D) 3.0 $\times$ 10^-11 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Total Length = 2.4 cm
Total number of atoms along the length = 2 $\times$ 10^8
Therefore diameter of each atom = $2.4 \over 2 × 10^8$ = 1.2 $\times$ 10^-8 cm
And radius of the atom = $ 1.2 \times 10^{-8}\over 2$ = 0.60 $\times$ 10^-8 cm 
= 6.0 $\times$ 10^-11m

Q15. Which of the following orbitals are not possible?
    (A) 3s
    (B) 3f   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 4d
    (D) 3p
    Answer: B
    Explanation: if n=3 then l = 0,1,2 i.e. only 3s,3p,3d orbitals are possible.
