Q1. When an electron from an excited hydrogen atom undergoes the transition from energy level n = 4 to n = 2, the emission of radiations will give rise to:
    (A) Brackett series
    (B) Paschen series
    (C) Lyman series
    (D) Balmer series   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The spectral lines which arise due to the transition of electrons from higher energy levels to the second energy level will appear in the visible region. Balmer series lies in the visible region of the EM spectrum.

Q2. Bohr’s model of the atom could explain quantitatively the general features of the structure of:
    (A) Hydrogen atom   <-- CORRECT
    (B) oxygen atom
    (C) nitrogen atom
    (D) carbon atom
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Neils Bohr proposed a model of hydrogen atom based on the quantum theory and explained the atomic spectrum of hydrogen.

Q3. The product of the uncertainties of the exact position and exact momentum (or velocity) of an electron. The product of their uncertainties is always
    (A) equal to or greater than h/3$\pi$
    (B) equal to or greater than h/2$\pi$
    (C) equal to or greater than h/$\pi$
    (D) equal to or greater than h/4$\pi$.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The uncertainty principle says that we cannot measure the position (x) and the momentum (p) of a particle with absolute precision. The more accurately we know one of these values, the less accurately we know the other. Multiplying together the errors in the measurements of these values has to give a number greater than or equal to half of a constant called "h-bar". This is equal to Planck's constant (usually written as h) divided by 2$\pi$.
$Δx. Δp \ge { h\over 4\pi}$

Q4. According to Heisenberg's Uncertainty Principle, the product of the uncertainties in the position and momentum of an electron is always:
    (A) greater than or equal to h/4$\pi$.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) greater than or equal to h/3$\pi$
    (C) greater than or equal to h/ 6$\pi$
    (D) greater than or equal to h/2$\pi$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The uncertainty principle says that we cannot measure the position (x) and the momentum (p) of a particle with absolute precision. The more accurately we know one of these values, the less accurately we know the other. Multiplying together the errors in the measurements of these values (the errors are represented by the triangle symbol in front of each property, the Greek letter "delta") has to give a number greater than or equal to half of a constant called "h-bar". This is equal to Planck's constant (usually written as h) divided by 2$\pi$.
$Δx. Δp \ge { h\over 4\pi}$

Q5. The orbital with quantum numbers n = 4, l = 3 is
    (A) 3d
    (B) 4p
    (C) 4f   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4d
    Answer: C
    Explanation: For n = 4 the possible values of l are 0,1, 2, 3. The orbital with l = 3 is f orbital.

Q6. An element with mass number 81 contains 31.7 % more neutrons as compared to protons. Assign the atomic symbol.
    (A) ${}_{35}^{81}{\text{S}}$
    (B) ${}_{35}^{81}{\text{Br}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${}_{35}^{81}{\text{Cl}}$
    (D) ${}_{35}^{81}{\text{Ag}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: P + N = 81
N = P + (0.317)P
Solving these two equations we get P = 35
The atomic number of Bromine is 35.
So the symbol is ${}_{35}^{81}{\text{Br}}$

Q7. The energy associated with the first orbit in the hydrogen atom is -2.18 $\times$ 10^-18 J/atom. What is the energy associated with the fifth orbit?
    (A) -7.72 × 10^-20 J/atom
    (B) -8.68 $\times$ 10^-20 J/atom   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -3.72 $\times$ 10^-20 J/atom
    (D) -5.72 $\times$ 10^-20 J/atom
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The energy of first (Bohr) orbit in hydrogen atom = -2.17 $\times$ 10^-18Jatom^-1
The energy of the fifth orbit will be given by $E_n= E_1\times {Z^2\over N^2}$
 $E_5={-2.17\times 10^{-18}\over 5^2}=-8.68\times 10^{-20}Jatom^{-1}$.
The energy of the fifth orbital = $=-8.68\times 10^{-20}Jatom^{-1}$

Q8. Arrange the electrons present in the 4s, 3d, 4p, and 3p orbitals in the order of their increasing energies.
    (A) (3d) < (3p) < (4p) < (4s)
    (B) (4s) < (4p) < (3p) < (3d)
    (C) (3p) < (4s) < (3d) < (4p).   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (4p) < (4s) < (3p) < (3d)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Energy of the orbital is determined by the n+l value. The orbital having a higher n+l value will have higher energy. If n+l value is the same then orbital having a higher n value will have higher energy.

Q9. Give the name and an atomic number of the inert gas atom in which the total number of d-electrons is equal to the difference between the numbers of total p and total s electrons.
    (A) As (atomic no.=36)
    (B) Cl (atomic no.=36)
    (C) Kr (atomic no.=36)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Br (atomic no.= 36)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Kr has atomic no. 36. And in Kr total number of d-electrons is equal to the difference between the numbers of total p and total s electrons.
1s^2,2s^2,2p^6,3s^2,3p^6,3d^10,4s^2,4p^6
Total s-electrons =8
Total p-electrons =18
Difference =18−8=10 
Total d-electrons =10

Q10. If a cation B^3+ has 18 electrons, the atomic number of element B will be
    (A) 15
    (B) 12
    (C) 24
    (D) 21   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In the formation of a cation with 3^+ charges, the atom loses 3 electrons. 
The no. of electrons in the atom will be 18 + 3 = 21.
In a neutral atom, the no. of protons is equal to the no. of electrons. So atomic no. is 21.

Q11. Among the following pairs of orbitals 2s and 3s, 4d and 4f, 3d and 3p, the orbitals that will experience the larger effective nuclear charge will be:
    (A) 3s, 4f and 3d respectively
    (B) 2s, 4f and 3d respectively
    (C) 2s, 4d and 3p respectively   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2s, 4d and 3d respectively
    Answer: C
    Explanation: An electron is shielded from the attractive interactions of the nucleus by the electrons in the inner shells.The repulsive and attractive interactions of an electron depend on the shell and the orbital in which the electron is present.

Q12. The wavelength of a ball of mass 0.1 kg moving with a velocity of 10 ms^-1 will be:
    (A) 6.626 $\times$ 10^-35 m
    (B) 6.626 $\times$ 10^34 m
    (C) 6.626 $\times$ 10^-34 m   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 7.626 $\times$ 10^-34 m
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given : mass = 0.1 kg; veloctiy = 10 m/s.
We know, 
$λ={h\over mv}$ where h is Planck's constant.
$\lambda = {6.626 \times 10^{-34}\over 10\times 0.1}=6.626 \times 10^{-34}$m

Q13. Which of the following sets of quantum numbers represent the highest energy of an electron?
    (A) n = 3, l = 2, m = 1, s = +1/ 2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) n = 3, l = 1, m = 1, s = +1/ 2
    (C) n = 3, l = 0, m = 0, s = +1/ 2
    (D) n = 4, l = 0, m = 0, s = +1/ 2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In a multi electron atom the energy of an electron is determined by its n+l value, higher the value, higher is the energy.

Q14. The wave character of electrons is used in the construction of
    (A) electron microscope   <-- CORRECT
    (B) compound microscope
    (C) fluorescence microscope
    (D) light microscope
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The electron microscope uses a beam of accelerated electrons as a source of illumination. The wavelength of an electron being much shorter than the visible light the electron microscope has a higher resolving power.

Q15. Lines in the hydrogen spectrum which appear in the ultraviolet region of the electromagnetic spectrum, then they are called as:
    (A) Pfund series
    (B) Balmer series
    (C) Lyman series   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bracket series
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The Lyman series is a hydrogen spectral series of transitions and resulting ultraviolet emission lines of the hydrogen atom as an electron goes from n $\ge $ 2 to n = 1 (where n is the principal quantum number), the lowest energy level of the electron.

Q1. Consider the isoelectronic species, Na^+, Mg^2+, F^-, and O^2-. The correct order of increasing length their radii is ________.
    (A) $\mathrm { O } ^ { 2 - } < \mathrm { F } ^ { - } < \mathrm { Mg } ^ { 2 + } < \mathrm { Na } ^ { + }$
    (B) $\mathrm { F } ^ { - } < \mathrm { O } ^ { 2 - } < \mathrm { Mg } ^ { 2 + } < \mathrm { Na } ^ { + }$
    (C) $\mathrm { O } ^ { 2 - } < \mathrm { F } ^ { - } < \mathrm { Na } ^ { + } < \mathrm { Mg } ^ { 2 + }$
    (D) $\mathrm { Mg } ^ { 2 + } < \mathrm { Na } ^ { + } < \mathrm { F } ^ { - } < \mathrm { O } ^ { 2 - }$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\mathrm { Mg } ^ { 2 + } < \mathrm { Na } ^ { + } < \mathrm { F } ^ { - } < \mathrm { O } ^ { 2 - }$
For isoelectronic species, ionic radii decrease with an increase in nuclear charge.

Q2. Mendeleev 'Periodic Law' states that:
    (A) The properties of the elements are a periodic function of the number of neutrons.
    (B) The properties of the elements are the periodic function of their atomic weights.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) The properties of the elements are a periodic function of their atomic number.
    (D) The properties of the elements are a periodic function of the number of electrons.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If the elements are arranged in the order of their increasing atomic weights, after a regular interval similar properties of elements are repeated.

Q3. Mendeleev arranged elements in a periodic table in order of their increasing atomic weights in such a way that the elements with similar properties occupies:
    (A) The same Horizontal row or series.
    (B) The positions on the top left to bottom right diagonal.
    (C) The positions on the bottom left to top right diagonal.
    (D) The same vertical column or group.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mendeleev arranged elements in horizontal rows and vertical columns of a table in order of their increasing atomic weights in such a way that the elements with similar properties occupied the same vertical column or group. This is because the properties of elements are repeating after a regular interval.

Q4. Correct option to complete the following statement is:
Mendeleev's classification of the element is based upon similarities in properties of different elements with increasing order of their atomic weights.
In cases where dissimilarities in properties of an element appeared he placed the elements with similar ______ together.
    (A) molecular weights
    (B) atomic weight
    (C) atomic number
    (D) properties   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mendeleev believed that the properties of elements are the function of their atomic weights. He arranged elements in increasing order of their atomic weight but gave priority to the properties overweight. Wherever a dissimilarity in properties of an element occurred during arranging them in ascending order of their atomic weights, he ignored the atomic weight of the element but kept the elements with similar properties together.
Thus, he laid more stress over the similarities in the properties of different elements rather than their atomic weights.

Q5. Mendeleev proposed that some of the elements were still undiscovered and, therefore, left several gaps in the table. He left the gap under aluminium and a gap under silicon and called these elements Eka-Aluminium and Eka-Silicon. These were later discovered and named.
    (A) Gallium and Godolinium respectively
    (B) Barium and Germanium respectively
    (C) Gallium and Germanium respectively   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Mendelivium and Germanium respectively
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mendeleev arranged the elements according to their atomic weights. He corrected the atomic weights of a few existing elements to explain their chemical and physical behaviour. Moreover, he felt that few elements are still to be discovered, so he left empty spaces for them in his periodic table. Two such elements whose properties he predicted; and were later discovered are Gallium and Germanium respectively.

Q6. Complete the statement with suitable word /(s)
Modern Periodic Law is stated as:
The physical and chemical properties of different elements are periodic functions of their ______.
    (A) Molecular mass
    (B) Isotopic masses
    (C) Atomic masses.
    (D) Atomic numbers   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The Modern periodic law is stated as:
The physical and chemical properties of elements are periodic functions of their atomic numbers. That is the properties of elements will be repeated after regular intervals.

Q7. It is now recognized that the ‘Modern Periodic Law’ is essentially the consequence of:
    (A) periodic variation in chemical bonds.
    (B) periodic variation in electronic configurations.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) periodic variation in chemical properties.
    (D) periodic variations in the element lattice.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Modern Periodic Law of the element may be defined as the Physical and chemical properties of the elements are periodic functions of their atomic numbers. It means, when the elements are arranged in the order of their increasing atomic numbers, it is observed that the elements of similar properties recur at regular intervals or periodically. As a result of this, the elements fall in certain groups and lead to an arrangement called the modern periodic table of elements. It must be noted that elements are arranged in the periodic table in order of atomic numbers because the atomic number is the most fundamental property of an element. The systematic arrangement of elements in the modern periodic table according to their atomic number helps in justification of isotopes of elements in one place.

Q8. In the modern periodic table:
    (A) The horizontal rows are called series and the vertical columns, groups.
    (B) The horizontal rows are called groups and the vertical columns, periods.
    (C) The horizontal rows are called periods and the vertical columns, groups.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The horizontal rows are called periods and the vertical columns, series.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the modern periodic table, the elements are arranged in the increasing order of their atomic number. It contains 7 horizontal rows called periods and 18 vertical columns called groups.

Q9. According to the recommendation of the International Union of Pure and Applied Chemistry (IUPAC), the groups in the modern periodic table are numbered from:
    (A) 1 to 10
    (B) 1 to 18   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1 to 8
    (D) 1 to 12
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The groups are numbered from 1 to 18; where group 1 is alkali metal group and group 18 is for the noble gases.

Q10. Choose one of the following in the order of increasing radii:
    (A) I^+ < I^- < I
    (B) I < I^+ < I^-
    (C) I^- < I^+ < I
    (D) I^- > I > I^+   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The size of the anion is greater than the size of the parent atom and the size of the cation. As the –ve charge of anion increases ionic radii increases due to a decrease in the effective nuclear charge and vice versa.

Q11. According to IUPAC nomenclature for elements with Z greater than 100, the root 'sept' corresponds to the digit:
    (A) 4
    (B) 7   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8
    (D) 3
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Sept is for 7.

Q12. Atomic number of element Unnilhexium is:
    (A) 107
    (B) 105
    (C) 110
    (D) 106   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: un = 1 Nil = 0 Hex = 6. So, 106 = uninilhexium.

Q13. According to IUPAC nomenclature,element Ununnillium have an atomic number of:
    (A) 111
    (B) 108
    (C) 109
    (D) 110   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: un = 1 nil = 0 So 110 = ununnilium.

Q14. Electronic configuration of an element is:
    (A) The distribution of electrons into magnetic states of an atom.
    (B) The distribution of electrons into different atomic orbitals.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) The distribution of electrons into a spin state of an atom.
    (D) The distribution of electrons into azimuthal orbitals of an atom only.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The electronic configuration of an atom describes the arrangement of electrons in space around the nucleus. The electrons are distributed over different energy levels. These energy levels are called the shell or orbits.

Q15. The third period (n = 3) begins at sodium with the addition of the first electron to:
    (A) 3p orbital
    (B) 2p orbital
    (C) 3s orbital   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2s orbital
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The electronic configuration of sodium is 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^1. The valence electron is in 3s orbital.

Classification of Elements and Periodicity CBSE Online Test 02  (id 942) [PAID]

Q1. Before the 4p orbital is filled, filling up of 3d orbitals becomes energetically favourable and there are 3d transition series of elements. This starts from scandium (Z = 21) which has the outermost electronic configuration of:
    (A) 3d^14p^2
    (B) 3d^14s^2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3s^1d^2
    (D) 2d^13s^2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The electronic configuration of scandium is [Ar] 3d^1 4s^2.

Q2. Maximum number of electrons occupied by s,p, and d orbitals are:
    (A) 2, 8, 8
    (B) 2, 10, 10
    (C) 2, 6 and 10   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2, 2, 8
    Answer: C
    Explanation: s-orbital ml=0, so it can accommodate 2 electron.
p-orbital has ml = -1,0,+1. It can accommodate 6 electrons.
d-orbital has ml = -2,-1,0,1,2.It can accommodate 10 electrons.

Q3. s-block elements comprise of:
    (A) Group 4 (alkali metals) and Group 7 (alkaline earth metals)
    (B) Group 1 and Group 4
    (C) Group 3 and Group 2
    (D) Group 1 (alkali metals) and Group 2 (alkaline earth metals)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: s-block contains two groups of elements including alkali earth metal and alkaline earth metal.

Q4. All the orbitals in the valence shell of the noble gases:
    (A) not completely filled by electrons and the arrangement is not stable.
    (B) completely filled by electrons and it is very easy to remove electrons.
    (C) not completely filled by electrons and it is very easy to alter this stable arrangement by the addition or removal of electrons.
    (D) are completely filled by electrons.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: These elements are called noble elements because they contain ns^2, np^6 valence shell electronic configuration. A complete octet in the outermost shell makes these elements chemically stable, and therefore they do not easily react with other elements to form compounds.

Q5. d-Block Elements are characterized by the:
    (A) absence of d orbital electrons.
    (B) filling of inner d orbitals by electrons.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) inner d orbitals are not filled.
    (D) filling of outer d orbitals.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: d-Block elements also known as transition elements are characterized by the filling of inner d orbitals by electrons before the valence-shell s orbital.

Q6. f-block of the Periodic Table consists of:
    (A) Halogens (Group 17) and the chalcogens (Group 16).
    (B) The first two groups of the periodic table.
    (C) Groups 13 and 14 “Transition Elements”.
    (D) Lanthanoid and Actinoids.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The two rows of elements at the bottom of the Periodic Table, called the Lanthanoids, Ce(Z = 58) – Lu(Z = 71) and Actinoids, Th(Z = 90) – Lr (Z = 103) are characterised by the outer electronic configuration (n-2)f^1-14 (n-1)d^0-1 ns^2. The last electron added to each element is filled in f- orbital. These two series of elements are hence called the Inner- Transition Elements (f-Block Elements).

Q7. Metalloids show the properties of:
    (A) properties that are characteristic of both metals and plastics.
    (B) properties that are characteristic of both metals and gases.
    (C) properties that are characteristic of both metals and nonmetals.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) properties that are characteristic of both metals and viscous liquids.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A metalloid is any chemical element which has properties in between those of metals and nonmetals, or that has a mixture of them. Typical metalloids have a metallic appearance, but they are brittle and only fair conductors of electricity. Chemically, they behave mostly as nonmetals. They can form alloys with metals. Most of their other physical and chemical properties are intermediate in nature. The six commonly recognized metalloids are boron, silicon, germanium, arsenic, antimony, and tellurium.

Q8. The first ionisation enthalpies of Na, Mg, Al and Si are in the order:
    (A) $\mathrm { Na } < \mathrm { Mg } < \mathrm { Al } < \mathrm { Si }$
    (B) $\mathrm { Na } > \mathrm { Mg } > \mathrm { Al } < \mathrm { Si }$
    (C) $\mathrm { Na } < \mathrm {Al } < \mathrm { Si } < \mathrm { Mg }$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\mathrm { Na } > \mathrm { Mg } > \mathrm { Al } > \mathrm { Si }$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\mathrm { Na } < \mathrm {Al } < \mathrm { Si } < \mathrm { Mg }$

Q9. Ionization enthalpy increases across a period because:
    (A) outermost electrons are held more and more tightly.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) shielding is more effective.
    (C) screening is more effective.
    (D) outermost electrons are not held tightly.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Consider moving from lithium to fluorine across the second period, where successive electrons are added to orbitals in the same principal quantum level. The shielding of the nuclear charge by the inner core of electrons does not increase very much to compensate for the increased attraction of the electron to the nucleus. Thus, across a period, increasing nuclear charge outweighs the shielding. Consequently, the outermost electrons are held more and more tightly and the ionization enthalpy increases across a period.

Q10. In the periodic table, Electronegativity generally:
    (A) increases across a period from left to right and decreases down a group.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) decreases across a period from left to right and decreases down a group.
    (C) decreases across a period from left to right and increases down a group.
    (D) increases across a period from left to right and increases down a group.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The electronegativity value increases as the effective nuclear charge on the atomic nucleus increases. In a period moving from left to right, the electronegativity increases due to a decrease in atomic radii resulting in an increase in effective nuclear charge. Whereas, in a group moving from top to bottom, the electronegativity decreases because of the atomic radius increases due to the subsequent addition of shells.

Q11. Select the species which are iso-electronic (same number of the electron) with each other.
    (A) Cl^- and Ca^2+   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cl^- and Rb^+
    (C) Ne and Ca^2+
    (D) Rb^+ and Ca^2+
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Neutral Cl ( Z=17) has 17 electrons and with the addition of one more electron, it becomes Cl^- anion which has 18 electrons.
Neutral Ca (Z=20) has 20 electrons and with the removal of 2 electrons, it becomes Ca^2+ cation which has 18 electrons.
Since Cl^- and Ca^2+ both has 18 electrons, so they are isoelectronic.

Q12. Generally, the first ionization energy increases along a period including some exceptions. One which is NOT an exception is ______.
    (A) Be and B
    (B) Mg and Al
    (C) N and O
    (D) Na and Mg   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The high ionization energy of B, N, and Mg is due to the presence of stable electronic configuration in these atoms as compared to the next element in the period. For example, Be (Is^2 2s^2) has completely filled orbitals as compared to B (1s^2 2s^2 2p^1) where there is one electron in p-orbital that can easily be lost. Therefore, B has lower ionization energy than Be.

Q13. The outer electronic configuration of a p- block element is:
    (A) 6s^24f^3
    (B) 3s^23p^64s^2
    (C) 3d^104s^2
    (D) ns^2 np^1-6   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In the p-block elements, the last electron enters in p-orbital of the valence shell and the electronic configuration of the valence shell is ns^2 np^1-6.

Q14. To which block of elements in the periodic table 3d^104s^2 belongs?
    (A) s- Block
    (B) d- Block   <-- CORRECT
    (C) f- Block
    (D) p- Block
    Answer: B
    Explanation: d-block element has the general outermost electronic configuration as (n-1)d^1-10 ns^0-2.

Q15. General electronic configuration of s-block elements is:
    (A) 3d^104s^2
    (B) 6s^24f^3
    (C) ns^1-2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 3s^23p^4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The elements of Group 1 (alkali metals) and Group 2 (alkaline earth metals) which have ns^1 and ns^2 outermost electronic configuration belong to the s-Block Elements. The general electronic configuration of the valence shell for s-block elements is ns^1-2.

Q1. The outer electronic configuration of f-Block elements are:
    (A) ns^2np^(1-6)
    (B) ns^(1-2)
    (C) (n-2)f^(0-14)(n-1)d^(0-1)ns^2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (n-1)d^(1-10)ns^(0-2)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The general outer electronic configuration of s block elements is ns^(1-2)
The general outer electronic configuration of p block elements is ns^2np^(1-6)
The general outer electronic configuration of d block elements is (n-1)d^(1-10)ns^(0-2)
The general outer electronic configuration of f-block elements is (n-2)f^(0-14)(n-1)d^(0-1)ns^2

Q2. The correct order for the increase in atomic radii is:
    (A) I< Br< Cl < F
    (B) F< C< I< Br
    (C) C< Br< I
    (D) F< Cl < Br < I   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In a group moving from top to bottom the number of shells increases. So the atomic size increases. Although the effective nuclear charge increases but its effect is negligible in comparison to the effect of the increasing number of shells. Therefore the correct trend is F< Cl < Br < I.

Q3. The correct order for the decrease in atomic radii is
    (A) Li> Be> B> C
    (B) C< Li< Be< B
    (C) Be< B> C< Li
    (D) Li< Be< B< C   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In a period moving from left to right, the effective nuclear charge increases because the next electron fills in the same shell. So the atomic size decreases.

Q4. One of the following has ns^1 as its outermost electronic configuration:
    (A) Lanthanoids
    (B) Alkaline earth metals
    (C) Transition elements
    (D) Alkali metals   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The elements of Group 1 (alkali metals) which have ns^1 outermost electronic configuration belong to the s-Block Elements.

Q5. Right order of increasing metallic character is:
    (A) P < Si < Be < Mg < Na.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Be < Mg < Na < P< Si
    (C) Si < Mg < Na < P < Be
    (D) Si < Be < Mg < Na < P
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Elements of s block are more matallic than p block elements.

Q6. The elements charecterised by the filling of 4 f-orbitals, are:
    (A) Transition elements
    (B) Lanthanoids   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Alkaline earth metals
    (D) Alkali metals
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The two rows of elements at the bottom of the Periodic Table, called the Lanthanoids, Ce(Z = 58) – Lu(Z = 71) and Actinoids, Th(Z = 90) – Lr (Z = 103) are characterized by the outer electronic configuration (n-2)f^1-14 (n-1)d^0-1ns^2. The last electron added to each element is filled in f- orbital. These two series of elements are hence called the Inner-Transition Elements (f-Block Elements).

Q7. One of the following options is not used for explaining atomic radius:
    (A) Covalent radius
    (B) Metallic radius
    (C) Van der waals’radius
    (D) Coordinate radius   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The distance from the centre of the nucleus to the outermost shell containing the electrons is called the atomic radius. There are four types that are widely used: covalent radii, metallic radii, van der Waal's radii, and ionic radii.

Q8. The correct increasing order of atomic radii for the same element is ____ ?
    (A) covalent radius < Metallic radius < van der Waal's radius   <-- CORRECT
    (B) covalent radius < crystal radius < Metallic radius
    (C) Metallic radius < covalent radius < van der Waal's radius
    (D) van der Waal's radius < Metallic radius < covalent radius
    Answer: A
    Explanation: For the same element ,
 Metallic radius of atoms are always greater than corresponding covalent radius.
 Metallic radius is always lesser than van der Waal's radius
 Hence , the correct increasing order of atomic radii of an element is covalent < Metallic < van der Waal's radius.

Q9. Which one of the following molecules represents the increasing order of bond length?
    (A) N_2 < O_2 < F_2 < Cl_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) F_2 < Cl_2 < O_2 < N_2
    (C) F_2 < N_2 < Cl_2 < O_2
    (D) Cl_2 < O_2 < N_2 < F_2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The bond lengths depend upon the number and type of bonds present in a molecule. The greater the number of bonds shorter would be the bond length.
Thus, the given molecules are all diatomic molecules where,
 N_2 has the smallest bond length as it is triple bonded.
 O_2 is double-bonded so its bond length is greater than N_2.
 F_2 and Cl_2 both, though single-bonded, the bond length of Cl_2 is greater than that of F_2 due to its larger atomic size.
Hence, the correct increasing order of given molecules is N_2 < O_2 < F_2 < Cl_2.

Q10. Choose one of the following in the increasing order of electron gain enthalpy.
    (A) Cl < I < Br < F
    (B) I < Br < F < Cl   <-- CORRECT
    (C) F < Cl < Br < I
    (D) Br < F < Cl < I
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In general, as we move down the group electron gain enthalpy decreases; so the expected trend should be I < Br < Cl < F but in actual the order is I < Br < F < Cl. This is due to the small size of the F atom. The valence electrons of F atom provide strong repulsion to incoming electron, hence F has unexpectedly low electron affinity.

Q11. The increasing order of ionic radii for given species is:
    (A) $Al^{3+} \ {<} \ Mg^{2+} {<} \ Na^+ \ {<} \ F^- {<} \ O^{2^-} \ {<} \ N^{3^-}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $Mg^{2+} \ {<} \ {Na^{+}} \ {<} \ F{^-} \ {<} \ O^{2-} \ {<} \ N^{3-} \ {<}\ Al^{3+}$
    (C) $ N^{3-} \ {<} \ O^{2-} \ {<} F^- \ {<} \ Na^+ \ {<} \ Mg^{2+} \ {<} \ Al^{3+}$
    (D) $Na^+ {<} \ F^- \ {<} \ O^{2-} \ {<} \ N^{3-} \ {<} \ Al^ {3+} \ {<} \ Mg^{2+}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the case of cations,
 there is a decrease in ionic radii of the resulting cation as compared to its neutral parent atom, due to loss of electron /(s)
 greater the positive charge over the cation more would be a decrease in ionic size or radius.
 In the case of anion,
 the addition of each new electron (or negative charge) results in an increase in anionic radius.
 With an increase in negative charge over anion the anionic radius also becomes larger.
 Thus, considering as above the correct answer is-
 $Al^{3+} \ {<} \ Mg^{2+} \ {<} \ Na^+ \ {<} \ F^- {<} O^{2-} \ {<} \ N^{3-}$

Q12. Al^(3+) < Mg^(2+) < Na^+ < F^- < O^(2-) < N^(3-)
The above can be aptly described as:
    (A) the same number of electrons (7 electrons).
    (B) the same number of electrons (8 electrons).
    (C) isoelectronic species.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the same number of electrons (9 electrons).
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Isoelectronic species are elements or ions that have the same or an equal number of electrons. Although isoelectronic species have the same number of electrons, they are different in their physical and chemical properties. This Al^(3+) < Mg^(2+) < Na^+ < F^- < O^(2-) < N^(3-) trend is isoelectronic species.

Q13. The correct increasing order of radii of following species is _______?
    (A) $I \ {<} \ I^+ \ {<} \ I^-$
    (B) $I^+ \ {<} \ I^- \ {<} \ I$
    (C) $I^+ \ {<} \ I \ {<} \ I^-$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $I^- \ {<} \ I^+ \ {<} \ I$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: It is because 
(i) radius of anion ( anionic radius ) is greater , and
(ii) radius of cation ( cationic radius ) is lesser 
than that of its parent neutral atom.

Q14. The increasing order of bond dissociation energies of the following species is_____.
    (A) F_2 < Cl_2 < O_2 < N_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) N_2 < O_2 < F_2 < Cl_2
    (C) Cl_2 < O_2 < N_2 < F_2
    (D) F_2 < N_2 < Cl_2 < O_2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As bond order increases bond dissociation energy also increases.
Thus N_2
 The triple bonded N_2 with bond order = 3 has the highest bond dissociation energy.
 The doubly bonded O_2 with bond order = 2 has lesser bond dissociation energy than N_2
 F_2 and Cl_2 both are single bonded having the same bond order = 1 
But, the electron-electron repulsive force (e-e repulsion) is maximum in the F_2 molecule due to its small size. This accounts for the lower bond dissociation energy of F_2 as compared to Cl_2.

Q15. The typical range of molar enthalpies for the strongest intermolecular (Hydrogen) bonds is:
    (A) (4 - 25) kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (300 - 500) kJ
    (C) (50 - 100) kJ
    (D) (200 - 300) kJ
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A hydrogen bond is an electrostatic attraction between two polar groups that occurs when a hydrogen (H) atom linked to a small-sized highly electronegative atom such as nitrogen (N), oxygen (O), or fluorine (F). Therefore unlike a covalent bond, it has very low dissociation energy with a range of molar enthalpy = (4 - 25) kJ.

Q1. In terms of period and group, where would you locate the element with Z = 114 in the modern periodic table?
    (A) 6th period and 13th group
    (B) 7th period and 14th group   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 6th period 14th group
    (D) 7th period and 13th group
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Elements with atomic numbers Z = (87 - 114) are placed in the 7th period.
Thus, the element with Z= 114 (Flerovium) is placed in the 7th period and 14th group of the modern periodic table.

Q2. For an ionic compound with the tetrahedral structure the ratio $\frac{{r^+}}{{r^{ - }}}$ lies in the range of_____.
    (A) 0.225 to 0.414   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.732 to 1.0
    (C) 0.414 to 0.732
    (D) 0.155 to 0.255
    Answer: A
    Explanation: For the tetrahedral structure of an ionic solid, $\frac{{{r^+ }}}{{{r- }}}$ lies in the range of 0.225 to 0.414.

Q3. The relative tendency of an atom in a molecule to attract the shared pair of electrons towards itself is termed as its:
    (A) electro-negativity   <-- CORRECT
    (B) electron gain enthalpy
    (C) ionisation enthalpy
    (D) electro-positivivity
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A qualitative measure of the ability of an atom in a chemical compound to attract shared electrons to itself is called electronegativity. Unlike ionization enthalpy and electron gain enthalpy, it is not a measurable quantity. However, a number of numerical scales of electronegativity of elements viz., Pauling scale, Mulliken-Jaffe scale, Allred-Rochow scale have been developed. The electronegativity of any given element is not constant; it varies depending on the element to which it is bound.

Q4. The order of screening effect of electrons of s, p, d and f orbitals of a given shell of an atom on its outer shell electrons is:
    (A) f > p > s > d
    (B) s > p > d > f   <-- CORRECT
    (C) p < d < s > f
    (D) f > d > p > s
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Screening effect order follows s>p>d>f, this due to the nature of the orbitals involved. s-orbitals are least diffused and the two electrons in s-orbitals provide greatest shielding of the nuclear charge to the outermost electron. The diffused character increases in the order p>d>f. f-orbitals are so diffused that fourteen electrons inside them provide virtually no screening of the nuclear charge.

Q5. Which of the following is not an actinoid?
    (A) Terbium (Z = 65)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Californium (Z = 98)
    (C) Curium (Z = 96)
    (D) Uranium (Z = 92)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Terbium (Z=65) has an electronic configuration of [Xe] 4f^9 6s^2. It is a member of 4f-inner transition series which is called lanthanoid series. Rest option are all the members of 5f-inner transition series, also known as the actinoid series i.e. Curium ([Rn] 5f^7 6d^1 7s^2) ; Californium ([Rn] 5f^10 7s_2); and Uranium ([Rn] 5f^3 6d^1 7s^2).

Q6. The electronic configuration of gadolinium (Atomic number 64) is
    (A) $[ \mathrm { Xe } ] 4 \mathrm { f } ^ { 8 } 5 \mathrm { d } ^ { 6 } 6 \mathrm { s } ^ { 2 }$
    (B) $[ \mathrm { Xe } ] 4 \mathrm { f } ^ { 3 } 5 \mathrm { d } ^ { 5 } 6 \mathrm { s } ^ { 2 }$
    (C) $[ \mathrm { Xe } ] 4 \mathrm { f } ^ { 7 } 5 \mathrm { d } ^ { 2 } 6 \mathrm { s } ^ { 1 }$
    (D) $[ \mathrm { Xe } ] 4 \mathrm { f } ^ { 7 } 5 \mathrm { d } ^ { 1 } 6 \mathrm { s } ^ { 2 }$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $[ \mathrm { Xe } ] 4 \mathrm { f } ^ { 7 } 5 \mathrm { d } ^ { 1 } 6 \mathrm { s } ^ { 2 }$

Q7. Among the alkali metals, Cesium is the most reactive because:
    (A) It is the heaviest alkali metal.
    (B) The outermost electron is very loosely bound than the outermost electron of the other alkali metals.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Its incomplete shell is nearest to the nucleus.
    (D) It has a single electron in the valence shell.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cesium has the lowest ionization energy in the alkali metal group because it has the biggest atomic size in the alkali metal family. The valence electron is most loosely held due to its bigger size, and it can easily be lost.

Q8. The effective distance between the centre of the nucleus of an ion and the point up to which the nucleus has an influence on its electron cloud is called_____.
    (A) cationic radius
    (B) ionic radius   <-- CORRECT
    (C) anionic radius
    (D) covalent radius
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since 'Ionic radius' is defined as the effective distance from the centre of the nucleus of an ion up to which it has an influence on its electron cloud. The correct answer is " ionic radius ".
The term Ionic radius is a general term used for both the cations as well as anions.

Q9. For alkali metals, which one of the following trends is INCORRECT?
    (A) Ionization energy: Li > Na > K > Rb
    (B) Density: Li < Na < K < Rb   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Hydration energy: Li > Na > K > Rb
    (D) Atomic size: Li < Na < K < Rb
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The expected trend for density is Li < Na < K < Rb but the actual trend is Li < K < Na < Rb. The size of the alkali metal increase down the group but when we move from Na to K, the increase in atomic size is more than expected.

Q10. For the four successive transition elements (Cr, Mn, Fe, and Co), the stability of + 2 oxidation state will be there in which of the following order? (At. nos. Cr = 24, Mn = 25, Fe = 26, Co = 27).
    (A) Mn > Fe > Cr > Co   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Fe > Mn > Co > Cr
    (C) Cr > Mn > Co > Fe
    (D) Co > Mn > Fe > Cr
    Answer: A
    Explanation: This is attributed to the extra stability of half-filled orbitals that is seen only in Mn^2+ (i.e. d^5). The other members have Fe (d^6); Cr (d^4) and Co (d^7) respectively.

Q11. Generally, the first ionization energy increases throughout the period. But there are some exceptions. One which is NOT an exception is ______.
    (A) Mg and Al
    (B) Be and B
    (C) N and O
    (D) Na and Mg   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The exception in ionization energy is due to the extra stability of fully filled and half-filled valence orbitals. It appears in the case of N and O where N is half-filled; Be and B where B has fully filled; Mg and Al where Mg has fully filled valence orbitals. No such exception appears when we move from Na to Mg.

Q12. Where is nitrogen found in the periodic table?
    (A) 2^nd period, group 15   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2^nd period, group 14
    (C) 2^nd period, group 18
    (D) 3^nd period, group 15
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Nitrogen is the seventh element on the periodic table. It is located in period 2 and group 15. It is at the top of the periodic table, between carbon and oxygen.

Q13. Which of the following is a Metalloid?
    (A) Phosphorus
    (B) Antimony   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Bismuth
    (D) Nitrogen
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A metalloid is any chemical element which has properties in between those of metals and nonmetals, or that has a mixture of them. The six commonly recognized metalloids are boron, silicon, germanium, arsenic, antimony, and tellurium. Antimony is capable of displacing hydrogen from water (like metal), but still, most of its chemistry is characteristic of a nonmetal.

Q14. Metals usually used as catalysts in different reactions belong to:
    (A) d - block   <-- CORRECT
    (B) p - block
    (C) f – block
    (D) s - block
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Transition metals and their compounds function as catalysts either because of their ability to change oxidation state or, in the case of the metals, to adsorb other substances on to their surface and activate them in the process.

Q15. Mg^2+ is isoelectronic with:
    (A) Na^+   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Cu^2+
    (C) Zn^2+
    (D) Ca^2+
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Total electrons in Mg^2+ and Na^+ are same i.e. 10.

Q1. Select the species with diamagnetic nature:
    (A) ${\left[ {{\text{Ni}}{{\left( {{\text{CN}}} \right)}_{\text{4}}}} \right]^{{\text{2}}-}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${\left[ {{\text{CuC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}} \right]^{{\text{2}}-}}$
    (C) ${\left[ {{\text{NiC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}} \right]^{{\text{2}}-}}$
    (D) ${\left[ {{\text{Co}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{6}}}} \right]^{{\text{3}}-}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: ${[Ni(CN]_4]}^{2-}$ is a diamagnetic species because:
 The $Ni^{2+}$ ion has the valence shell electronic configuration: $3d^8 , 4s^0$ .
 The presence of a strong field $CN^-$ ions, as a legand forces all the electrons to get paired up in 3d orbitals providing 4 pairs of paired electrons and one empty d shell. 
 The empty 3d, 3s, and two 4p orbitals undergo dsp^2 hybridization to get bonded up with [CN]^- ion. Thus, [Ni(CN)_4]^2- shows a diamagnetic nature.

Q2. Which of the following characteristic is not correct regarding alkali metals?
    (A) High ionisation energy   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Low electronegativity
    (C) Their ions are isoelectronic with noble gas
    (D) Low melting point
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Alkali metals have the lowest ionization energy value in the respective period.

Q3. The correct statement with regard to $H_2^ + $ and $H_2^ - $ is:
    (A) $H_2^ + $ is more stable than $H_2^ - $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Both $H_2^ + $ and $H_2^ - $ do not exist
    (C) $H_2^ - $is more stable than $H_2^ + $
    (D) Both $H_2^ + $ and $H_2^ - $ are equally stable
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Bond order of both species is $\frac {1}{2}$ but $H_2^ -$​ contains one electron in the antibonding orbital which results in repulsion and decreases the stability. On the other hand, $H_2^ + $ does not contain any electron in the antibonding molecular orbital.
Hence $H_2^ + $​ is more stable.

Q4. The magnetic moment of a transition metal ion is $\sqrt {15} $ B.M. Therefore the number of unpaired electrons present in it is______.
    (A) 3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2
    (C) 4
    (D) 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The spin magnetic moment is $= \sqrt{n(n+2)}$ BM; where n is a number of unpaired electrons. When n =3; then magnetic moment with be $\sqrt{15}$ BM.

Q5. An element with atomic number 21 is a:
    (A) Representative element
    (B) Alkali metal
    (C) Halogen
    (D) Transition element   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The element is Scandium (Sc) with atomic number (Z) = 21
The electronic configuration of _21Sc s [Ar] 3d^1, 4s^2. Hence, it is a transition element.

Q6. The electronic configuration of an element in Group 15 and period 3 of the periodic table is ______.
    (A) ${\text{1}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{6}}}3s^2 3 p^2$
    (B) ${\text{1}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{6}}}{\text{3}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{3}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{4}}}$
    (C) ${\text{1}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{6}}}\ 3 s^2 3 p^1$
    (D) ${\text{1}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{2}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{6}}}{\text{3}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{3}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{3}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since, according to the classification of elements in the modern periodic table,
The period number gives an idea of Valence shell number (n) while the group number gives an idea of Valence electrons i.e. no. of electrons short to nearest octet or duplet. 
$\therefore$ The electronic configuration of the element in the 3rd period and 15th Group is $( 1s^2 , 2s^2 2p^6 , 3s^2 3p^3 )$.

Q7. The formula for Xenon compounds containing $\sigma \ bonds = 5 \ and \ \pi \ bonds = 3$ is
    (A) ${\text{Xe}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{3}}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$
    (B) ${\text{Xe}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${\text{XeFO}}$
    (D) ${\text{Xe}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The presence of $five \ \sigma \ bonds \ and \ three \ \pi \ bonds $ in compound ${\text{Xe}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}$ has been confirmed by its IR spectra.

Q8. Dmitri Mendeleev (1834-1907) and the German chemist, Lothar Meyer (1830-1895) proposed arranging elements in:
    (A) Decreasing order of their atomic numbers
    (B) Increasing order of their atomic numbers
    (C) Increasing order of their atomic weights   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Decreasing order of their atomic weights
    Answer: C
    Explanation: When they arranged elements in the increasing order of their atomic weights, both of them observed that the chemical and physical properties of the elements repeated after a regular interval.

Q9. A transition metal ion exists in its highest oxidation state. It is expected to behave as:
    (A) A reducing agent
    (B) An oxidising agent   <-- CORRECT
    (C) A chelating agent
    (D) A central metal in a coordination compound
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The transition metal in its highest oxidation state will have no desire to further loose electrons. It will act as an oxidizing agent where it will accept electrons and is reduced in a chemical reaction.

Q10. Which of the following statements is false?
 Alkali metals form covalent bonds with oxygen.
 Alkali metals form oxides that act as basic anhydrides.
 Alkali metals usually have a +1 oxidation state.
 Alkali metals have relatively low first ionization energies.
    (A) D
    (B) C
    (C) A   <-- CORRECT
    (D) B
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Alkali metals have lowest ionization energies in their respective periods. They prefer to loose an electron to form a cation and thereby form an ionic compound.

Q11. Which one of the following species is smallest in its size Al^3+, Mg^2+, Na^+, Ne?
    (A) Ne
    (B) Mg^2+
    (C) Na^+
    (D) Al^3+   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The given species are all isoelectronic species.
 Ne though isoelectronic with other species is a neutral and inert element, so in the absence of any charge over its atom would have the largest size. 
 In the case of other cationic species;
 Greater the number of positive charges over a cation more is the effective nuclear attraction resulting in a greater reduction in the size of the cation. Therefore, out of $Al^3+ \ , \ Mg^{2+} \ , \ Na^+ \ , Ne$ 
 $Al^{3+}$ is the smallest in size.

Q12. Which of the following will have the most negative electron gain enthalpy and which one the least negative? P, S, Cl, F.
    (A) P, F
    (B) Cl, P   <-- CORRECT
    (C) P,Cl
    (D) P,S
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chlorine has the electronic configuration of 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^5, it need one more electrons to get fully filled electronic configuration. It will accept an electron easily to acquire stability, hence it has most negative electron gain enthalpy. Whereas phosphorus has 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^3; here p-orbitals are half filled. This half filled configuration gives extra stability to phosphorus, hence it will be resistent to accept an electron. It has a positive electron affinity or in simple words energy is added to make P accept an electron.

Q13. S-block elements comprise:
    (A) Group 4 (alkali metals) and Group 7 (alkaline earth metals)
    (B) Group 3 and Group 2
    (C) Group-1 (alkali metals) and Group-2 (alkaline earth metals)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Group 1 and Group 4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: S-block elements comprise of Group 1 (alkali metals) and Group 2 (alkaline earth metals) with the general outermost electronic configuration as ns^1-2.

Q14. It is now recognized that the ‘Modern Periodic Law’ is essentially the consequence of the:
    (A) periodic variation in chemical bonds.
    (B) periodic variations in the element lattice.
    (C) periodic variation in electronic configurations.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) periodic variation in chemical properties.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Modern Periodic law states that the physical and chemical properties of elements are the periodic functions of their atomic numbers. It implies that the chemical and physical properties of the elements and any variations in these properties can easily be predicted via the outermost electronic configuration.

Q15. The correct decreasing order of chemical reactivities in terms of their oxidizing properties for F, Cl, O and N is:
    (A) O > F > N > Cl
    (B) F > O > Cl > N   <-- CORRECT
    (C) F > Cl > O > N
    (D) Cl > F > O > N
    Answer: B
    Explanation: All these elements are p-block elements.
The oxidizing character of elements increases from left to right across a period because of the presence of vacant d - orbitals in their valence shells. Thus we get the decreasing order of oxidizing properties as F > O > N
Again, the oxidizing character of elements decreases down the group. Thus, we get F > Cl. However, the oxidizing character of O is more than that of Cl ie. O > Cl
Hence, the correct order of chemical reactivities of F, Cl, O, N in terms of their oxidizing properties is F > O > Cl > N.

Q1. The hybridizations of atomic orbitals of nitrogen in NO_2^+, NO_3^- and NH_4^+ respectively are:
    (A) sp^2, sp and sp^3
    (B) sp^2, sp^3 and sp
    (C) sp, sp^3 and sp^2
    (D) sp, sp^2 and sp^3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The types of hybrid orbitals of nitrogen in NO_2^+, NO_3^–, and NH_4^+ respectively are expected to be sp, sp^2, and sp^3.

Q2. The inertness of noble gas was observed to be due to their electronic configurations. Choose the most appropriate:
    (A) Atomic mass is low so they are stable.
    (B) Total number of electrons in the outermost shell is duplets.
    (C) Outermost orbitals of the noble gases are fully filled.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Noble gases form ions to complete their outermost orbitals.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The six noble gases (Helium, Neon, Argon, Krypton, Xenon, Radon) are found in group 18 of the periodic table. These elements were considered to be inert gases until the 1960s because their oxidation number of 0 prevents the noble gases from forming compounds readily. All noble gases have the maximum number of electrons possible in their outer shell (2 for Helium, 8 for all others), making them stable.

Q3. Stable outer octet of electrons is achieved in chlorine atom during the formation of NaCl by:
    (A) The formation of a hybrid orbital
    (B) The gain of an electron   <-- CORRECT
    (C) The formation of a coordinate bond
    (D) The loss of an electron
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Na loses its one electron forming Na^+ while Cl gains the electron forming Cl^-.

Q4. The bond formed, as a result of the electrostatic attraction between the positive and negative ions was termed as:
    (A) coordinate bond
    (B) covalent bond
    (C) single covalency
    (D) electrovalent bond   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The chemical bond formed between two atoms due to the transfer of electron(s) from one atom to the other. atom is called an "ionic bond" or "electrovalent bond". In an electrovalent bond one atom loses an electron to form a positive ion and the other atom gains the electron to form a negative ion. The resulting ions are held together by electrostatic attraction.

Q5. The number of dots around the Lewis symbols for the elements represent:
    (A) electrovalency
    (B) the number of valence electrons of the element   <-- CORRECT
    (C) group valence of the element
    (D) coordinate valency
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Gilbert N. Lewis is widely known for his use of simple symbolic representations of elements that show valence electrons as dots.
The Lewis electron-dot symbols focus on the electrons in the highest principal energy level in the atom, the valence electrons.
After all, these are the electrons that participate in chemical reactions. Lewis electron-dot symbols work well for the representative elements.

Q6. The formation of the Cl_2 molecule can be understood in terms of the sharing of a pair of electrons between the two chlorine atoms, each chlorine atom contributing one electron to the shared pair. Choose the most appropriate name of the bond that is formed:
    (A) a single covalent bond   <-- CORRECT
    (B) multiple bond
    (C) double bond
    (D) ionic bond
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Two chlorine atoms will each share one electron to get a full outer shell and form a stable Cl_2 molecule. By sharing the two electrons where the shells touch each chlorine atom can count 8 electrons in its outer shell. These full outer shells with their shared electrons are now stable and the Cl_2 molecule will not react further with other chlorine atoms. One pair of shared electrons form a single covalent bond.

Q7. The electronic configurations of three elements, A, B and C are given below.
A 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6
B 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^3
C 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6 3s^2 3p^5 
The molecular formula of the compound formed from B and C will be
    (A) B_2C
    (B) BC_2
    (C) BC
    (D) BC_3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: B represents phosphorus (P) and C represents Chlorine (Cl). Thecompound formed is PCl_3 i.e., BC_3.

Q8. 788 kJ of energy is required to separate one mole of solid NaCl into one mole of Na^+ (g) and one mole of Cl^- (g) to an infinite distance. This process explains:
    (A) Electron affinity
    (B) electron gain enthalpy
    (C) lattice enthalpy   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ionization enthalpy
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Lattice enthalpy is simply the change in Enthalpy associated with the formation of one mole of an ionic compound from its oppositely charged ions in their standard states under standard conditions.

Q9. A qualitative measure of the stability of an ionic compound is provided by:
    (A) ionization enthalpy
    (B) electron gain enthalpy
    (C) Electron affinity
    (D) lattice enthalpy   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Lattice energy is an estimate of the bond strength in ionic compounds. It is defined as the heat of formation for ions of opposite charge in the gas phase to combine into an ionic solid. The stability of the ionic bond is directly proportional to lattice energy.

Q10. Bond lengths are lower in elements having:
    (A) double bond
    (B) single bond
    (C) triple bond   <-- CORRECT
    (D) crystal structure
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The bond length depends on the strength of the bond. The stronger the bond is, the shorter it will be. The triple bonds are the strongest and hence the shortest. Then comes double bonds which are of intermediate strength between the triple and single bonds. And finally, the single bonds are weaker than the other two. This way, Triple bonds are the shortest. Then comes double bonds. Finally, single bonds are the longest among the three.
The order of bond lengths is given as Triple bond < Double bond < Single bond.

Q11. Bond angle helps us in:
    (A) determining molecular shape   <-- CORRECT
    (B) determining the reactivity of the element
    (C) determining the stability of the element
    (D) determining molecular size
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Bond angles also contribute to the shape of a molecule. Bond angles are the angles between adjacent lines representing bonds. The bond angle can help differentiate between linear, trigonal planar, tetrahedral, trigonal-bipyramidal, and octahedral. The ideal bond angles are the angles that demonstrate the maximum angle where it would minimize repulsion, thus verifying the VSEPR theory.

Q12. The amount of energy required to break one mole of bonds of a particular type between two atoms in a gaseous state is called ________.
    (A) ionization enthalpy
    (B) lattice enthalpy
    (C) bond enthalpy   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Electron affinity
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Bond enthalpy also known as bond energy is the energy that is needed to break a particular bond in a gaseous compound. The unit that expresses bond enthalpy is kilojoules per mole or kJ/mol.

Q13. H.O.H bond angle in water is:
    (A) 416°
    (B) 240°
    (C) 110°
    (D) 104.5^0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Due to the presence of two lone pairs on O in the H_2O bond angle reduce to 104.5^0 from 109^0.

Q14. For N_2, bond order is:
    (A) 3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 4
    (C) 1
    (D) 2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Bond order is the number of chemical bonds between a pair of atoms. in diatomic nitrogen N≡N, Triple covalent bond is present in nitrogen so the bond order is 3.

Q15. N_2, CO, and NO^+ are isoelectronic molecules. Their respective bond order is:
    (A) 2,3,3
    (B) 2,3,4
    (C) 3,3,3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1,1,3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Total number of electrons in N_2 molecule is 7+ 7= 14.
As per the formula Bonded pair of electrons N_b: $σ1s^2\ σ2s^2\ {tex}\pi$2p_y^2\ $\pi$2p_z^2\ σ 2p_x^2{/tex}
Total 10 electrons.
Anti bond pairs of electrons N_a: $σ 1s*^2\ σ 2s*^2$ Total 4 electrons.
Bond Order (B.O.) = ${N_b-N_a\over 2} ={ 10-4\over 2} = 3 $
Similarly bond order of CO And NO^+ is 3

Q1. Structures of ${\text{CO}}_3^{2 - }$. ion given below explains the phenomenon of _____________.
    (A) dipole moment
    (B) resonance   <-- CORRECT
    (C) isoelectronic ionic character
    (D) isomerism
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Resonance is the phenomenon when a molecule can be represented by 1 or more structure differing in the position of bonds and charge.

Q2. The product of the magnitude of the charge and the distance between the centres of positive and negative charge is called _______.
    (A) electronegativity
    (B) covalent character
    (C) Dipole moment   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ionic character
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A dipole moment ​is a measurement of the separation of two opposite electrical charges. Dipole moments are a vector quantity. The magnitude is equal to the charge multiplied by the distance between the charges and the direction is from negative charge to positive charge: $\mu$ = q $\times$ r

Q3. The valence shell electron pair repulsion (VSEPR) theory helps in the:
    (A) ionic formation of molecules
    (B) prediction of lewis structure of molecules
    (C) electronic configurations of atoms
    (D) prediction of geometrical shapes of molecules   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Valence shell electron pair repulsion (VSEPR) theory is a model used in chemistry to predict the geometry of individual molecules from the number of electron pairs surrounding their central atoms. It is also named the Gillespie-Nyholm theory after its two main developers.

Q4. In the formation of hydrogen molecule, the overlapping of atomic orbitals occur which results in the pairing of electrons. These are:
    (A) valence shell electrons with same spins
    (B) valence shell electrons with opposite spins.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) lone pair of electons
    (D) valence shell electrons irrespective of the spins
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Overlapping of atomic orbitals having electrons of opposite spin take place in the formation of a molecule to cancel the dipole moment.

Q5. In NO^-_3 ion, the number of bond pairs and lone pairs of electrons on nitrogen atom are
    (A) 3, 1
    (B) 1, 3
    (C) 2, 2
    (D) 4,0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The nitrate ion is formed by the loss of the hydrogen ion, and so its structure is:
Around the central nitrogen there are 4 pairs of shared electrons, and no remaining lone pair. The original lone pair has now become a bonding pair. Two of those pairs make up a double bond. The double bond unit and the two single bonds arrange themselves as far apart as possible in a trigonal planar arrangement - exactly the same as the carbonate ion.

Q6. In case of a heteronuclear molecule like HF, the shared electron pair between the two atoms gets displaced more towards fluorine since the electronegativity of fluorine is far greater than that of hydrogen. This results in the molecule a
    (A) resonance hybrid
    (B) resonance
    (C) Lewis structure
    (D) dipole moment   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: because of slight shifting of electron towards more electronegative element like F in HF brings a small amount of negative charge on F and positive charge on H which results in dipole moment.

Q7. Elements in which apart from 3s and 3p orbitals, 3d orbitals also available for bonding In a number of compounds of these elements there are more than eight valence electrons around the central atom. One such example is:
    (A) HNO_3
    (B) HCl
    (C) H_2SO_4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) H_2O
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In H_2SO_4, S has more than 8 electrons in the valence shell. It has 12 electrons in its valence shell.

Q8. The shift in electron density is symbolised by crossed arrow in the below diagram. It depicts
    (A) resonance hybrid
    (B) Lewis structure
    (C) dipole moment   <-- CORRECT
    (D) resonance
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The cross base arrow demonstrates the net dipole. On the cross-base arrow, the cross represents the positive charge and the arrow represents the negative charge.

Q9. In BF_3, molecule below the dipole moment is zero although the B - F bonds are oriented at an angle of 120° to one another. Net dipole moment in BF_3, molecule is
    (A) two
    (B) zero   <-- CORRECT
    (C) one
    (D) three
    Answer: B
    Explanation: BF_3 has symmetrical structure in which the three B-F bonds are oriented at an angle of 120° to one another. Also the three bonds lie in one plane and the dipole moments of these bonds cancel one another giving net dipole moment equal to zero.

Q10. The shape of the below molecule is
    (A) bent   <-- CORRECT
    (B) trigonal planar
    (C) see saw
    (D) trigonal
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Bent shape is the shape of a molecule with 3 atoms that have a bond angle less than 180°.

Q11. Ionic crystalline compounds formed by ion-formation by electron transfer proves:
    (A) Molecular Orbital (MO) Theory
    (B) Valence Bond (VB) Theory
    (C) Valence Shell Electron Pair Repulsion VSEPR Theory
    (D) Electronic theory of chemical bonding   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ionic crystalline compounds formed by ion-formation by electron transfer proves the electronic theory of chemical bonding. According to this theory, ionic bonds are formed when an atom loses electron/ electrons to become a positive ion and another atom gains the electron/ electrons to become a negative ion. Ionic bonding is a process of complete transfer of Valence electrons.

Q12. The tetrahedral molecule below where there are two lone pairs of electrons is
    (A) SO_2
    (B) H_2O   <-- CORRECT
    (C) O_3
    (D) BF_3
    Answer: B
    Explanation: An important feature of water is its polar nature. The structure has a bent molecular geometry for the two hydrogens from the oxygen vertex. The oxygen atom also has two lone pairs of electrons.

Q13. The criterion of overlap of atomic orbitals is the main factor for the formation of:
    (A) covalent bonds   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Hydrogen bonds
    (C) coordinate bonds
    (D) ionic bonds
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The valence bond theory is introduced to describe the bonding in organic molecules. In this model, bonds are considered to form from the overlapping of two atomic orbitals on different atoms, each orbital containing a single electron.
In general, greater the overlap, stronger is the bond formed between the two atoms. Thus, according to the orbital overlap concept, atoms combine together by overlapping their orbital and thus forming a lower energy state where their valence electrons with opposite spin, pair up to form the covalent bond.

Q14. The octet of electrons represents a particularly stable electronic arrangement. Atoms achieve a stable octet when they are linked by chemical bonds. This rule is associated with which one of the following theories?
    (A) Molecular Orbital (MO) Theory
    (B) Valence Shell Electron Pair Repulsion VSEPR Theory
    (C) Valence Bond (VB) Theory
    (D) Lewis approach   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: G.N.Lewis, proposed the octet rule to explain the valence electron sharing between atoms that resulted in a bonding type with the atoms attaining noble gas electronic configuration.
The statement is: "a bond is formed between two atoms by mutual sharing of pairs of electrons to attain a stable outer-octet of electrons for each atom involved in bonding".

Q1. The maximum number of hydrogen bonds that a molecule of water can have is
    (A) 3
    (B) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2
    (D) 1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The two hydrogens of the water molecule can form hydrogen bonds with other oxygens in water, and the two lone pair of electrons on oxygen of the water molecule can attract other hydrogens in water. Hence, 4 possible hydrogen bonds.

Q2. During the formation of a chemical bond:
    (A) energy of the system does not change
    (B) electron-electron repulsion becomes more than the nucleus-electron attraction
    (C) energy decreases   <-- CORRECT
    (D) energy increases
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A chemical bond is a lasting attraction between atoms that enables the formation of chemical compounds. The bond may result from the electrostatic force of attraction between atoms with opposite charges, or through the sharing of electrons as in the covalent bonds. When a bond forms, electrons are attracted to the space between nuclei where the electrostatic force of attraction is greater. As the electrons fall to a position of lower potential energy, the total mechanical energy of the molecular system decreases. Part of the mechanical energy of the unbound atoms is lost when they form the molecular system with a lower total mechanical energy.

Q3. Which of the following has maximum number of lone pairs associated with Xe?
    (A) XeF_6
    (B) XeF_4
    (C) XeF_2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) XeO_3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In XeF_​​​​2: Xe has 2 of its electrons in bonding with F. So, since Xe has 8 valence electrons, the no.of lone pairs = ${no. \ of \ non-bonding \ electrons\over 2}={6\over 2}=3$
 In XeO_3: Xe has 6 of its electrons in bonding with O (bcoz of double bond). So, Xe will have 2 non bonding electrons and therefore 1 lone pair.
 In XeF_4: Xe has 4 of its electrons in bonding with F. So, Xe will have 4 non bonding electrons and therefore 2 lone pairs.
 In XeF_6: Xe has 6 of its electrons in bonding with F. So, Xe will have 2 non bonding electrons and therefore 1 lone pair.
So XeF_2 has the maximum no. of lone pairs associated with Xe.

Q4. The structure of IF_7 is
    (A) Octahedral
    (B) Trigonal bipyramid
    (C) Pentagonal bipyramid   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Square pyramid
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In IF_7 Iodine heptafluoride out of 7 Flourine atoms, 5 of them are placed on a plane in Pentagon shape. In the remaining 2 flourines one is placed above the plane and the other below the plane each at 90 degrees

Q5. The number of types of bonds between two carbon atoms in calcium carbide is
    (A) Two sigma, one pi
    (B) Two sigma, two pi
    (C) One sigma, two pi   <-- CORRECT
    (D) One sigma, one pi
    Answer: C
    Explanation: CaC_2 has a combination of bonds. It is an ionic lattice that has Ca^2+ cations and acetylide C_2^2- anions. Within each C_2^2-there is a triple bond between the 2C atoms, consisting of 1 sigma and 2 pi bonds.

Q6. The hybridization of orbitals of N atom in ${\text{NO}}_3^ - $, ${\text{NO}}_2^ + $ and $NH_4^ + $ are respectively:
    (A) sp , sp^2 , sp^3
    (B) sp^2 , sp , sp^3   <-- CORRECT
    (C) sp^2 , sp^3 , sp
    (D) sp , sp^3 , sp^2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Hybridization of orbitals of N atom in ${\text{NO}}_3^ - $, ${\text{NO}}_2^ + $ and ${\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{4}}}^ + $are sp^2, sp, sp^3 which can be explained by their Lewis structures. The empty p- orbitals of N take part in hybridization.

Q7. Among the following, the maximum covalent character is shown by the compound is:
    (A) SnCl_2
    (B) MgCl_2
    (C) AlCl_3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) FeCl_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Few ionic bonds have partial covalent characteristics which were first discussed by a scientist, Kazimierz Fajans in 1923. He gave the rule to predict whether a chemical bond will be covalent or ionic which is now commonly known as Fajan’s rule. The rule can be stated as:
 Size of the ion: Smaller the size of cation, larger the size of anion, greater is the covalent character of the ionic bond.
 Charge of Cation: Greater the charge of cation, greater is the covalent character of the ionic bond.
 Electronic configuration- For cations with the same charge and size, the one, with (n-1)d^nns^​​​0 which is found in transition elements, has greater covalent character than the cation with ns^2np^6 electronic configuration, which is commonly found in alkali or alkaline earth metals.
Keeping these rules in mind, we can say that AlCl_​​​3 has a high covalent character.

Q8. Which one of the following is paramagnetic?
    (A) NO   <-- CORRECT
    (B) O_3
    (C) N_2
    (D) CO
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The number of electrons in Nitrogen is 7 and in oxygen is 8. Hence the number of electrons that would be present in the molecular orbitals in NO is 7 + 8 = 15. As the number of electrons is odd, all the electrons in the NO molecule cannot be paired. Hence, a single electron would be present in a $\pi$*2p orbital. Therefore NO is an odd electron species and the gas is hence paramagnetic due to the presence of unpaired electron.

Q9. Hybridization of C_2 and C_3 of H_3C - CH = C = Ch - CH_3 are:
    (A) sp, sp^3
    (B) sp^2, sp   <-- CORRECT
    (C) sp^2 , sp^2
    (D) sp, sp
    Answer: B
    Explanation: C_2 is sp^2 while C_3 is sp (a special case of allenes).

Q10. The ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{3}}}{{\text{d}}^{\text{2}}}$ hybridization of central atom of a molecule would lead to
    (A) Trigonal bipyramidal geometry
    (B) Octahedral geometry   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Tetrahedral geometry
    (D) square planar geometry
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In sp^3d^2 Hybridization one s, three p and two d-orbitals get hybridized to form six sp^3d^2 hybrid orbitals which adopt octahedral arrangement as given in image below

Q11. The state of hybridization of the central atom and the number of lone pairs over the central atom in POCl_3 are:
    (A) sp^2, 0
    (B) sp, 0
    (C) dsp^2, 1
    (D) sp^3, 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: 4$\sigma$ bonds are present without any lone pair of electrons so sp^3 hybridisation.

Q12. When ${{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$ is converted into ${{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}^ + $
    (A) bond order decreases
    (B) paramagnetic character decreases and the bond order increases   <-- CORRECT
    (C) paramagnetic character increases
    (D) both paramagnetic character and bond order increase
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For O_2: $\sigma$1s^2, $\sigma$*1s^2, $\sigma$2s^2, $\sigma$*2s^2, $\sigma$2pz^2 
($\pi$2py^2 = $\pi$2px^2), ($\pi$*2py^1 = $\pi$*2px^1)$\sigma$*2pz
For O_2: $\sigma$1s^2, $\sigma$*1s^2, $\sigma$2s^2, $\sigma$*2s^2, $\sigma$2pz^2 
($\pi$2py^2 = $\pi$2px^2), ($\pi$*2py^1 = $\pi$*2px^0)$\sigma$*2pz
Bond order = $N_b-N_a\over 2 $
For O_2 = $10-6\over 2$ = 2
For O_2^+ = $10-5\over 2$= 2.5

Q13. Which one of the following conversions involve change in both hybridization and shape?
    (A) ${\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} \to {\text{ N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{4}}}^ + $
    (B) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{4}}} \to {\text{ }}{{\text{C}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{6}}}$
    (C) ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} \to {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{{\text{O}}^ + }$
    (D) ${\text{B}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{3}}} \to {\text{ B}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{4}}}^-$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: BF_3 has sp^2 hybridization and its shape is a triangular planar. While BF_4^- has sp^3 hybridization and shape is tetrahedral.

Q14. Based on VSEPR theory, the number of 90^0 F — Br — F angles in BrF_5 is:
    (A) 2
    (B) 8
    (C) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The steric number of BrF_5 is 6. So the geometry is octahedral. It will have 5 bps and one lp which is present in the axial position. Because of distortion caused by lp, there is no 90^o F—Br—F bond angle in BrF_5.

Q15. The species having pyramidal shape is:
    (A) SF_2O   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $SiO_3^{2-}$
    (C) SO_3
    (D) BrF_3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: SF_2O has pyramidal shape as it is sp^3 hybridised and it has 3bp and 1 lp.
