Q1. For a stable molecule the value of bond order must be:
    (A) positive   <-- CORRECT
    (B) negative
    (C) there is no relationship between stability and bond order
    (D) zero
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Bond order $\propto $ Stability
Hence, for a stable molecule, the value of bond order must be positive. When bond order is zero and negative the molecule will not exist.

Q2. In acetylene molecule, between the carbon atoms there are
    (A) two sigma and one pi bonds
    (B) three pi bonds
    (C) three sigma bonds
    (D) one sigma and two pi bonds   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Acetylene is C_2H_2.
C atoms are bound with triple bond i.e. 1 sigma and 2 pie bonds.

Q3. In ${\text{PO}}_4^{3 - }$ ion the formal charge on the oxygen atom of P–O bond is
    (A) + 0.75
    (B) -1
    (C) + 1
    (D) – 0.75   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Formal change = $\frac{Total \ charge}{no.\ of\ o-atom}$
= $\frac {-3}4$ = -0.75

Q4. Which molecule/ion out of the following does not contain unpaired electrons?
    (A) ${{\text{B}}_2}$
    (B) ${\text{N}}_2^ + $
    (C) ${\text{O}}_2^{2 - }$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${{\text{O}}_2}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: There is no unpaired electrons.

Q5. In which of the following substances will hydrogen bond be strongest?
    (A) H_2O   <-- CORRECT
    (B) HCl
    (C) HI
    (D) H_2S
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Out of all H_2O will form strongest hydrogen bonding due to high electronegativity of O.

Q6. When a gas phase atom in its ground state gains an electron, this is called ______.
    (A) Electron gain enthalpy   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Electron affinity
    (C) Ionization enthalpy
    (D) Lattice enthalpy
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When a gas-phase atom in its ground state gains an electron, this is called Electron gain enthalpy.

Q7. Which of the following angle corresponds to sp^2 hybridisation?
    (A) 120°   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 180°
    (C) 90°
    (D) 109°
    Answer: A
    Explanation: sp^2 hybridisation have triangular planar structure so bond angle is 120^o

Q8. Which of the following statement is not correct from the view point of molecular orbital theory?
    (A) Bond strength of N_2 is maximum amongst the homonuclear diatomic molecules belonging to the second period.
    (B) Be_2 is not a stable molecule
    (C) $\sigma 2 s<\sigma^{*} 2 s<\sigma 2 p_{2}<\left(\pi 2 p_{x}=\pi 2 p_{y}\right)<\left(\pi^{*} 2 p_{x}=\pi^{*} 2 p_{y}\right)<\sigma^{*} 2 p_{z}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) He_2 is not stable but He^2+is expected to exist.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The correct order of energies of molecular orbitals in N_2 molecule $\sigma 2 s<\sigma^{*} 2 s<\sigma 2 p_{2}<\left(\pi 2 p_{x}=\pi 2 p_{y}\right)<\left(\pi^{*} 2 p_{x}=\pi^{*} 2 p_{y}\right)<\sigma^{*} 2 p_{z}$

Q9. The electronic configuration of the outer most shell of the most electronegative element is
    (A) 5s^25^5
    (B) 4s^24p^5
    (C) 3s^23p^5
    (D) 2s^22p^5   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Most electronegative element is F. Its atomic number is 9. So electronic configuration is 2s^22p^5.

Q10. Using MO theory predicts which of the following species has the shortest bond length?
    (A) ${\text{O}}_2^ + $
    (B) ${\text{O}}_2^{2 - }$
    (C) ${\text{O}}_2^ - $
    (D) $O_2^{2 + }$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Bond length is inversely proportional to bond order. $O_2^{2 + }$ has highest bond order as electrons are removed from antibonding MO.

Q11. Which one of the following pairs of species has the same bond order?
    (A) NO^+and CN^+
    (B) CN^- and NO^+   <-- CORRECT
    (C) CN^- and CN^+
    (D) ${{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}^ - $and CN^-
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Bond order=${n_b−n_a\over 2}$
In CN^-, there are 8 bonding electrons and 2 antibonding electrons,
Therefore B.O.=$8−2\over 2$ = 3
NO^+ has 10 electrons, a triple bond between N and O, and two pairs, one on each atom. This means that both N and O follow the octet rule. The bond order is 3.

Q12. Which of the following attain the linear structure?
    (A) BeCl_2 and PCl_5
    (B) CS_2 and IF_5
    (C) BeCl_2 and CS_2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) BeCl_2 and NO_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Molecular geometry is determined by the hybridization of the central atom. In CS_2 the carbon atom is surrounded by two regions of electron density, one for each double bond it forms with the sulfur atoms. The molecular geometry will thus be linear, the basic AX_2 model.
The molecular geometry of BeCl_2 is linear with symmetric charge distribution around the central atom.

Q13. CO is isoelectronic with:
    (A) $NO_2^ - $ and SnCl_2
    (B) ${\text{N}}{{\text{O}}^ + }$and N_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) SnCl_2 and NO^+
    (D) N_2 and ${\text{SnC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: CO, N_2, and NO^+ have same number of electrons = 14.

Q14. Which of the following species have the same shape?
    (A) O_3 and N${\text{O}}_2^ - $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) CCl_4 and $NO_2^ - $
    (C) O_3 and CO_2
    (D) $ NO_2^ - $ and CCl_4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: O_3 and NO_2^- have same shape i.e planar.

Q15. Hydrogen bonds are formed in many compounds e.g., H_2O, HF, NH_3. The boiling point of such compounds depends to a large extent on the strength of the hydrogen bond and the number of hydrogen bonds. The correct decreasing order of the boiling points of the above compounds is:
    (A) ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} > {\text{ HF }} > {\text{ N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${\text{HF }} > {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} > {\text{ N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$
    (C) ${\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} > {\text{ HF }} > {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
    (D) ${\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} > {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} > {\text{ HF}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The smaller the size of the atom, the greater is the electronegativity, and hence stronger is the H−bonding. Thus, the order of strength of H-bonding is HF > H_2O > NH_3. 
But each HF molecule is linked only to two other HF molecules while each H2​O molecule is linked to four other H2​O molecules through H−bonding.
Hence, the decreasing order of boiling points is H_2​O > HF > NH_3.

Q1. Polarity in a molecule and hence the dipole moment depends primarily on electronegativity of the constituent atoms and shape of a molecule. Which of the following has the highest dipole moment?
    (A) HI
    (B) CO_2
    (C) H_2O   <-- CORRECT
    (D) SO_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Because of presence of lp on head of O atom in H_2O therefore it has max dipole moment.

Q2. The types of hybrid orbitals of nitrogen in ${\text{NO}}_2^ + $, ${\text{NO}}_3^ - $ and $N{\text{H}}_4^ + $ respectively are expected to be
    (A) sp, ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{2}}}$ and ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{3}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{2}}}$, ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{3}}}$and sp.
    (C) sp, ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{3}}}$and ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{2}}}$
    (D) ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{2}}}$, sp and ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{3}}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In NO_2^+
 Number of electron pairs =2
 Number of bond pairs = 2
 Number of lone pair = 0
 So, the species is linear with sp hybridisation.
 In $NO_3^− $
 Number of electron pairs =3
 Number of bond pairs = 3
 Number of lone pair = 0
 So, the species is trigonal planar with sp​​​​2 hybridisation
 In $NH_4^+$
 Number of electron pairs =4
 Number of bond pairs = 4
 Number of lone pair = 0
 So, the species is tetrahedral with sp^3 hybridisation.

Q3. Isostructural species are those which have the same shape and hybridisation. Among the given species identify the isostructural pairs.
    (A) [NH_3 and $NO_3^ -$ ]
    (B) [$BF_4^ -$ and $NH_4^ +$ ]   <-- CORRECT
    (C) [BCl_3and BrCl_3]
    (D) [ NF_3 and BF_3 ]
    Answer: B
    Explanation: BF_4^- and NH_4^+ both have sp^3 hybridisation.

Q4. In ${\text{NO}}_3^ - $ ion, the number of bond pairs and lone pairs of electrons on nitrogen atom are
    (A) 2, 2
    (B) 1, 3
    (C) 3, 1
    (D) 4, 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The nitrate ion is formed by the loss of the hydrogen ion, and so its structure is:
Around the central nitrogen there are 4 pairs of shared electrons, and no remaining lone pair. The original lone pair has now become a bonding pair. Two of those pairs make up a double bond.

Q5. Amongst the following elements whose electronic configurations are given below, the one having the highest ionisation enthalpy is
    (A) $[Ne]3s^23p^2$
    (B) $[Ne]3s^23p^1$
    (C) $[Ar]3d^{10}4s^24p^3$
    (D) $[Ne]3s^23p^3$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $[Ne]3s^23p^3$ and $[Ar]3d^{10}4s^24p^3$ both have stable half-filled configuration but in $[Ne]3s^23p^3$ the atomic radii are smaller than $[Ar]3d^{10}4s^24p^3$. So ionization enthalpy of $[Ne]3s^23p^3$ is highest amongst all.

Q6. Species having same bond order are:
    (A) ${\text{F}}_2^ + $ and ${\text{O}}_2^ - $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${{\text{N}}_2}$ and ${\text{N}}_2^ - $
    (C) ${\text{O}}_2^ - $ and ${\text{N}}_2^ - $
    (D) ${\text{F}}_2^ + $ and ${\text{N}}_2^ + $
    Answer: A
    Explanation: bond order of F_2^+ and O_2^- is same i.e 1.5

Q7. Which of the following statements are not correct?
    (A) In canonical structures, there is no difference in the arrangement of atoms.
    (B) NaCl being an ionic compound is a good conductor of electricity in the solid state.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Hybrid orbitals form stronger bonds than pure orbitals.
    (D) VSEPR Theory can explain the square planar geometry of XeF_4.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: NaCl is not a good conductor in solid-state. NaCl is a good conductor of electricity only in their molten state or in aqueous solution.

Q8. Rank the bonds in the set C=O, C-O, C $ \equiv $ O in order of decreasing bond length.
    (A) C-O > C=O > C $ \equiv $ O   <-- CORRECT
    (B) C $ \equiv $ O < C-O < C=O
    (C) C=O > C $ \equiv $ O > C-O
    (D) C-O > C $ \equiv $ O > C=O
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The length of the bond is determined by the number of bonded electrons (the bond order). The higher the bond order, the stronger the pull between the two atoms and the shorter the bond length. Generally, the length of the bond between two atoms is approximately the sum of the covalent radii of the two atoms. CO has a triple bond so has minimum bond length.

Q9. Rank the bonds in the set C=O, C-O, C$ \equiv $O in order of decreasing bond strength.
    (A) C$ \equiv $O > C-O < C=O
    (B) C$ \equiv $O > C=O > C-O   <-- CORRECT
    (C) C=O < C$ \equiv $O > C-O
    (D) C-O < C$ \equiv $O > C=O
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The more bonds between atoms, the shorter the bond is. For example, a triple bond will be shorter than a double bond. The shorter the bond is the stronger it is (higher dissociation energy). Bond order is basically the number of bonds between atoms, so a larger number bond order=more bonds=shorter bonds=stronger bonds. i.e., C$ \equiv $O > C=O > C-O.

Q10. Quartz is very hard and melts at 1550°C. Reason is:
    (A) Quartz (SiO_2) has silicon-oxygen covalent bonds that extend throughout the sample   <-- CORRECT
    (B) separate SiO_2 molecules exist that are held together by pi bonds that extend in three dimensions throughout the sample
    (C) Quartz (SiO_2) has silicon-oxygen electrovalent bonds that extend throughout the sample
    (D) separate SiO_2 molecules exist they are held together by coordinate bonds that extend throughout the sample
    Answer: A
    Explanation: It's because quartz has a network of covalent bonds which means that they are covalently bonded in a network solid. The many covalent bonds must be broken which is why they have very high melting points.

Q11. Rank the following bonds in order of increasing polarity: H-N, H-O, H-C.
    (A) H-O < H-N < H-C
    (B) H - C < H-O < H-N.
    (C) H-N < H-O < H-C
    (D) H-C < H-N < H-O.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: O is more electronegative than N which is more electronegative than C.

Q12. The electronegativity difference $\left( {\Delta {\text{EN}}} \right)$ is large in one of the following:
    (A) Metal and a Nonmetal   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Two nonmetals
    (C) Two metals
    (D) Hydrogen and Helium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Metals are electropositive in nature as they easily lose electrons, so they are reducing agents. On the contrary, Non-metals are electronegative because they gain electrons and thus they are oxidizing agents.

Q13. N_2, CO and NO^+ are isoelectronic molecules. Their respective bond order is :
    (A) 3,3,3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1,1,3
    (C) 2,3,3
    (D) 2,3,4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Total number of electrons in the N_2 molecule is 7+ 7= 14.
As per the formula Bonded pair of electrons N_b: $σ1s^2\ σ2s^2\ {tex}\pi$2p_y^2\ $\pi$2p_z^2\ σ 2p_x^2{/tex}
Total 10 electrons.
Anti bond pairs of electrons N_a: $σ 1s*^2\ σ 2s*^2$ Total 4 electrons.
Bond Order (B.O.) = ${N_b-N_a\over 2} ={ 10-4\over 2} = 3 $
Similarly, the bond order of CO and NO^+ is 3.

Q14. Bond order of ${\text{O}}_2^ + $ and ${\text{O}}_2^ - $ are:
    (A) 3.2 and 2.5
    (B) 2.5 and 1. 5   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2.4 and 1.3
    (D) 1.1 and 2.5
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The electronic configuration of the O_2^+ ion containing 15 electrons can be written as: $\sigma $1s^2< $\sigma $*1s^2< $\sigma $2s^2< $\sigma $*2s^2< $\sigma $2p_z^2 < ($\pi $2p_x^2= $\pi $2p_y^2) < ($\pi $*2p_x^1= $\pi $*2p_y) < $\sigma $*2p_z
The bond order can be found as:
B.O = $N_b-N_a\over 2$
N_b= Number of electrons in the bonding orbitals = 10
N_a = Number of electron in the anti-bonding orbitals = 5
B.O = ^${10-5\over 2 }= {5\over 2 }$= 2.5
The electronic configuration of the O_2^- ion containing 17 electrons can be written as: $\sigma $1s^2< $\sigma $*1s^2< $\sigma $2s^2< $\sigma $*2s^2< $\sigma $2p_z^2 < ($\pi $2p_x^2 = $\pi $2p_y^2) < ($\pi $*2p_x^2= $\pi $*2p_y^1) < σ*2p_z
The bond order can be calculated as: B.O = ${10-7\over 2} ={ 3\over 2}$= 1.5

Q15. NaCl does not conduct electricity in the ____________ but do conduct it when melted.
    (A) molten state
    (B) when kept at low temperatures
    (C) solid state   <-- CORRECT
    (D) when dissolved in water
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The essential requirement for conducting electricity is the presence of free electrons or mobile/free ions. Sodium chloride in the solid-state is closely packed by the strong electrostatic force of attraction and the ions are immobile. Therefore as there is no mobile ions conduction of electricity is not possible. But ionic compounds in molten state ions have enough energy to break the electrostatic forces of attraction and become mobile therefore conduct electricity.

States of Matter CBSE Online Test 01  (id 951) [FREE]

Q1. Which are three important states of matter?
    (A) Solid, Liquid, and Gas   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Atoms, Molecules, and Ions
    (C) Solid, Glasses, and Gases
    (D) Solid, Liquid, and Plasma
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Three phases of matter are:
 Solid - firm and stable in shape; not liquid or fluid, strongest intermolecular forces.
 Liquid - A liquid is a nearly incompressible fluid that conforms to the shape of its container but retains a (nearly) constant volume independent of pressure. Intermediate molecular forces. 
 Gas -Takes the volume of the container, weakest intermolecular forces.

Q2. Physical behavior of the states differs greatly even though chemical behavior of the three states is identical because chemical properties depends upon?
    (A) intermolecular non bonding forces whereas physical properties depend on intermolecular bonding forces.
    (B) non bonding forces whereas physical properties depend on intermolecular bonding forces.
    (C) intramolecular bonding forces whereas physical properties depend on intermolecular Non-bonding forces.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) covalent bonding forces whereas physical properties depend on energy supplied.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The question is based on the understanding of how the forces operate in a molecule. It is known that chemical properties depend on intramolecular bonding forces (holding the atoms in a molecule together), whereas physical properties depend on intermolecular non-bonding force (such as different kinds of polar interactions holding the molecules together).

Q3. The Dipole-dipole forces act between molecules that have:
    (A) a permanent magnetic dipole moment.
    (B) an induced electrical dipole moment.
    (C) a permanent electrical dipole moment.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) an electron cloud that causes temporary dipoles.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The dipole-dipole forces act between molecules that have a permanent electrical dipole moment, the partial charge of one molecule get attracted to the opposite charge of another molecule.

Q4. Which of the following statements about Hydrogen bond incorrect?
    (A) In hydrogen bonding, the H atom becomes partially positive and is attracted to the more negative N atom.
    (B) In hydrogen bonding, the H atom becomes partially negative and is attracted to the more positive N atom.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) In hydrogen bonding, the H atom becomes partially positive and is attracted to the more negative O atom.
    (D) In hydrogen bonding, the H atom becomes partially positive and is attracted to the more negative F atom.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Hydrogen atom covalently bonded to highly electronegative atom such as N, O experience the electrostatic field of another highly electronegative atom due to which a partial positive charge is developed on H atom.

Q5. The intermolecular force primarily responsible for the condensed states of nonpolar substances is the:
    (A) dipole-dipole attraction.
    (B) hydrogen bond.
    (C) dispersion force (or London force)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ion-dipole forces.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The intermolecular force primarily responsible for the condensed states of nonpolar substances is the dispersion force (or London force).

Q6. The average kinetic energy and thermal energy are proportional to:
    (A) Pressure
    (B) Specific heat
    (C) Absolute temperature   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Volume
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The average KE and Thermal energy are proportional to absolute temperature.
The kinetic energy is the amount of motion in the atoms and molecules of a substance. The molecules of the gas gain energy as the temperature increases as there is more motion of the molecules. As the temperature decreases the motion lessens until at absolute zero all motion (kinetic energy) stops.

Q7. Three states of matter are the result of?
    (A) The balance between intermolecular forces and the intramolecular binding energy of the molecules.
    (B) The balance between Van Der Waals forces and the London forces.
    (C) The balance between intermolecular forces and the thermal energy of the molecules.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The balance between Hydrogen bonding forces and the London forces.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Three states of matter are the result of a balance between intermolecular forces and the thermal energy of the molecules. These two factors differentiate them from each other. For understanding, the strongest intermolecular forces are in solid than in liquid and weakest in gases.

Q8. Gases have a much lower density than the solids and liquids because:
    (A) Gases do not have intermolecular forces that attract each molecule to another.
    (B) Gases contain lower specific enthalpy than solids.
    (C) Thermal energy overcomes on the attractive intermolecular forces.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Distance between the molecules is small compared to solids.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In gases, molecules are far apart from each other, thermal energy which is a measure of freeness of motion is thus very high resulting in a very large volume for the same mass (compared to solid and liquid). Hence there density is the lowest.

Q9. At constant temperature, the pressure of a fixed amount (i.e., number of moles n) of gas is:
    (A) Varies inversely with its volume.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Varies as square of its volume.
    (C) Is constant irrespective of volume.
    (D) Varies directly with its volume.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: From ideal gas equation PV = nRT,
keeping n and T fixed,
P $\alpha$ $\frac{1}{V}$. (Boyles Law)
Here, T = Temperature
P = Pressure
$\alpha$ = sign of Proportionality
V = Volume
n = number of moles of gas
R = Universal gas constant

Q10. Charles’ law states that pressure remaining constant, the volume of a fixed mass of a gas is?
    (A) Constant irrespective of its absolute temperature.
    (B) Directly proportional to square of absolute temperature.
    (C) Directly proportional to its absolute temperature.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Inversely proportional to its absolute temperature.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: According to Charles law, At constant pressure, the volume of a given mass of a gas increases or decreases by $\frac{1}{273}$ of its volume at 0^oC for each one-degree rise or fall in temperature. Therefore at constant pressure, volume of given mass of gas is directly proportional to absolute temperature.
Mathematically; 
$V\,=kT$ (at contant P)

Q11. Gay Lussac’s law states that at constant volume, the pressure of a fixed amount of gas:
    (A) Directly proportional to the square of absolute temperature.
    (B) Constant irrespective of its absolute temperature.
    (C) Varies directly with the temperature.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Varies inversely with the temperature.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The question is based on the statement of Gay Lussac’s law- “At constant temperature, the pressure of a given mass of a gas is directly proportional to its absolute temperature.”
Mathematically; 
$P\alpha T$ (at constant temperature)
or $\frac{P}{T}$ = constant

Q12. According to __________ equal volumes of all gases at the same temperature and pressure contain an equal number of molecules.
    (A) Graham's Law
    (B) Dalton's Law
    (C) Avogadro's Law   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Charle's Law.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: This question is based on the statement of Avogadro's law that states 'equal volumes of all gases under the same conditions of temperature and pressure contain an equal number of molecules'.
V $\propto$ n (at constant T and P)

Q13. Which of the following is the correct ideal gas law?
    (A) pV = nT
    (B) pV = 2nR
    (C) pV = nRT   <-- CORRECT
    (D) pV = 2RT
    Answer: C
    Explanation: PV = nRT is the correct Ideal Gas equation.
Here, P: Pressure
V: Volume
n: Number of Moles
R: Universal Gas Constant
T: Temperature

Q14. CO_2 can be easily liquified and even solidified because
    (A) It has comparatively more force of attraction than other gases   <-- CORRECT
    (B) It is present in atmosphere
    (C) It has weak forces of attraction
    (D) It has more intermolecular space
    Answer: A
    Explanation: It has comparatively more force of attraction than other gases

Q15. Dalton’s Law of Partial Pressures states that the total pressure exerted by the mixture of non-reactive gases is equal to the:
    (A) the difference in the partial pressures of individual gases.
    (B) sum of the partial pressures of individual gases.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) maximum of the partial pressures of individual gases.
    (D) average of the partial pressures of individual gases.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The Dalton Law of Partial pressures for Gases states that total pressure exerted by a mixture of non-reacting gases is equal to the sum of the partial pressure of individual gases.

States of Matter CBSE Online Test 02  (id 952) [PAID]

Q1. In the kinetic molecular theory attraction between molecules of the gas is:
    (A) greater zero
    (B) zero   <-- CORRECT
    (C) depends on the speed of the molecule
    (D) less than zero
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The Kinetic Theory of Gases assumes that no intermolecular forces exert between the gas molecules.

Q2. Real gases show deviations from ideal gas law because
    (A) molecules interact with each other.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) molecules repel each other.
    (C) size of molecules cannot be measured.
    (D) of experimental errors.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Real gases have intermolecular forces of interaction due to which there is a difference in the actual pressure values when compared to the ideal gases, the pressure is found to be less than the pressure of ideal gases under similar conditions, similar deviation occurs when the size of molecules is taken into account due to which volume correction is required.

Q3. Which is the correct form of van der Waals equation?
    (A) $\left( {p + \frac{{a{n^2}}}{{{V^2}}}} \right)\left( {V - nb} \right) = nRT$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\left( {p - \frac{{a{n^2}}}{{{V^2}}}} \right)\left( {V + nb} \right) = nRT$
    (C) $\left( {p + \frac{{a{n^2}}}{{{V^2}}}} \right)\left( {V + nb} \right) = nRT$
    (D) $\left( {p - \frac{{a{n^2}}}{{{V^2}}}} \right)\left( {V - nb} \right) = nRT$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\left( {p + \frac{{a{n^2}}}{{{V^2}}}} \right)\left( {V - nb} \right) = nRT$ is van der Waals gas equation of real gases for 'n' moles of gas.

Q4. The deviation from ideal behavior can be measured in terms of compressibility factor Z, which is
    (A) Z = $ \frac{{pV}}{{nRT}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Z = $ \frac{V}{{nRT}}$
    (C) Z = $ \frac{{pV}}{{RT}}$
    (D) Z = $ \frac{{pV}}{{nR}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Z = $ \frac{{pV}}{{nRT}}$ is a correction factor which describes the deviation of real gas from ideal gas behaviour. It is defined as the ratio of the molar volume of a gas to the molar volume of an ideal gas at the same temperature and pressure.

Q5. The behaviour of the gas becomes more ideal when:
    (A) Pressure is very high
    (B) Number of moles is very low
    (C) Pressure is very low   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Temperature is very low
    Answer: C
    Explanation: This question is based on understanding the concept of molecular interactions between a molecule of real gases which is least at low P and High T conditions. Thus under these conditions real gases behave as ideal.

Q6. Critical temperature (T_C) of carbon dioxide is the highest temperature at which liquid carbon dioxide is observed. Above this temperature it is ________.
    (A) Mixture of solid and liquid
    (B) Gas   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Solid
    (D) Liquid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: T_c is the highest temperature where gas can exist in a liquid state. Above this, no liquid state exists. It is impossible to compress the gas into liquid above the critical temperature, no matter whatever amount of pressure is applied.

Q7. Above the Critical temperature (T_C) of carbon dioxide, what happens?
    (A) Increase of pressure makes.
    (B) Liquefaction of the gas is not possible.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Liquefaction of the gas is possible.
    (D) Solidification of the gas is possible.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: T_c is the highest temperature where gas can exist in a liquid state. Above this, no liquid state exists hence it is not possible to liquefy the gas no matter what pressure is applied.

Q8. The three states of matter of H_2O are in equilibrium:
    (A) Steam point
    (B) Critical point
    (C) Ice point
    (D) The triple point   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The triple point of a substance is the temperature and pressure at which three phases (i.e. gas, liquid and solid) of that substance coexist at thermal equilibrium.
The triple point of pure water is at 0.01°C (273.16K, 32.01°F) and 4.58 mm (611.2Pa) of mercury, where all the three (i.e., solid, liquid and gas) states coexist in equilibrium.

Q9. Surface tension decreases as the temperature is raised because increase in temperature
    (A) decreases the kinetic energy of the molecules and the effectiveness of intermolecular attraction is not changed.
    (B) decreases the kinetic energy of the molecules and the effectiveness of intermolecular attraction decreases.
    (C) increases the kinetic energy of the molecules and the effectiveness of intermolecular attraction increases.
    (D) increases the kinetic energy of the molecules and the effectiveness of intermolecular attraction decreases.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Surface tension is inversely proportional to the temperature. So surface tension decreases with rising temperature. With the rise in temperature liquids expands, the interparticle distance increases, and the kinetic energy of molecules and hence disorder decreases, so intermolecular forces decrease results in a decrease in surface tension.

Q10. Viscous force is directly proportional to
    (A) velocity gradient and inversely proportional to area.
    (B) area and velocity gradient.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) area and inversely proportional to velocity gradient.
    (D) velocity gradient squared and inversely proportional to area.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Viscous force is directly proportional to area and velocity gradient.
We have,
${F_\upsilon } = \eta A(dV/dH)$
where A = Area
We have, dV/dH = velocity gradient
$\eta = Coefficient\;of\;viscocity$

Q11. Water has high surface tension and high capillarity because of _______.
    (A) ionic bonds
    (B) hydrogen bonds   <-- CORRECT
    (C) covalent bonds
    (D) dispersion forces
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In water molecules, due to high electronegativity difference between H and O atoms and lone pairs of electrons on oxygen atom, a greater number of hydrogen bonds formed.

Q12. What will be the minimum pressure required to compress 500 dm^3 of air at 1 bar to 200 dm^3 at 30°C?
    (A) 2.5 bar   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3.5 bar
    (C) 2.0 bar
    (D) 1.5 bar
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Using the ideal gas equation, PV = nRT,
Since T is constant, we have
P_1V_1 = P_2V_2 i.e.
500 dm^3 $\times$ 1 bar = 200 dm^3 $\times$ P_2
Which gives P_2 = 2.5 bar

Q13. A vessel of 120 mL capacity contains a certain amount of gas at 35°C and 1.2 bar pressure. The gas is transferred to another vessel of volume 180 mL at 35°C. What would be its pressure?
    (A) 2.8 bar
    (B) 0.4 bar
    (C) 0.8 bar   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1.8 bar
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Case I PV = nRT; n = $ \frac{{PV}}{{RT}}$
Here P = 1.2bar; V = 120ml and T = 308K.
Here n = $ \;\frac{{1.2 \times 120}}{{R \times (308)}} = \frac{{0.46}}{R}$
CaseII PV = nRT; P = $\frac{{nRT}}{V}$
here V = 180ml T = 308K and P = $ \frac{{0.46\; \times \;R\; \times \;308}}{{R \times \;180\;}}$ = 0.8bar

Q14. At 0°C, the density of a certain oxide of a gas at 2 bar is the same as that of dinitrogen at 5 bar. What is the molecular mass of the oxide?
    (A) 70 g/mol   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 90 g/mol
    (C) 170 g/mol
    (D) 270 g/mol
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Using relation; PV = ($\frac{m}{M}$)RT
we have
P_1M_1 = P_2M_2
P1 = $ \frac{{{P_2}{M_2}}}{{{M_1}}} = \frac{{5 \times 28}}{2}$ = 70 g/mol

Q15. Pressure of 1 g of an ideal gas A at 27°C is found to be 2 bar. When 2 g of another ideal gas B is introduced in the same flask at same temperature the pressure becomes 3 bar. Relationship between their molecular masses is:
    (A) M_B = 10M_A
    (B) M_B = 5M_A
    (C) M_B = 2M_A
    (D) M_B = 4M_A   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: using realtion, PV = ($\frac{m}{M}$)RT
P of 1g an ideal gas at 27 °C = 2 bar
P of 2g another ideal gas in same flask = 3 bar
pressure due to B P_total - P_A= 3 - 2 = 1bar. Now using relation,
$P = \frac{{mRT}}{{MV}}$
2 = $ \frac{{1RT}}{{{M_A}V}}$ .... (1)
1 = $ \frac{{2RT}}{{{M_B}V}}$ .... (2)
now, (1)/(2), we get
$\frac{2}{1} = \frac{{{M_B}}}{{2{M_A}}}$
M_B = 4M_A

Q1. The drain cleaner, Drainex contains small bits of aluminum which react with caustic soda to produce dihydrogen. What volume of dihydrogen at 20°C and one bar will be released when 0.15g of aluminum reacts?
    (A) 108.2 mL
    (B) 252.5 mL
    (C) 202.5 mL   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 302.5 mL
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {2Al + 2NaOH + 2{H_2}O}&{ \to 2NaAl{O_2} + 3{H_2}} \\ \begin{gathered} 2 \times 27 \hfill \\ 0.15g \hfill \\ \end{gathered} &\begin{gathered} 3mol \hfill \\ ? \hfill \\ \end{gathered} \end{array}$
Moles of $Al = \frac{{0.15}}{{27}} = $ 0.0055 moles
2 mole of Al produces 3 moles of H_2
so 0.0055 moles of AL will produce ${\frac{3}{2}\;}$$\times$ 0.0055 = 0.00825 moles of H_2
Now PV = nRT where n = 0.00825, P = 1 bar and T = 293K.
$V_{H_2}\;=\frac{0.00825\;\times0.0821\;\times\;293\;}{1\times0.987}=$ 0.2025dm^3 = 202.5mL

Q2. What will be the pressure exerted by a mixture of 3.2 g of methane and 4.4 g of carbon dioxide contained in a 9 dm^3 flask at 27°C?
    (A) 7.452 $\times$ 10^4 Pa
    (B) 9.313 $\times$ 10^4 Pa
    (C) 6.224 $\times$ 10^4 Pa
    (D) 8.314 $\times$ 10^4 Pa   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Acc. to Daltons Law
P = P_1 + P_2
and by applying PV = nRT
P_1 $\times$ 9 = 0.2 $\times$ RT and P_2 $\times$ 9 = 0.1 $\times$ RT where T = 300K
now using P = P_1 + P_2
P = P1 + P2 = $\frac{{(0.2 + 0.1)}}{9} \times RT = \frac{{(0.2 + 0.1)}}{9} \times \frac{{0.0821 \times 300}}{1} $= 0.82 atm 
P = 0.82 atm = 0.82 $\times$ 101325 = 83086.5 pa = 8.3 $\times$ 10^4 Pa

Q3. What will be the pressure of the gaseous mixture when 0.5 L of ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}$ at 0.8 bar and 2.0 L of dioxygen at 0.7 bar are introduced in a 1L vessel at ${\text{27}}^\circ {\text{C}}$ ?
    (A) 3.7 bar
    (B) 0.8 bar
    (C) 2.6 bar
    (D) 1.8 bar   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Here, ${P_{{H_2}}} \times 1 = 0.8 \times 0.5$ =0.40 bar
${P_{{O_2}}} \times 1 = 0.7 \times 2$ =1.4 bar
And by applying $P=\;P_{H_{2\;}}+P_{O_2}$= 0.40 +1.40 =1.80 bar

Q4. The density of a gas is found to be 5.46 g/dm^3 at 27°C at 2 bar pressure. What will be its density at STP?
    (A) 5g/dm^3
    (B) 2g/dm^3
    (C) 4g/dm^3
    (D) 3g/dm^3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: For the same gas at different temperature and presuure; ratio of densities is given by relation $\frac{\rho_1}{\rho_2}=\frac{P_1T_2}{P_2T_1}$
${\rho _1} = ?,{\rho _2} = 5.46,$ We have, P_1 = 1 bar, P_2 = 2bar, T_2 = 300K, T_1 = 273K
Putting values,$\rho_1=\frac{P_1\;T_2\;\rho_2}{P_2\;T_1}=\;\frac{1\times300\times5.46}{2\times273}=$ 3g/dm^3
$\rho_1$ = 3g/dm^3

Q5. 34.05 mL of phosphorus vapour weighs 0.0625 g at 546°C and 0.1 bar pressure. What is the molar mass of phosphorus? (in one decimal value)
    (A) 1325.9 g/mol
    (B) 1097.6 g/mol
    (C) 124.75 g/mol   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1120.3 g/mol
    Answer: C
    Explanation: PV = $ \frac{{mRT}}{M}$
M = $ \frac{{mRT}}{{PV}}$
M = $\frac{{0.0625g \times 0.083bar\;d{m^3}{K^{ - 1}}mo{l^{ - 1}} \times 819K}}{{0.1bar \times 34.05 \times {{10}^{ - 3}}d{m^3}}}$
The molar mass of phosphorus = 124.75g/mol

Q6. A student forgot to add the reaction mixture to the round-bottomed flask at 27°C, but instead, he/she placed the flask on the flame. After a lapse of time, he realized his mistake and using a pyrometer he found the temperature of the flask was 477 °C. What fraction of air would have been expelled out?
    (A) 0.67
    (B) 0.5
    (C) 0.42
    (D) 0.6   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Using ideal gas equation PV = nRT, at constant pressure and volume(here volume of the container remains constant as it is open to atmosphere)
n_1T_1 = n_2T_2
$\frac{{{n_2}}}{{{n_1}}} = \frac{{300}}{{750}} = 0.4$
This is the fraction of air remaining in a flask, so a fraction of air expelled out = 1 - 0.4 = 0.6

Q7. Calculate the temperature of 4.0 mol of a gas occupying 5 dm^3 at 3.32 bar. (R = 0.083 bar dm^3K^-1mol^-1).
    (A) 150 K
    (B) 310 K
    (C) 50 K   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 70 K
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have PV = nRT
or ${T = \;\frac{{PV}}{{nR}} = \;\frac{{\;3.22bar\; \times 5d{m^3}}}{{4mol\; \times 0.083bar\;d{m^3}{K^{ - 1}}\;mo{l^{ - 1}}}}}$ = 50K

Q8. Calculate the total number of electrons present in 1.4 g of dinitrogen gas.
    (A) 5.0832 $\times$ 10^23 electrons
    (B) 4.6329 $\times$ 10^23 electrons
    (C) 4.4521 $\times$ 10^23 electrons
    (D) 4.2154 $\times$ 10^23 electrons   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: moles of ${{N_2} = \frac{{1.4}}{{28}}\; = \;}$ 0.05 mol
And 1 mole of N_2 = 3.011 $\times$ 10^22 molecules of N_2
And 1 molecule of N_2 has 14 electrons
total number of electrons in 1.4 g of N_2 = 3.011 $\times$ 10^22 $\times$ 14 = 4.2154 $\times$ 10^23

Q9. Bose-Einstein Condensate have
    (A) Low kinetic energy
    (B) Highest kinetic energy.
    (C) Very low kinetic energy   <-- CORRECT
    (D) High kinetic energy
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Very low kinetic energy

Q10. The colour of vapours formed on sublimation of iodine solid is
    (A) Yellow
    (B) Purple (violet)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Orange
    (D) Colourless
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Purple (violet)

Q11. The payload is defined as the difference between the mass of displaced air and the mass of the balloon. Calculate the payload when a balloon of radius 10 m, mass 100 kg is filled with helium at 1.66 bar at 27°C. (Density of air = 1.2 kg m^-3 and R = 0.083 bar dm^3K^-1mol^-1)
    (A) 3807.6 kg   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3568.2 kg
    (C) 3345.2 kg
    (D) 3905.3 kg
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Volume of balloon, V = $ \frac{4}{3} \times (3.14) \times {r^3} $ = 4187 m^3
Mass of displaced air, m = V $\times $ $\rho$ = 4187 $\times$ 1.2 = 5024.4kg
Temperature, T = 300 K
Mass of He filled in balloon, m_He = $ \frac{{PVM}}{{RT}}\; = \;\frac{{1.66 \times 4187\; \times 4 \times {{10}^{ - 3}}}}{{0.083 \times 300}} $ = 1116.4 kg
Total Mass of filled balloon, m' = 100 + 1116.4 = 1216.4 kg
Payload = mass of displaced air - mass of balloon = 5024.04 - 1216.44 = 3807.6 kg

Q12. Calculate the volume occupied by 8.8 g of CO_2 at 31.1°C and 1 bar pressure. R = 0.083 bar dm^3K^-1mol^-1.
    (A) 6.35 L
    (B) 3.03 L
    (C) 4.25 L
    (D) 5.05 L   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: ${V\; = \frac{{wRT}}{{MP}}}$
${V = \;\frac{{8.8\; \times 0.083\; \times 304.1}}{{44 \times 1}} = 5.05L}$

Q13. 2.9 g of a gas at 95°C occupied the same volume as 0.184 g of dihydrogen at 17°C, at the same pressure. What is the molar mass of the gas?
    (A) 43 g mol^-1
    (B) 46 g mol^-1
    (C) 40 g mol^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 50 g mol^-1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We know that, ${PV = \frac{{mRT}}{M}}$
For unknown gas, P_1V_1 = ${\frac{{{m_1}R{T_1}}}{{{M_1}}}}$
For H_2 gas, P_2V_2${ = \frac{{{m_2}R{T_2}}}{{{M_2}}}}$
Here, P_1V_1 = P_2V_2
Hence, ${\frac{{{m_1}R{T_1}}}{{{M_1}}} = \frac{{{m_2}R{T_2}}}{{{M_2}}}\;}$
${ \Rightarrow \frac{{2.9\;g \times R \times 368K}}{{{M_1}}} = \frac{{0.184g\; \times R \times 290K}}{{2\;g/mol}}}$
$\Rightarrow$ Molar mass of unknown gas, M_1 = 40 g/mol

Q14. A mixture of dihydrogen and dioxygen at one bar pressure contains 20% by weight of dihydrogen. Calculate the partial pressure of dihydrogen.
    (A) 1.12 bar
    (B) 0.65 bar
    (C) 0.97 bar
    (D) 0.8 bar   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A mixture of H_2_ and O_2 contains 20% by weight of H_2 means H_2 = 20g and O_2 = 80g
moles of hydrogen, $n_{H_2}\;=\frac{20}2$ = 10 mol
moles of oxygen, $n_{O_2} = \frac{80}{32}$ = 2.5 mol
mole fraction of hydrogen,$\begin{array}{l}{x_H}_{{}_2\;}=\frac{n_{H_2}\;}{n_{H_2}+n_{O_2}}=\frac{10}{10+2.5}=\;0.8\\\end{array}$
partial pressure of H_2, $P_{H_2}=P_{Total}\times x_{H_2}=1bar\times0.8=0.8\;bar$

Q15. The vapor pressure of different substances at the same temperature increases if:
    (A) the intermolecular forces of the substance are strong.
    (B) the intermolecular forces of the substance are weak.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the molecules of the substance are ionic bonded.
    (D) the molecules of the substance are covalent bonded.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Vapour pressure of a substance is inversely proportional to the intermolecular forces between molecules.

Q1. A person living in Shimla observed that cooking food without using pressure cooker takes more time. The reason for this observation is that at high altitude:
    (A) temperature decreases
    (B) temperature increases
    (C) pressure increases
    (D) pressure decreases   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As we move to higher altitude, the atmospheric pressure decreases. Therefore, boiling point of water also decreases, hence , cooking of food takes longer time without using pressure cooker.

Q2. Which of the following property of water can be used to explain the spherical shape of rain droplets?
    (A) pressure
    (B) viscosity
    (C) surface tension   <-- CORRECT
    (D) critical phenomena
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Due to surface Tension, the water droplet tends to acquire minimum surface area, hence water droplet attains spherical shape.

Q3. A plot of volume (V) versus temperature (T) for a gas at constant pressure is a straight line passing through the origin. The plots at different values of pressure are shown in Figure. Which of the following order of pressure is correct for this gas?
    (A) p_1 > p_2 > p_3 > p_4
    (B) p_1 = p_2 = p_3 = p_4
    (C) P_1 < P_2 < P_3 < P_4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) p1 < p_2 = p_3 < p_4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Keeping Temperature constant we know V α 1/P . So as P increases V decreases.

Q4. The interaction energy of London force is inversely proportional to sixth power of the distance between two interacting particles but their magnitude depends upon
    (A) charge of interacting particles
    (B) mass of interacting particles
    (C) polarisability of interacting particles   <-- CORRECT
    (D) strength of permanent dipoles in the particles
    Answer: C
    Explanation: London dispersion forces operate only over very short distance. The energy of interaction varies as 1/(distance between two interacting particles)^6.^ Large or more complex are the molecules, greater is the magnitude of London forces. This is obviously due to the fact that the large electron clouds are easily distorted or polarised. Hence, greater the polarisability of the interacting particles, greater is the magnitude of the interaction energy.

Q5. Dipole-dipole forces act between the molecules possessing permanent dipole. Ends of dipoles possess ‘partial charges’. The partial charge is
    (A) less than unit electronic charge   <-- CORRECT
    (B) double the unit electronic charge
    (C) equal to unit electronic charge
    (D) more than unit electronic charge
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Partial charge is a small charge developed by displacement of electrons. It is less than unit electronic charge and is represented as δ^+ or δ^–

Q6. The pressure of a 1:4 mixture of dihydrogen and dioxygen enclosed in a vessel is one atmosphere. What would be the partial pressure of dioxygen?
    (A) $8\times10^4\;Nm^{-2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.25 atm
    (C) $0.008\;Nm^{-2}$
    (D) $0.{\text{8 }} \times {\text{ 1}}{0^{\text{5}}}$atm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: moles of H_2 and O_2 are 1 and 4.
moles of ${O_2} = \frac{4}{5}$
Partial pressure of O_2 = mole fraction $ \times $ total pressure $ = \frac{4}{5} \times 1 = 0.8atm$
$ = 0.8 \times {10^5}N{m^{ - 2}} = 8 \times {10^4}N{m^{ - 2}}$

Q7. As the temperature increases, average kinetic energy of molecules increases. What would be the effect of increase of temperature on pressure provided the volume is constant?
    (A) decreases
    (B) increases   <-- CORRECT
    (C) remains same
    (D) becomes half
    Answer: B
    Explanation: P α T at constant volume.This is according to Gay Lussac’s law-“ At constant volume, the pressure of a given mass of a gas is directly proportional to its absolute temperature.”

Q8. Gases possess characteristic critical temperature which depends upon the magnitude of intermolecular forces between the particles. Following are the critical temperatures of some gases.  Gases

    (B) ${\text{He}},{\text{ }}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}},{\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}},{\text{ }}{{\text{N}}_{\text{2}}}$

    (D) ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}},{\text{ He}},{\text{ }}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}},{\text{ }}{{\text{N}}_{\text{2}}}$

Q9. The domestic power supply in India is:
    (A) 24V DC
    (B) 110V, 60 Hz
    (C) 416V , 60Hz
    (D) 220V, 50Hz   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The domestic power supply in India is 220V voltage and 50Hz frequency.

Q10. What is SI unit of viscosity coefficient$\left( \eta \right)$?
    (A) km^-2s
    (B) Nsm^-2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Nm^-2
    (D) Pascal
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Units of coefficient of viscosity, $\eta=\frac{Fd}{AV}\;=\;\frac{Nm}{m^2ms^{-1}}=\;Nsm^{-2}$

Q12. Which curve in Figure represents the curve of ideal gas?
    (A) A and B only
    (B) E and F only
    (C) C and D only
    (D) B only   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D

Q13. Increase in kinetic energy can overcome intermolecular forces of attraction. How will the viscosity of liquid be affected by the increase in temperature?
    (A) Increase
    (B) Decrease   <-- CORRECT
    (C) No regular pattern will be followed
    (D) No effect
    Answer: B
    Explanation: viscosity is inversely proportional to the temperature. As the temperature increase, viscosity decreases.

Q14. How does the surface tension of a liquid vary with increase in temperature?
    (A) Increases
    (B) No regular pattern is followed
    (C) Remains same
    (D) Decreases   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As temperature increases surface tension decreases beacuse the cohesive forces decreases with increase of molecular thermal activity.

Q15. With regard to the gaseous state of matter which of the following statements is correct?
    (A) Fixed position of molecules and complete order of molecules.
    (B) Complete order of molecules and the fixed position of molecules.
    (C) Random motion of molecules and the fixed position of molecules.
    (D) Complete disorder of molecules and Random motion of molecules.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The extent of disorder or randomness among three sates of the matter is gases > liquid > solids.

States of Matter CBSE Online Test 05  (id 955) [PAID]

Q1. Which of the following figures does not represent 1 mole of dioxygen gas at STP?
    (A) 22.7 liters of gas
    (B) 32 grams of gas
    (C) 6.022 $\times$ 10^23 dioxygen molecules
    (D) 16 grams of gas   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: 1 mole of O_2 at STP has mass 32g and volume 22.7L. It contains 6.022 $\times$ 10^23 molecules of dioxygen.

Q2. Under which of the following two conditions, a gas deviates most from the ideal behaviour?
    (A) Low temperature only.
    (B) Low pressure only.
    (C) High temperature and low pressure.
    (D) High pressure and low temperature.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A gas which obeys the ideal gas equation, pV = nRT under all conditions of temperature and pressure is called an ‘ideal gas’.
However, there is no gas that obeys the ideal gas equation under all conditions of temperature and pressure. Hence, the concept of an ideal gas is only theoretical or hypothetical. The gases are found to obey the gas laws fairly well when the pressure is low or the temperature is high.
Such gases are, therefore, known as ‘real gases’. All gases are real gases. Hence, at high pressure and low temperature, a real gas deviates most from ideal behaviour.

Q3. Which of the following changes decrease the vapour pressure of water kept in a sealed vessel?
    (A) Decreasing the quantity of water.
    (B) Adding salt to water.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Increasing the temperature of water.
    (D) Decreasing the volume of the vessel to one-half.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Adding a non-volatile solute like salt decreases the vapour pressure of water. This is because some of the solute(salt) particles occupy the position of solvent molecules (water) on the liquid surface. So escaping the tendency of molecules (water) is reduced and hence vapour pressure decreases.

Q4. Heat of vaporization is always larger than the Heat of fusion because it takes:
    (A) no energy to separate particles completely than just to free them from their oscillating positions in the solid.
    (B) less energy to separate particles completely than just to free them from their fixed positions in the solid.
    (C) more energy to separate particles completely than just to free them from their random positions in the solid.
    (D) more energy to separate particles completely than just to free them from their fixed positions in the solid.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: While melting (fusion) of a substance the molecules get separated to some extent but when the same substance is vaporised the molecules get separated to a greater extent which requires more energy, i.e. more heat.

Q5. The fraction of molecules with enough energy to escape the liquid
    (A) is greater at the higher temperature.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) is lesser at the higher temperature
    (C) is greater at the lower temperature.
    (D) is independent of temperature.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The fraction of molecules ($\frac{\triangle N}N$)with enough energy to escape the liquid is greater at the higher temperature.

Q6. The ease with which the electron cloud of a particle can be distorted is called _______.
    (A) negativity
    (B) polarizability   <-- CORRECT
    (C) cloud strength
    (D) polarity
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The polarizability in isotropic media is defined as the ratio of the induced dipole moment of an atom to the electric field that produces this dipole moment.

Q7. Molecules in the interior of liquid experience intermolecular
    (A) repulsion in all directions
    (B) attractions in all directions   <-- CORRECT
    (C) repulsion away from surface only
    (D) attractions towards surface only
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The net force on the molecules presents inside in bulk is zero. For example, the molecule 'p' will experience zero.

Q8. Surface tension results because
    (A) a liquid tends to minimize the number of molecules at the surface.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a liquid tends to increase the number of molecules at the surface.
    (C) a liquid tends to maximize the number of molecules at the surface.
    (D) surface molecules have different properties.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Surface tension results because a liquid tends to minimize the number of molecules at the surface (i.e to minimize the surface area).

Q9. Capillarity results from a competition between the intermolecular forces within the
    (A) intermolecular forces within tube walls and liquid (adhesive forces) only.
    (B) liquid and intramolecular forces between walls and liquid.
    (C) liquid and intramolecular forces between liquid (cohesive forces).
    (D) liquid (cohesive forces) and those between the liquid and the tube walls (adhesive forces).   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Capillarity action results because of intermolecular forces within the liquid (cohesive forces) and those between the liquid and the tube walls (adhesive forces). Generally, capillary action occurs when the adhesion to the walls is stronger than the cohesive forces between the liquid molecules.

Q10. The van der Waals equation adjusts the measured pressure
    (A) up by adding a factor that accounts for intramolecular attractions.
    (B) up by subtracting a factor that accounts for intermolecular attractions.
    (C) down by adding a factor that accounts for intermolecular attractions.
    (D) up by adding a factor that accounts for intermolecular attractions.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\frac{an^2}{V^2}$ is added. The value of constant 'a' gives the magnitude of attractive forces between molecules of the gas.

Q11. In van der Waals, an equation of state of the gas law, the constant b is a measure of:
    (A) intermolecular repulsions
    (B) intermolecular repulsion per unit volume
    (C) volume occupied by molecule   <-- CORRECT
    (D) intermolecular attraction
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In van der Waals equation of state of the gas law, the constant b is a measure of the volume occupied by the molecules.
It gives the effective size of the gas molecules. The greater value of b indicates a larger size of the molecules and smaller compressible volume.

Q12. Acetylene (C_2H_2), an important fuel in welding, is produced in the laboratory when calcium carbide (CaC_2) reacts with water:${\text{Ca}}{{\text{C}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{s}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ 2}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}0\left( {\text{l}} \right){\text{ }} \to {\text{ }}{{\text{C}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ Ca}}{\left( {{\text{OH}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}\left( {{\text{aq}}} \right)$ For a sample of acetylene collected over water, total gas pressure (adjusted to barometric pressure) is 738 torr and the volume is 543 mL. At the temperature of the gas (23°C), the vapour pressure of water is 21 torr. How many grams of acetylene are collected?
    (A) 0.832g C_2H_2
    (B) 0.540g C_2H_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1.236g C_2H_2
    (D) 0.763g C_2H_2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The total pressure is the sum of the partial pressure due to C_2H_2(g) and H_2O(g):
P_total = 748mm of Hg = pH_2O + pC_2H_2 = (21 mm of Hg) + PC_2H_2;PC_2H_2 = (738 - 21) = 717mm of Hg
As 760 mm of Hg corresponds to 1 atm,
$P{c_2}{H_2} = \frac{{717}}{{760}}atm $ = 0.943atm.
Using the ideal gas law, pV = nRT,
The number of moles of C_2H_2 formed is: $n = \frac{{pV}}{{RT}} = \frac{{(0.943atm) \times (0.543L)}}{{(0.08206\;Latm\;{K^{ - 1}}mo{l^{ - 1}})\left\{ {(23 + 273)K} \right\}}} $ = 0.0207mol
The molar mass of C_2H_2 is {2 $\times$ 12(C)} + {2 $\times$ 1(H)} = 26g mol^-1
This amount, therefore, corresponds to a mass of acetylene collected
mass = number of moles $ \times $ molar mass = 0.0207mol $\times$ 26g mol^-1 = 0.540g

Q13. A scale model of a blimp rises when it is filled with helium to a volume of 55.0 dm^3. When 1.10 mol of He is added to the blimp, the volume is 26.2 dm^3. How many more grams of He must be added to make it rise? Assume constant T and P.
    (A) 4.26 g He
    (B) 3.98 g He
    (C) 5.21 g He
    (D) 4.84 g He   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: By, Avogadro's Law; $\frac{{{V_1}}}{{{V_2}}} = \frac{{{n_1}}}{{{n_2}}}$
$\frac{{55}}{{26.2}} = \frac{{{n_1}}}{{1.10}}$
So, ${n_1} = \frac{{55 \times 1.10}}{{26.2}}$ = 2.309mol
n_1 = 2.309 mol.
So, $\Delta n$ = 2.309 - 1.10 = 1.209 mol of He
Therefore mass of He that should be added = (2.309 - 1.10)mol $\times$ 4.003 g/mol = 4.84g.

Q14. Hot H_2 can reduce copper(II) oxide, forming pure metal and H_2O. What volume of H_2 at 765°C torr and 225 is needed to reduce 35.5 g of copper(II) oxide?
    (A) 18.1 L   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 15.7 L
    (C) 22.3 L
    (D) 13.1 L
    Answer: A
    Explanation: CuO + H_2 $\to$ Cu + H_2O
1 mol of H_2 is required to reduce 1 mol of CuO. Mole of CuO = $\frac{35.5}{79.5}$ = 0.45 mol. So, moles of H_2 = 0.45mol.
PV = nRT
Here P = 765torr, n = 0.45mol, T = 498K
so V = 18.1L

Q15. What mass of potassium chloride forms when 5.25 L of chlorine gas at 0.950 atm and 293 K reacts with 17.0 g of potassium?
    (A) 23.3 g KCl
    (B) 41.5 g KCl
    (C) 30.9 g KCl   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 35.7 g KCl
    Answer: C
    Explanation: K + 0.5Cl_2 $\to$ KCl 
1 mol of K reacts with 0.5 mol of Cl_2 gas. Using relation; PV = nRT where P = 0.95 atm, V = 5.25 L and T = 293K
we have, n = 0.20733 mol
So, moles of Cl_2 = 0.20733 mol
mole of K = 0.43 mol
Cl_2 is limiting reagent. 0.5 mole of Cl_2 give 1 mole of KCl.
So, 0.20733 mole will give 0.414 mole of KCl = 30.9 g

Q1. Thermodynamics is the branch of physical science concerned with
    (A) heat and its transformations to and from other forms of energy.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) mass and its transformations to and from other forms of energy.
    (C) potential and its transformations to and from other forms of energy.
    (D) kinetic energy and its transformations to and from other forms of energy.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Thermodynamics deals with heat and its transformation from one form to another. The branch of physical science that deals with the relations between heat and other forms of energy (such as mechanical, electrical, or chemical energy) and by extension of the relationships between all forms of energy.

Q2. In a closed system, which of the following take place?
    (A) The boundaries prevent the flow of matter out of it but not vice versa.
    (B) The boundaries permit the flow of matter into it but not vice versa.
    (C) The boundaries permit the flow of matter into or out of it.
    (D) The boundaries prevent the flow of matter into or out of it.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In a closed system, there is no flow of matter from system to surrounding or vice versa. For example, a certain quantity of fluid bounded within a closed cylinder constitutes a closed system.

Q3. In an open system, which of the following take place?
    (A) The boundaries prevent the flow of energy into it.
    (B) The boundaries prevent the flow of matter into or out of it.
    (C) The boundaries permit the flow of matter into or out of it.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The boundaries prevent the flow of matter but not of energy.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In an open system, there is a flow of matter and energy in and out of the system or vice versa. For example, an air compressor in which the air enters at low pressure and exit at high pressure and there is energy interaction with the surrounding.

Q4. First law of thermodynamics is a restatement of:
    (A) law of conservation of energy.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) law of conservation of parity.
    (C) law of conservation of charge.
    (D) law of conservation of mass.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: It is a restatement of the law of conservation of energy.
It states that Thermodynamics is the branch of physical science that deals with the relations between heat and other forms of energy (such as mechanical, electrical, or chemical energy) and by extension, of the relationships between all forms of energy.

Q5. According to the first law of thermodynamics $\Delta$U = q + w, here what is a sign of q and w?
    (A) q is negative if heat is transferred from the system and w is negative if work is done by the system.
    (B) q is positive if heat is transferred into the system and w is positive if work is done on the system.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) q is negative if heat is transferred into the system and w is negative if work is done on the system.
    (D) q is positive if heat is transferred into the system and w is positive if work is done by the system.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The first law is simply the conservation of energy equation. q is positive if heat is added to the system, and negative if heat is removed; w is positive if work is done on the system, and negative if work is done by the system.

Q6. If V_f is the final volume and V_i is the initial volume and ${{\text{p}}_{{\text{ex}}}}$ external pressure then the work is done can be calculated by?
    (A) $\mathop \smallint \limits_{{V_i}}^{{V_f}} {p_{ex}}dV$
    (B) $ - \mathop \smallint \limits_{{V_i}}^{{V_f}} {p_{ex}}dV$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $ - \mathop \smallint \limits_{{V_i}}^0 {p_{ex}}dV$
    (D) $\mathop \smallint \limits_0^{{V_f}} {p_{ex}}dV$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $ - \mathop \smallint \limits_{{V_i}}^{{V_f}} {p_{ex}}dV$ = w
It is equal to the integration of change in volume with respect to the initial and final volume.

Q7. For the isothermal reversible free expansion of an ideal gas from V_i, the initial volume to V_f, the final volume of the work done on the gas is:
    (A) w = $- nRTln\left( {\frac{{{V_f}}}{{{V_i}}}} \right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) w = $- nRln\left( {\frac{{{V_f}}}{{{V_i}}}} \right)$
    (C) w = $ - RTln\left( {\frac{{{V_f}}}{{{V_i}}}} \right)$
    (D) w = $ - nTln\left( {\frac{{{V_f}}}{{{V_i}}}} \right)$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: w = $- nRTln\left( {\frac{{{V_f}}}{{{V_i}}}} \right)$
This is work done by the system in an isothermal process where
w is the work done
n is the number of moles
R is the universal gas constant 
T is the temperature in Kelvin scale

Q8. The correct equation for the change in enthalpy is:
    (A) $\Delta$H = $\Delta$U + $\frac{p}{V}$
    (B) $\Delta$H = $\Delta$U + n $\frac{p}{V}$
    (C) $\Delta$H = $\Delta$U + T$\Delta$V
    (D) $\Delta$H = $\Delta$U + p$\Delta$V   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Enthalpy is a thermodynamic quantity equivalent to the total heat content of a system. It is equal to the internal energy of the system plus the product of pressure and volume.

Q9. The molar specific heat capacity of a substance is the quantity of heat needed to raise the temperature of one
    (A) kilogram by one degree Fahrenheit.
    (B) mole by one degree Fahrenheit.
    (C) gram by one degree celsius.
    (D) mole by one degree celsius or one kelvin.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Molar specific heat capacity can be defined as the amount of heat energy required to raise the temperature of 1 mole of a substance by 1^o C.

Q10. Which one among the following is the correct option for right relationship between C_p and C_v for one mole of ideal gas?
    (A) C_P = RC_V
    (B) C_p - C_v = R   <-- CORRECT
    (C) C_P - C_V = R
    (D) C_P + C_V = R
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For a mole of an ideal gas, The difference between C_p and C_v is always constant i.e. equals to the gas constant.
Therefore, for one mole of an ideal gas, C_p - C_V = R.

Q11. Calorimetry is an experimental technique or process of:
    (A) measuring the amount of chemicals consumed.
    (B) measuring the maximum pressure developed in a reaction.
    (C) measuring the amount of work done in a reaction.
    (D) measuring the energy changes associated with chemical or physical processes.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Calorimetry is an experimental technique or process of measuring the heat of chemical reactions or physical changes as well as heat capacity.

Q12. An exothermic process:
    (A) results in a increase in the internal energy of the system.
    (B) results in a decrease in the enthalpy of the system.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) results in a increase in the enthalpy of the system.
    (D) results in a decrease in the temperature of the system.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Exothermic process results in a decrease in enthalpy of the system hence for exothermic reaction $\Delta$H = -ve.

Q13. The enthalpy change of a chemical reaction ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{\text{H}}$ equals (a_i and b_i are stoichiometric coefficients)?
    (A) $\mathop \sum \limits_i {a_i}{H_{products}} - \mathop \sum \limits_i {b_i}{H_{reactants}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\mathop \sum \limits_i {a_i}{H_{products}}$
    (C) $\mathop \sum \limits_i {a_i}{H_{products}} + \mathop \sum \limits_i {b_i}{H_{reactants}}$
    (D) $\mathop \sum \limits_i {a_i}{H_{products}} \pm \mathop \sum \limits_i {b_i}{H_{reactants}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The enthalpy of reaction (${\Delta _r}H$) = (Sum of enthalpies of products)- (sum of enthalpies of reactants) = $\sum {{a_i}{H_{(product)}}} - \sum {{b_i}{H_{(reactant)}}} $

Q14. Standard enthalpy of fusion or molar enthalpy of fusion is:
    (A) the enthalpy change that accompanies vaporization of one kg of a solid substance in the standard state.
    (B) the enthalpy change that accompanies melting of one kg of a solid substance in the standard state.
    (C) the enthalpy change that accompanies melting of one mole of a solid substance in the standard state.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the enthalpy change that accompanies vaporization of one mole of a solid substance in the standard state.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Molar enthalpy of fusion (always increases i.e. $\Delta$H = positive) is the amount of energy needed to change completely one mole of a substance from the solid phase to the liquid phase in the standard state.

Q15. Standard Molar Enthalpy of formation is:
    (A) the standard enthalpy change for the formation of one mole of a compound from its elements in at a pressure of 10 bar and 30°C.
    (B) the standard enthalpy change for the formation of one mole of a compound from its elements in at a pressure of 2 bar and 25^o C.
    (C) the standard enthalpy change for the formation of one kg of a compound from its elements in their most stable states of aggregation.
    (D) the standard enthalpy change for the formation of one mole of a compound from its elements in their most stable states of aggregation.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The standard enthalpy change for the formation of one mole of a compound from its elements in their most stable states of aggregation (reference states) is called standard molar enthalpy of formation.

Q1. According to Hess’s Law, if a reaction takes place in several steps then its standard reaction enthalpy is:
    (A) the sum of the standard enthalpies of the intermediate reactions into which the overall reaction may be divided at the same temperature.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the difference of the standard enthalpies of the intermediate reactions into which the overall reaction may be divided at the same temperature.
    (C) the sum of the standard enthalpies of the intermediate reactions into which the overall reaction may be divided at 2 bar.
    (D) the sum of the standard enthalpies of the intermediate reactions into which the overall reaction may be divided at 35°C.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Hess’s Law states that if a reaction takes place in several steps then its standard reaction enthalpy is the sum of the standard enthalpies of the intermediate reactions into which the overall reaction may be divided at the same temperature.

Q2. Enthalpy of atomization is enthalpy change on breaking:
    (A) one kg of bonds completely to obtain atoms in the gas phase.
    (B) one kg of bonds completely to obtain atoms in the liquid phase.
    (C) one mole of bonds completely to obtain atoms in the liquid phase.
    (D) one mole of bonds completely to obtain atoms in the gas phase.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Enthalpy of atomization is the enthalpy change that takes place on breaking one mole of bonds completely of a compound or an element, to obtain atoms in the gas phase.

Q3. In the case of compounds such as CH_3CH_2Cl, CH_3NO_2, etc. which of the following term is used as bond enthalpy?
    (A) Minimum bond enthalpy
    (B) Mean bond enthalpy   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Bond dissociation enthalpy
    (D) Maximum bond enthalpy
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For polyatomic molecules, the term means bond enthalpy is used for the enthalpy changes associated with chemical bonds.

Q4. Enthalpy of the solution of a substance is the enthalpy change:
    (A) when one kg of it reacts with a specified amount of solvent.
    (B) when one mole of it reacts with a specified amount of solvent.
    (C) when one mole of it dissolves in a specified amount of solvent.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) when one kg of it dissolves in a specified amount of solvent.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Enthalpy of the solution of a substance is the enthalpy change when one mole of it dissolves in a specified amount of solvent.

Q5. The lattice enthalpy of an ionic compound is the enthalpy change which occurs when
    (A) one mole of an ionic compound dissociates into its ions in a liquid state.
    (B) one gm of an ionic compound dissociates into its ions in a gaseous state.
    (C) one kg of an ionic compound dissociates into its ions in a liquid state.
    (D) one mole of an ionic compound dissociates into its ions in a gaseous state.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The lattice enthalpy of an ionic compound is the enthalpy change which occurs when one mole of an ionic compound dissociates into its ions in a gaseous state.

Q6. Spontaneity in the context of chemical thermodynamics means
    (A) having the potential to proceed without the assistance of an external agency.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) having the potential to proceed with the assistance of an external agency.
    (C) having the potential to proceed instantaneously.
    (D) having the potential to proceed fast.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Spontaneity means a reaction occurring on its own without any help of an external agency.

Q7. Entropy is a state function and measures
    (A) the internal energy of the system.
    (B) the enthalpy of the system.
    (C) the degree of randomness or disorder in the system.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the degree of regularity or order in the system.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Entropy is a state function and it measures the degree of randomness or disorder of a system. It is denoted by 'S'.

Q8. Change in entropy of a reversible process can be calculated by:
    (A) $\Delta {S_{sys}} = RT{q_{sys,rev}}$
    (B) $\Delta {S_{sys}} = \frac{{{q_{sys,rev}}}}{T}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\Delta {S_{sys}} = T{q_{sys,rev}}$
    (D) $\Delta {S_{sys}} = \frac{{{q_{sys,rev}}}}{{2T}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\Delta {S_{sys}} = \frac{{{q_{sys,rev}}}}{T}$. The equation can be used to calculate the change in entropy of a system of a reversible process as entropy is a state property.
Where, q_sys, rev = Heat supplied to a system at temperature T.

Q9. If change in Gibbs energy $\Delta {\text{G}}$ is negative (< 0) at constant pressure and temperature?
    (A) The process is spontaneous   <-- CORRECT
    (B) The process is non spontaneous
    (C) The process will never take place
    (D) The process will rarely take place
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\Delta {\text{G}}$ gives criteria for the spontaneous and non-spontaneous process at constant temperature and pressure. $\Delta {\text{G}}$ < 0 (negative) means reaction is spontaneous and $\Delta {\text{G}}$ > 0 (positive) means reaction is non spontaneous.

Q10. Standard Gibbs energy change ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{G}}^0}$ is related to the equilibrium constant of the reaction as follows:
    (A) ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{G}}^0}$= -nRTln K
    (B) ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{G}}^0}$ = -RTln K   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{G}}^0}$ = -Rln K
    (D) ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{G}}^0}$ = -Tln K
    Answer: B
    Explanation: ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{G}}^0}$ = -RTln K 
where ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{G}}^0}$ is standard Gibbs energy change, K is the equilibrium constant, R is the universal gas constant and T is the temperature in kelvin scale.

Q11. A thermodynamic state function is a physical quantity whose value:
    (A) independent of path.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) determine PV work.
    (C) determine heat changes.
    (D) depends on temperature only.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: State function is one which is only dependent on the initial and final state of the system and is independent of the path by which that change has occurred.

Q12. For an adiabatic change:
    (A) $\Delta {\text{T}}$ = 0
    (B) w = 0
    (C) $\Delta {\text{p}}$ = 0
    (D) q = 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: An adiabatic process would not allow the exchange of heat between the system and surroundings, hence q = 0.

Q13. By convention, standard enthalpy for the formation of an element in reference state is:
    (A) different for each element.
    (B) zero   <-- CORRECT
    (C) < 0
    (D) unity
    Answer: B
    Explanation: By convention, enthalpies of formation of all elements in their most stable state of aggregation (reference state) at 25^oC and 1atm are taken as zero.

Q14. $\Delta {{\text{U}}^\ominus} $of combustion of methane is -X kJ ${\text{mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$. The value of $\Delta {{\text{H}}^\ominus}$ is
    (A) > $\Delta {{\text{U}}^\ominus}$
    (B) = 0
    (C) = $\Delta {{\text{U}}^\ominus}$
    (D) $ < {\text{ }}\Delta {{\text{U}}^\ominus}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: CH_4 (g) + 2O_2 (g) → CO_2 (g) + 2H_2O (l)
 We know, $\Delta {H^\ominus} = {\text{ }}\Delta {U^\ominus} + {\text{ }}\Delta {n_g}$ RT
Δn_g is negative as product water in combustion reaction is in liquid state.
$\Delta {H^\ominus} = {\text{ }}-X-{\text{ }}\Delta {n_g}RT $
This implies $\Delta H \ominus$ will be more negative than $\Delta U \ominus$
Hence, $\Delta H \ominus$ < $\Delta U \ominus$

Q15. The enthalpy of combustion of methane, graphite and dihydrogen at 298 K are, -890.3 kJ mol^-1, -393.5 kJ mol^-1 and -285.8 kJ mol^-1 respectively. Enthalpy of formation of CH_4 (g) will be
    (A) -52.27 kJ mol^-1
    (B) -74.8 kJ mol^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) +52.26 kJ mol^-1
    (D) +74.8 kJ mol^-1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\mathrm{CH}_{4}+2 \mathrm{O}_{2} \rightarrow \mathrm{CO}_{2}+2 \mathrm{H}_{2} \mathrm{O}$ $\Delta \mathrm{H}_{1}=-890.3 \mathrm{KJ} / \mathrm{mol}$ ...(1)
$\mathrm{C}(\mathrm{s})+\mathrm{O}_{2} \rightarrow \mathrm{CO}_{2}$ $\Delta \mathrm{H}_{2}=-393.5 \mathrm{KJ} / \mathrm{mol}$ ...(2)
$\mathrm{H}_{2}+0.5 \mathrm{O}_{2} \rightarrow \mathrm{H}_{2} \mathrm{O}$ $\Delta \mathrm{H}_{3}=-285.8 \mathrm{KJ} / \mathrm{mol}$ ...(3)
$\mathrm{C}(\mathrm{s})+2 \mathrm{H}_{2} \rightarrow \mathrm{CH}_{4}$ $\Delta \mathrm{H}=\Delta \mathrm{H}_{2}+2\left(\Delta \mathrm{H}_{3}\right)-\Delta \mathrm{H}_{1}$
$\triangle$H = -393.5 +2(-285.8) - (-890.3)
= -74.8 kJ/mol

Thermodynamics CBSE Online Test 03  (id 958) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Chemistry > Chemical Thermodynamics
