Q1. A reaction, A + B $\to$ C + D + q is found to have a positive entropy change. The reaction will be:
    (A) nonspontaneous at all temperature.
    (B) spontaneous at all temperature.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) spontaneous only at low temperature.
    (D) spontaneous only at high temperature.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\Delta$G = $\Delta$H -T $\Delta$S
$\Delta$S is positive and $\Delta$H is negative as heat is liberated in the reaction.
So $\Delta$G is negative hence reaction will be spontaneous at all temperatures.

Q2. In a process, 701 J of heat is absorbed by a system and 394 J of work is done by the system. What is the change in internal energy for the process?
    (A) $\Delta {\text{U}}$ = 347 J
    (B) $\Delta {\text{U}}$ = 307 J   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\Delta {\text{U}}$ = 327 J
    (D) $\Delta {\text{U}}$ = 367 J
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\Delta {\text{U}}$ = q + w (1st law of thermodynamics)
q = +701J (heat is absorbed by system)
w = -394 J (work is done by system)
$\Delta {\text{U}}$ = 701- 394
= 307J

Q3. The reaction of cyanamide, NH_2CN (s), with dioxygen was carried out in a bomb calorimeter, and $\Delta$U was found to be 742.7 kJ mol^-1 at 298 K. Calculate enthalpy change for the reaction at 298 K.
NH_2CN(s) + $\frac{3}{2}$O_2(g) + N_2(g) +CO_2(g) + H_2O(l)?
    (A) -767.8 kJ
    (B) +741.5 kJ mol^-1
    (C) -741.5 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -702.2 kJ
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Here, $\Delta$n_g = 2 - ($\frac{3}{2}$) = $\frac{1}{2}$
$\Delta$H° = $\Delta$U° + $\Delta$n_gRT
$\Delta$H° = - 742.7 kJ/mol + (0.5 mol $\times$ 8.314 $\times$ 10^-3kJ/mol $\times$ 298K)
$\Rightarrow $ $\Delta$H° = ( - 742.7 kJ + 1238.786 $\times$ 10^-3kJ) mol^-1
$\Rightarrow $ $\Delta$H° = - 741.46 kJ mol^-1

Q4. Calculate the number of kJ of heat necessary to raise the temperature of 60.0 g of aluminium from 35^o C to 55^o C. [Molar heat capacity of Al is 24 J mol^-1K^-1 ]
    (A) 1.78 kJ
    (B) 1.34 kJ
    (C) 1.067 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1.52 kJ
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given, Mass of Al = 60.0g 
Molar mass = 27 g/mol
Molar heat capacity, C = 24 J mol^-1 K^-1. $\Delta$T = 55^oC - 35^oC = 20^oC or 20 K.
Heat, q = nC $\Delta$T = ${\frac{{60}}{{27}}}$ $\times$ 24 $\times$ 20 = 1066.66 J = 1.067 kJ, where n = 60.0/27 mole

Q5. Calculate the enthalpy change on freezing of 1.0 mol of water at 10.0°C to the ice at -10.0^o C. ${\Delta _{{\text{fus}}}}$H = 6.03 kJ ${\text{mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$at 0°C.
 C_P[H_2O(l)] = 75.3 Jmol^-1K^-1
 C_P[H_2O(s)] = 36.8 Jmol^-1K^-1
    (A) $\Delta$H = -6.114kJmol^-1
    (B) $\Delta$H = -5.231 kJmol^-1
    (C) $\Delta$H = -7.151 kJ mol^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\Delta$H = - 7.415kJ mol^-1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Water (10.0^oC) $ \to $ ice (-10.0^oC) $\Delta H = ?$
The enthalpy change for the conversion of 1 mole liquid water at 10.0^oC into 1 mole liquid water 0^oC, water (10.0^o C) $ \rightleftharpoons$ water(0^o C).
$\triangle H_1=C_p\times H_2O(l)\times\triangle T$ = -75.3 Jmol^-1 K^-1 = -753 J mol^-1 
Enthalpy of fusion, water (0^o C) $ \rightleftharpoons$ ice(0^o C) , $\Delta {H_2} = {\Delta _{fus}}H$
${l}\triangle H_2\;=\;\triangle H_{freezing}=-\triangle H_{fusion\;}$ = -6.06 kJ mol^-1 
Enthalpy change for conversion of 1 mole of ice at 0^oC to 1 mole of ice at 10^oC, Ice (0^o C) $\rightleftharpoons$ ice(10.0^o C); $\Delta {H_3} = {C_p}[{H_2}O(s)]\Delta T$ = -36.8 Jmol^-1K^-1 x 10K =-368 J mol^-1
$\Delta H = {\text{ }}\Delta {H_1} + {\text{ }}\Delta {H_2} + {\text{ }}\Delta {H_3}$= - (0.753 + 6.03 + 0.368)kJ mol^-1 = -7.151 kJmol^-1

Q6. Enthalpy of combustion of carbon to CO_2 is 393.5 kJ mol^-1. Calculate the heat released upon formation of 35.2 g of CO_2 from carbon and dioxygen gas.
    (A) -315 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -375 kJ
    (C) -275 kJ
    (D) -398 kJ
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When 1 mole of CO_2 is produced energy released is –393.5 kJ mol^-^1. Moles of CO_2 given = $\frac{35.2}{44}$ = 0.8 moles
So energy released = 0.8 $\times$ -393.5 kJ/mol = -315 kJ/mol

Q7. Enthalpies of formation of CO(g), CO_2(g), N_2O(g), and N_2O_4(g) are -110, –393, 81, and 9.7 kJ mol^-1 respectively. Find the value of ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{\text{H}}$ for the reaction:${{\text{N}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ 3CO}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} \to {\text{ }}{{\text{N}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ 3C}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right)$
    (A) -778 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (B) - 850 kJ
    (C) -600 kJ
    (D) -802 kJ
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Heat of reaction, $\Delta_r$H = ${\textstyle\sum_{}}\triangle_rH_{products}-{\textstyle\sum_{}}{\textstyle{\scriptstyle\triangle}_r}{\textstyle{\scriptstyle H}_{reactants}}{\textstyle\;}{\textstyle\;}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\Delta_{r} H$ = [$\Delta_{f} H$(N_2O) + 3$\Delta_{f} H$(CO_2)] - [$\Delta_{f} H$(N_2O_4) + 3$\Delta_{f} H$(CO)]
$\Rightarrow$ $\Delta_{r} H$ = [81 + {3 $\times$ (-393)}] - 99.7 + {3 $\times$ (-110)}] kJ
$\Rightarrow$ $\Delta_{r} H$ = -777.7 kJ $\approx$ -778 kJ

Q8. Given N_2(g) + 3H_2(g) $\to$ NH_3(g); $\Delta_r$H° = -92.4 kJ mol^-1. What is the standard enthalpy of formation of NH_3 gas?
    (A) -56.5 kJ mol^-1
    (B) -46.2 kJ mol^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -41.3 kJ mol^-1
    (D) -36.9 kJ mol^-1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given, N_2(g) + 3H_2(g) $\to$ 2NH_3(g) ; $\Delta_r$H° = –92.4 kJ mol^-1.
Chemical reaction for the enthalpy of formation of NH_3 (g) is as follows:
${\frac{1}{2}{N_{2\;}}(g)\; + \frac{3}{2}{H_2}(g)\; \to N{H_3}(g)}$
Therefore, ${{\Delta _f}{H^\circ } = \frac{{ - 92.4}}{2} = }$ - 46.2 kJ/mol

Q9. Calculate the standard enthalpy of formation of CH_3OH(l) from the following data:
CH_3OH (1) + O_2(g) $\rightarrow$ CO_2(g) + 2H_2O (1); $\Delta_rH^o$ = -726 kJ mol^-1 
C(graphite) + O_2(g) $\rightarrow$ CO_2(g); $\Delta_{\mathrm{c}} \mathrm{H}^{o}$ = -393 kJ mol^-1
H_2(g + O_2(g) $\rightarrow$ H_2O (1); $\Delta_{\mathrm{c}} \mathrm{H}^{o}$ = -286 kJ mol^-1
    (A) -209 kJ mol^-1
    (B) -339 kJ mol^-1
    (C) -239 kJ mol^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -269 kJ mol^-1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Required reaction for the formation of methanol is:
C(s) + 2H_2(g) + $\frac{1}{2}{O_2}$ (g) $\to$ CH_3OH(l) $\Delta_f$H^o = ?
Enthalpy for the combustion of methanol;
 CH_3OH (l) + $\frac{3}{2}{O_2}$(g) $\to$ CO_2(g) + 2H_2O (l) $\Delta_f$H^o = - 726 kJ mol^-1 ...(1)
 Enthalpy for the formation of 1 mole of CO_2(g)
 C(s) + O_2 (g) $\to$ CO_2(g) $\Delta_f$H^o = - 393 kJ mol^-1 ...(2)
 Enthalpy for the formation of 2 moles of H_2O(l)
 H_2(g) + $\frac{1}{2}{O_2}$ (g) $\to$ H_2O(l) $\Delta_f$H^o = - 286 kJ mol^-1 ...(3)
Now, [eq...(3) $\times$ 2 + eq ...(2) + [ by reversing equation(1)] we get]
C(s) + 2H_2(g) + $\frac{1}{2}{O_2}$ (g) $\to$ CH_3OH (l) $\Delta_f$H^o = - 239 kJ mol^-1

Q10. Calculate the enthalpy change for the process ${\text{CC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} \to {\text{ C }}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ 4 Cl }}\left( {\text{g}} \right)$and calculate the bond enthalpy of C--Cl in ${\text{CC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}$ (g).
${\Delta _{{\text{vap}}}}{{\text{H}}^0}\left( {{\text{CC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}} \right){\text{ }} = {\text{ 3}}0.{\text{5 kJ mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$.
${\Delta _{\text{f}}}{{\text{H}}^0}\left( {{\text{CC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}} \right){\text{ }} = {\text{ }} - {\text{135}}.{\text{5 kJ mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$.
${\Delta _{\text{a}}}{{\text{H}}^0}\left( {\text{C}} \right){\text{ }} = {\text{ 715}}.0{\text{ kJ mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$, where ${\Delta _{\text{a}}}{{\text{H}}^0}$ is enthalpy of atomisation
${\Delta _{\text{a}}}{{\text{H}}^0}\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}} \right)$= 242 kJ ${\text{mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$
    (A) 326 kJ ${\text{mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 397 kJ ${\text{mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$
    (C) 307 kJ ${\text{mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$
    (D) 345 kJ ${\text{mo}}{{\text{l}}^{ - {\text{1}}}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\mathrm{C}(\mathrm{s})+2 \mathrm{Cl}_{2}(\mathrm{g}) \rightarrow \mathrm{CCl}_{4}(\mathrm{l})$ $\Delta_{\mathrm{f}} \mathrm{H}^{0}\left(\mathrm{CCl}_{4}\right)=-135.5 \mathrm{KJ} / \mathrm{mol}$ ....(1)
$\mathrm{C}(\mathrm{s}) \rightarrow \mathrm{C}(\mathrm{g})$ $\Delta_{\mathrm{a}} \mathrm{H}^{0}(\mathrm{C})=715.0 $KJ mol^-1 ......(2)
$\mathrm{Cl}_{2}(\mathrm{g}) \rightarrow 2 \mathrm{Cl}(\mathrm{g})$ $\Delta_{\mathrm{a}} \mathrm{H}^{0}\left(\mathrm{Cl}_{2}\right)=242 \ {{kJ}} \mathrm{mol}^{-1}$ .....(3)
$\mathrm{CCl}_{4}(1) \rightarrow \mathrm{CCl}_{4}(\mathrm{g})$ $\Delta_{\mathrm{vap}} \mathrm{H}^{0}\left(\mathrm{CCl}_{4}\right)=30.5 \mathrm{kJ} \mathrm{mol}^{-1}$ ....(4)
$\mathrm{CCl}_{4}(\mathrm{g}) \rightarrow \mathrm{CCl}_{4}(\mathrm{l})$ $\Delta_{\mathrm{vap}} \mathrm{H}^{0}\left(\mathrm{CCl}_{4}\right)=-30.5 \mathrm{kJ} \mathrm{mol}^{-1}$ ....(5)
Equation (1) - (2) - 2(3) + (4)
So For CCl_4 (g) → C (g) + 4 Cl (g) reaction ΔH^0 = -( -135.5 - 715 - 2(242) + 30.5) = 1304 KJ/mol
Bond enthalpy of C—Cl bond will be 1304/4 KJ/mol = 326KJ/mol

Q11. For an isolated system, $\Delta {\text{U}}$ = 0, what will be $\Delta {\text{S}}$?
    (A) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ will increase for some time and then reduce
    (B) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ > 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ < 0
    (D) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ = 0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For an isolated system, $\begin{array}{l}\triangle U=\;0\\\\\\\end{array}$and for a spontaneous process, Total entropy change must be positive.
Moreover, $\begin{array}{l}\triangle S=\;\frac{q_{rev}}T=\frac{\triangle H}T=\;\frac{\triangle U\;+p\triangle V}T=\;\frac{0+p\triangle V}T\\i.e.\;T\triangle S>0\;\\Or\;\;\;\triangle S>0\\\\\\\end{array}$

Q12. For the reaction at 298 K, 2A + B $\to$ C, $\Delta$H = 400 kJ mol^-1 and $\Delta {\text{S}}$ = 0.2 kJ K^-1mol^-1. At what temperature will the reaction become spontaneous considering $\Delta {\text{H}}$ and $\Delta {\text{S}}$ to be constant over the temperature range.
    (A) 3500 K
    (B) 2500 K
    (C) 1500 K
    (D) 2000 K   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Gibbs free energy, $\Delta$G = $\Delta$H - T$\Delta$S
At equilibrium $\Delta$G = 0; then T= $\frac{\Delta H}{\Delta S}$ = 2000K
Therefore, above 2000K, the reaction will be spontaneous.

Q13. For the reaction, 2Cl(g) $\rightarrow$ Cl_2(g), what are the signs of $\Delta {\text{H}}$ and $\Delta {\text{S}}$?
    (A) $\Delta H$ < 0, $\Delta S$ < 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\Delta H$ < 0, $\Delta S$ > 0
    (C) $\Delta H$ > 0, $\Delta S$ > 0
    (D) $\Delta H$ > 0, $\Delta S$ < 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As in this case bond formation between two Cl atom is taking place so energy will be released so $\Delta$H < 0 and since 2 atoms are combining to form 1 molecule randomness decreases so $\Delta$S < 0.

Q14. For the reaction 2A(g) + B(g) $\to$ 2D(g) $\Delta {U^0}$ = - 10.5kJ and $\Delta {S^0}$ = - 44.1J K^-1. Calculate $\Delta {{\text{G}}^0}$ for the reaction, and predict whether the reaction may occur spontaneously?
    (A) 0.164 kJ, the reaction is spontaneous
    (B) 0.225 kJ, the reaction is not spontaneous
    (C) 0.165 kJ, the reaction is not spontaneous   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.225 kJ, the reaction is spontaneous
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\Delta {G^0} = \Delta {H^0} - T\Delta {S^0}$
and $\Delta {H^0} = \Delta {U^0} + \Delta {n_g}RT$
Here $\Delta {n_g} = - 1$,
$\Delta$H° = - 10.5 kJ + (-1 $\times$ 8.314 $\times$ 10^-3 kJ K^-1mol^-1 $\times$ 298K = - 10.5 (-2.477) kJ mol^-1
$\Delta$H° = - 12.977 kJ mol^-1
Now, $\Delta$G° = - 12.977 - (298 $\times$ 44.1 $\times$ 10^-3) = - 12.977 + 13.14 = + 0.165 kJ mol^-1
The reaction will not occur spontaneously because $\Delta$G°is positive.

Q15. The equilibrium constant for a reaction is 10. What will be the value of $\Delta G^0$? R = 8.314 JK^-1, T= 300 K, T = 300 K?
    (A) -6.132 kJ mol^-1
    (B) -5.456 kJ mol^-1
    (C) -5.978 kJ mol^-1
    (D) -5.744 kJ mol^-1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\Delta$_rG^0 = -RTln K_c.
$\Delta G^0$ = -2.303 $\times$ 8.314 $\times$ 300 $\times$ log10 = -5744.14 Jmol^-1 = -5.74414 kJmol^-1

Q1. Comment on the thermodynamic stability of NO(g), Given:
$\frac{1}{2}$N_2 (g) +$\frac{{1}}{2}$ O_2(g) $ \to $ NO (g); ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{H}}^0}$ = 90 kJ mol^-1
NO(g) +$\frac{1}{2}$ O_2(g) $ \to $ NO_2 (g); ${\Delta _{\text{r}}}{{\text{H}}^0}$ = -74 kJ mol^-1
    (A) NO_2 (g) is stable, but NO(g) is formed
    (B) NO(g) is unstable, but NO_2 (g) is formed   <-- CORRECT
    (C) NO_2 (g) is unstable, but NO(g) is formed
    (D) NO(g) is stable, but NO_2 (g) is formed
    Answer: B
    Explanation: NO(g) is unstable because the formation of NO is endothermic, but NO_2(g) is formed because its formation is exothermic. Therefore, unstable NO(g) converts into stable NO_2(g).

Q2. Calculate the heat and the work associated with a process in which 5 mol of gas expands reversibly at constant temperature T = 298 K from a pressure of 10.00 to 1.00 atm
    (A) 27.0 kJ, -28.5 kJ
    (B) 30.5 kJ, -28.5 kJ
    (C) 28.5 kJ, -28.5 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 25.5 kJ, -28.5 kJ
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\begin{array}{l}Work\;done\;for\;an\;isothermal\;process,\;w=-2.303nRT\;\log\frac{P_1}{P_2}=-2.303\times5\times8.314\times298\times\log\frac{10}1=-2.303\times5\times8.314\times298\times1=-28529.24J=-28.5kJ\\Acoording\;to\;equation\;of\;first\;law\;of\;thermodynamics,\;\triangle U=\;q+w\\For\;isothermal\;process,\triangle U=0;\;\\\Rightarrow Heat,\;q=-w=-(-28.5\;kJ)=28.5\;kJ\\\end{array}$

Q3. Thermodynamics is not concerned about
    (A) the extent to which a chemical reaction proceeds.
    (B) the feasibility of a chemical reaction.
    (C) the rate at which a reaction proceeds.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) energy changes involved in a chemical reaction.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Thermodynamics tells whether a reaction will take place or not. It doesn't tell about the rate (speed) of reaction.

Q4. Which of the following statements is correct?
 The presence of reactants in a closed vessel made up of copper is an example of a closed system.
 There is an exchange of energy as well as a matter between the system and the surroundings in a closed system.
 The presence of reacting species in a covered beaker is an example of an open system.
 The presence of reactants in a thermos flask or any other closed insulated vessel is an example of a closed system.
    (A) B
    (B) C
    (C) A
    (D) D   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In a closed system, there is no exchange of matter with the surroundings, but there can be an exchange of energy (typically in the form of heat). In this case, a closed insulated vessel like a thermos flask prevents both the exchange of matter and minimizes the exchange of energy with the surroundings, making it a closed system.

Q5. The state of a gas constant can be described by quoting the relationship between
    (A) temperature, amount, pressure
    (B) pressure, volume, temperature, amount   <-- CORRECT
    (C) amount, volume, temperature
    (D) pressure, volume, temperature
    Answer: B
    Explanation: State of gas constant is determined by stating the value of P,V,n,T.
i.e. $R=\frac{PV}{nT}$

Q6. The volume of gas is reduced to half from its original volume. The specific heat will be
    (A) increase four times
    (B) be doubled
    (C) remain constant   <-- CORRECT
    (D) reduce to half
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Specfic heat (c) of a substance is defined as the amount of heat required to raise the temperature of 1 gram of substance through 1^0C.
 $\begin{array}{l}C=\frac q{\triangle T}\;\\\\\\\end{array}$,Specific heat is independent of volume, so it will remain constant.

Q7. During complete combustion of one mole of butane, 2658 kJ of heat is released. The thermochemical reaction for above change is
    (A) $\begin{gathered} {C_4}{H_{10}}\left( g \right) + {O_2}\left( g \right) \to 4C{O_2}\left( g \right) + 5{H_2}O\left( l \right){\Delta _c}H \hfill= -1329.0{\text{ }}kJ{\text{ }}mo{l^{-1}} \hfill \\ \end{gathered}$
    (B) $\begin{gathered} 2{C_4}{H_{10}}\left( g \right) + 13{O_2}\left( g \right) \to 8C{O_2}\left( g \right) + 10{H_2}O\left( l \right){\Delta _c}H \hfill= -2658.0{\text{ }}kJ{\text{ }}mo{l^{-1}} \hfill \\ \end{gathered}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\begin{gathered} {C_4}{H_{10}}\left( g \right) + {O_2}\left( g \right) \to 4C{O_2}\left( g \right) + 5{H_2}O\left( l \right){\text{ }}{\Delta _c}H \hfill = -2658.0{\text{ }}kJ\,mo{l^{-1}} \hfill \\ \end{gathered} $
    (D) $\begin{gathered} {C_4}{H_{10}}\left( g \right) + {O_2}\left( g \right) \to 4C{O_2}\left( g \right) + 5{H_2}O\left( l \right){\Delta _c}H \hfill= + 2658.0{\text{ }}kJ{\text{ }}mo{l^{-1}} \hfill \\ \end{gathered}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Enthapy of combustion is the energy released when 1mole of a hydrocarbon (butane ) reacts completely in presence of excess of oxygen. The chemical equation for exothermic reaction for combustion of one mole of butane is represented as;
$\begin{gathered} 2{C_4}{H_{10}}\left( g \right) + 13{O_2}\left( g \right) \to 8C{O_2}\left( g \right) + 10{H_2}O\left( l \right){\Delta _c}H \hfill= -2658.0{\text{ }}kJ{\text{ }}mo{l^{-1}} \hfill \\ \end{gathered}$

Q8. ${\Delta _{\text{f}}}{{\text{U}}^ \ominus }$of formation of CH_4 (g) at certain temperature is –393 kJmol^-1. The value of ${\Delta _{\text{f}}}{{\text{H}}^\ominus}$ is
    (A) > ${\Delta _{\text{f}}}{{\text{U}}^\ominus}$
    (B) zero
    (C) <${\Delta _{\text{f}}}{{\text{U}}^\ominus}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) equal to ${\Delta _{\text{f}}}{{\text{U}}^\ominus}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The combustion of metahne is given as follows: CH_4(g) + 2O_2(g) $\to$ CO_2(g) + 2H_2O(l)
Since $\Delta_{f} H^{\circ}=\Delta_{f} U^{\circ}+\Delta n_{g} R T$ and $\triangle_{f} U^{\circ}$ = - 393 kJmol^-1, $\triangle_{f} H^{\circ}$ = (-393) + $\triangle n_{g} R T$
(Here, $\triangle n_{g}<0$) $\Rightarrow \Delta_{f} H^{\circ}<\Delta_{f} U^{\circ}$

Q9. In an adiabatic process, no transfer of heat takes place between system and surroundings. Choose the correct option for free expansion of an ideal gas under adiabatic condition from the following.
    (A) q = 0, $\Delta {\text{T }} \ne $ 0, w = 0
    (B) q = 0, $\Delta {\text{T}}$ = 0, w = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) q $ \ne $ 0, $\Delta {\text{T}}$ = 0, w = 0
    (D) q = 0, $\Delta {\text{T}}$ < 0, w $ \ne $ 0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For free expansion $P_{ext} =0$. So w=0 and for adiabatic process q = 0 ; Now from from 1st law of thermodynamics,
$\Delta$U = q + w =0 + 0 = 0 therefore $\Delta$U = 0
Since, there is no change of internal energy, and temperature will also remain constant, making $\Delta$T=0

Q10. The pressure-volume work for an ideal gas can be calculated by using the expression w = −$\mathop \smallint \limits_{{V_i}}^{{V_f}} {p_{ex}}dV$. The work can also be calculated from the pV–plot by using the area under the curve within the specified limits. When an ideal gas is compressed (a) reversibly or (b) irreversibly from volume V_i to V_f. choose the correct option.
    (A) w (reversible) > w (irreversible)
    (B) w (reversible) = w (irreversible)
    (C) w (reversible) < w (irreversible)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) w (reversible) = w (irreversible) + ${{\text{p}}_{{\text{ex}}}}.\Delta {\text{V}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: w (reversible) < w (irreversible) (for compression process)
Justification: Area under the curve is always more in irreversible compression as can be seen from Fig (a) and (b).

Q11. The entropy change can be calculated by using the expression $\Delta {\text{S }} = $$\frac{{{q_{rev}}}}{T}$ When water freezes in a glass beaker, choose the correct statement amongst the following :
    (A) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (system) decreases and $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (surroundings) also decreases.
    (B) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (system) increases but $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (surroundings) decreases.
    (C) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (system) decreases but $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (surroundings) increases.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (system) decreases but $\Delta {\text{S}}$ (surroundings) remains the same.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: For freezing of process since process is spontaneous therefore if ΔS (system) decreases but ΔS (surroundings) increases.Also, Freezing is exothermic process. The heat released increases the entropy of surrounding.

Q12. On the basis of thermochemical equations (A), (B) and (C), find out which of the algebraic relationships given in options (i) to (iv) is correct:
 C(graphite) + O_2(g) $\rightarrow$ CO_2(g); $ \triangle_{r} H$ = x KJ mol^-1
 C(graphite) + $\frac{1}{2} O_{2}(g) \rightarrow C O(g) ; \Delta_{r} H$ = y KJ mol^-1
 $C O(g)+\frac{1}{2} O_{2}(g) \rightarrow C O_{2}(g) ; \Delta_{r} H=z k J m o l^{-1}$
    (A) x = y – z
    (B) z = x + y
    (C) x = y + z   <-- CORRECT
    (D) y = 2z – x
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have, C(graphite) + O_2(g) $\rightarrow$ CO_2(g); $\triangle_{r} H$ = x KJ mol ^-1 ..... (1)
C(graphite) $+\frac{1}{2} O_{2}(g) \rightarrow C O(g) ; \Delta_{r} H=y k J m o l^{-1}$ .... (2)
Subtacting (1) and (2), we get;
$C O(g)+\frac{1}{2} O_{2}(g) \rightarrow C O_{2}(g)$; $\triangle_{r} H$ = (x-y) kJmol^-1
$\therefore$ z = x - y $\Rightarrow$ x = y + z

Q13. Consider the reactions given below. On the basis of these reactions find out which of the algebraic relations given in options (i) to (iv) is correct?
 C (g) + 4 H (g) $ \to {\text{ C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{4}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right);{\text{ }}{\Delta _{\text{r}}}{\text{H }} = {\text{ x kJ mo}}{{\text{l}}^{-{\text{1}}}}$
 C (graphite,s) + ${\text{2}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} \to {\text{ C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{4}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right);{\text{ }}{\Delta _{\text{r}}}{\text{H }} = {\text{ y kJ mo}}{{\text{l}}^{-{\text{1}}}}$
    (A) x > y   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x < y
    (C) x = y
    (D) x = 2y
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Here, x > y. Because in equation (B) all the reactants are in their most stable states of aggregation hence have zero standard molar enthalpies of formation.

Q14. The enthalpies of elements in their standard states are taken as zero. The enthalpy of formation of a compound is:
    (A) is always negative.
    (B) may be positive or negative.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) is always positive.
    (D) is never negative.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Standard molar enthalpy of formation of a compound from its elements can be +ve or –ve.
For example: $C+O_{2}(g) \rightarrow C O_{2}(g) ; \Delta_{r} H$ = 393.5 kJ mol^-1
$N_{2}(g)+\frac{1}{2} O_{2}(g) \rightarrow N_{2} O(g);$ $\Delta_{r} H$ = +92 k J mol^-1

Q15. Enthalpy of sublimation of a substance is equal to
    (A) enthalpy of fusion + enthalpy of vapourisation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) twice the enthalpy of vapourisation
    (C) enthalpy of fusion
    (D) enthalpy of vapourisation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The process of sublimation involves the change of solid into vapour. Though in sublimation a solid does not pass through the liquid phase on its way to the gas phase, the enthalpy change is equal to the sum of enthalpy of fusion and enthalpy of vaporization because enthalpy is a state function.

Q1. Which of the following statement is not correct?
    (A) $\Delta {\text{G}}$ is zero for a reaction at equilibrium
    (B) $\Delta {\text{G}}$ is positive for a non-spontaneous reaction
    (C) $\Delta {\text{G}}$ is positive for a spontaneous reaction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\Delta {\text{G}}$ is negative for a spontaneous reaction
    Answer: C
    Explanation: ΔG <0 (negative) for a spontaneous change.

Q2. When gasoline burns in a car engine, the heat released causes the products CO_2 and H_2O to expand, which pushes the pistons outward. Excess heat is removed by the car’s cooling system. If the expanding gases do 451J of work on the pistons and the system loses 325 J to the surroundings as heat, calculate the change in energy ($\Delta {\text{E}}$).
    (A) -776 J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -702 J
    (C) -745 J
    (D) -797 J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: q = - 325J w = - 415J
Now, $\Delta$U = q + w = - 325 + (- 451J) = - 776J

Q3. For the reaction H_2(g) + $\frac{1}{2}$ O_2(g) $\rightarrow$ H_2O(l) 285.8 kJ,
Select the correct statement.
    (A) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ > 0, endothermic
    (B) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ < 0, exothermic   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ < 0, endothermic
    (D) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ > 0, exothermic
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Heat is liberated in the process so the reaction is exothermic and $\Delta$H < 0.

Q4. For the process, H_2O (l) + 40.7 kJ $\rightarrow$ H_2O (g)
Select the correct statement.
    (A) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ < 0 hence process is exothermic.
    (B) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ > 0 hence process is endothermic.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ > 0 hence process is exothermic.
    (D) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ < 0 hence process is endothermic.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Heat is utilized in this reaction so the reaction is endothermic and for an endothermic process $\Delta {\text{H}}$ > 0.

Q5. A layer of copper welded to the bottom of a skillet weighs 125 g. How much heat is needed to raise the temperature of the copper layer from 25°C to 300°C? The specific heat capacity (C) of Cu is 0.387J/g K.
    (A) 1.33 $\times$ 10^4J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1.55 $\times$ 10^4J
    (C) 1.11 $\times$ 10^4J
    (D) 1.76 $\times$ 10^4J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: q = mc $\Delta$T
q = (125 g) ${ \times \left( {\frac{{0.387\;J}}{{gK\;}}} \right)\; \times }$ (300 - 25)K = 1.33 $\times$ 10^4J

Q6. You place 50.0 mL of 0.500 M NaOH in a coffee-cup calorimeter at 25.00°C and carefully add 25.0 mL of 0.500 M HCI, also at 25 .00°C. After stirring, the final temperature is 27.21°C. Calculate ${{\text{q}}_{{\text{soln}}}}$ (in J) and $\Delta {{\text{H}}_{{\text{rxn}}}}$ (in kJ/mol)?(Assume the total volume is the sum of the individual volumes and that the final solution has the same density and specific heat capacity as water: d = 1.00 g/mL and C = 4. 184 J/g·K.)
    (A) 693 J, -55.4 kJ/mol   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 623 J, -55.4 kJ/mol
    (C) 733 J, -55.4 kJ/mol
    (D) 593 J, -55.4 kJ/mol
    Answer: A
    Explanation: HCl(aq) + NaOH(aq) $\to$ NaCl(aq) + H_2O(l)
H^+ (aq) + OH^-(aq) $\to$ H_2O(l)
For NaOH 0.500 M $\times$0.0500 L = 0.0250 mol OH^-
For HCl 0.500 M $\times$ 0.0250 L = 0.0125 mol H^+
HCl is the limiting reactant.
0.0125 mol of H_2O will form during the reaction
Total volume after mixing = 0.0750
Now,0.0750 L $\times$ 10^3 mL/L $\times$ 1.00 g/mL = 75.0 g of water
q = mass $\times$ specific heat $\times$ $\Delta$T = 75.0 g $\times$ 4.18 J/g°C$\times$ (27.21 - 25.00)°C = 693 J
Now, ${\vartriangle {H_{reaction}} = \;\frac{{{q_{reaction}}}}{{moles\;of\;{H_2}O}} = \frac{{ - 693}}{{0.0125\;mol}} \times \frac{{1kJ}}{{{{10}^{3\;}}J}} = \;}$ - 55.4 kJ mol^-1 of H_2O

Q7. A cylinder confines 2.00 L gas under a pressure of 1.00 atm. The external pressure is also 1.00 atm. The gas is heated slowly, with the piston sliding freely outward to maintain the pressure of the gas close to 1.00 atm. Suppose the heating continues until a final volume of 3.50 L is reached. Calculate the work done on the gas?
    (A) -152 J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -112 J
    (C) -172 J
    (D) -132 J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: This is an expression of a system from 2.00 to 3.00L against a cons tan t external pressure of 1 atm. The work done on the system = w = -P_extV = -(1.00atm)(3.50L-2.00L) = -1.50 L atm = (-1.50 L atm) (101.325 J L^-1 atm^-1) = -152J

Q8. Suppose a 10.00 kg mass drops through a height difference of 3.00 m, and the resulting work is used to turn a paddle in 200.0 g water, initially at 15.00°C. The final water temperature is found to be 15.35°C. Assuming that the work is done is used entirely to increase the water temperature, calculate the conversion factor between joules and calories.
    (A) 1 calorie $ \approx $ 3.2J
    (B) 1 calorie $ \approx $ 6.1J
    (C) 1 calorie $ \approx $ 5.2J
    (D) 1 calorie $ \approx $ 4.2J   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Total work done on the water = w = - mg $\Delta$h = - (10) $\times$ (9.8) $\times$ (-3) = 294J
The heat required to increase the temperature of water by the same amount = q = mc $\Delta$T = 200 $\times$ 1 $\times$ 0.35 = 70cal
Because the work is done has the same effect on water as a direct transfer of heat, The two expression can be set equal to each other, giving
70cal = 294J
1 cal $\approx$ 4.2J

Q9. Standard Molar Enthalpy of Formation is the standard enthalpy change for the formation of:
    (A) one kg of a compound from its elements in their most stable states of aggregation.
    (B) one mole of a compound from its elements in their most stable states of aggregation.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) one mole of a compound from its elements in at a pressure of 2 bar and 25° C.
    (D) one mole of a compound from its elements in at a pressure of 10 bar and 30° C.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The standard enthalpy change for the formation of one mole of a compound from its elements in their most stable states of aggregation (reference states) is the standard molar enthalpy of formation.

Q10. Suppose that 1.00 kJ of heat is transferred to 2.00 mol argon (at 298 K, 1 atm). What will the final temperature T_f, if the heat is transferred at constant volume?
    (A) 308 K
    (B) 347 K
    (C) 338 K   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 313 K
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Argon is monoatomic, Here, ${{C_v} = \frac{3}{2}R = \;\frac{3}{2} \times 8.314J{K^{ - 1}}mo{l^{ - 1}}}$ = 12.47J K^-1 mol^-1
As volume is kept constan t, q_v = nC_v $\Delta$T
$\Rightarrow$ 1000J = (2.00mol) $\times$ (12.47JK^-1 mol^-1) $\times$ $\Delta$T
$\Rightarrow $ $\Delta$ T = 40.09K
$\Rightarrow $ T_f = 298 + 40.1 = 338K

Q11. Suppose that 1.00 kJ of heat is transferred to 2.00 mol argon (at 298 K, 1 atm). What will the final temperature T_f be if the heat is transferred at constant pressure?
    (A) 376 K
    (B) 301 K
    (C) 322 K   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 335 K
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Argon is monoatomic, Here, $C _ { p } = \frac { 5 } { 2 } R = \frac { 5 } { 2 } \times 8.314 J K ^ { - 1 } m o l ^ { - 1 } = 20.79 J K ^ { - 1 } m o l ^ { - 1 }$
As pressure is kept constant, $q _ { p } = n C _ { p } \Delta T$
$\Rightarrow 1000 J = ( 2.00 m o l ) \times \left( 20.79 J K ^ { - 1 } m o l ^ { - 1 } \right) \times \Delta T$
$\Rightarrow \Delta T = 24.05 K$
$\Rightarrow T _ { f } = 298 + 24.05 = 322.05 K$

Q12. Red phosphorus reacts with liquid bromine in an exothermic reaction $2P(s)\;+3Br_2(l)\rightarrow2PBr_3(g)\:;\;\triangle H=-243kJ$ Calculate the enthalpy change when 2.63 g phosphorus reacts with an excess of bromine in this way.
    (A) −10.3 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (B) −6.8 kJ
    (C) −12.3 kJ
    (D) −8.3 kJ
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The given reaction is, $2 P ( s ) + 3 B r _ { 2 } ( l ) \rightarrow 2 P B r _ { 3 } ( g ) ; \Delta H = - 243 k J$
moles of $P ( s ) = \frac { 2.63 } { 31 } = 0.084 \text { moles. }$
Heat liberated, when 2 mol of P(s) reacted = -243 kJ
Heat liberated, when 0.084 mol of P(s) reacted $= \frac { 243 } { 2 } \times 0.084 = -10.206 k J$

Q13. To vaporize 100.0 g carbon tetrachloride at its normal boiling point, 349.9 K, and P =1 atm, 19.5 kJ of heat is required. Calculate $\Delta {{\text{H}}_{{\text{vap}}}}$ for CCl_4?
    (A) 34.0 kJ
    (B) 30.0 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 42.0 kJ
    (D) 23.0 kJ
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Number of moles of CCl_4 = ${\frac{{100}}{{154}}}$ = 0.6493 moles.
Heat required for 0.6493 moles = 19.5kJ
$\Rightarrow$ Heat required for 1.00 moles = ${ \frac{{19.5}}{{0.6493\;}}}$ = 30.032kJ

Q14. Calculate the heat and the work associated with a process in which 5.00 mol of gas expands reversibly at constant temperature $T = 298k$ from a pressure of 10.00 to 1.00 atm
    (A) 30.5 kJ, -28.5 kJ
    (B) 27.0 kJ, -28.5 kJ
    (C) 28.5 kJ, -28.5 kJ   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 25.5 kJ, -28.5 kJ
    Answer: C
    Explanation: At constant $T , \frac { P _ { 1 } } { P _ { 2 } } = \frac { 10 a t m } { 1 a t m } = 10$; n = 5 mol, T = 298K
Thus, work ​​​​​​​$w = - 2.303nRT\log \frac{{{P_1}}}{{{P_2}}} = - 2.303 \times 5 \times 8.314 \times 298 \times \log 10$$ = - 2.85 \times {10^4}J = - 28.5kJ$
Here, heat $\Delta U = 0 ; \Rightarrow q = - w = + 28.5 k J$

Q15. Suppose 5.00 mol of an ideal monatomic gas at an initial temperature of 298 K and pressure of 10.0 atm is expanded adiabatically and reversibly until the pressure has decreased to 1.00 atm. Calculate the enthalpy change, and the work is done?
    (A) -20300 J, -11200 J
    (B) -18600 J, -11200 J   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -17200 J, -11200 J
    (D) -16300 J, -11200 J
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The initial volume = V_1 = $- \frac{{nR{T_1}}}{{{P_1}}} = \frac{{\left( {5mol} \right)\; \times \left( {0.08206\;Latm{K^{ - 1}}mo{l^{ - 1\;}}} \right) \times 298K}}{{10atm}} $ = 12.2 L
The heat capacity ratio for a monoatomic gas = $ \gamma = \frac{{{C_p}}}{{{C_v}}} = \frac{{\frac{5}{2}R}}{{\frac{3}{2}R}} = \frac{5}{3}$
For reversible adiabatic process = ${\frac{{{P_1}}}{{{P_2}}}{{\left( {{V_1}} \right)}^\gamma } = {{\left( {{V_2}} \right)}^\gamma }}$
${ \Rightarrow \frac{{10}}{1}{{\left( {12.2L} \right)}^{\frac{{^5}}{3}}} = {{\left( {{V_2}} \right)}^{\frac{5}{3}}}\;}$
${ \Rightarrow {V_2} = \left( {12.2L} \right) \times {{\left( {10} \right)}^{\frac{3}{5}}}\; = \;48.7L}$
Final temperature can now be calculated from ideal gas law
${{T_2}\; = \frac{{{P_2}{V_2}}}{{nR}} = 119K}$
Now, work done ${ = \;w = \vartriangle U = n{C_v}\vartriangle T}$
= 5 $\times$ (${\left( {\frac{3}{2}R} \right)}$ $\times$ (119 - 298) = 5 $\times$ ( ${\left( {\frac{3}{2} \times 8.314} \right) \times }$ (119 - 298) = -11200J
Also, Enthalpy change = $ \vartriangle H = n{C_p}\vartriangle T = 5 \times \left( {\frac{5}{2}R} \right) \times$ (119 - 298) ${ = 5 \times \left( {\frac{5}{2} \times 8.314} \right) \times }$ (119 - 298) = - 18600J

Equilibrium CBSE Online Test 01  (id 961) [FREE]

Q1. When the rate of evaporation is equal to the rate of condensation, it is called _______.
    (A) stable reaction
    (B) equilibrium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) balanced reaction
    (D) reaction at rest
    Answer: B
    Explanation: At equilibrium, the rate of evaporation is equal to the rate of condensation.
It may be represented by H_2O (l) ⇌ H_2O (vap)
The double half arrows indicate that the processes in both the directions are going on simultaneously. The mixture of reactants and products in the equilibrium state is called an equilibrium mixture.

Q2. In the dynamic equilibrium stage, one of the following events takes place?
Choose the right one:
    (A) Rates of the forward reaction is faster.
    (B) The concentrations of the reactants are decreased.
    (C) The concentrations of the products are increased.
    (D) No change in the concentrations of either of the reactants or products.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There is no change in the conc of reactant and product. At dynamic equilibrium, reactants are converted to products, and products are converted to reactants at an equal and constant rate. Reactions do not necessarily—and most often do not—end up with equal concentrations. Equilibrium is the state of equal, opposite rates, not equal concentrations.

Q3. The rates of transfer of molecules from ice into water and of reverse transfer from water into the ice are equal at atmospheric pressure and 273 K. Both the processes occur simultaneously and at the same rate so that the amount of ice and water remains constant. This process is called _______.
    (A) Liquid-Gas Equilibrium
    (B) Liquid-Vapour Equilibrium
    (C) dynamic equilibrium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ionic equilibrium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ice and water kept in a perfectly insulated thermos flask at 273K and the atmospheric pressure are in an equilibrium state and the system shows interesting characteristic features. The mass of ice and water do not change with time and the temperature remains constant. However, the equilibrium is not static. The intense activity can be noticed at the boundary between ice and water. Molecules from the liquid water collide against ice and adhere to it and some molecules of ice escape into the liquid phase. There is no change of mass of ice and water, as the rates of transfer of molecules from ice into water and of reverse transfer from water into the ice are equal at atmosphere pressure and 273K.

Q4. H_2O(l) $ \rightleftharpoons $ H_2O (vap). This equation best illustrates the ________.
    (A) Solid-gas Equilibrium
    (B) Ionic equilibrium
    (C) Liquid-Vapour Equilibrium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Liquid-solid Equilibrium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The number of water molecules from the gaseous state into the liquid state also increases till the equilibrium is attained i.e., rate of evaporation = rate of condensation.
At equilibrium, the pressure exerted by the water molecules at a given temperature remains constant and is called the equilibrium.

Q5. During the process of transformation from liquid to vapour, the pressure exerted by the water molecules at a given temperature remains constant. This is called ________.
    (A) melting point of water
    (B) freezing point of water
    (C) boiling point of water
    (D) vapour pressure of water   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The number of water molecules from the gaseous state into the liquid state also increases till the equilibrium is attained.
i.e.rate of evaporation = rate of condensation
H_2O(l) $ \rightleftharpoons $ H_2O (vap)
At equilibrium, the pressure exerted by the water molecules at a given temperature remains constant and is called the equilibrium vapour pressure of water increases with temperature.

Q6. If we place solid iodine in a closed vessel after some time the vessel gets filled up with violet vapour. When equilibrium is attained, the intensity of colour will be:
    (A) decreases
    (B) increases
    (C) constant   <-- CORRECT
    (D) no colour at all
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We place solid iodine in a closed vessel, after some time the vessel gets filled up with violet vapour and the intensity of colour increases with time. After a certain time, the intensity of colour becomes constant and at this stage, equilibrium is attained. Hence solid iodine sublimes to give iodine vapour and the iodine vapour condenses to give solid iodine. The equilibrium can be represented as I_2 (solid) $ \rightleftharpoons $ I_2 (vapour).

Q7. The boiling point of water at atmospheric pressure is ________.
    (A) 110° C
    (B) 100° C   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 95° C
    (D) 90° C
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Water and water vapour are in equilibrium position at atmospheric pressure (1.013 bar) and at 100°C in a closed vessel. The boiling point of water is 100°C at 1.013 bar pressure. For any pure liquid at one atmospheric pressure (1.013 bar), the temperature at which the liquid and vapours are at equilibrium is called the normal boiling point of the liquid. The boiling point of the liquid depends on the atmospheric pressure.

Q8. _______ states that "the mass of a gas dissolved in a given mass of a solvent at any temperature is proportional to the pressure of the gas above the solvent."
    (A) Arrhenius
    (B) Haber's process
    (C) Le Chatelier
    (D) Henry’s law   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: This equilibrium is governed by Henry’s law, which states that the mass of a gas dissolved in a given mass of a solvent at any temperature is proportional to the pressure of the gas above the solvent. This amount decreases with an increase in temperature.

Q9. When the soda bottle is opened, some of the dissolved carbon dioxide gas escapes because of:
    (A) difference in solubility of carbon dioxide at different pressures.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) some of the undissolved carbon dioxide gas in the soda bottle.
    (C) difference in solubility of carbon dioxide at different temperatures.
    (D) to reach a new equilibrium condition required for the higher pressure.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Soda water, like other carbonated beverages, contains carbon dioxide that has dissolved under pressure. When the pressure is released by opening the soda container, the liquid cannot hold as much carbon dioxide, so the excess bubbles out of the solution. If the soda is left open, additional carbon dioxide will slowly escape into the air. Under warm conditions, the carbon dioxide leaves the solution faster.

Q10. The dynamic nature of chemical equilibrium can be demonstrated in the synthesis of ammonia by Haber's process. Choose the appropriate option given below:
    (A) by using hydrogen isotope
    (B) by using deuterium isotope   <-- CORRECT
    (C) by maintaining high temperature and low pressure
    (D) by using sulphur isotope
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The use of isotope (deuterium) in the formation of ammonia clearly indicates that chemical reactions reach a state of dynamic equilibrium in which the rates of forward and reverse reactions are equal and there is no net change in composition.

Q11. At a given temperature, equilibrium is possible only in a system which is a:
    (A) partially closed system
    (B) open system
    (C) partially open system
    (D) closed system   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Equilibrium is possible only in a closed system at a given temperature for physical processes. When equilibrium is attained for a physical process, it is characterized by the constant value of one of its parameters at a given temperature.

Q12. For liquid $ \rightleftharpoons $ vapour equilibrium, at a given temperature, the constant is ________.
    (A) vapour pressure   <-- CORRECT
    (B) mass of a gas
    (C) mass of a solvent
    (D) solubility
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The vapour pressure is constant at a given temperature for liquid $ \rightleftharpoons $ vapour equilibrium. The equilibrium vapour pressure of a compound at a given temperature is an intrinsic property of the compound, meaning it does not depend on variables like volume, the quantity of the compound, etc.

Q13. Which of the following statements is incorrect?
 In equilibrium mixture of ice and water kept in perfectly insulated flask mass of ice and water does not change with time.
 The intensity of red colour increases when oxalic acid is added to a solution containing iron (III) nitrate and potassium thiocyanate.
 On addition of a catalyst, the equilibrium constant value is not affected.
 Equilibrium constant for a reaction with negative ΔH value decreases as the temperature increases
    (A) C
    (B) D
    (C) B   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The intensity of red colour increases when oxalic acid is added to a solution containing iron (III) nitrate and potassium thiocyanate.

Q14. For the dissolution of solids in liquids, at a given temperature, the constant is ________.
    (A) mass of the solvent
    (B) mass of the solute
    (C) pressure
    (D) solubility   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: It is because at a particular temperature only a certain amount of solute can be dissolved. But it may be increased after increasing the temperature, so the solubility is constant at a given temperature.

Q15. For dissolution of gases in liquids, the concentration of a gas in a liquid is:
    (A) lower to the pressure of the gas as compared to the liquid
    (B) proportional to the vapour pressure of the gas
    (C) equal to the pressure of the gas in relation to the liquid
    (D) proportional to the pressure of the gas over the liquid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: For the dissolution of gases in liquids, Henry's Law is applicable i.e. the mass of the gas dissolved in a given solvent at any temperature is proportional to the pressure of the gas above the solvent.

Equilibrium CBSE Online Test 02  (id 962) [PAID]

Q1. The concentrations in an equilibrium mixture are related by the following equilibrium equation, ${{\text{K}}_{\text{c}}} = $ $\frac{{\left[ C \right]\left[ D \right]}}{{\left[ A \right]\left[ B \right]}}$ Where Kc is called as ________.
    (A) active mass constant
    (B) reaction quotient
    (C) molecular constant
    (D) equilibrium constant   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let us consider a general reversible reaction:
A + B $ \rightleftharpoons $ C + D
where A and B are the reactants, C and D are the products in the balanced chemical equation.
On the basis of experimental studies of many reversible reactions, opposed in 1864 that the concentrations in an equilibrium mixture are related by the following equilibrium equation, K_c = [C] [D] /[A] [B]
Where K_c is the equilibrium constant and the expression on the right side is called the equilibrium constant expression.

Q2. Equilibrium constant for the reaction, 4NH_3(g) + 5O_2(g) $\longrightarrow$ 4NO(g) + 6H_2O (g) is written as:
    (A) ${\text{1}}/{\left[ {{\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right]^{\text{4}}}{\left[ {{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}} \right]^{\text{5}}}$
    (B) ${{\text{K}}_{\text{c}}} = {\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}\left] {^{\text{4}}} \right[{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}\left] {^{\text{5}}/{\text{ }}} \right[{\left[ {{\text{NO}}} \right]^{\text{4}}}{\left[ {{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}} \right]^{\text{6}}}$
    (C) ${\left[ {{\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right]^{\text{4}}}{\left[ {{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}} \right]^{\text{5}}}/{\text{ 2}}$
    (D) ${{\text{K}}_{\text{c}}} = {\text{ }}{\left[ {{\text{NO}}} \right]^{\text{4}}}{\left[ {{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}} \right]^{\text{6}}}/{\text{ }}{\left[ {{\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right]^{\text{4}}}{\left[ {{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}} \right]^{\text{5}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: K_c is equilibrium constant $ = \frac{{{{\left[ {products} \right]}^{stoichiimetry}}}}{{{{[reactant]}^{stoichiimetry}}}}$ 
${{\text{K}}_{\text{c}}} = {\text{ }}{\left[ {{\text{NO}}} \right]^{\text{4}}}{\left[ {{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}} \right]^{\text{6}}}/{\text{ }}{\left[ {{\text{N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right]^{\text{4}}}{\left[ {{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}} \right]^{\text{5}}}$

Q3. For reactions involving gases, however, it is usually more convenient to express the equilibrium constant in terms of
    (A) temperature
    (B) partial pressure   <-- CORRECT
    (C) molar concentration of the products
    (D) molar concentration of the reactants
    Answer: B
    Explanation: K_p = $\frac{\left(\mathbf{P}_{\text { products }}\right)^{\text { sttoichimery }}}{\left(\mathbf{P}_{\text { reactant }}\right)^{\text { stoichimetry }}}$

Q4. For reactions in equilibrium involving gases, like N_2(g) + 3H_2 $ \rightleftharpoons $ 2NH_3(g), choose one of the following options.
    (A) K_p = K_c (RT)^-2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) K_c=K_p(RT)^3
    (C) K_p =K_c (RT)^3
    (D) K_c = K_p
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In reaction, N_2 (g) + 3H_2 (g) $ \rightleftharpoons $ 2NH_3 (g)
Here, $\Delta$n_g = 2- (1+3) = 2 - 4 = -2
Therefore, K_p = K_c (RT)^-2

Q5. If the K_c is neither too small nor too large, one of the following will happen:
    (A) reaction hardly proceeds
    (B) both reactants and products are at equilibrium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) reaction proceeds to completion
    (D) reaction proceeds very slowly.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A High value of K is a high concentration of products. If Kc > 10^3, products predominate over reactants.
 If Kc < 10^–3, reactants predominate over products, i.e., if Kc is very small, the reaction proceeds rarely.
 If Kc is in the range of 10^– 3 to 10^3, appreciable concentrations of both reactants and products are present.

Q6. Find K_c for the following reaction, if CO_2 pressure is in atmospheres:
CaCO_3(s) $\rightarrow$ CaO(s) + CO_2(g), K_p = 2.1 $\times$ 10^-^4 (at 1000K).
    (A) 4.1 $\times$ 10^-6
    (B) 2.4 $\times$ 10^-6
    (C) 1.1 $\times$ 10^-6
    (D) 2.6 $\times$ 10^-6   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Kp = Kc (RT)^∆n
Here change in no. of moles i.e. ∆n = 1 because it is taken only for gaseous products and reactants by differing reactant from product.
$2.1 \times {10^{ - 4}} = {K_c}{(0.0821 \times 1000)^1}$
${K_c} = \frac{{2.1 \times {{10}^{ - 4}}}}{{82.1}} = 2.57 \times {10^{ - 6}} = 2.6 \times {10^{ - 6}}$

Q7. A particular ratio of product to reactant helps in predicting the direction in which a given reaction will proceed at any stage is called ________.
    (A) molecular constant
    (B) active mass constant
    (C) reaction quotient   <-- CORRECT
    (D) equilibrium constant
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The reaction quotient Q. For a general reaction: aA + bB ⇌ cC + dD
Qc = [C]^c [D]^d / [A]^a [B]^b 
Then, If Q_c > Kc,
the reaction will proceed in the direction of reactants (reverse reaction).
If Q_c < K_c, the reaction will proceed in the direction of the products (forward reaction).
If Q_c = K_c, the reaction mixture is already at equilibrium.

Q8. The value of K_c for a reaction is directly related to the thermodynamics of the reaction and in particular with:
    (A) $\Delta {{\text{n}}_{{\text{gas}}}}$
    (B) Q_C
    (C) $\Delta$G   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Q_P
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A mathematical expression of this thermodynamic view of equilibrium can be described by the following equation: $\Delta$G = $\Delta$G^0 + RT ln Q
where G^0 is standard Gibbs energy.
At equilibrium, when $\Delta$G = 0 and Q = K_c,
$\Delta$G = $\Delta$G^0 + RT ln K = 0
$\Delta$G^0 = – RT lnK (7.22)
lnK = – $\Delta$G^0 / RT
Taking antilog of both sides, we get,
K = e^– $\Delta$G0 / RT

Q9. In order to decide what course the reaction adopts and make a qualitative prediction about the effect of a change in conditions on equilibrium we use:
    (A) Arrhenius theory,
    (B) Bronsted-Lowry theory,
    (C) Lewis theory
    (D) Le Chatelier's theory   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Le Chatelier’s principle- It states that a change in any of the factors that determine the equilibrium conditions of a system will cause the system to change in such a manner so as to reduce or to counteract the effect of the change.

Q10. A catalyst increases the rate of the chemical reaction for the conversion of reactants to products by:
    (A) lowering the temperature
    (B) lowering the equilibrium composition of a reaction mixture
    (C) increasing the activation energy for the forward reaction
    (D) making available a new low energy pathway   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A catalyst increases the rate of the chemical reaction by making available a new low energy pathway for the conversion of reactants to products. It increases the rate of forward and reverse reactions that pass through the same transition state and does not affect equilibrium. Catalyst lowers the activation energy for the forward and reverse reactions by exactly the same amount. Catalyst does not affect the equilibrium composition of a reaction mixture. It does not appear in the balanced chemical equation or in the equilibrium constant expression.

Q11. A bare proton, H^+ is very reactive and cannot exist freely in aqueous solutions. Thus, it bonds to the oxygen atom of a solvent water molecule to give:
    (A) ${H_3}O_2^ + $
    (B) ${H_3}O_3^ + $
    (C) ${H_3}O_4^ + $
    (D) H_3O^+   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Hydrogen ion by itself is a bare proton with a very small size (~10–15 m radius) and intense electric field, binds itself with the water molecule at one of the two available lone pairs on it giving H_3O^+. This species has been detected in many compounds (e.g., H_3O^+Cl ^– ) in the solid-state.
In aqueous solution, the hydronium ion is further hydrated to give species like ${H_5}O_2^ + $.

Q12. Hydronium ion concentration in molarity is more conveniently expressed on a logarithmic scale known as the _______.
    (A) basic scale
    (B) litmus scale
    (C) pH scale   <-- CORRECT
    (D) acidic scale
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Hydronium ion concentration in molarity is more conveniently expressed on a logarithmic scale known as the pH scale. The pH of a solution is defined as the negative logarithm to base 10 of the activity (H^+) of hydrogen ion. In dilute solutions (< 0.01 M), the activity of hydrogen ion (H^+) is equal in magnitude to molarity represented by [H^+].
From the definition of pH= – log H^+= – log [H^+] / mol L^–1.
Thus, an acidic solution of HCl (10^-2 M) will have a pH = 2.
Similarly, a basic solution of NaOH having [OH^​​​​​-] =10^-4 M and [H_3O^+] = 10^-10 M will have a pH = 10.
At 25 °C, pure water has a concentration of hydrogen ions, [H^+] = 10^-7M. Hence, the pH of pure water is given as: pH = –log(10^–7) = 7.

Q13. The solutions which resist change in pH on dilution or with the addition of small amounts of acid or alkali is called ________.
    (A) Bronsted-Lowry acids and bases
    (B) Conjugate pair of acid-base
    (C) Buffer solutions   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Electrolytic solutions
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The solutions which resist change in pH on dilution or with the addition of small amounts of acid or alkali are called Buffer Solutions. Buffer solutions of known pH can be prepared from the knowledge of pKa of the acid or pK b of base and by controlling the ratio of the salt and acid or salt and base. A mixture of acetic acid and sodium acetate acts as a buffer solution around pH 4.75 and a mixture of ammonium chloride and ammonium hydroxide acts as a buffer around pH 9.25.

Q14. We know that the relationship between K_c and K_p is K_p = K_c (RT)^$\Delta$n. What would be the value of $\Delta$n for the reaction NH_4CI(s) $ \rightleftharpoons $ NH_3(g) + HCl (g)?
    (A) 2.0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.5
    (C) 1
    (D) 1.5
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\Delta n_{gas}$ = 2 = $n_{gas}(\text {Product})$ - $n_{g a s}(r e a c t a n t)$

Q15. For the reaction ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ }}{{\text{I}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right)$ $ \rightleftharpoons $ 2HI (g), the standard free energy is $\Delta {G^ - } > 0$ The equilibrium constant (K ) would be __________.
    (A) K < 1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) K = 1
    (C) K = 0
    (D) K > 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $ΔG0=-RTlnK$
• If $∆G0 > 0,$ then $–∆G0 /RT$ is negative, and $e–∆G0 /RT < 1,$ that is , $K < 1,$ which implies a non-spontaneous reaction or a reaction which proceeds in the forward direction to such a small degree that only a very minute quantity of product is formed.

Q1. Which of the following is not a general characteristic of equilibria involving physical processes?
    (A) The opposing processes occur at the same rate and there is dynamic but stable condition
    (B) All the physical processes stop at equilibrium.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) All measurable properties of the system remain constant.
    (D) Equilibrium is possible only in a closed system at a given temperature.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: This is a wrong statement that all the physical processes stop at equilibrium, the processes never stops at equilibrium i.e. the rate of formation of products and rate of formation of reactants become equal.

Q2. PCl_5, PCl_3 and Cl_2 are at equilibrium at 500 K in a closed container and their concentrations are 0.8 $\times$ 10^-3 mol L^-1, 1.2 $\times$ 10^-3 mol L^-1 and 1.2 $\times$ 10^-3 mol L^-1 respectively. The value of K_c for the reaction PCl_5(g) $\rightleftharpoons$ PCl_3(g) + Cl_2(g) will be:
    (A) $0.{\text{55 }} \times {\text{ 1}}{0^{\text{4}}}$
    (B) ${\text{1}}.{\text{8 }} \times {\text{ 1}}{0^{\text{3}}}$
    (C) ${\text{1}}.{\text{8 }} \times {\text{ 1}}{0^{ - {\text{3}}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\text{1}}.{\text{6}} \times {\text{ 1}}{0^{\text{3}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Kc = $\frac{{\left[ {PC{l_3}} \right]\left[ {C{l_2}} \right]}}{{\left[ {PC{l_5}} \right]}}$ = 1.2 x 10^-3 x 1.2 x 10^-3 / 0.8 x 10^-3 = 1.8 x 10^-3 L mol^-1

Q3. Which of the following statements is correct?
 In equilibrium mixture of ice and water kept in perfectly insulated flask mass of ice and water does not change with time.
 The intensity of red colour increases when oxalic acid is added to a solution containing iron (III). nitrate and potassium thiocyanate.
 On addition of catalyst the equilibrium constant value is not affected.
 Equilibrium constant for a reaction with negative $\Delta $H value decreases as the temperature increases
    (A) Option (iv)
    (B) Option (i)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Option (ii)
    (D) Option (iii)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Ice and water kept in a perfectly insulated thermos flask (no exchange of heat between its contents and the surroundings) at 273K and the atmospheric pressure are in equilibrium state and the system shows interesting characteristic features. We observe that the mass of ice and water do not change with time and the temperature remains constant.

Q4. When hydrochloric acid is added to cobalt nitrate solution at room temperature, the following reaction takes place and the reaction mixture becomes blue. On cooling the mixture it becomes pink. On the basis of this information mark the correct answer.
$\mathop {{{\left[ {{\text{Co }}\left( {{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}} \right){\text{6}}} \right]}^{{\text{3}} + }}\left( {{\text{aq}}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ 4C}}{{\text{l}}^ - }(aq)}\limits_{pink}$ $ \rightleftharpoons \mathop {{{\left[ {{\text{CoC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}} \right]}^{{\text{2}} - }}\left( {{\text{aq}}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ 6}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}(l)}\limits_{Blue} $
    (A) $\Delta {\text{H}} = $ 0 for the reaction
    (B) $\Delta {\text{H}}$ > 0 for the reaction   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\Delta {\text{H}} < $ 0 for the reaction
    (D) The sign of $\Delta $H cannot be predicted on the basis of this information.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For an endothermic reaction - If temperature is decreased reaction will shift to backward direction
$\mathop {{{[Co{{({H_2}O)}_6}]}^{3 + }}(aq)}\limits_{pink} + \mathop {4C{l^ - }(aq)}\limits_{colourless} \rightleftharpoons$ $ \mathop {{{\left[ {{\text{CoC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}} \right]}^{{\text{2}} - }}\left( {{\text{aq}}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ 6}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}(l)}\limits_{Blue} $
At room temperature, the equilibrium mixture is blue due to [CoCl 4 ]^2–. When cooled in a freezing mixture, the colour of the mixture turns pink due to [Co(H2O)6 ]^3+.

Q5. The pH of neutral water at ${\text{25}}^\circ {\text{C}}$ is 7.0. As the temperature increases, ionisation of water increases, however, the concentration of ${{\text{H}}^ + }$ ions and $O{H^ - }$ ions are equal. What will be the pH of pure water at ${\text{6}}0^\circ {\text{C}}?$
    (A) Greater than 7.0
    (B) Equal to 7.0
    (C) Less than 7.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Equal to zero
    Answer: C
    Explanation: pH of water will be less 7 only. Water will be acidic even at 60°C

Q6. The ionisation constant of an acid, K_a, is the measure of strength of an acid. The K_a values of acetic acid, hypochlorous acid and formic acid are 1.74 $\times$ 10^-5, 3.0 $\times$ 10^-8 and 1.8 $\times$ 10^-4 respectively. Which of the following orders of pH of 0.1 mol dm^-3 solutions of these acids is correct?
    (A) hypochlorous acid > acetic acid > formic acid
    (B) acetic acid > hypochlorous acid > formic acid
    (C) formic acid > hypochlorous acid > acetic acid
    (D) formic acid > acetic acid > hypochlorous acid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Here, K_a for Formic Acid (HCOOH) = 1.8 $\times$ 10^–4 , Acetic Acid (CH_3COOH) = 1.74 $\times$ 10^–5 and Hypochlorous Acid (HCIO) = 3.0 $\times$ 10^–8
At a given temperature T, K_a is a measure of the strength of the acid HX i.e., larger the value of K_a , the stronger is the acid. K_a is a dimensionless quantity with the understanding that the standard state concentration of all species is 1M.
K_a = [H^+][X^-] / [HX]
${[{H_3}{O^ + }]\; = \;\sqrt {{K_a}.C} }$
${pH = \; - \log \;[{H_3}{O^ + }]}$
larger the value of K_a larger will be H_3O^+,hence lower will be pH

Q7. K_a_1, K_a2 and K_a3 are the respective ionisation constants for the following reactions:
H_2S $ \rightleftharpoons $ H^+ + HS^-
HS^- $ \rightleftharpoons $ H^+ + S^2-
H_2S $ \rightleftharpoons $ 2H^+ + S^2-
The correct relationship between K_a1, K_a2 and K_a3 is:
    (A) ${{\text{K}}_{{\text{a3}}}} = {{\text{K}}_{{\text{a1}}}}/{{\text{K}}_{{\text{a2}}}}$
    (B) ${{\text{K}}_{{\text{a3}}}} = {{\text{K}}_{{\text{a1}}}} + {{\text{K}}_{{\text{a2}}}}$
    (C) $\;K_{a_3}=K_{a_1}\times\;K_{a_2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${{\text{K}}_{{\text{a3}}}} = {{\text{K}}_{{\text{a1}}}}-{{\text{K}}_{{\text{a2}}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The ionization reactions for example for a dibasic acid H_2X are represented by the equations:
H_2X(aq) ⇌ H^+ (aq) + HX^– (aq)
HX^– (aq) ⇌ H^+ (aq) + X^2– (aq)
the corresponding equilibrium constants are given below:$K_{a_1}=\frac{\lbrack H^+\rbrack\lbrack HX^–\rbrack}{\lbrack H_2X\rbrack}$and $K_{a_2}=\frac{\lbrack H^+\rbrack\lbrack X^{2–}\rbrack}{\lbrack HX^-\rbrack}$
Here, Ka_1 and Ka_2 are called the first and second ionization constants respectively of the acid H_2 X.
For ${\;{H_2}S\; \rightleftharpoons \;2{H^ + }\; + \;{S^{2 - }}}$
${{K_{{a_3}}} = \frac{{{{[{H^ + }]}^2}[{X^2}]}}{{[{H_2}X]}}}$
It is clear that, $K_{a_1}\times K_{a_2}=\frac{\lbrack H^+\rbrack\lbrack HX^–\rbrack}{\lbrack H_2X\rbrack}\times\frac{\lbrack H^+\rbrack\lbrack X^{2–}\rbrack}{\lbrack HX^-\rbrack}=\frac{\lbrack H^+\rbrack^2\lbrack X^{2–}\rbrack}{\lbrack H_2X\rbrack}\;=K_{a_3}$
Therefore, $\;K_{a_3}=K_{a_1}\times\;K_{a_2}$

Q8. The acidity of BF_3 can be explained on the basis of which of the following concepts?
    (A) Bronsted Lowry as well as Lewis concept
    (B) Arrhenius concept
    (C) Lewis concept   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Bronsted Lowry concept
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As BF_3​ is an electron-deficient species that is why it is a Lewis acid. (All Lewis acid can accept a pair of electrons).

Q9. Which of the following will produce a buffer solution when mixed in equal volumes?
    (A) 0.1 mol dm^-3 NH_4OH and 0.05 mol dm^-3 HCl   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.1 mol dm^-3 CH_4COONa and 0.1 mol dm^-3 NaOH
    (C) 0.1 mol dm^-3 NH_4OH and 0.1 mol dm^-3 HCl
    (D) 0.05 mol dm^-3 NH_4OH and 0.1 mol dm^-3 HCl
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\begin{array}{l}\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;NH_4OH+\;HCl\rightarrow NH_4Cl\;+\;H_2O\\at,\;t=0\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;0.1\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;0.05\\at,\;t=t\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;0.05\;\;\;\;\;\;\;0\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;0.05\\\end{array}$
At the end of the reaction we will get the mixture of weak base (NH_4OH) and salt of weak base and strong acid (NH_4Cl).

Q10. In which of the following solvents is silver chloride most soluble?
    (A) H_2O
    (B) 0.1 mol dm^-3 HCl solution
    (C) 0.1 mol dm^-3 AgNO_3
    (D) Aqueous ammonia solution   <-- CORRECT

Q11. What will be the value of pH of 00.1 mol dm^-3 CH_3COOH (K_a = 1.74 $\times$ 10^-5)?
    (A) 3.0
    (B) 3.6
    (C) 3.9
    (D) 3.4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Acetic acid is a weak acid with K_a = 1.74 $\times$ 10^-5 and in this case cweak acid >>> K_0,
that is the equation to use is: [H^+] = (Ka.Cweakacid)^1/2 = (1.7 $\times$ 10^-5 $\times$ 0.01)^1/2 = 4.3 $\times$ 10^-4
pH = -log [H^+] = - log (4.3 $\times$ 10^-4) = - [log 4.3 + (-4)log 10] = -[0.633^-4] = 3.367

Q12. K_a for CH_3COOH is $1.8 \times {10^{ - 5}}$ and K_b for NH_4OH is $1.8 \times {10^{ - 5}}$. The pH of ammonium acetate will be
    (A) Between 6 and 7
    (B) 4.75
    (C) 7.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 7.005
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ammonium acetate is a salt of weak acid and weak base.
pH = 1/2[pK_w + pK_a - pKb].
$ = 1/2[14 - \log (1.8 \times {10^{ - 5}}) + \log (1.8 \times {10^{ - 5}}) = 7.0$

Q13. Which of the following options will be correct for the stage of half completion of the reaction A $ \rightleftharpoons $ B.
    (A) $\Delta {{\text{G}}^0} > {\text{ }}0$
    (B) $\Delta {{\text{G}}^0} = {\text{ }}0$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\Delta {{\text{G}}^0} < {\text{ }}0$
    (D) $\Delta {G^0} = - RT{\ln _2}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: we know that $\Delta {G^0} = - RT\ln K$
for the stage of half completion of the reaction A $ \rightleftharpoons $ B.
Therefore K = 1
[A] = [B]
$\Delta {G^0} = - RT\ln 1$
$\Delta {G^0} = 0$

Q14. On increasing the pressure, in which direction will the gas phase reaction proceed to re-establish equilibrium is predicted by applying the Le Chatelier’s principle. Consider the reaction. ${N_2}(g) + 3{H_2}(g) \rightleftharpoons 2N{H_3}$ (g) Which of the following is correct, if the total pressure at which the equilibrium is established, is increased without changing the temperature?
    (A) K will increase initially and decrease when pressure is very high
    (B) K will decrease
    (C) K will remain same   <-- CORRECT
    (D) K will increase
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the reaction $Na(g) + 3{H_2}(g) \rightleftharpoons 2N{H_3}(g)$
According to the the Le Chatelier’s principle, at constant temperture, the equilibrium constant will change but K will remain same.

Q15. What will be the correct order of vapour pressure of water, acetone and ether At ${\text{3}}0^\circ {\text{C}}$. Given that among these compounds, water has maximum boiling point and ether has minimum boiling point?
    (A) Acetone < ether < water
    (B) Ether < acetone < water
    (C) Water < ether < acetone
    (D) Water < acetone < ether   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Greater the boiling point, less is the vapour pressure. Hence, the correct order of vapour pressure will be water < acetone < ether.

Q1. At 500 K, equilibrium constant, ${{\text{K}}_{\text{c}}}$, for the following reaction is 5.2. $\frac{1}{2}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right) + \frac{1}{2}{\text{ }}{{\text{I}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right) \rightleftharpoons $ HI (g) What would be the equilibrium constant Kc for the reaction $2HI(g) \rightleftharpoons {H_2}(g) + {I_2}(g)$
    (A) 0.4
    (B) 0.04   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2.5
    (D) 25
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The second equation can be obtained by reversing the 1st reaction. 
${K_1} = [HI]/{[{H_2}]^{1/2}} \times {[12]^{1/2}}$
squrare the equation
${K_1} = {[HI]^2}/[{H_2}] \times [{I_2}]$ ......... (1)
${K_2} = [{H_2}] \times [{I_2}[/[HI]$ ......... (2)
From eq (1) and (2)
${({K_1})_2} = 1/{K_2}$
(5.2)^2 = 1/K_2
K_2 = 1/27.04 = 0.0369

Q2. In which of the following reactions, the equilibrium remains unaffected on addition of small amount of argon at constant volume?
    (A) ${N_2}(g) + 3{H_2}(g) \rightleftharpoons 2N{H_3}(g)$
    (B) H_2 (g) + I_2 (g) $ \rightleftharpoons $ 2HI (g)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${\text{PC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{5}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right)$ $ \rightleftharpoons $ PCl_3 (g) + Cl_2 (g)
    (D) The equilibrium will remain unaffected in all the three cases.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For addition of inert gas at constant pressure, the reaction having same number of moles in reactant and product side will not go any change in the position of equilibrium.
H_2 (g) + I_2 (g) $ \rightleftharpoons $ 2HI (g)
The equilibrium constant will be affected on addition of inert gas in all the three cases.

Q3. For the reaction N_2O_4(g) $ \rightleftharpoons $ 2NO2(g), the value of K is 50 at 400 K and 1700 at 500 K. Which of the following option is incorrect?
    (A) If NO_2 (g) and N_2O_4 (g) are mixed at 400 K at partial pressures 20 bar and 2 bar respectively, more N_2O_4 (g) will be formed.
    (B) The entropy of the system increases.
    (C) The reaction is endothermic.
    (D) The reaction is exothermic.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As the value of K increases with an increase in temperature and K = K_f / K_b._ This means that K_f increases, i.e. forward reaction is favoured. Hence, the reaction is endothermic.

Q4. At a particular temperature and atmospheric pressure, the solid and liquid phases of a pure substance can exist in equilibrium. Which of the following term defines this temperature?
    (A) Phase change temperature
    (B) Normal melting point and Freezing point   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Boiling point
    (D) Equilibrium temperature
    Answer: B
    Explanation: These are normal melting point and freezing point since they are measured at atmospheric pressure.

Q5. The ionisation of hydrochloric in water is given below:
${\text{HCl }}\left( {{\text{aq}}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }}\left( {\text{l}} \right)$ $ \rightleftharpoons $ $\begin{array}{l}H_3O^+\:+\;Cl^-\\\end{array}$
Label two conjugate acid-base pairs respectively in the ionization.
    (A) HCl, H_3O^+and H_3O^+ ,Cl^-
    (B) H_2O, Cl^- and H_3O^+ ,HCl
    (C) HCl, Cl^- and^ H_2O, H_3O^+ .   <-- CORRECT
    (D) H_3O,Cl^- and HCl, H_2O.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A species formed by receiving a proton from a base is known as conjugate acid and Conjugate base is a species formed by the removal of proton from an acid.
In this case, Cl^​​​​​- is formed by donating a proton to water molecule hence it is a conjugate base while protonated water (H_3O^+)becomes conjugate acid.

Q6. For the reaction H_2(g) + I_2(g) $ \Leftrightarrow $ 2HI (g), the standard free energy is $\Delta$G^⊖ > 0. The equilibrium constant (K ) would be __________.
    (A) K = 0
    (B) K = 1
    (C) K < 1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) K > 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The given reaction is:
$H_{2}(g)+I_{2}(g) \rightleftharpoons 2 H I(g); \triangle G^{0}=0$
By, thermodynamical view of equilibrium, $\Delta G^{0}=-R T \ln K>0$
free energy
$ \Rightarrow$ −RTlnK>0
Now, R>0&T>0
$ \Rightarrow$ −lnK>0
$ \Rightarrow$ K<1

Q7. BF_3 does not have a proton but still acts as an acid and reacts with NH_3. Choose the correct option.
    (A) BF_3 is a Lewis base and coordinate bond is formed.
    (B) BF_3 acts as Lewis acid and coordinate bond is formed.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) BF_3 is a Brönsted acid and coordinate bond is formed.
    (D) BF_3 is a Brönsted base and coordinate bond is formed.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: BF_3 is an electron-deficient compound. Hence, it acts as Lewis acid.
NH_3 has a lone pair of electrons. Hence, it acts as a Lewis base.
A coordinate bond is formed between the two, as the nitrogen atom of ammonia acts as an electron donor, while B of BF_3 acts as an electron acceptor.
H_3N: $\rightarrow$ BF_3

Q8. 0.3g of Ca(OH)_2 is dissolved in water to give 500 mL of solution. The pH of the solution is ________.
    (A) 12.33   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 14.027
    (C) 10.099
    (D) 11.053
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Molarity=$\;\frac{mass\;of\;Ca(OH)_2\times1000}{Molar\;mass\;\times Volume}=\frac{0.3\times1000}{56\times500}=$ 0.0107M
The chemical reaction involved are, CaO + H_2O = Ca(OH)_2
Here, Ca(OH)_2 = Ca^2+ + 2OH^-
Concentration of OH^- = 2[OH^-] = 2 $\times$ 0.0107 = 0.0214M
Now,
K_w = [H_3O^+][OH^-] ${ \Rightarrow [{H_3}{O^ + }] = \frac{{{K_w}}}{{[O{H^ - }]}} = \frac{{{{10}^{ - 14}}}}{{0.0214}}}$ = 46.27 $\times$ 10^-14
Therefore, pH = -log[H_3O^+] = - log [46.27 $\times$ 10^-14] = 12.33

Q9. Calculate the hydrogen ion concentration in the human blood whose pH is 7.38.
    (A) 4.17 $\times$ 10^-8 M   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 6.33 $\times$ 10^18 M
    (C) 5.16 $\times$ 10^-8 M
    (D) 3.19 $\times$ 10^-8 M
    Answer: A
    Explanation: pH = -log[H^+]
7.38 = -log[H^+]
$\log\lbrack H^+\rbrack\;=-7.38=\overset-8.62$
Taking antilog on both sides, we get [H^+] = 4.17 $\times$ 10^-8 M

Q10. The ionization constant of acetic acid is $1.74 \times {10^{ - 5}}$. Calculate the degree of dissociation of acetic acid in its 0.05 M solution. Calculate the concentration of acetate ion in the solution and its pH.
    (A) 0.00193M and pH 3.03
    (B) 0.00203M and pH 3.03
    (C) 0.00093M and pH 3.03   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.00013M and pH 3.03
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\alpha=\sqrt{\frac{K_a}C}$
Here, C=0.05M,
 $K_a=1.74\times10^{-5}$
$\alpha = {\left\{ {\frac{{1.74 \times {{10}^{ - 5}}}}{{0.05}}} \right\}^{1/2}}$ $\alpha = {\{ 1.74 \times {10^{ - 5}}/0.05\} ^{1/2}}$
$\alpha = [34.8 \times {10^{ - 5}}]$
$\alpha = (3.48)1/2 \times {10^{ - 4}}$
$\alpha = 1.86 \times {10^{ - 2}}$
CH_3COOH = CH_3COO^- + H^+
Concentration of $C{H_3}CO{O^ - } = C\alpha $
$ = 0.05 \times 1.86 \times {10^{ - 2}} = 0.093 \times {10^{ - 2}} = 0.00093M$
Since [CH_3COO^-] = [H^+]
[H^+] = 0.00093 = $0.093 \times {10^{ - 2}}$
$pH = - \log [{H^ + }] = - \log [0.093 \times {10^{ - 2}}]$
pH = -[log(0.093) + (-2)log10]
$pH = 3.03$

Q11. It has been found that the pH of a 0.01M solution of an organic acid is 4.15. Calculate the ionization constant of the acid, the concentration of the anion, and its pK_a.
    (A) K_a = 5.01 $\times$ 10^-7, [A^-] = 7.08 $\times$ 10^-5 and pK_a = 5.3007
    (B) K_a = 5.01 $\times$ 10^-7, [A^-] = 7.99 $\times$ 10^-5 and pK_a = 7.5009
    (C) K_a = 5.01 $\times$ 10^-7, [A^-] = 7.39 $\times$ 10^-5 and pK_a = 6.3001
    (D) K_a = 5.01 $\times$ 10^-7, [A^-] = 7.08 $\times$ 10^-5 and pK_a = 6.3001   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: pH = -log[H^+]
4.15 = -log[H^+]
[H^+] = 7.08 $\times$ 10^-5 = [A^-]
K_a = [H^+][A^-][HA]
K_a = 5.01 $\times$ 10^-7
pK_a = - log [5.01 $\times$ 10^-7] = 6.3001

Q12. If in the reaction ${{\text{N}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$ $ \rightleftharpoons $ ${\text{2N}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}},{\text{ x}}$ is that part of ${{\text{N}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$which dissociates, then the number of molecules at equilibrium will be
    (A) 1 + x   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1
    (C) ${\left( {{\text{1 }} + {\text{ xy}}} \right)^{\text{2}}}$
    (D) 3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: N_2O_4 $\rightleftharpoons$ 2NO_2 
 t = 0
 1
 0
 t = t
 1 - x
 2x
total moles at eqm(t = t) = 1 - x + 2x = 1+ x

Q13. The K_sp for Cr(OH)_3 is 1.6 $\times$ 10^-30. The molar solubility of this compound in water is:
    (A) ${\text{1}}.{\text{6 }} \times {\text{ 1}}{0^{-{\text{3}}0}}/{\text{27}}$
    (B) $\sqrt[2]{{1.6 \times {{10}^{ - 30}}}}$
    (C) $\sqrt[4]{{1.6 \times {{10}^{ - 30}}/27}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\sqrt[4]{{1.6 \times {{10}^{ - 30}}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\begin{array}{l}Cr(OH)_3=Cr^{3+}+3\;OH^-\\\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;s\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;\;3s\end{array}$
K_sp = (s)(3s)^3 = 27s^4
^Now, 1.6 $\times$ 10^-30 = 27s^4
${ \Rightarrow {s^4} = \frac{{1.6 \times {{10}^{ - 30}}}}{{27}}}$
${ \Rightarrow s = \sqrt[4]{{\frac{{1.6 \times {{10}^{ - 30}}}}{{27}}}}}$

Q14. The pH of a saturated solution of Ba(OH)_2 is 12. The value of the solubility product (K_sp) of Ba(OH)_2 is:
    (A) 4.0 $\times$ 10^-6
    (B) 5.0 $\times$ 10 ^- 6
    (C) 3.3 $\times$ 10^- 7
    (D) 5 $\times$ 10^-7   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: pH + pOH = 14
pOH = 14 - 12 = 2
pOH = -log[OH^-]
OH^- = 10 - pOH = 10^ - 2 .......... (1)
At equilibrium, Ba(OH)_2 = Ba^+2 + 2OH^-
let [OH^-] = x , therefore, From above equation; 2[OH^-] = 2x = 10 ^- 2 (from equation 1)
Therefore $x = \frac{{{{10}^{ - 2}}}}{2} = 0.5 \times {10^{ - 2}}$
K_sp = [Ba^+2] [OH^-]^2 = [0.5 $\times$ 10^- 2[10^-2]^2 = 0.5 $\times$ 10^- 6 = 5 $\times$ 10^-7

Q15. The solubility of ${\text{C}}{{\text{a}}_{\text{3}}}{\left( {{\text{P}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$ in water is y moles/litre. Its solubility product is:
    (A) 6y^4
    (B) 36y^4
    (C) 64y^5
    (D) 108y^5   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\mathop {C{a_3}}\limits_y {\left( {P{O_4}} \right)_2} = \mathop {3C{a^{2 + }}}\limits_{3y} + \mathop {2PO_4^{3 - }}\limits_{2y} $ 
Solubility product = $K_{sp}=\;\lbrack Ca^{{}_{2+}}\rbrack^3\lbrack PO_4^{3-}\rbrack^2\;=(3y)^3\;(2y)^2\;=108y^5$
