Q1. Consider the following gaseous equilibria with equilibrium constants k_1 and k_2 respectively.
${\text{S}}{{\text{O}}_{{\text{2}}({\text{g}})}} + \frac{1}{2}{{\text{O}}_{{\text{2}}({\text{g}})}}$ $\rightleftharpoons $ ${\text{S}}{{\text{O}}_{{\text{3}}({\text{g}})}}$
${\text{2S}}{{\text{O}}_{{\text{3}}({\text{g}})}}$$\rightleftharpoons $${\text{2S}}{{\text{O}}_{{\text{2}}({\text{g}})}} + {\text{ }}{{\text{O}}_{{\text{2}}({\text{g}})}}$
The equilibrium constants are related as ______.
    (A) ${K_2} = \frac{2}{{\mathop K\nolimits_1^2 }}$
    (B) $\mathop K\nolimits_1^2 = \frac{1}{{{K_2}}} $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $2{K_1} = \mathop K\nolimits_2^2 $
    (D) $\mathop K\nolimits_2^2 = \frac{1}{{{K_1}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Here, $K_1=\frac{\left[SO_3\;(g)\right]}{\left[O_2(g)\right]^{1/2}\left[SO_2(g)\right]}$ ......(1)
$K_2=\frac{\left[SO_2\;(g)\right]^2\left[O_2(g)\right]}{\left[SO_3(g)\right]^2}$ ......... (2)
Square the equation (1) and equal the eq (1) and (2), we get: K_2 = 1/(K_1)^2

Q2. 0.023 g of sodium metal is reacted with 100 cm^3 of water. The pH of the resulting solution is ______.
    (A) 9
    (B) 12   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 10
    (D) 8
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Moles of NaOH formed = 0.023/23 =0.001
Concentration of NaOH = $\frac{\left(0.001\right)\times\left(1000\right)}{\left(100\right)}=0.01$M
pOH=-log[OH-] = - log [ 0.01] = -log [10-2 ] = - (-2) log 10 = 2
We know that, pH + pOH =14
pH =14-2 = 12

Q3. pH value of which one of the following is NOT equal to one?
    (A) 0.1 M HNO_3
    (B) 50 cm^30.4M HCl + 50 cm^30.2 M NaOH
    (C) 0.1 M CH_3COOH   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.05 MH_2SO_4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $CH_3COOH\;+H_2O\rightleftharpoons\;CH_3COO^-+H_3O^+$
Since the dissociation constant of acetic acid is so small, we can assume that the concentration of acetic acid is still approximately 0.1 M even after dissociating.
Also [CH_3COO^-] = [H_3O^+]
Therefore,
$K_a=\frac{\left[CH_3COO^-\right]\left[H_3O^+\right]}{\left[CH_3COOH\right]}$
$\begin{array}{l}K_a=\frac{\left[CH_3COO^-\right]\left[H_3O^+\right]}{\left[CH_3COOH\right]}=\frac{\left[H_3O^+\right]^2}{\left[CH_3COOH\right]}\\\Rightarrow1.7\times10^{-5}\;=\frac{\left[H_3O^+\right]^2}{0.1}\\\Rightarrow\left[H_3O^+\right]=\sqrt{1.7\times10^{-6}}\\\Rightarrow\left[H_3O^+\right]=1.32\times10^{-3}\\now,\;pH=\;-\log\left[H_3O^+\right]=\;-\log1.32\times10^{-3}\;=2.88\end{array}$

Q4. H_2S is passed into one dm^3 of a solution containing 0.1 mole of Zn^2+ and 0.01 mole of Cu^2+ till the sulphide ion concentration reaches 8.1$\times$10^-19 moles. Which one of the following statements is true? [K_sp of ZnS and CuS are 3 $\times$ 10^-22 and 8 $\times$ 10^-36 respectively]
    (A) Both CuS and ZnS precipitate   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Only CuS precipitates
    (C) No precipitation occurs
    (D) Only ZnS precipitates
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Precipitation occurs only when the ionic product exceeds the value of the solubility product.
1 dm^3 of the solution containing 0.1 mole of Zn^2+, 0.01 mole of Cu^2+, and 8.1 $\times$ 10^-39 mole of S^2-.
Let us calculate the ionic product in each case.
Ionic product of ZnS = [Zn^2+] [S^2-]
0.1 $ \times$ 8.1 $ \times$ 10^-19 = 8.1 $ \times$ 10^-20
K_sp of ZnS = 3 $ \times$ 10^-22
Here, Ionic Product > K_sp
Ionic Product of CuS = [Cu^2+] [S^2-]
= 0.01 $ \times$ 8.1 $ \times$ 10 ^- 19 = 8.1 $ \times$ 10^-21
But it has K_w = 8 $ \times$ 10^-36
Since, Ionic product > K_sp
As both ZnS and CuS have less K_sp value than their ionic product so ZnS and CuS both get precipitated.

Q5. A vessel at 1000 K contains CO_2 with a pressure of 0.5 atm. Some of the CO_2 is converted into CO on the addition of graphite. If the total pressure at equilibrium is 0.8 atm, the value of K is ________.
    (A) 0.3 atm
    (B) 0.18 atm
    (C) 1.8 atm   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 3 atm
    Answer: C
    Explanation: CO_2 + C $\rightarrow$ 2CO
t = 0, 0.5, 0
t = t, 0.5-x, 2x
P_total = 0.5 - x + 2x = 0.8
i.e. x = 0.3 atm
i.e. $K = \frac{{{{\left( {{P_{co}}} \right)}^2}}}{{{P_{co2}}}} = \frac{{0.6 \times 0.6}}{{0.2}} = 1.8atm$

Q6. What is the best description of the change that occurs when Na_2O(s) is dissolved in water?
    (A) Oxidation number of oxygen increases.
    (B) Oxide ion accepts sharing in a pair of electrons.
    (C) Oxidation number of sodium decreases.
    (D) Oxide ion donates a pair of electrons.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In water Na_2O dissociates as -
Na_2O + H_2O → 2Na^+ + O_2^-
The oxide ion formed can form hydrogen bonds with water and is stabilized. Thus it is easy for Na_2O and all other oxides to dissolve in water as it brings about further stability in the system.

Q7. Conjugate acid of a weak base is always stronger. What will be the decreasing order of basic strength of the following conjugate bases? OH^-, RO^-, CH_3COO^-, Cl^-
    (A) RO^- > OH^- > Cl^- > CH_3COO^-
    (B) OH^- > R > CH_3CO >
    (C) ${\text{R}}{{\text{O}}^ - }$ > ${\text{O}}{{\text{H}}^ - }$ > ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{CO}}{{\text{O}}^ - }$ > ${\text{C}}{{\text{l}}^ - }$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{CO}}{{\text{O}}^ - }$> ${\text{C}}{{\text{l}}^ - }$ > ${\text{R}}{{\text{O}}^ - }$ > ${\text{O}}{{\text{H}}^ - }$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: conjugate acids of given bases are H_2O, ROH, CH_3COO^-, Cl^-
their acidic strength in the order
Cl^- > CH_3COO^- > H_2O > ROH
basic strength in the order ${\text{R}}{{\text{O}}^ - }$ > ${\text{O}}{{\text{H}}^ - }$ > ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{CO}}{{\text{O}}^ - }$ > ${\text{C}}{{\text{l}}^ - }$

Q8. Arrange the following in increasing order of pH KNO_3 (aq),CH_3COONa (aq), NH_4Cl(aq),C_6H_5COONH_4(aq).
    (A) NH_4Cl < C_6H_5COONH_4 < KNO_3 < CH_3COONa   <-- CORRECT
    (B) KNO_3 < CH_3COONa < NH_4Cl < C_6H_5COONH_4
    (C) C_6H_5COONH_4 < KNO_3 < CH_3COONa < NH_4Cl
    (D) NH_4Cl < KNO_3 < CH_3COONa < C_6H_5COONH_4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: KNO_3: Salt of strong acid-strong base, solution is neutral, ph = 7
CH_3COONa salt of weak acid - strong base, solution is basic, ph > 7
NH_4Cl: Salt of strong acid-weak base , solution is acidic pH < 7
C_6H_5COONH_4 both weak put NH_4OH is slightly stronger than C_6H_5COOH, pH close to 7 but slightly > 7
Hence in order of pH is NH_4Cl < C_6H_5COONH_4 < KNO_3 < CH_3COONa

Q9. pH of a solution of a strong acid is 5.0. What will be the pH of the solution obtained after diluting the given solution a 100 times?
    (A) 5.6999
    (B) 7.6907
    (C) 6.0090
    (D) 6.699   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: pH=5 means the solution is acidic. On dilution, it will remain acidic. However, acidic character decreases so much that it is almost neutral (pH=5 means [H^+] = 10^-5M). After dilution, [H^+] = $\frac{10^{-5}}{100}=10^{-7}M$ ; [H^+] from H_2O cannot be neglected.
Hence total [H^+] = 10^-7 + 10^-7 = 2 $\times$ 10^-7 M
$\Rightarrow$ pH=-log(2 $\times$ 10^-7 ) = 7-0.3010=6.699

Q10. Following data is given for the reaction: ${\text{CaC}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}\left( {\text{s}} \right){\text{ }} \to {\text{ CaO }}\left( {\text{s}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ C}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right)$
${\Delta _f}HV|CaO(s)] = - - 635.1\;kJ1mo{l^{ - 1}}$
${\Delta _f}HV[C{O_2}(g)] = - - 393.5\;kJ\;mo{l^{ - 1}}$
${\Delta _f}HV[CaC{O_3}(s)] = - - 1206.9\;kJmo{l^{ - 1}}$
Predict the effect of temperature on the equilibrium constant of the above
Reaction (Hint: Apply Le-Chatelier’s principle)
    (A) increase in temperature reaction will attain equilibrium
    (B) increase in temperature reaction will stop.
    (C) increase in temperature reaction will proceed in forward direction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) increase in temperature reaction will proceed in reverse direction
    Answer: C
    Explanation: ${\Delta _{rxn}}H = (\Delta {H_{product}} - \Delta {H_{reac\tan t}})$
= -393.5 - 635.1 + 1206.9 = +ve
This is endothermic reaction, which is favoured at high temperature.

Q11. Does the number of moles of reaction products increase, decrease or remain same when each of the following equilibria is subjected to a decrease in pressure by increasing the volume? ${\text{PC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{5}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right)$ $ \rightleftharpoons $ ${\text{PC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{3}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right){\text{ }} + {\text{ C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}\left( {\text{g}} \right)$
    (A) decrease largely
    (B) remain the same
    (C) decrease
    (D) increase   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Pressure will increase in the forwarded reaction and the number of moles of the products increase.
 Pressure will increase in the backward reaction and the number of moles of the products decrease.
 The change in pressure will have no effect on the equilibrium constant and there will be no change in the no. of moles.

Q12. One of the reaction that takes place in producing steel from iron ore is the reduction of iron (II) oxide by carbon monoxide to give iron metal and CO_2. FeO(s) + CO (g) $\rightarrow$ Fe (s) + CO_2 (g) K_p = 0.265 at 1050 K. What are the equilibrium partial pressures of CO and CO_2 at 1050 K if the initial partial pressures are: P_co = 1.4 atm and $P_{CO_2}$ = 0.80 atm?
    (A) $P_{CO_2}$ and P_CO = 0.416 atm and 1.135 atm
    (B) $P_{CO_2}$ and P_CO = 0.461atm and 0.739 atm
    (C) $P_{CO_2}$ and P_CO = 0.461atm and 1.739 atm   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $P_{CO_2}$ and P_CO = 1.557atm and 2.739 atm
    Answer: C
    Explanation: For the given reaction; $\mathop {FeO + CO(g)}\limits_{1.4atm} = \mathop {Fe(s) + C{O_2}(g)}\limits_{0.80atm} $
$Q_p=\frac{P_{CO_2}}{P_{CO}}=\frac{0.80}{1.4}=\;0.571$
It is given that K_p = 0.265
Since Q_P > K_p
The reaction will proceed in the backward reaction.
Therefore, we can say that the pressure of CO will increase while the pressure of CO_2 will decrease.
Now, let the increase in pressure of CO = decrease in pressure of CO_2 be P.
Then we can write
${{K_p} = \frac{{{P_{C{O_2}}}}}{{{P_{CO}}}} = \frac{{0.80 - P}}{{1.4 + P}}}$
${ \Rightarrow 0.265 = \frac{{0.80 - P}}{{1.4 + P}}}$
$\Rightarrow$ 0.265 (1.4 + P) = 0.80 - P
$\Rightarrow$ 0.371 + 0.265P = 0.80 - P
$\Rightarrow$ 1.265P = 0.429 $\Rightarrow$ p = 0.339atm
Therefore, equilibrium partial pressure of CO_2 = 0.80 - 0.339= 0.461 atm
Also, equilibrium partial pressure of CO = 1.4 + 0.339 = 1.739 atm

Q13. The ionization constant of HF is 3.2 $\times$ 10^-4. Calculate the degree of dissociation of HF in its 0.02 M solution. The concentrations of all species present i.e. H_3O^+,F^- and HF in the solution, and its pH respectively are.
    (A) 3.6 $\times$ 10^-3M, 3.6 $\times$ 10^-3 M, 18.6 $\times$ 10^-3,2.62
    (B) 1.4 $\times$ 10^-3M 16.6 $\times$ 10^-3 M , 2.62.
    (C) 2.5 $\times$ 10^-3 M, 2.5 $\times$ 10^-3 M,17.6 $\times$10^-3,2.62   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 5.9 $\times$ 10^-3 M,19.6 $\times$ 10^-3 M 2.62.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: HF $\rightleftharpoons$ H^+ + F^-
Initial Concentration 1 0 0
Equilibrium concentration C(1 - $\alpha$) C $\alpha$ C $\alpha$
Now, ${{K_a}\; = \frac{{\left[ {{H^ + }} \right]\left[ {{F^ - }} \right]}}{{\left[ {HF} \right]}} = \frac{{\left[ {\;C\alpha } \right]\left[ {\;C\alpha } \right]}}{{\left[ {C(1 - \alpha )\;} \right]}} = \frac{{\;C{\alpha ^2}}}{{(1 - \alpha )\;}} \approx C{\alpha ^2}}$ (Since $\alpha$ is less (1 - $\alpha$ ) can be written as 1
${ \Rightarrow \alpha = \sqrt {\frac{{{K_a}\;}}{C}} = \sqrt {\frac{{3.2 \times {{10}^{ - 4}}}}{{0.02}}} = 12.65 \times {{10}^{ - 2}}}$
[H_3O^+] = C$\alpha$ =0.02 $\times$ 0.1265 = 2.53 $\times$ 10^-3
[F^-] = C$\alpha$ = 0.02 $\times$ 0.1265 = 2.53 $\times$10^-3
[HF]= C(1-$\alpha$) = 0.02 $\times$ (1-0.1265) = 17.6 $\times$ 10^-3
Now,
pH= - log [H_3O^+] = - log (2.53 $\times$ 10^-3) = 3 - 0.4031 = 2.5969

Q14. Amines behave as:
    (A) Lewis acids
    (B) Lewis base   <-- CORRECT
    (C) aprotic acid
    (D) neutral compound
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Amines behave as lewis base because they have a lonepair of electrons.

Q15. Assuming complete dissociation, calculate the pH of 0.002 M KOH solution.
    (A) 2.01
    (B) 10.93
    (C) 11.31   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 10.11 only
    Answer: C
    Explanation: KOH $\to$ K^+ + OH^- (As KOH undergoes complete ionization)
$\Rightarrow$ [OH^-] = [KOH] = 0.02
Now, K_w = [H^+] [OH^-]${ \Rightarrow \left[ {{H^ + }} \right] = \frac{{\;{K_w}\;}}{{\left[ {O{H^ - }} \right]}} = \frac{{{{10}^{ - 14}}}}{{0.02}} = \;5 \times {{10}^{ - 12}}}$
$\Rightarrow$ pH of KOH = - log [5 $\times$ 10^-12] = 12 - log 5 = 12 - 0.699 $\approx$ 11.31

Redox Reactions CBSE Online Test 01  (id 966) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Chemistry > Redox Reactions
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The term oxidation was coined for the class of chemical reactions wherein one of the following options take place?
    (A) Addition of electropositive element to a substance.
    (B) Addition of oxygen to a substance   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Removal of the electronegative element from a substance.
    (D) Addition of hydrogen to a substance
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Oxidation means the addition of oxygen, removal of hydrogen, increase in oxidation number, the addition of an electronegative element or removal of an electropositive element.
 ​​​​​​The term oxidation was first used to describe chemical reactions in which oxygen was added to an element of a compound. Later on, the term oxidation was extended to describe many more reactions that occurred without the use of even oxygen.
 Addition of Oxygen: Oxidation is a chemical reaction in which oxygen is added to any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 Removal of Hydrogen: Oxidation is a chemical reaction in which hydrogen is removed from any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 Addition of an Electronegative Element: Oxidation is a chemical reaction in which an electronegative element is added into any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 Removal of an Electropositive Element: Oxidation is a chemical reaction in which an electropositive element is removed from any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 A substance that brings oxidation is known as oxidizing agents.

Q2. Does the term reduction have one of the following options taking place?
    (A) Removal of the electropositive element from a substance
    (B) Removal of hydrogen to a substance
    (C) Addition of an electronegative element to a substance
    (D) Removal of oxygen from a substance   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The reduction is addition of hydrogen, removal of oxygen, removal of an electronegative element or addition of an electropositive element.
 Removal of Oxygen: Reduction is a chemical reaction in which oxygen is removed from any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 CuO + C $\longrightarrow$ Cu + CO
 H_2O + C $\longrightarrow$ CO + H_2
 2CO + O_2 $\longrightarrow$ 2CO_2
 Fe_3O_4 + 4H_2 $\longrightarrow$ 3F_2 + 4H_2O
 Addition of Hydrogen: Reduction is a chemical reaction in which hydrogen is added to any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 Cl_2 + H_2 $\longrightarrow$ 2HCl
 S + H_2 $\longrightarrow$ H_2S
 C_2H_4 + H_2 $\longrightarrow$ C_2H_6
 Removal of an Electronegative Element: Reduction is a chemical reaction in which an electronegative element is removed from any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 2HgCl_2 + SnCl_2 $\longrightarrow$ Hg_2Cl_2 + SnCl_4 (Reduction of mercuric chloride)
 2FeCl_3 + H_2 $\longrightarrow$ 2FeCl_2 + 2HCl (Reduction of ferric chloride)
 2FeCl_3 + H_2S $\longrightarrow$ 2FeCl_2 + 2HCl + S (Reduction of ferric chloride)
 Addition of an Electropositive Element: Reduction is a chemical reaction in which an electropositive element is added any chemical species (atom, ion or molecule).
 HgCl_2 + Hg $\longrightarrow$ Hg_2Cl_2 (Reduction of mercuric chloride)
 CuCl_2 + Cu $\longrightarrow$ Cu_2Cl_2 (Reduction of cupric chloride)
 The substance which brings reduction is known as a reducing agent.
 A substance, which undergoes oxidation, acts as a reducing agent while a substance, which undergoes reduction, acts as an oxidizing agent.
Mg, S, Cu, Na_2SO_3, H_2S, HI, H_2, C, KI are reducing agents, while O_2, Cl_2, F_2, H_2O_2, MnO_2, FeCl_3, CuCl_2, Fe_3O_4, CuO, etc., are oxidizing agents in the above examples.
 All oxidation and reduction reactions are complimentary of one another and occur simultaneously, one cannot take place without the other.
 No single oxidation and no single reduction process is known. The simultaneously oxidation and reduction reactions are generally termed as redox reactions. e.g., 2FeCl_3 + SnCl_2 $\longrightarrow$ 2FeCl_2 + SnCl_4.
In above example iron undergoes reduction from +3 to +2.

Q3. Oxidation and reduction always occur simultaneously, hence, the word “redox” was coined for this class of chemical reactions. In the following redox reaction, identify the species undergoing oxidation and reduction: 3Fe_3O_4(s) + 8 Al (s) $\longrightarrow$ 9 Fe (s) + 4Al_2O_3(s)
    (A) Fe_3O_4 is oxidised, Fe is reduced
    (B) Al_2O_3 is reduced, Fe_3O_4 is oxidised
    (C) Aluminium (Al) is oxidised, (Fe_3O_4) is reduced   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Fe_3O_4 is oxidised, Aluminium is reduced
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the above reaction, oxygen is transferred from Fe_3O_4 to Al, so Fe_3O_4 is reduced while Al is oxidised. As per the definition of oxidation and reduction, loss of oxygen i.e reduction occurs in Fe_3O_4, and gain of oxygen i.e Oxidation occurs in Al.

Q4. The formation of sodium chloride involves two half-reactions, which clearly shows the involvement of electrons.
2Na (s) $\longrightarrow$ 2Na + (g) + 2e
Cl_2 (g) + 2e $\longrightarrow$ 2 Cl(g)
Sum of the half reactions gives
2 Na(s) + Cl_2(g) $\longrightarrow$ 2 Na + Cl (s) or 2 NaCl (s)
In terms of electron-transfer change, name the oxidising agent(s) and reducing agent(s).
    (A) Oxidising agents: Chlorine, oxygen and reducing agents: sodium and sulphur
    (B) Oxidising agent: Chlorine and Reducing agent: Sodium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Reducing agents: Chlorine, oxygen and oxidising agents: sodium and sulphur
    (D) Reducing agents: Chlorine, oxygen and sulphur and oxidising agent: sodium
    Answer: B
    Explanation: According to the modern concept, the loss of electrons is oxidation whereas the gain of electrons is reduction. Redox reaction involves two half-reactions, one involving loss of electron or electrons (oxidation) and the other involving gain of electrons or electrons (reduction)
 Oxidizing agent is a species that can gain one or more electrons.
 Reducing agent is a species which can lose one or more electrons.
In the given reaction Sodium(Na) is losing 2 electrons, thus it is the reducing agent. Chlorine(Cl) is gaining 2 electrons, thus it is an oxidising agent.

Q5. Copper nitrate is a blue coloured solution. Place a strip of metallic zinc in an aqueous solution of copper nitrate for about one hour. What happens?
    (A) The zinc strip becomes coated with blue colour
    (B) The blue colour of the solution turns to red
    (C) The aqueous solution of copper nitrate turns green in colour and the metallic zinc strip turns darker in colour.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The blue colour of the solution becomes more intense blue.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: On placing a strip of metallic zinc in an aqueous solution of copper nitrate for about one hour, the copper nitrate solution turns green in colour and zinc strip turns darker.
Formula and Ionic equation for the reaction are as follows.
 Formula Equation:
 Zn (s) + Cu(NO_3)_2 (aq) $\longrightarrow$ Cu (s) + Zn(NO_3)_2 (aq)
 Ionic Equation:
 Zn (s) + Cu^2+ (aq) $\longrightarrow$ Zn^2+ (aq) + Cu (s)
As is seen in ionic equation Zn is losing 2 electrons, thus oxidation occurs and Cu is gaining 2 electrons, thus reduction occurs. Since oxidation and reduction take place simultaneously in this reaction, it is a redox reaction. Also since Zn is losing electrons and becoming darker in colour, it is the reducing agent and Cu is gaining 2 electrons, it is the reducing agent. The resultant solution Zinc nitrate [Zn(NO_3)_2] is green in colour.

Q6. Redox reaction between copper and an aqueous solution of silver nitrate happens when the copper rod is dipped in silver nitrate solution. What happens in the final stage?
    (A) Silver deposits in the solution; Ag+(aq) is reduced to Ag(s).
    (B) The solution turns intense blue, and silver is deposited on the copper rod.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Silver deposits on the rod; Ag+(aq) is oxidised to Ag(s).
    (D) Copper deposits in the solution; Cu(aq) is reduced to ${\text{Cu}}_2^ + $ (s).
    Answer: B
    Explanation: This is due to the formation of Cu^2+ ions in the solution illustrated in the following ionic reaction:
Cu(S) + 2Ag^+(aq) $\longrightarrow$ Cu^2+(aq) + 2Ag(s)
Here, Cu is oxidized to Cu^2+ (means releasing of 2 electrons from Cu to Cu^2+ ) and Ag^+ is reduced to Ag(s) (means gaining of 2 electrons from 2Ag^+ to 2Ag ) and thus, silver converted into a solid-state and deposited on a copper rod.

Q7. Identify the correct statement (s) in relation of the following reaction:
$\mathrm { Zn } + 2 \mathrm { HCl } \rightarrow \mathrm { ZnCl } _ { 2 } + \mathrm { H } _ { 2 }$
    (A) Zinc is acting as a reductant
    (B) Hydrogen ion is acting as an oxident and Zinc is acting as a reductant   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Zinc is acting as an oxident
    (D) Chlorine is acting as a reductant
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Hydrogen ion is acting as an oxident and Zinc is acting as a reductant.

Q8. In the reaction of metallic cobalt placed in nickel sulphate solution, there is a competition for release of electrons At equilibrium, chemical tests reveal that both Ni^2+ (aq) and Co^2+ (aq) are present at moderate concentrations. The result is that:
    (A) Neither the reactants nor the products are greatly favoured   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Only one reactant and one product is greatly favoured.
    (C) Only ${\text{Co}}_2^ + $ (aq) and Ni (s)] are favoured
    (D) Only [Co(s) and ${\text{Ni}}_2^ + $ (aq)] are favoured
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Reaction will not complete and it will remain at equilibrium.

Q9. Oxidation number denotes the oxidation state of an element in a compound ascertained on the basis that electron in a covalent bond belongs
    (A) entirely to more electronegative element   <-- CORRECT
    (B) entirely to halogens in a compound
    (C) entirely to less electronegative element
    (D) entirely to transition elements if present
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Oxidation number is a number assigned to an element in a compound according to some rules. This number enable us to describe oxidation-reduction reactions, and balancing redox chemical reactions. When a covalent bond forms between two atoms with different electronegativities the shared electrons in the bond lie closer to the more electronegative atom eg. HCl
The oxidation number of an atom is the charge that results when the electrons in a covalent bond are assigned to the more electronegative atom. It is the charge on an atom would possess if the bonding were ionic. In HCl (above) the oxidation number for the hydrogen would be +1 and that of the Cl would be -1

Q10. The highest value of oxidation number changes from 1 to 7 is:
    (A) the first three groups.
    (B) In alkaline earth metals.
    (C) across the third period in the periodic table.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) in the atoms of transition elements.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The highest value of oxidation number exhibited by an atom of an element generally increases across the period in the periodic table.

Q11. The oxidation number of oxygen in most compounds is:
    (A) 1
    (B) -3
    (C) 4
    (D) -2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Oxygen is the most electronegative element. Oxygen has 6 electrons in its outermost shell and to gain noble gas configuration oxygen has to take 2 more electrons.

Q12. Aurous chloride and auric chloride are written as Au(l)Cl and Au(lll)Cl_3. The roman numeral in parenthesis after the symbol of the metal in the molecular formula represents the:
    (A) Basic character
    (B) Electronegativity
    (C) Oxidation number   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ionic state
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The roman number represents the oxidation number/oxidation state of an element. It is popularly known as Stock notation given by the german scientist Alfred stock.

Q13. Both CO_2 and H_2 gases are
    (A) heavier than air
    (B) acidic in nature
    (C) colourless   <-- CORRECT
    (D) soluble in water
    Answer: C
    Explanation: colourless

Q14. All combustion reactions, which make use of elemental dioxygen, as well as other reactions involving elements other than dioxygen are:
    (A) Displacement reactions
    (B) Disproportionation reactions
    (C) Combination reaction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Decomposition reactions
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A combination reaction (also known as a synthesis reaction) is a reaction where two or more elements or compounds (reactants) combine to form a single compound (product). Such reactions may be represented by equations of the following form: X + Y $\longrightarrow$ XY.

Q15. Which of the following gases can be used for storage of fresh sample of oil for a long time?
    (A) Nitrogen or helium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Nitrogen or oxygen
    (C) Helium or oxygen
    (D) Carbon dioxide or oxygen
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Nitrogen or helium

Q1. The electrolytic decomposition of water gives H_2 and O_2 in the ratio of
    (A) 8 : 1 by mass
    (B) 1 : 2 by mass
    (C) 1 : 2 by volume
    (D) 2 : 1 by volume   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: 2 : 1 by volume

Q2. Displacement of hydrogen from cold water is done by:
    (A) All alkaline earth metals
    (B) All alkali metals   <-- CORRECT
    (C) All transition elements
    (D) Superoxides
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A common characteristic of most Alkali metal is their ability to displace H_2 (g) from water. This is represented by their large, negative electrode potentials. In this event, the Group 1 metal is oxidized to its metal ion, and water is reduced to form hydrogen gas and hydroxide ions. The general reaction of an alkali metal (M) with H_2O (l) is given in the following equation:
2M(s) + 2H_2O(l) $\longrightarrow$ 2M + (aq) + 2OH−(aq) + H_2(g)
From this reaction it is apparent that OH- is produced, creating a basic or alkaline environment. Group 1 elements are called alkali metals because of their ability to displace H_2 (g) from water and create a basic solution. Alkali metals are also known to react violently and explosively with water. This is because enough heat is given off during the exothermic reaction to ignite the H_2(g).

Q3. Fractional Oxidation Number exists because:
    (A) middle carbon in such elements has always zero oxidation state.
    (B) the element is present in different oxidation states.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) electrons are never shared/transferred in that element.
    (D) the average oxidation state of the element is divided into two.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The oxidation states are usually in whole numbers, but in some cases, they are in fractional numbers. Consider Fe_3O_4.
 Using rule #2, the sum of the oxidation state of all atoms is 0
 Using rule #6, the O has the oxidation state of -2. 4 $\times$ (-2) = -8
 Equation: 3Fe + (-8) = 0
 3Fe = 8
 Fe = $8 \over 3$
In most cases, atoms of the same element in a given compound have the same oxidation states, but each atom can have a different state than the other. For Fe_3O_4, two Fe atoms have an oxidation state of +3 and one of +2, which makes the total oxidation state of Fe= $8 \over 3$.
Instead of averaging the oxidation states, we must keep them separated. This is called fragmenting, which occurs if there is an ionic compound, and the ions can be separated. The oxidation state of the individual atoms in the different ions can be determined.

Q4. The strength of a reductant/oxidant in redox systems can be determined:
    (A) by taking into consideration the different oxidation states of the atom in the element.
    (B) by taking into consideration only half-reactions involving reduction.
    (C) by the titration method using a redox-sensitive indicator.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) by taking into consideration only half-reactions involving oxidation.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Because a redox indicator (also called an oxidation-reduction indicator) is an indicator which undergoes a definite colour change at a specific electrode potential.

Q5. One of the following has application in electrode processes and cells:
    (A) half reactions involving oxidation.
    (B) the concept of redox reactions.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) half reactions involving reduction.
    (D) the different oxidation states of the atom in the element.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The concept of a redox reaction is used in electrode processes and cells. Because in these processes an electrode loses or gains electrons, an electrode with a higher reduction potential undergo reduction, the electrode potential is given a positive sign if oxidation occurs at the electrode.

Q6. Zn^2+/Zn represents:
    (A) the reduced form of Zinc
    (B) the oxidation number of +2 of Zinc
    (C) redox couple   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the oxidised form of Zinc
    Answer: C
    Explanation: This is a redox couple where the following reaction takes place:
Zn^2+ + 2e^- $\rightarrow$ Zn

Q7. In Daniell cell, the direction of current is:
    (A) towards centre.
    (B) in the same direction of electron flow.
    (C) towards anode.
    (D) opposite to the direction of electron flow.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Current is taken at the direction in which positive charge is flowing, but electrons are negatively charged. So, the direction of current and the direction of electron flow is the opposite.

Q8. The flow of current is possible in Daniel cell only:
    (A) if the zinc and copper rods are connected by the platinum wire only.
    (B) if there is a potential difference between the copper and zinc electrodes.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) if the zinc and copper rods are connected by a salt bridge only.
    (D) if the transfer of electrons does take place directly from Zn to Cu^2+.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The flow of current is possible only due to potential difference.

Q9. In oxygen difluoride (OF_2) and dioxygen difluoride (O_2F_2), the oxygen is assigned an oxidation number of:
    (A) +2
    (B) +2 and +4
    (C) +4 and +3
    (D) +2 and +1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Oxidation state of O in OF_2 is +2 and O_2F_2 is +1. Because the number assigned to oxygen will depend upon the bonding state of oxygen.

Q10. The oxidation number of $ - \frac{1}{2}$ is assigned to an Oxygen atom in:
    (A) When oxygen is bonded to fluorine
    (B) When oxygen is bonded to metals
    (C) Peroxides
    (D) Superoxides   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In the superoxide ion, $O_2^ - $, the oxygen has an oxidation number of $ - \frac{1}{2}$. The stability of metal superoxides depends on the size and the electropositive character of the metal. The larger the metal and the more electropositive it is, the greater the stability of its superoxide.

Q11. Assign oxidation number to P in NaH_2PO_4.
    (A) +1
    (B) +6
    (C) 5.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) +4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The oxidation state of P in NaH_2PO_4 is +5.
Let the oxidation number of P be x. As we already know the oxidation number of other atoms so we can calculate that of P too.
Na = +1
H= +1 (+2 for hydrogen molecule)
O = -2
Now calculating oxidation number of P:-
1 +2 + x +(-8) = 0
On solving we get x = +5.

Q12. Assign oxidation number to S in KAl(SO_4)_2.12H_2O:
    (A) 6.0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) +5
    (C) +4
    (D) +12
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Oxidation state of S in KAl(SO_4)_2.12H_2O is +6.
As, Oxidation number of S in KAl(SO_4)_2.12 H2O can be calculated as-
1 + 3 + 2X - 16 + 0 = 0 (H_2O is neutral so oxidation No. is 0)
2X = 12
X = +6

Q13. If an excess of P_4 is treated with F_2, then_____will be produced wherein the oxidation number of P is +3. The compound is________.
    (A) PF
    (B) PF_3   <-- CORRECT
    (C) PF_5
    (D) PF_6
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Whenever a reaction between an oxidising agent and a reducing agent is carried out, a compound of lower oxidation state is formed if the reducing agent is in excess and a compound of higher oxidation state is formed if the oxidising agent is in excess. This can be illustrated as follows: P_4 and F_2 are reducing and oxidising agents respectively. If an excess of P_4 is treated with F_2, then PF_3 will be produced, wherein the oxidation number (O.N.) of P is +3.
PF_4(excess)+F_2 $\longrightarrow$ PF_3

Q14. Which of the following is not an example of redox reaction?
    (A) Fe_2O_3 + 3CO $\to$ 2Fe + 3CO_2
    (B) BaCl_2 + H_2SO_4 $\to$ BaSO_4 + 2HCl   <-- CORRECT
    (C) CuO + H_2 $\to$ Cu + H_2O
    (D) 2K + F_2 $\to$ 2KF
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The reaction is not redox because there is no oxidation or reduction of any element (i.e. no change in oxidation state/number).
Ba in BaCl_2 is at a +2 charge because it is in group 2. On the other side of the equation Ba in BaSO_4 is still +2. Cl_2 on the first side of the equation is -2 (as 2 chlorines) and Cl is -2 on the other side as there are 2 of them.
H on both sides are both +1 (but technically +2 as there are two of them).
SO_4 does not change oxidation number and always remains -2.
So, the reaction is not a redox reaction.

Q15. Electrochemical processes for extraction of highly reactive metal and non-metal involves one of the following. Choose the most appropriate option.
    (A) reaction with inert gases
    (B) reduction processes
    (C) oxidation processes
    (D) redox processes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The electrochemical process for extraction of metal or non-metal from its ore involves the redox reaction i.e. oxidation and reduction takes place simultaneously. For example, extraction of Na and Cl_2 from NaCl.

Q1. 2 Na(s) $\longrightarrow$ 2Na^+ + 2e^-
2H^+ + 2 e^-​​​​_​​​​ $\longrightarrow$ H_​​​​​​2
Which is oxidizing and Reducing?
    (A) Sodium is reduced
    (B) Sodium is oxidised and hydrogen is reduced   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Hydrogen is oxidised
    (D) Electronegativity of sodium determines the direction of the reaction
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Oxidation is a process in which one or more electrons are lost and the oxidation number is increased. Sodium has 0 oxidation state as a reactant and +1 oxidation state as a product.
Similarly, Reduction is a process in which one or more electrons are gained and the oxidation number is reduced i.e. from +1 to 0.

Q2. In the free or the uncombined state, each atom in O_2, O_3, P_4, S_8, and Mg has the oxidation number______.
    (A) 7
    (B) 3
    (C) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In a free or uncombined state each element has zero oxidation state.

Q3. For ions composed of only one atom, the oxidation number is equal to the:
    (A) The sum of different oxidation states
    (B) Always +1
    (C) Charge on the ion   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Always -1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: By definition, the oxidation number of an atom is the charge that an atom would have if the compound was composed of ions. The oxidation number of simple ions is equal to the charge on the ion. The oxidation number of sodium in the Na^+ ion is +1, for example, and the oxidation number of chlorine in the Cl^- ion is -1.

Q4. In the decomposition of lead (II) nitrate to give lead (II) oxide, nitrogen dioxide and oxygen gas, the coefficient of nitrogen dioxide (in the balanced equation) is
    (A) 3
    (B) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2
    (D) 1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: 4

Q5. Silver article turns black when kept in the open for a few days due to formation of
    (A) H_2S
    (B) AgSO_4
    (C) Ag_2S   <-- CORRECT
    (D) AgS
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ag_2S

Q6. An oxidation number of +1 is found in all their compounds of one of the below-given options:
    (A) All alkaline earth metals
    (B) Superoxides
    (C) All alkali metals   <-- CORRECT
    (D) All transition elements
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The alkali metals (Group 1) have 1 valence electron. Alkali metals lose this electron to achieve noble gas configuration, and so alkali metals have oxidation number +1.

Q7. The oxidation number of hydrogen in LiH, NaH and CaH_7 is_____.
    (A) -1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -2
    (C) 1and 2
    (D) -1 and -2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: This is according to the rules of assigning oxidation number i.e.
Metal hydrides, such as NaH, LiH, etc., in which the oxidation state for H is -1.

Q8. Chlorine, bromine, and iodine when combined with oxygen, have oxidation numbers:
    (A) -1
    (B) +1 or any positive number   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -1 or any negative number
    (D) -2

Q9. The oxidation number of an element in a compound is evaluated on the basis of certain rules. Which of the following rules is not correct in this respect?
    (A) In all its compounds, the oxidation number of fluorine is – 1.
    (B) The oxidation number of hydrogen is always +1.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) The algebraic sum of all the oxidation numbers in a compound is zero.
    (D) An element in the free or the uncombined state bears oxidation number zero.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Normally hydrogen's oxidation number is +1, except for when it is part of a binary compound (2 elements) along with a metal. For example, LiH, NaH, CaH_​​​​2, all have hydrogen with oxidation number -1.

Q10. The more positive the value of $E^{\ominus}$, the greater is the tendency of the species to get reduced. Using the standard electrode potential of redox couples given below to find out which of the following is the strongest oxidising agent.
$E^{\ominus}$ values: $\frac{{{\text{F}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{3 + }}}}}}{{{\text{F}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2 + }}}}}}$^ = +0.77; $\frac{{{{\text{I}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{(s)}}}}{{{{\text{I}}^{\text{ - }}}}}$^ = +0.54;
$\frac{{{\text{C}}{{\text{u}}^{{\text{2 + }}}}}}{{{\text{Cu}}}}$^ = +0.34; $\frac{{{\text{A}}{{\text{g}}^{\text{ + }}}}}{{{\text{Ag}}}}$= +0.80 V
    (A) Ag^+   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Fe^3+
    (C) I_2 (s)
    (D) Cu^3+
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The more positive the value of $E^{\ominus}$, the greater is the tendency of the species to get reduced, therefore $\frac{{{\text{A}}{{\text{g}}^{\text{ + }}}}}{{{\text{Ag}}}}$^ = +0.80 is the strongest oxidizing agent.

Q11. $E^{\ominus}$ values of some redox couples are given below. On the basis of these values choose the correct option. 
$E^{\ominus}$ values: $\frac{{{\text{B}}{{\text{r}}_{\text{2}}}}}{{{\text{B}}{{\text{r}}^{\text{ - }}}}}$^ = +1.90; $\frac{{{\text{A}}{{\text{g}}^{\text{ + }}}}}{{{\text{Ag}}}}$^ = +0.80;
$\frac{{{\text{C}}{{\text{u}}^{{\text{2 + }}}}}}{{{\text{Cu}}}}$^ = +0.34; $\frac{{{{\text{I}}^{\text{2}}}{\text{(s)}}}}{{{{\text{I}}^{\text{ - }}}}}$^ = +0.54
    (A) Cu will reduce Br^-
    (B) Cu will reduce Ag
    (C) Cu will reduce Br_2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cu will reduce l^-
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Because in electrochemical series Cu is above all in sequence I_2, Ag and Br_2, therefore, Cu will reduce Br_2.

Q12. Using the standard electrode potential, find out the pair between which redox reactions is not feasible.
$E^{\ominus}$ values: $\frac{{{\text{F}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{3 + }}}}}}{{{\text{F}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2 + }}}}}}$^ = +0.77; $\frac{{{{\text{I}}^{\text{2}}}}}{{{{\text{I}}^{\text{ - }}}}}$(s)^ = +0.54;
$\frac{{{\text{C}}{{\text{u}}^{{\text{2 + }}}}}}{{{\text{Cu}}}}$^ = +0.34; $\frac{{{\text{A}}{{\text{g}}^{\text{ + }}}}}{{{\text{Ag}}}}$^ = +0.80V
    (A) Ag and Fe^3+   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Fe^3+ and I^-
    (C) Ag^+ and Cu
    (D) Fe^3+ and Cu
    Answer: A
    Explanation: 2Ag $\rightarrow$ 2Ag^+1 + 2e^- $E^{\ominus}$ =- 0.80 V
2Fe_3+ + 2e^- $\rightarrow$ 2Fe^+2 $E^{\ominus}$ = +0.77 V
On adding the values we get,
$E^{\ominus}$cell = -0.03 V
$E^{\ominus}$ a cell is an electromotive force (also called cell voltage or cell potential) between two half-cells. The greater the
$E^{\ominus}$ a cell of a reaction the greater the driving force of electrons through the system, the more likely the reaction will proceed.
Thus, the reaction will not proceed as standard cell potential is less than zero.

Q13. An oxidation number of +2 is found in all their compounds of one of the below-given options:
    (A) All transition elements
    (B) Superoxides
    (C) All alkaline earth metals   <-- CORRECT
    (D) All alkali metals
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Alkaline earth metals have in common an outer s- electron shell which is full; that is, that is why orbital contains its full complement of two electrons, which these elements readily lose to form cations with charge +2, and an oxidation state (oxidation number) of +2.

Q14. The oxidizing power of halogens increase in the order of:
    (A) Cl_2 < F_2 < I_2 < Br_2
    (B) F_2 < I_2 < Br_2 < Cl_2
    (C) Br_2 < Cl_2 < F_2 < I_2
    (D) I_2 < Br_2 < Cl_2 < F_2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Halogens have high electronegativity and electron affinity. They have a greater tendency to accept electrons or easily reduced, therefore they are a strong oxidizing agent.
As the reduction potential decrease down the group, the oxidizing power decrease down the group the order of the oxidizing power will be as under
F_2 > Cl_2> Br_2> I_2
The oxidizing power depends on,
The heat of dissociation of halogen molecule.
Electron affinity of the atom.
Hydration energy of the ion.
Heat of vaporization
If a halogen has low energy of dissociation, a high electron affinity, and higher hydration of its ion, it will have high oxidizing power.
F has although low electron affinity than Cl but low dissociation energy and has high hydration energy of its ion, therefore Fluorine is the strongest oxidizing agent.

    (A) N_2H_4
    (B) N_3H
    (C) NH_4NO_3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) NH_2OH
    Answer: C
    Explanation: NH_4^+NO_3^-.In NH_4^+
N is -3 and 
NO_3^- , N is +5.

Q1. Which of the following arrangements represent increasing oxidation number of the central atom?
    (A) $Cr{\text{o}}_2^ - $, $Cr{\text{o}}_4^{2 - }$, $Mn{\text{o}}_4^ - $, $Cl{\text{o}}_3^ - $
    (B) $Cr{\text{o}}_4^{2 - }$, $Mn{\text{o}}_4^ - $ , $Cr{\text{o}}_2^ - $, $Cl{\text{o}}_3^ - $
    (C) $Cl{\text{o}}_3^ - $ , $Cro_4^{2 - }$, Mn${\text{o}}_4^ - $ , $Cr{\text{o}}_2^ - $
    (D) CrO^-_2 ,ClO^-_3 ,CrO^2-_4 , ​​_​​MnO^-_4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In CrO^-_2, Cr is in +3 oxidation state
In ClO^-_3, Cl is in +5 oxidation state
In CrO^2-_4, ​​_​​​​Cr is in +6 oxidation state
In MnO^-_4, Mn is in +7 oxidation state

Q2. The largest oxidation number exhibited by an element depends on its outer electronic configuration. With which of the following outer electronic configurations the element will exhibit largest oxidation number?
    (A) ${\text{3}}{{\text{d}}^{\text{1}}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}$
    (B) ${\text{3}}{{\text{d}}^{\text{5}}}{\text{4}}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${\text{3}}{{\text{d}}^{\text{3}}}{\text{4 }}{{\text{s}}^{\text{2}}}$
    (D) ${\text{3}}{{\text{d}}^{\text{5}}}{\text{4 }}{{\text{s}}^{\text{1}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In (3d^54s^2) +7 will be the maximum oxidation state.

Q3. Consider the elements: Cs, Ne, I, and F.
Identify the element which exhibits neither the negative nor does the positive oxidation state?
    (A) Ne and F
    (B) F
    (C) Ne   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Cs
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ne is a noble gas, so does not show any positive or negative oxidation state.

Q4. Which of the following elements does not show disproportionation tendency?
    (A) F   <-- CORRECT
    (B) I
    (C) Br
    (D) Cl
    Answer: A
    Explanation: F (Fluorine) is most electronegative element so it always show -1 oxidation state.

Q5. Consider the elements: Cs, Ne, I, and F.
Identify the element(s) that exhibits only a Positive oxidation state?
    (A) Caesium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Neon
    (C) Caesium and Iodine
    (D) Iodine
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cs is alkali metal so will show a positive oxidation state of +1.

Q6. The exhibition of various oxidation states by an element is also related to the outer orbital electronic configuration of its atom. Atom(s) having which of the following outermost electronic configurations will exhibit more than one oxidation state in its compounds?
    (A) 3d^24s^2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3s^2p^3
    (C) 3s^1
    (D) 3d^14s^2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: (3d^24s^2) is the configuration of the transition element which shows a variable oxidation state.

Q7. Which of the following electrodes will act as anodes, when connected to Standard Hydrogen Electrode?
    (A) Cu/Cu^2+ E° = + 0.34
    (B) Fe/Fe^3+ E^0 = -0.04
    (C) Al/Al^3+ E^0 = -1.66   <-- CORRECT
    (D) F_2(g)/2F^-(aq) E°
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The anode is where oxidation occurs means species that undergo reaction at the anode should have negative electrode potential (reduction). A large negative value (e.g. Al/Al^3+ E^0 = -1.66) means that the element or compound ionizes easily, in other words, it releases electrons easily. This element or compound is easily oxidised and is, therefore, a good reducing agent.

Q8. The decomposition of hydrogen peroxide to form water and oxygen is an example of:
    (A) Decomposition reactions
    (B) Displacement reactions
    (C) Combination reactions
    (D) Disproportionation reaction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\mathop {2{H_2}}\limits_{ + 1} \mathop {{O_2}(}\limits_{ - 1} aq) \to \mathop {2{H_2}}\limits_{ + 1} \mathop O\limits_{ - 2} + \mathop {{O_2}}\limits_0 $
Here the oxygen of peroxide, which is present in -1 state, is converted to zero oxidation state in O_2 and decreases to -2 oxidation state in H_2O.

Q9. Identify the correct statements with reference to the given reaction as follows:
 ${P_4} + 3O{H^ - } \to P{H_3} + 3{H_2}PO_2^ - $.
    (A) Phosphorus is undergoing oxidation as well as reduction.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Phosphorus is undergoing oxidation only.
    (C) Hydrogen is undergoing oxidation as well as reduction.
    (D) Phosphorus is undergoing reduction only.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\mathop {{P_4}}\limits_0 + 3O{H^ - } \to \mathop {P{H_3}}\limits_{ - 3} + \mathop {3{H_2}PO_2^ - }\limits_{ + 1} $
Phosphorus_ is undergoing oxidation as well as reduction. As the oxidation number of P_ is 0 in the reactant and in the product it is -3 as well as +1.

Q10. The electron releasing tendency of the metals, zinc, copper, and silver is in the order:
    (A) Zn > Ag > Cu
    (B) Cu > Ag > Zn
    (C) Zn > Cu > Ag   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ag > Cu > Zn
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The electron releasing tendency of the metals, zinc, copper, and silver is in the order Zn > Cu > Ag. This is according to the metal activity series or electrochemical series.

Q11. A complex compound in which the oxidation number of metal is zero is:
    (A) [Ni(CO)_4]   <-- CORRECT
    (B) K_3[Fe(CN_6]
    (C) [Pl (NH_3)_4]C_2
    (D) K_4[Fe (CN)_6]
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The oxidation number is the charge left on the central atom when all the bonding pairs of electrons are removed, with the charge devolved to the most electronegative atom.
For Ni(CO)_4, we break the Ni−CO bond and we get $Ni^0 +4×^−: C≡ O^+. $ And thus nickel has a formal oxidation state of 0.
Because Ni(CO)_4 is quite volatile, its formation forms the basis for the Mond process for nickel purification.

Q12. Identify the correct statement (s) in relation to the following reaction: ${\text{Zn }} + {\text{ 2HCl }} \to {\text{ ZnC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}} + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}$
    (A) Chlorine is acting as a reductant
    (B) Hydrogen ion is acting as an oxidant   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Zinc is acting as an oxidant
    (D) Hydrogen ion is acting as a reductant
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Zn→ Zn^2+ and H------> H_2, it means that Zn was oxidized since it lost electrons, and H was reduced since it gained electrons. (Cl is a spectator ion here as its oxidation state does not change).
So then by definition, Zn is the reducing agent and H is the oxidizing agent (Oxidant).

Q13. The standard emf of a galvanic cell involving 2 moles of electrons in its redox reaction is 0.59 V. The equilibrium constant for the redox reaction of the cell is______.
    (A) 10^20   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 10^10
    (C) 10
    (D) 10^5
    Answer: A
    Explanation: constant K_c can be calculated as
here, no. of moles of electrons = 2
$E^0cell = {0.059 \over n}logKc$ or $0.59 = {0.059 \over 2}logKc$
or $logKc= {0.59\times2 \over 0.059}= 20$
Kc = antilog 20 = 10^20
Kc = 10^20

Q14. Dalda is prepared from oils by________.
    (A) oxidation
    (B) distillation
    (C) reduction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) hydrolysis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Oils are esters of unsaturated fatty acids whereas Dalda is an ester of saturated fatty acids. The former is converted into the latter by catalytic hydrogenation i.e., reduction.

Q15. Formation of a coloured solution is possible when metal ion in the compound contains:
    (A) Unpaired electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Negative ionic state
    (C) Lone pair of electrons
    (D) Paired electrons
    Answer: A
    Explanation: For any salt or solution to exhibit any colour, the central atom of the compound should have at least an unpaired d electron in it. This unpaired d electron is responsible for its colour in the solutions and salts.

Redox Reactions CBSE Online Test 05  (id 970) [PAID]

Q1. The standard electrode potential for a couple is +0.15 V and that for the ${\text{C}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{3}} + }}$/Cr couple is –0.74 V. These two couples in their standard state are connected to make a cell. The cell potential will be________.
    (A) +1.19 V
    (B) +1.83 V
    (C) +0.18 V
    (D) +0.89 V   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: E_cell = E_cathod - E_anode
Anodic half cell will be Cr^3+/Cr.
The cathodic half cell will be Sn^4+/Sn^2+.
So, E_cell = 0.15+0.74 = +0.89 V

Q2. Standard electrode potential of three metals X, Y and Z are –1.2 V, +0.5 V and –3.0 V respectively. The reducing power of these metals will be:
    (A) X > Y > Z
    (B) Z > X > Y   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Y > X > Z
    (D) Y > Z > X
    Answer: B
    Explanation: E^0_x= –1.2 V; E^0_y=+0.5 V; E^0_z= -3.0 V
Because higher the reduction potential, lesser the reducing power.
Therefore, Z > X > Y

Q3. The oxidation state of iron in K_4[Fe (CN)_6] is:
    (A) 3
    (B) 4
    (C) +2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: K_4 [Fe(CN)_6]
4(+1) + x + 6(-1) = 0
Hence x = +2

Q4. The standard emf of a galvanic cell involving 3 moles of electrons in its redox reaction is 0.59 V. The equilibrium constant for the reaction of the cell is ______.
    (A) 10^15
    (B) 10^30   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 10^20
    (D) 10^25
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $nFE_{cell}^0 = 2.303RT\;\log K$
$E_{cell}^0 = \frac{{2.33RT}}{{nF}}\log K = \frac{{0.0591}}{n}\log K$
n = 3
$\log K = \frac{{0.59 \times 3}}{{0.0591}} $ = 29.9
$K \approx {10^{30}}$

Q5. E1, E2, and E3 are the emfs of the following three galvanic cells respectively: 
 ${\text{Zn }}\left( {\text{s}} \right){\text{ }}\left| {{\text{ Z}}{{\text{n}}^{{\text{2}} + }}\left( {0.{\text{1 M}}} \right){\text{ }}} \right|\left| {{\text{ C}}{{\text{u}}^{{\text{2}} + }}\left( {{\text{1M}}} \right){\text{ }}} \right|{\text{ Cu }}\left( {\text{s}} \right)$
 ${\text{Zn }}\left( {\text{s}} \right){\text{ }}\left| {{\text{ Z}}{{\text{n}}^{{\text{2}} + }}\left( {{\text{1 M}}} \right){\text{ }}} \right|\left| {{\text{ C}}{{\text{u}}^{{\text{2}} + }}\left( {{\text{1M}}} \right){\text{ }}} \right|{\text{ Cu }}\left( {\text{s}} \right)$
 ${\text{Zn }}\left( {\text{s}} \right){\text{ }}\left| {{\text{ Z}}{{\text{n}}^{{\text{2}} + }}\left( {{\text{1 M}}} \right){\text{ }}} \right|\left| {{\text{ C}}{{\text{u}}^{{\text{2}} + }}\left( {0.{\text{1M}}} \right){\text{ }}} \right|{\text{ Cu }}\left( {\text{s}} \right)$
Which one of the following is true?
    (A) E3 > E1 > E2
    (B) E1 > E2 > E3   <-- CORRECT
    (C) E3 > E2 > E1
    (D) E2 > E1 > E3
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\mathbf{E}=\mathbf{E}^{\circ}-(0.059 \mathbf{1} / \mathbf{n}) \times \frac{\log [\text { Product }]}{[\text { Reactant }]}$

Q6. $6{I^ - }(aq) + 2MnO_4^ - (aq) + 4{H_2}O(I) $ $\longrightarrow$ $3{I_2}(s) + 2MnO(s) + 8O{H^ - }(aq)$
The above balanced ionic equation represents a redox reaction where one of the following takes place.
    (A) iodide ion in basic solution oxidizes permanganate ion
    (B) $MnO_4^ - $ in basic solution oxidizes I^- to produce I_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) permanganate ion in basic solution oxidizes water
    (D) permanganate (VII) ion in basic solution reduces iodide ion to produce molecular iodine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mn in $MnO_4^ - $ (Oxidation state = +7) is itself getting reduced to MnO_2 (+4) and I^​​​​​​- (Oxidation state = -1) is getting oxidized to I_2 (Oxidation state = 0).

Q7. Metal in a compound can be displaced by another metal in the uncombined state. Which metal is a better reducing agent in such a case?
    (A) The reduced metal is a better reducing agent than the reducing metal
    (B) Both are the same in reducing capacity
    (C) A better reducing agent is the one that loses more electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A better reducing agent is the one that loses fewer electrons
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The metal causing displacement is a better reducing agent than the one that is being replaced. In simple words, such a metal shows more capability to loose electrons as compared to the one that is reduced.

Q8. Hydrogen is prepared from H_2O by adding:
    (A) Ca, which acts as a reducing agent.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) AI, which acts as oxidising agent.
    (C) Ag, which acts as a reducing agent.
    (D) Au, which acts as oxidising agent.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Calcium is a silvery-white metal; it is relatively soft but much harder than sodium metal. Calcium is a member of the alkaline-earth metals (Group II on the periodic table); these metals react vigorously with water, although not as violently as the Group I metals such as sodium or potassium:
Ca(s) + 2H_2O(l) $\longrightarrow$ Ca(OH)_2(aq) + H_2(g)

Q9. In the conversion of Br_2 to Bro^3-, the oxidation number of Br changes from:
    (A) 0 to -3
    (B) zero to +5   <-- CORRECT
    (C) +1 to +5
    (D) +2 to +5
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In Br_2 oxidation number of Br is 0 while in BrO_3 ^-Br has an oxidation number of +5 as each O carries a -2 charge and the net charge is -1.

Q10. In the reaction 2H_2O_2 $\rightarrow$ 2H_2O + O_2?
    (A) Oxygen is reduced only
    (B) Oxygen is neither oxidised nor reduced
    (C) Oxygen is oxidised as well as reduced   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Oxygen is oxidised only
    Answer: C
    Explanation: This is a disproportionate reaction. (Disproportionation is a specific type of redox reaction in which an element from a reaction undergoes both oxidation and reduction to form two different products).

Q11. Consider the elements: Cs, Ne, I and F.
identify the element(s) that exhibits only a negative oxidation state?
    (A) Sodium
    (B) Fluorine   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Caesium and Fluorine
    (D) Iodine
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Fluorine is more electronegative as it belongs to group 17 or 7 and can show only a negative oxidation state of -1.

Q12. In which of the following compounds, an element exhibits two different oxidation states?
    (A) N_2H_4
    (B) NH_4NO_3   <-- CORRECT
    (C) N_3H
    (D) NH_2OH
    Answer: B
    Explanation: NH_4NO_3 is an ionic compound consisting of NH_4^+ and NO_3^- ion. The oxidation number of N in two species is different as shown below:
In the case of NH_4^+,
Let the oxidation state of N in NH_4^+ be x.
x + 4 $\times$ (+1) = +1
x = -3
In the NO_3^-_,
Let the oxidation state of N in NO_3^- be y,
y + 3 $\times$ (-2) = -1
y = +5
Hence, NH_4NO_3 exhibits two different oxidation states.

Q13. Consider the elements: Cs, Ne, I and F. Identify the element that exhibits both positive and negative oxidation states.
    (A) Caesium
    (B) Iodine   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Neon and Fluorine
    (D) Neon
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Iodine has 7 electrons in its valency shell and can, therefore, exhibit an oxidation state of –1, However since Iodine has empty d orbitals it can also exhibit different oxidation state like +1,+3,+5, +7.

Q14. Consider the elements: Cs, Ne, I and F. Identify the element(s) which exhibits neither the negative nor does the positive oxidation state.
    (A) Ne and F
    (B) Ne   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Cs
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since, Ne is noble gas having stable electronic configuration i.e. 1s^2 2s^2 2p^6. So it do not show any positive or negative oxidation state.

Q15. In Ostwald’s process for the manufacture of nitric acid, the first step involves the oxidation of ammonia gas by oxygen gas to give nitric oxide gas and steam. What is the maximum weight of nitric oxide that can be obtained starting only with 10.00 g of ammonia and 20.00 g of oxygen?
    (A) 25g of NO
    (B) 16g of NO
    (C) 15g of NO   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 20g of NO
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The reaction that takes place in ammonia and oxygen is given below:
$\mathop {4N{H_3}}\limits_{68g} + \mathop {5{O_2}}\limits_{160g} \to \mathop {4NO}\limits_{120g} + 6{H_2}O$
Limiting reagent
160g of oxygen reacts with 68g of ammonia
20g of oxygen reacts with $\frac{68\times20}{160}
$ = 8.5g of ammonia
Therefore for 20g of oxygen 8.5g of ammonia is used. Therefore 1.5g ammonia is in excess and therefore oxygen is the limiting reagent.
160 g of O_2 produces = 120g of NO 
Therefore, 20 g of O_2 produces= $\frac{120\times20}{60}$ = 15 g of NO.

Q1. The s-block elements of the Periodic Table have only:
    (A) one group
    (B) two groups.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) four groups
    (D) three groups
    Answer: B
    Explanation: S-block comprises of only two groups alkali metal group and alkaline earth metal groups.

Q2. Group I elements of the periodic table are collectively known as:
    (A) noble gases
    (B) alkali metals.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) alkaline earth metals.
    (D) transition elements
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Group I (ns^1) elemens react vigorously with water to produce an alkaline solution thus collectively known as alkali metals.

Q3. Group IlA of the periodic table consists of the six elements are collectively known as _________.
    (A) noble gases
    (B) transition elements
    (C) alkali metals.
    (D) alkaline earth metals.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Group IlA of the periodic table consists of the six elements are collectively known as alkaline earth metals because their oxide and hydroxide are alkaline in nature and these metal oxide are found in earth's crust.

Q4. Which one of the following is not called alkaline earth metal?
    (A) Beryllium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Radium
    (C) Barium
    (D) Strontium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Alkaline earth metals are called so because of two reasons
 Alkaline earth metals are obtained on earth in the form of ores
 Oxides and hydroxides of Alkaline earth metals are basic in nature,
However, Beryllium fulfills 1st reason but its oxides and hydroxides are amphoteric so sometimes they say it is not alkaline earth metal. but as it is amphoteric IUPAC has accepted this as alkaline earth metal.

Q5. Calcium and Magnesium belong to the category of:
    (A) transition elements
    (B) Alkaline earth metals.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) alkali metals.
    (D) coordination compounds
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Calcium and magnesium are 2^nd group element of the periodic table which are obtained on earth in the form ore, their oxides and hydroxide are alkaline in nature so they are alkaline earth metals.

Q6. Sodium and potassium belong to the category of:
    (A) alkali metals.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) alkaline earth metals.
    (C) noble gases
    (D) transition elements
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Na and K are shiny, soft, highly reactive metal at standard temperature and pressure and electronic configuration of Na & K is ns^2, compounds of Na & K are available most abundantly in nature so these two are alkali metal.

Q7. Which one of the following is highly radioactive?
    (A) Francium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Lithium
    (C) Rubidium
    (D) Caesium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Fr is a highly radioactive metal, that decays into astatine, radium, and radon. It is also highly unstable element found only in trace amount on earth.

Q8. The correct sequence in decreasing order of the percentage of nitrogen in the given compounds is
    (A) Urea > Ammonium chloride > Ammonium nitrate > Ammonium nitrite
    (B) Urea > Ammonium nitrite > Ammonium chloride > Ammonium nitrate
    (C) Urea > Ammonium nitrate > Ammonium nitrite > Ammonium chloride
    (D) Urea > Ammonium nitrite > Ammonium nitrate > Ammonium chloride   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Correct sequence is $N H _ { 2 } C O N H _ { 2 } > N H _ { 4 } N _ { 3 } > N H _ { 3 } N O _ { 3 } > N H _ { 4 } C l$

Q9. Increase in ionic radii of alkali metals in aqueous solution (hydration) follow the order:
    (A) Rb^+ > Cs^+ < Li^+ < Na^+ < K^+
    (B) Na^+ > K^+ > Rb^+ > Cs^+ < Li^+
    (C) Li^+ > Na^+ > K^+ > Rb^+ > Cs^+   <-- CORRECT
    (D) K^+ > Rb^+ > Cs^+ < Li^+ < Na^+
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The alkali metal ions get extensively hydrated in aqueous solution. Smaller the ion more is the degree of hydration.

Q10. Monovalent sodium and potassium ions found in large proportions in biological fluids. They help in:
    (A) maintenance of cardiac rhythm
    (B) maintenance of peristalsis
    (C) maintenance of pulse rate
    (D) maintenance of nerve impulse conduction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Na and K ions help in the transmission of nerve impulses, in regulating the flow of water across the cell membranes, and in the transport of sugar and amino acids into cells. so monovalent sodium and potassium ions found in large proportions in biological fluids.

Q11. Choose the appropriate one that shows the hydration enthalpies of alkali metal ions in the decreasing order is.
    (A) Rb^+ > Cs^+ < Li^+ < Na^+ < K^+
    (B) K^+ > Rb^+ > Cs^+ < Li^+ < Na^+
    (C) Na^+ > K^+ > Rb^+ > Cs^+ < Li^+
    (D) Li^+ > Na^+ > K^+ > Rb^+ > Cs^+   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As the size increases positive charge density decreases so hydration energy also decreases. Hydration varies inversely with the size.

Q12. Divalent magnesium and calcium ions are found in large proportions in biological fluids. They help in:
    (A) maintenance of cardiac rhythm
    (B) maintenance of ion balance   <-- CORRECT
    (C) maintenance of peristalsis
    (D) maintenance of pulse rate
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Monovalent sodium and potassium ions and divalent magnesium and calcium ions are found in large proportions in biological fluids. These ions perform important biological functions such as maintenance of ion balance and nerve impulse conduction.

Q13. Which one of the following is the rarest of all alkaline earth metals?
    (A) Strontium
    (B) Beryllium
    (C) Barium
    (D) Radium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ra is found in Uranium and Thorium ores in trace amounts as small as a seventh of a gram per ton of uraninite. So, it is rarest of all alkaline earth metals.

Q14. Among the alkali metals, the most abundant metals are:
    (A) Rubidium and Lithium
    (B) Rubidium and Potassium
    (C) Sodium and Potassium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Sodium and Lithium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Na and K are highly abundant. Constituting 2.5 and 2.4 percent of the Earth's crust respectively the other alkali metals are considerably rare.

Q15. The general electronic configuration of alkali metals is:
    (A) ns^2
    (B) ns^1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1s^2
    (D) 1s^12s^1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The general electronic configuration of alkali metals is ns^1 as their outermost electron enters the s orbital and they have only on an electron in their valence shell.

Q1. The general electronic configuration of ns^2 exists in:
    (A) alkaline earth metals   <-- CORRECT
    (B) alkali metals
    (C) coordination compounds
    (D) transition elements
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The general electronic configuration of ns^2 exists in alkaline earth metals as their outer most electron enter the S orbital and they have only two electrons in their valence shell.

Q2. The alkali metals and their salts impart characteristic colour to an oxidizing flame because:
    (A) there is emission of radiation in the visible region from the excited electron   <-- CORRECT
    (B) sufficient light energy is absorbed to make an atom gain an electron
    (C) the smallest atomic size makes them to absorb radiation
    (D) the largest atomic size makes them to emit radiation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Alkali metals have one unpaired electron in their valence shell which gets excited by absorbing the energy from the flame, excited states are very unstable and quickly move back to a lower state, at that time they emit the energy in the form of radiation in visible reason of electromagnetic spectrum and is observed as characteristic colour.

Q3. Flame photometry is used to determine the concentration of the:
    (A) alkaline earth metals
    (B) noble gases
    (C) alkali metal ions   <-- CORRECT
    (D) transition elements
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Flame photometry is used to determine the concentration of alkali metal ions, alkaline earth metals are quite sensitive to flame photometry.

Q4. The electronic configuration of Rn7s^1 belongs to:
    (A) Francium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Rubidium
    (C) Caesium
    (D) Lithium
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Francium will fill orbitals all the way up to 7s (7^th period) subshell where it will have half-filled orbital: 7s^1.

Q5. The alkali metals burn vigorously in oxygen forming oxides. Hence, potassium forms ________.
    (A) hydroxide
    (B) peroxide
    (C) monoxide
    (D) superoxide   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Alkali metals burn vigorously to form superoxides. Superoxide O_2^- ion is formed only in the presence of large cations such as K, Rb, and Cs.

Q6. What is the oxidation state of K in KO_2?
    (A) +2
    (B) +4
    (C) +3
    (D) +1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: K has +1 oxidation state. "The potassium atom losses one electron when forming compound as it has one electron on it's valence shell".

Q7. ${\text{2M }} + {\text{ 2}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} \to {\text{2}}{{\text{M}}^ + } + {\text{ 2O}}{{\text{H}}^ - } + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}$. What is M?
    (A) transition elements
    (B) alkaline earth metals
    (C) noble gases
    (D) alkali metals   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: M is alkali metal. Alkali metals react with water vigorously to form hydroxide (OH^-) and dihydrogen (H_2).

Q8. Lithium has the most negative E^0 value, its reaction with water is less vigorous than that of sodium which has the least negative E^0 value among the alkali metals. The reason is:
    (A) it is a strong reducing agent
    (B) low hydration energy of Li
    (C) small size of Li   <-- CORRECT
    (D) it is a proton donor
    Answer: C
    Explanation: This behaviour of lithium is attributed to its small size and very high hydration energy. Li^+ has a maximum degree of hydration.

Q9. When sodium is dissolved in liquid ammonia, a solution of deep blue colour is obtained. The colour of the solution is due to
    (A) sodium amide
    (B) sodium ion
    (C) ammoniated electron   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ammoniated sodium ion
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The alkali metals dissolve in liquid ammonia giving deep blue solutions which are conducting in nature. The blue colour of the solution is due to the ammoniated electron which absorbs energy in the visible region of light and thus imparts blue colour to the solution.
$M+(x+y)NH_3\to[M(NH_3)_x]^+[e(NH_3)_y]^-$

Q10. The alkali metals dissolve in liquid ammonia giving deep blue solutions. When they become diamagnetic, the solution turns into:
    (A) green colour
    (B) bronze colour   <-- CORRECT
    (C) purple colour
    (D) white colour
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When the solution becomes diamagnetic due to the formation of an electron cluster in which ammoniated electron with the opposite spin group. It changes its color to bronze.

Q11. Lithium halides are somewhat covalent because
    (A) Li+ ion is very large in size and has high tendency to distort electron
    (B) Li+ ion is very small in size and has low tendency to distort electron
    (C) low polarisation capability of lithium ion
    (D) high polarisation capability of lithium ion   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Li^+ ion has a small size and maximum tendency to attract the electrons towards itself from the negative ion. This distortion of the electron cloud of the negative ion by the positive ion is known as polarization. Thus Li^+ has high polarization capability. Lithium iodide is the most covalent in nature.

Q12. Choose the correct trend of the melting and boiling points in the alkali metal halides: MF, MCl, MI, MBr.
    (A) MCl > MBr > MI
    (B) MF > MCl > MBr > MI   <-- CORRECT
    (C) MBr > MI
    (D) MI
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Smaller is the size of anion less is the polarizing power of anion so greater is the ionic character hence greater will be the melting point.

Q13. All alkali metal halides are soluble in water except:
    (A) Francium
    (B) Lithium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Rubidium
    (D) Caesium
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Greater the lattice energy, the higher is the melting point of the MX (metal halide) and the lower is its solubility.

Q14. Why KO_2 is paramagnetic?
    (A) because of large size of the metal ion
    (B) because of one unpaired electron in ${\pi ^ * }$ 1p
    (C) because of oxygen atom in -1/2 oxidation state   <-- CORRECT
    (D) because of lattice energy effects
    Answer: C
    Explanation: KO_2 is superoxide, K is in the +1 oxidation state, and O_2 has -1 oxidation state, thus each O has -1/2 oxidation state. So due to the presence of unpaired electron, it behaves as free radical. As we know that a molecule containing an unpaired electron is paramagnetic in nature. So KO_2 is paramagnetic in nature because of one unpaired electron in $\pi$*2p molecular orbital.

Q15. Alkali metal chlorides donot form hydrates except for one metal. Choose from among the options given below.
    (A) Rubidium
    (B) Francium
    (C) Lithium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Caesium
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Lithium due to its high hydration energy (deliquescent) forms hydrate.

The s Block Elements CBSE Online Test 03  (id 978) [PAID]
