Q1. In the preparation of sodium carbonate the by-products formed are:
    (A) NH_4Cl
    (B) CaCl_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) NH_3
    (D) Ca(OH)_2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Sodium carbonate is generally prepared by Solvay Process. First ammonium bicarbonate is prepared by passing CO_2 to a concentrated solution of sodium chloride saturated with ammonia, where ammonium carbonate followed by ammonium hydrogen carbonate is formed. The equations for the complete process may be written as : 
$2NH_3+H_2O+CO_2\to(NH_4)_2CO_3$
$(NH_4)_2CO_3+H_2O+CO_2\to2NH_4HCO_3$
$NH_4HCO_3+NaCl\to NH_4Cl+NaHCO_3$
Sodium hydrogen carbonate crystal separates. These are heated to give sodium carbonate. 
$2NaHCO_3\to Na_2CO_3+CO_2+H_2O$
In this process, NH_3 is recovered when the solution containing NH_4Cl is treated with Ca(OH)_2. Calcium chloride is obtained as a by-product.
$2NH_4Cl+Ca(OH)_2\to 2NH_3 + CaCl_2+H_2O$

Q2. Washing soda is:
    (A) Na_2CO_3.5H_2O
    (B) Na_2CO_3.10H_2O   <-- CORRECT
    (C) NH_4Cl
    (D) Na_2CO_3.9H_2O
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Washing soda is Na_2CO_3.10H_2O i.e. sodium carbonate decahydrate. It is used in water softening, laundering and cleaning, manufacture of glass, etc.

Q3. The common salt or table salt is:
    (A) Ammonium chloride
    (B) Sodium chloride   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Calcium chloride
    (D) Potassium chloride
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Common salt is sodium chloride i.e. NaCl. It is generally obtained by the evaporation of seawater. It is used as table salt for domestic purposes.

Q4. Caustic soda is:
    (A) Ammonium hydroxide
    (B) Calcium hydroxide
    (C) Potassium hydroxide
    (D) Sodium hydroxide   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Caustic Soda is Sodium hydroxide i.e. NaOH. Sodium hydroxide is generally prepared commercially by the electrolysis of sodium chloride in the Castner-Kellner cell. It is used in the manufacture of soap.

Q5. Sodium hydrogen carbonate is known as:
    (A) baking soda   <-- CORRECT
    (B) washing soda
    (C) caustic soda
    (D) table salt
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Sodium hydrogen carbonate i.e. NaHCO_3 is baking soda because it decomposes on heating to generate bubbles of carbon dioxide (leaving holes in cakes or pastries and making them light and fluffy).

Q6. Potassium ions are the most abundant cations. They
    (A) found primarily on the outside of cells.
    (B) have a role in the oxidation of glucose to produce ATP.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) inactivate many enzymes which help in penetration of cell membrane.
    (D) are the most abundant anions within cell fluids.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Potassium ions are the most abundant cations. They activate many enzymes and participate in the oxidation of glucose to produce ATP.

Q7. To acquire a noble gas configuration, alkaline earth metals lose:
    (A) 4 electrons
    (B) 3 electrons
    (C) 2 electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1 electron
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Alkaline earth metals have two electrons in the s-orbital of the valence shell. Their general electronic configuration may be represented as [noble gas] ns^2. So they lose 2 electrons to attain noble gas configuration.

Q8. Alkaline earth metals have a large size of the atoms. Therefore, they shows
    (A) Low hydration enthalpies.
    (B) Low ionization enthalpies.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Low electopositivity.
    (D) Low nuclear charge.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The reason is that the atoms of alkali metals are of large sizes. therefore, the outermost electron is for away from the nucleus and can be easily removed.

Q9. Choose the correct order of increase in electropositivity of alkaline earth metals in the options given below:
    (A) ${\text{B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${\text{C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    (C) ${\text{M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    (D) ${\text{S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As we move down the group size increases so IE value decreases thus electropositivity also decreases (shielding effect also decreases as we go down the Group).

Q10. Choose the correct order of increase in the ionic size of alkaline earth metals in the options given below:
    (A) ${\text{M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    (B) ${\text{C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    (C) ${\text{B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\text{S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} > {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As we move down the group ionic radii increases.

Q11. Beryllium carbonate is unstable and can be kept only in the atmosphere of:
    (A) O_2
    (B) NO_2
    (C) SO_2
    (D) CO_2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Beryllium carbonate is reported to be unstable under normal conditions and decomposes into BeO and CO_2 so it has to be stored under CO_2 to maintain equilibrium.
BeCO_​​​3 $ \leftrightarrow $ BeO+CO_2

Q12. Radium salts are used in:
    (A) the treatment of infectious diseases
    (B) the treatment of metal sheets
    (C) the treatment of tuberculosis
    (D) the treatment of cancer   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Radium salts are used in radiotherapy, for example, in the treatment of cancer.

Q13. Choose the correct order of decrease in hydration enthalpies of alkaline earth metals in the options given below.
    (A) ${\text{S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    (B) ${\text{C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    (C) ${\text{M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$
    (D) ${\text{B}}{{\text{e}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ M}}{{\text{g}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ C}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ S}}{{\text{r}}^{{\text{2}} + }} < {\text{ B}}{{\text{a}}^{{\text{2}} + }}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As the size increases due to increase in ionic radii , hydration energy decreases.

Q14. Why does the solubility of alkaline earth metal carbonates and sulphates in water decrease down the group?
    (A) hydration enthalpy decreases down the group   <-- CORRECT
    (B) lattice enthalpy decreases down the group
    (C) size of anions being much shorterer compared to cations
    (D) coordination numbesr more than four
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The solubility of sulphates and carbonates decreases down the group because of decrease in hydration energy which is insufficient to overcome the lattice energy of ions.

Q15. Calcium oxide is prepared on a commercial scale by using:
    (A) limestone and Solvay process
    (B) limestone and rotary kiln   <-- CORRECT
    (C) limestone and Daniell cell
    (D) limestone and Castner-Kellner cell
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Rotary kiln is used for the calcination of limestone (CaCO_3) to produce calcium oxide (quicklime).
CaCO_3 $\longleftrightarrow$ CaO+CO_2

Q1. Heating a pulverised mixture of limestone and clay in a rotary kiln is used in the manufacture of:
    (A) Slaked lime
    (B) Portland cement   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Plaster of Paris
    (D) Lime
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Heating a pulverised mixture of limestone and clay in a rotary kiln is used in the manufacture of Portland cement. Cement is a product obtained by combining a material rich in lime, CaO with other materials such as clay which contains silica, SiO_2 along with the oxides of aluminium, iron, and magnesium.

Q2. Cement is an industrially important compound of:
    (A) Magnesium
    (B) Potassium
    (C) Sodium
    (D) Calcium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Cement is an important compound of Calcium. Cement is a product obtained by combining a material rich in lime, CaO with other materials such as clay which contains silica, SiO_2 long with the oxides of aluminium, iron, and magnesium.

Q3. The alkali metals are low melting. Which of the following alkali metal is expected to melt if the room temperature rises to ${\text{3}}0^\circ {\text{C}}?$
    (A) Na
    (B) Rb
    (C) Cs   <-- CORRECT
    (D) K
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Cs has very low melting point (24.44 degree Celsius). It can melt even with the heat of the hand.

Q4. Alkali metals react with water vigorously to form hydroxides and dihydrogen.Which of the following alkali metals reacts with water least vigorously?
    (A) Cs
    (B) Na
    (C) K
    (D) Li   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Li reacts with water least vigorously, since the density of Li is only about half that of water,so it floats on the surface and ultimately dissappears,giving off H_2 gas

Q5. The reducing power of a metal depends on various factors. Suggest the factor which makes Li, the strongest reducing agent in aqueous solution.
    (A) Electron-gain enthalpy
    (B) Hydration enthalpy   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Sublimation enthalpy
    (D) Ionisation enthalpy
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Lithium (Li) is the strongest reducing agent in aqueous solution because of its extremely high hydration enthalpy.
 When Li loses an electron to form Li⁺, the small ion with high charge density gets very strongly hydrated in water.
 This large negative hydration enthalpy compensates for its high ionization energy.
 As a result, the overall reduction potential becomes highly negative, making Li a very strong reducing agent.
So, hydration enthalpy is the dominant factor here.

Q6. Metal carbonates decompose on heating to give metal oxide and carbon dioxide. Which of the metal carbonates is most stable thermally?
    (A) CaCO_3
    (B) MgCO_3
    (C) SrCO_3
    (D) BaCO_3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: BaCO_3 is very stable due to the size compatibility factor. A larger cation can stabilize a larger anion. Group 2 elements become more thermally stable down the group.

Q7. The diagonal relationship exists between:
    (A) Lithium and aluminium
    (B) Beryllium and Magnesium
    (C) Lithium and Beryllium
    (D) Lithium and Magnesium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: 1^st element of 1^st group and the second element of 2^nd group exist in the diagonal relationship due to their nearly same polarizing power.

Q8. Metals form basic hydroxides. Which of the following metal hydroxide is the least basic?
    (A) ${\text{Ca}}{\left( {{\text{OH}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$
    (B) ${\text{Mg}}{\left( {{\text{OH}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${\text{Ba}}{\left( {{\text{OH}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$
    (D) ${\text{Sr}}{\left( {{\text{OH}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Due to small size of Mg. Mg-O become more stronger hence tendency of OH to leave decreases thus basic character decreases.

Q9. Some of the Group 2 metal halides are covalent and soluble in organic solvents. Among the following metal halides, the one which is soluble in ethanol is
    (A) SrCl_2
    (B) CaCl_2
    (C) BeCl_2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) MgCl_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: BeCl_2 is soluble in ethanol. As BeCl_2_ is hygroscopic it is soluble in many polar solvent.

Q10. The order of decreasing ionisation enthalpy in alkali metals is
    (A) K < Li < Na < Rb
    (B) Li > Na > K > Rb   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Rb < Na < K < Li
    (D) Na > Li > K > Rb
    Answer: B
    Explanation: As we more down the group size increases and also ionization energy decreases.

Q11. The solubility of metal halides depends on their nature, lattice enthalpy and hydration enthalpy of the individual ions. Amongst fluorides of alkali metals,the lowest solubility of LiF in water is due to
    (A) High hydration enthalpy for lithium ion.
    (B) Ionic nature of lithium fluoride
    (C) High lattice enthalpy   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Low ionisation enthalpy of lithium atom
    Answer: C
    Explanation: LiF has very high lattice energy which cannot be compensated by Hydration Energy.

Q12. Amphoteric hydroxides react with both alkalies and acids. Which of the following Group 2 metal hydroxides is soluble in sodium hydroxide?
    (A) Ca(OH)_2
    (B) Mg(OH)_2
    (C) O_2(OH)_2
    (D) Ba(OH)_2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: BaOH_2 is soluble in NaOH. Since Be act as amphoteric unlike other groups 2 elements.

Q13. In the synthesis of sodium carbonate, the recovery of ammonia is done by treating NH_4Cl with Ca(OH)_2. The by-product obtained in this process is
    (A) CaCl_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) NaOH
    (C) NaCl
    (D) NaHCO_3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: By product obtained in this process is CaCl_​2​​.
NH_4Cl + Ca(OH)_2 $\to$ CaCl_2 + 2NH_3+H_2O

Q14. The nitrate of which of the following alkaline earth metals crystallizes as anhydrous salt?
    (A) Mg
    (B) Sr
    (C) Ca
    (D) Ba   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Magnesium nitrate crystallizes with six molecules of water, whereas barium nitrate crystallizes as the anhydrous salt. This shows a decreasing tendency to form hydrates with increasing size and decreasing hydration enthalpy.

Q15. By adding gypsum to cement
    (A) setting time of cement becomes less.
    (B) shining surface is obtained.
    (C) colour of cement becomes light.
    (D) setting time of cement increases.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When mixed with water, the setting of cement takes place to give a hard mass. This is due to the hydration of the molecules of the constituents and their rearrangement. The purpose of adding gypsum is only to slow down the process of setting of the cement so that it gets sufficiently hardened

Q1. Dead burnt plaster is
    (A) CaSO_4.$\frac{1}{2}$H_2O
    (B) CaSO_4   <-- CORRECT
    (C) CaSO_4.2H_2O
    (D) CaSO4.H_2O
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Above 393 K, no water of crystallisation is left and anhydrous calcium sulphate, CaSO_4 is formed. This is known as ‘dead burnt plaster’.

Q2. The suspension of slaked lime in water is known as:
    (A) aqueous solution of slaked lime
    (B) lime water
    (C) quick lime
    (D) milk of lime   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Slaked lime is Ca(OH)_2. Suspension of slaked lime in water is known as milk of lime because it looks just like milk.

Q3. Which of the following elements does not form hydride by direct heating with dihydrogen?
    (A) Sr
    (B) Mg
    (C) Ba
    (D) Be   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Be does not form hydride directly by reacting with hydrogen. It possesses a polymeric bridge structure with H_2 between two atoms.

Q4. The formula of soda ash is _________.
    (A) ${\text{N}}{{\text{a}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}.{\text{ 1}}0{\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
    (B) ${\text{N}}{{\text{a}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}.{\text{ 2}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
    (C) Na_2CO_3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\text{N}}{{\text{a}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}.{\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Above 373K, sodium carbonate monohydrate becomes completely anhydrous and changes to a white powder called soda ash i.e. Na_2CO_3.

Q5. A substance which gives brick red flame and breaks down on heating to give oxygen and a brown gas is
    (A) Barium nitrate
    (B) Magnesium nitrate
    (C) Calcium nitrate   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Strontium nitrate
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ca give brick red flame.

Q6. Which of the following statements is true about Ca(OH)_2?
    (A) It is a light blue solid
    (B) It does not possess disinfectant property.
    (C) It is used in the preparation of bleaching powder   <-- CORRECT
    (D) It is used in the manufacture of cement.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ca(OH)_2 is a white amorphous powder which is used in the manufacture of bleaching powder. It is used in the white wash because of its disinfectant nature.

Q7. A chemical A is used for the preparation of washing soda to recover ammonia. When CO_2 is bubbled through an aqueous solution of A, the solution turns milky. It is used in white-washing due to disinfectant nature. What is the chemical formula of A?
    (A) CaO
    (B) ${\text{CaC}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}$
    (C) ${\text{Ca}}{\left( {{\text{HC}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$
    (D) ${\text{Ca}}{\left( {{\text{OH}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ca(OH)_2 is used for the preparation of washing soda to recover ammonia. 
$2NH_4Cl+Ca(OH)_2\to CaCl_2+2NH_3+H_2O$ 
When CO_2 is passed through Ca(OH)_2, CaCO_3 is formed which turns the solution milky.
Ca(OH)_2 + CO_2 $\longrightarrow$ CaCO_3

Q8. Dehydration of hydrates of halides of calcium, barium and strontium i.e., ${\text{CaC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{6}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}},$ ${\text{BaC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}.{\text{2 }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}},{\text{ SrC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}.{\text{2 }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}},$ can be achieved by heating. These become wet on keeping in air. Which of the following statements is correct about these halides?
    (A) Tendency to form hydrate decreases from calcium to barium
    (B) can absorb moisture from air
    (C) act as dehydrating agent
    (D) All of these   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: All of these statements are coorect as these halides absorb water and due to decrease in the hydration energy down the group tendency to from hydrates decreases.

Q9. Choose the correct statements from the following.
 Beryllium is not readily attacked by acids because of the presence of an oxide film on the surface of the metal.
 Beryllium sulphate is insoluble in water as the greater lattice enthalpy factor of Be^2+ overcomes the hydration enthalpy.
 Beryllium exhibits a coordination number of more than four.
 Beryllium oxide is purely acidic in nature.
    (A) (D)
    (B) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (B)
    (D) (C)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The surface of the Beryllium metal is covered with a thin layer of oxides that helps protect the metal from attack by acid, but powdered beryllium metal dissolves readily in dilute acids.

Q10. Identify the correct formula of halides of alkaline earth metals from the following:
    (A) ${\text{CaC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}.{\text{3}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
    (B) ${\text{BaC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}.{\text{2}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${\text{BaC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}.{\text{4}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
    (D) ${\text{SrC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}.{\text{4}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The tendency to form halide hydrates gradually decreases down the group.${\text{BaC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}.{\text{2}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$ i.e., Barium chloride dihydrate exists.

Q11. Several sodium compounds find use in industries. Which of the following compounds is/ are used for textile industry?
    (A) NaHCO_3
    (B) NaCl
    (C) Na_2CO_3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Na_2SO_4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Sodium carbonate i.e. Na_2CO_3​​​​​​​ is used in paper, paints and textile industries.

Q12. Which of the following compounds are readily soluble in water?
    (A) ${\text{BeS}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) SrSO_4
    (C) BaSO_4
    (D) Na_2SO_4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: BeSO_4 being unstable is readily soluble in water. Also, the hydration energy of Be is high due to the small size.

Q13. When Zeolite, which is hydrated sodium aluminium silicate is treated with hard water, the sodium ions are exchanged with which of the following ion(s)?
    (A) H^+ ions
    (B) O^2- ions
    (C) Mg^2+ ions   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $S{\text{O}}_4^{2 - }$ ions
    Answer: C
    Explanation: When hard water containing Mg^2+ and Ca^2+ passes through a bed of sodium zeolite, then the sodium ions are replaced with by the calcium and magnesium ions. This is used in the water softening process.

Q14. Which of the following are the correct reasons for anomalous behaviour of lithium?
    (A) Its low polarising power
    (B) Exceptionally low ionisation enthalpy
    (C) Exceptionally small size of its atom   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Low degree of hydration
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The anomalous behaviour of lithium is due to the : (i) exceptionally small size of its atom and ion, and (ii) high polarising power (i.e., charge/ radius ratio). As a result, there is an increased covalent character of lithium compounds which is responsible for their solubility in organic solvents.

Q15. Magnesium do not impart any colour to the flame because:
    (A) Low thermal conductivities.
    (B) The electrons in magnesium are too loosly bound to get excited.
    (C) The electrons in magnesium are too strongly bound to get excited.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Low absorption of light energy.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Electrons in Mg are held closer to nucleus as it is very small in size. So does not get excited by the energy provided by flame.

The p Block Elements CBSE Online Test 01  (id 981) [FREE]

Q1. The valence shell electronic configuration of p-block elements is ns^2np^1-6. But this is not true in the case of______.
    (A) Nitrogen
    (B) Helium   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Boron
    (D) Carbon
    Answer: B
    Explanation: He has 1s^2 configuration. It is a noble gas.

Q2. There are six groups of p-block elements in the periodic table numbering from:
    (A) 11 to 16
    (B) 12 to 17
    (C) 14 to 19
    (D) 13 to 18   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: After two s block and 10 d block, p block elements starts from group 13 to group 18.

Q3. The variation in properties in a group of p-block of elements is due to:
    (A) difference in ionisation enthalpies.
    (B) difference in electronegativities.
    (C) difference in inner core of the electronic configuration.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) difference in oxidation states.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The difference in properties of p block element is because of the presence of inner lying d and f electrons which have poor shielding effect.

Q4. The maximum oxidation state shown by any p-block element is:
    (A) The sum of the s electrons
    (B) The sum of the p-electrons
    (C) The sum of the s and p-electrons   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Half of the sum of the s and p-electrons
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The maximum oxidation state of any p block element is the number of ionizable electrons which is equal to the sum of s and p electrons present in the valence shell. For example, the valance shell electronic configuration of group 15 element is ns^2np^3. So the maximum oxidation state is +5.

Q5. The sum of the s and p-electrons is called:
    (A) The most unstable valence number of p-block elements
    (B) The group oxidation state of p-block elements   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Inert pair of p-block elements
    (D) The most stable valence number of p-block elements
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The group oxidation state is the highest oxidation state exhibited by the elements present in any particular group.
For p block elements it is the sum of the s and p-electrons.

Q6. The inert pair effect of p-block elements is due to the:
    (A) the most stable valence number of p-block elements.
    (B) the group oxidation state of p-block elements.
    (C) the most unstable valence number of p-block elements.
    (D) the inertness of the inner ns electrons because of ineffective shielding.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The inert pair effect is nothing but the extra stability concept. Generally, P-block elements show variable valiancy which is equal to the maximum oxidation (Group oxidation state) state of that group of p-block elements, p block elements may show another oxidation state i.e.+2.
Group oxidation state +4 is obtained when electrons are lost from both ns and np levels, +2 oxidation state is obtained while only np level electrons are lost due to extra stability and poor shielding of ns electron which are called inert pair. The effect is the inert effect.

Q7. The element which exists in liquid state for a wide range of temperature and can be used for measuring high temperature is______.
    (A) Ga   <-- CORRECT
    (B) AI
    (C) B
    (D) In
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The melting point of gallium is 30^o C and the boiling point is 2240^o C. Thus, the element exists in the liquid state for a wide range of temperatures.

Q8. As we move from B to Al in the p-block elements the sum of the first three ionisation enthalpies:
    (A) Considerably decreases   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Remains the same
    (C) Slightly decreases
    (D) Increases
    Answer: A
    Explanation: On moving from B to Al size of the atom increases. So ionization enthalpy decreases. Thus as we move from B to Al in the p-block elements the sum of the first three ionization enthalpies considerably decreases.
This is the reason aluminium forms Al^3+ ion.

Q9. Boron forms only covalent compounds and not +3 ions because:
    (A) the sum of its first two ionization enthalpies is very low.
    (B) the sum of its first two ionization enthalpies is very high.
    (C) the sum of its first three ionization enthalpies is very low.
    (D) the sum of its first three ionization enthalpies is very high.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Due to smaller size and high nuclear charge B has a very high ionization energy value so does not show a +3 oxidation state. Further according to Fajan's rule, cation with a small size and high positive charge leads to a covalent bond.

Q10. One of the following p-block elements has unusually low melting point_________.
    (A) aluminium
    (B) boron
    (C) indium
    (D) gallium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ga does not do not follow any of the simple crystal structures. And two nearest Ga atoms are bonded by a covalent bond which leads to the low melting point.

Q11. Which of the following p-block elements in group 13 could exist in a liquid state during summer?
    (A) Gallium   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Indium
    (C) Aluminium
    (D) Boron
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Ga has a very low melting point (MP = 29.76^oC), and because of that, it can exist in a liquid state during summer.

Q12. The relative stability of +1 oxidation state progressively increases for heavier elements. Choose one of the following having most stable +1 oxidation state.
    (A) In
    (B) Al
    (C) Tl   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ga
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Due to the inert pair effect, Tl^+1 is the most stable oxidation state.

Q13. Aluminium when exposed to air protects itself from further attack by:
    (A) reacting with air and liberating dihydrogen.
    (B) forming a very thin oxide layer on its surface.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) forming aluminium trioxide.
    (D) reacting with hydrogen in the air.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Al forms a thick layer of oxide (Al_2O_3) on its surface which protects it from further attack.

Q14. White fumes appear around the bottle of anhydrous aluminium chloride. Why?
    (A) Formation of HCl on reaction with atmospheric moisture and then Aluminium dissolves in dilute HCl and liberates dihydrogen.
    (B) Formation of HCl on reaction with atmospheric moisture and then Aluminium reacts with dilute HCl and forms aluminium chloride.
    (C) Liberation of HCl on reaction with atmospheric moisture.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Formation of dihydrogen on reaction with atmospheric moisture.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: White fumes appear because of the formation of HCl on reaction with atmospheric moisture. White fumes appear due to the formation of HCl gas. Anhydrous aluminium chloride is partly hydrolyzed by the moisture in the atmosphere and produces HCl gas. This HCl further combines with the moisture of the air and appears white fumes.
AlCl_3 +3H_2O $\longrightarrow$ Al(OH)_3 +3HCl

Q15. Diborane is produced on an industrial scale by the reaction of BF_3 with:
    (A) Sodium hydride   <-- CORRECT
    (B) LiBH_4
    (C) Diethyl ether
    (D) NaBH_4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Reaction of BF_3 with NaH produces B_2H_6 At 450K following reaction happens
2BF_3 + 6NaH $\longrightarrow$ B_2H_6 + 6NaF

Q1. The angular shape of ozone molecules (O_3) consists of
    (A) 2 sigma and 2 pi bonds
    (B) 2 sigma and 1 pi bonds   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1 sigma and 2 pi bonds
    (D) 4 sigma and 3 pi bonds
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The ozone structure will have a single bond, a double bond, and two resonance structure, therefore, O_3 consists of 2 sigma bond and 1 pie bond.

Q2. Boric acid is an acid because of its molecule:
    (A) accepts OH^- from water releasing proton.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) contains replaceable H^+ ion.
    (C) gives up a proton.
    (D) combines with proton from water molecule.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Because of the small size of the boron atom and the presence of only six electrons in its valence shell, B(OH)_3 accepts a pair of electrons from OH^- ion of H_2O, releasing a proton.

Q3. Silicon is the second most abundant element on the earth’s crust and is a component of:
    (A) Flux for soldering metals
    (B) Glass wool
    (C) Antiseptic materials
    (D) Ceramics   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Si is the most imp component of ceramics, which is comprised of metal, non-metal, or metalloids held by an ionic or covalent bond.

Q4. Carbon is most widely distributed in nature. In the combined state, it is available as:
    (A) hydrocarbons   <-- CORRECT
    (B) coal
    (C) graphite
    (D) diamond
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In combined state C can occur as hydrocarbons (which is a compound of carbon and hydrogen).

Q5. Stable isotopes of carbon are:
    (A) C^14 and C^15
    (B) C^14 and C^13
    (C) C^12 and C^14
    (D) C^12 and C^13   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: C^12 and C^13 are the most abundant isotopes of Carbon which are very stable. Other isotopes like C^14 is radioactive (disintegrate to give other products).

Q6. The elements of group 14 are slightly more electronegative than group 13 elements because of:
    (A) High melting point
    (B) Small size   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Their being liquids
    (D) High boiling point
    Answer: B
    Explanation: As we move along the period electronegativity increases due to an increase in nuclear charge and a decrease in size.

Q7. In general, non-metals as compared to metals have:
    (A) Lower covalent character of the compounds formed between them
    (B) Higher ionization enthalpies   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Non-metals readily form cations
    (D) Lower ionisation enthalpies
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Non-metals have a high value of ionization energy while metals have a comparatively low value of ionization energy.
As we move across a period (Metal are there in the left-hand side and nonmetals are there in the right-hand side), the ionization energy of an element increases. This is because of the effective nuclear charge increases.

Q8. The compounds formed by highly reactive non-metals with highly reactive metals are generally:
    (A) Slightly different in their ionisation enthalpies
    (B) Covalent
    (C) Slightly different in their electronegativities
    (D) Ionic   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Compounds formed by highly reactive non-metals and metals is an ionic bond. Here metal will loose electron to form cation and nonmetal will gain an electron to form an anion.

Q9. The non-metal oxides are:
    (A) Basic
    (B) Basic or acidic
    (C) Basic or neutral
    (D) Acidic or neutral   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Nonmetallic oxides are either neutral or acidic. Example CO, NO, H_2O is neutral while CO_2 is acidic.

Q10. The element having the noble gas plus 14 f- electrons plus 10 d-electron cores______.
    (A) Boron
    (B) Gallium
    (C) Aluminium
    (D) Thallium   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Thallium has noble gas + 14 f +10 d electrons.
[Xe] 4f^_14 5d^_10 6s^_2 6p^_1 . Thus the electronic structure of these element is more complex.

Q11. The element having the noble gas plus 10 d-electron cores________.
    (A) Aluminium
    (B) Thallium
    (C) Gallium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Boron
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Both gallium and Indium has noble gas +10 d electrons [Ar] 3d^10 4s^2 4p^1 and [ Kr] 4d^105s^25p^1 respectively.

Q12. Which of the following is a Lewis acid?
    (A) AlCl_3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) CaCl_2
    (C) BaCl_2
    (D) MgCl_2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: AlCl_3 is lewis acid. Group 13 halides are lewis acid because of having incompletely filled orbitals.

Q13. Which of the following oxides is acidic in nature?
    (A) In_2O_3
    (B) Al_2O_3
    (C) B_2O_3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Ga_2O_3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As we go down the group metallic character increases. So most acidic oxide is the oxide of most non metallic element, i.e. B_2O_3

Q14. Boron from covalent Compound due to
    (A) Small size
    (B) higher ionisation enthalpy and Small size   <-- CORRECT
    (C) higher ionisation enthalpy
    (D) Lower ionisation enthalpy
    Answer: B
    Explanation: higher ionisation enthalpy and Small size

Q15. The geometry of a complex species can be understood from the knowledge of the type of hybridization of orbitals of the central atom. The hybridization of orbitals of the central atom in $\left[ {{\text{Be}}{{\left( {{\text{OH}}} \right)}_{\text{4}}}} \right]$ and the geometry of the complex is respectively.
    (A) sp^3 ^ -square planar
    (B) dsp^2, square planar
    (C) sp^3 and tetrahedral   <-- CORRECT
    (D) sp^3d^2,octahedral
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In [Be(OH)_4] Be is tetrahedrally surrounded by 4 OH^- ion.

Q1. Catenation i.e., linking of similar atoms depends on size and electronic configuration of atoms. The tendency of catenation in Group 14 elements follows the order:
    (A) Ge > Sn > Si > C
    (B) Si > C > Sn > Ge
    (C) ${\text{C }} > > {\text{ Si }} > {\text{ Ge }} \approx {\text{ Sn}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) C > Si > Ge > Sn
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Catenation property decreases down the group as size of the atom increases.

Q2. Silicon has a strong tendency to form polymers like silicones. The chain length of silicone polymer can be controlled by adding:
    (A) Me_3SiCl   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Me_2SiCl_2
    (C) Me_4Si
    (D) MeSiCl_3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Me_3SiCl has only one Cl and (can react once) to forms only dimer thus it is used as a chain controlling agent (terminate the polymerisation process).

Q3. In the structure of diborane:
    (A) All hydrogen atoms lie in one plane and boron atoms lie in a plane perpendicular to this plane.
    (B) 2 boron atoms and 4 terminal hydrogen atoms lie in the same plane and 2 bridging hydrogen atoms lie in the perpendicular plane.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) All the atoms are in the same plane.
    (D) 4 bridging hydrogen atoms and boron atoms lie in one plane and two terminal hydrogen atoms lie in a plane perpendicular to this plane.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: B_2H_6 has 4 terminal H attached to B atoms and all these lies in the same plane. Also in diborane, we have 2 bridging hydrogens (3 centre 2 electrons) which lie perpendicular to the plane.

Q4. Quartz is extensively used as a piezoelectric material, it contains ___________.
    (A) Sn
    (B) Ti
    (C) Pb
    (D) Si   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Quartz contains Si. [Piezoelectric materials produces electricity when pressure is applied]

Q5. A compound X, of boron, reacts with NH_3 on heating to give another compound. Y which is called inorganic benzene. The compound X can be prepared by treating BF_3 with Lithium aluminium hydride. The compounds X and Y are represented by the formulas.
    (A) B_2O_3, B_3N_3H_6
    (B) B_3N_3H_6, B_2H_6
    (C) BF_3, B_3N_3H_6
    (D) B_2H_6, B_3N_3H_6   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: BF_3 reacts with LiAlH_4 to form B_2H_6 which reacts with NH_3 in 1:2 ratio forming B_3N_3H_6 (Borazine, inorganic benzene). Reaction is as below:
3B_2H_6 + 6NH_3 $\rightarrow$ 2B_3N_3H_6 + 12H_2
Preparation of B_2H_6
4BF_3 + 3LiAlH_4 $\rightarrow$ 2B_2H_6 + 3LiF + 3AlF_3.

Q6. The linear shape of CO_2 is due to _________.
    (A) dsp^2 hybridisation of carbon
    (B) sp^2 hybridisation of carbon
    (C) sp^3 hybridisation of carbon
    (D) p$\pi$– p$\pi $ bonding between carbon and oxygen   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In CO_2 (​​​​O=C=O) hybridization of C is sp so due to p$\pi$ –p$\pi$ bonding it is linear. Further carbon is sp hybridized, and have a linear structure.

Q7. The reason for the small radius of Ga compared to Al is:
    (A) Higher atomic number
    (B) Poor screening effect of d and f orbitals   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Decrease in nuclear charge
    (D) Presence of higher orbitals
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The presence of an additional 10d- electrons offers a poor screening effect for the outer electrons from the increased nuclear charge in gallium.
[Electronic configuration of Ga is [Ar] 3d^10 4s^2 4p^1, that of aluminum is [Ne]3s^23p^1].

Q8. Cement, the important building material is a mixture of oxides of several elements. Besides iron and sulphur, oxides of elements of which of the group (s) are present in the mixture?
    (A) groups 2 and 13
    (B) groups 2 and 14
    (C) Groups 2, 13 and 14   <-- CORRECT
    (D) group 2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Main Composition of Portland cement are: lime (CaO) (group 2), silica (SiO _2)(group 14) and alumina (Al _2O _3).(group 13) 
Cement is a heavy powder of calcium aluminates and silicates

Q9. Dry ice is:
    (A) Solid CO_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Solid N_2
    (C) Solid NH_3
    (D) Solid SO_2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Dry ice is solid CO_2. Solid CO_2 sublimates. Thus it does not wet anything and called dry ice.

Q10. In trivalent state, for example, the trichlorides, being covalent are hydrolysed in water form:
    (A) Planar structure
    (B) Pentagonal structure
    (C) Trigonal structure
    (D) Tetrahedral structure   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Trihalides hydrolysis to form a tetrahedral structure with four covalent bonds.

Q11. Diamond is covalent, yet it has a high melting point because of:
    (A) the presence of rigid three dimensional extended networks thought the lattice.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) sp^2 hybridisation with strong C-C bonds difficult to break.
    (C) planar structure with strong C-C bonds difficult to break.
    (D) 2-dimensional network with strong C-C bonds difficult to break.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Carbon atom undergoes sp^3 hybridization and linked to four other carbon atoms by using hybridized orbitals in tetrahedral fashion-led a rigid three-dimensional extended network thought the lattice.

Q12. The valence shell electronic configuration of p-block elements is ns^2np^1 - 6. But this is not true in the case of ______.
    (A) Boron
    (B) carbon
    (C) Helium   <-- CORRECT
    (D) nitrogen
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As only one I^st period element of p-block, it has unique 1s^2 configuration besides another element of that block (ns^2np^1 - 6). It is a noble gas.

Q13. Cohen Orthoboric acid (H_3BO_3) is strongly heated, the residue is
    (A) Al_4O_2,
    (B) Boron
    (C) Al_2O_3, 2H_2O
    (D) Meta boric acid   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Meta boric acid

Q14. Me_3SiCl is used during polymerization of organosilicones because:
    (A) Me_3 SiCl does not block the end terminal of the silicone polymer.
    (B) Me_3 SiCl acts as a catalyst during polymerisation.
    (C) Me_3 SiCl improves the quality and yield of the polymer.
    (D) to control the chain length of the polymer.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The chain length of the polymers can be controlled by adding Me_3SiCl which blocks the ends of the chain to produce silicone.

Q15. Which of the following statements are correct?
 Fullerenes are cage-like molecules.
 Fullerenes have dangling bonds.
 Graphite is thermodynamically not stable allotrope of carbon.
 Graphite is slippery and hard and therefore used as a dry lubricant in Machines.
    (A) A   <-- CORRECT
    (B) C
    (C) D
    (D) B
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Fullerene has a cage-like spheroidal molecular (C_60) structure and has no dangling bonds.

Q1. Which one of the following orders correctly represents the increasing acid strengths of the given acids?
    (A) HOCl < HOClO < HOClO_2 < HOClO_3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) HOClO < HOCl < HOClO_3 < HOClO_2
    (C) HOClO_2 < HOClO_3 < HOClO < HOCl
    (D) HOClO_3 < HOClO_2 < HOClO < HOCl
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Acidity increases as the number of a terminal oxygen atom attached to the halogen (Cl) atom because of the inductive-effect.

Q2. Regular use of which of the following fertilizers increases the acidity of the soil?
    (A) Superphosphate of lime
    (B) Ammonium sulphate   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Urea
    (D) Potassium nitrate
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Ammonium sulphate addition increases acidity in the soil.
In the presence of water and oxygen in the soil, ammonium and sulfate are decomposed by naturally occurring microbes. During this process, acids are released into the soil, along with nitrogen and sulfur compounds.

Q3. The percentage of p-character in the orbitals forming P - P bonds in P_4 is______.
    (A) 50
    (B) 75   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 25
    (D) 33
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The species P_4 has a tetrahedron structure. Each P involves sp^3 hybrid orbital. Hence p-character will be 75.

Q4. When Cl_2 gas reacts with hot and concentrated sodium hydroxide solution, the oxidation number of chlorine changes from:
    (A) Zero to – 1 and zero to +5   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Zero to – 1 and zero to +3
    (C) Zero to + 1 and zero to –5
    (D) Zero to + 1 and zero to –3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Reaction of Cl_2 and hot and concentrated sodium hydroxide solution is as below:
6 NaOH + 3Cl_2 → 5NaCl + NaClO_3 + 3H_2O
Here Cl_2 disproportionate to -1 and +5

Q5. In which of the following compounds, nitrogen exhibits highest oxidation state?
    (A) N_3H   <-- CORRECT
    (B) NH_2OH
    (C) N_2H_4
    (D) NH_3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: N_3H is Hydrazoic acid and can be seen as N_3^- H+.

Q6. Three reactions involving ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{P}}$$O_4^ - $ are given below
 ${{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{P}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}} + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} \to {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{{\text{O}}^ + } + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{P}}o_4^ - $
 ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{P}}o_4^ - + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} \to {\text{ HP}}O_2^ + + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{{\text{O}}^ + }$
 ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{P}}O_4^ - + O{H^ - }?H3PO4 + O_2^ - $
In which of the above does ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}$P$O_4^ - $ act as an acid?
    (A) C. only
    (B) A. and B.
    (C) B. only   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A. only
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In B only $H_2P O_4^ - $ is losing its proton therefore act as acid.

Q7. The correct order of increasing bond angles in the following species is:
    (A) ${\text{Cl}}O_2^ - < {\text{ C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} < {\text{ Cl}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${\text{C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} < {\text{ Cl}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}} < {\text{ Cl}}O_2^ - $
    (C) ${\text{Cl}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}} < {\text{ C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} < {\text{ Cl}}O_2^ - $
    (D) ${\text{C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} < {\text{ Cl}}O_2^ - < {\text{ Cl}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The correct order of increasing bond angles in the following species is ${\text{Cl}}O_2^ - < {\text{ C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O }} < {\text{ Cl}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$
lp-lp repulsion and lp-bp repulsion is responsible behind it.

Q8. The tendency of BF_3, BCl_3, and BBr_3 to behave as Lewis acid decreases in the sequence:
    (A) BBr_3 > BCl_3 > BF_3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) BF_3 > BCl_3 > BBr_3
    (C) BCl_3 > BF_3 > BBr_3
    (D) BBr_3 > BF_3 > BCl_3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The strength of Lewis acid is in the order of BBr_3 > BCl_3 > BF_3. as the size of halogen, acid increases the acidic strength of boron halide increases thous BF_3 is the weakest acid This is because of the tendency of the halogen atom to form back bonding by its lone pairs of electrons to the vacant p-orbitals of boron. In BF_3 this back bonding is formed by the overlap of 2p-2p orbital (same energy). Thus the tendency to accept lone pair (Lewis acid property) decreases. But in the case of BBr_3 and BI_3 the back bond is formed by p orbitals of different energy, thus less effective.

Q9. P_4O_10 is the anhydride of:
    (A) H_3PO_2
    (B) H_3PO_4   <-- CORRECT
    (C) H_4P_2O_7
    (D) H_3PO_3
    Answer: B
    Explanation: P_4O_10 is the anhydride of H_3PO_4
P_4O_10 + 6 H_2O $\longrightarrow$ 4 H_3PO_4

Q10. Which of the following statements regarding ozone is not correct?
 The oxygen-oxygen bond length in ozone is identical with that of molecular oxygen
 The ozone is response hybrid of two structures
 The ozone molecule is angular in shape
 Ozone is used as a germicide and disinfectant for the purification of air.
    (A) B
    (B) A   <-- CORRECT
    (C) C
    (D) D
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Bond order of O-O bond in ozone is less than that in oxygen.
Ozone molecule can be represented as a resonance hybrid of two canonical structures, each structure has one single bond on one side and a double bond on the another side.

Q11. Which of the following contains P- O - P bond?
    (A) Orthophosphoric acid
    (B) Pyrophosphoric acid   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Phosphorous acid
    (D) Hypophosphorous acid
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Pyrophoshoric acid (also known as diphosphoric acid) contains P-O-P bond. The molecular formula of pyrophosphoric acid is H_4P_2O_7.

Q12. Which noble gas is most abundant in the atmosphere?
    (A) Ne
    (B) He
    (C) Kr
    (D) Ar   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There's so much Ar in the atmosphere because most of it was produced by a long-lived radioactive isotope of potassium in the earth's crust and released over geologic time.

Q13. The reaction of P_4 with X leads selectively to P_4O_6. The X is:
    (A) Moist O_2
    (B) A mixture of O_2 and N_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Dry O_2
    (D) O_2 in the presence of aqueous NaOH
    Answer: B
    Explanation: P_4 + 3O_2 $\longrightarrow$P_4O_6( in presence of N_2 ). N_2 is used to retard further oxidation).

Q14. Which of the following reactions of xenon compounds is not feasible?
    (A) XeF_6 + RbF $\longrightarrow$ Rb [ XeF_7]
    (B) 3XeF_4 + 6H_2O $\longrightarrow$ 2Xe + XeO_3 + 12HF + 1.5O_2
    (C) 2XeF_2 + 2H_2O $\longrightarrow$ 2Xe + 4HF + O_2
    (D) XeO_3 + 6HF $\longrightarrow$ XeF_6 + 3H_2O   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: 1st reaction is not feasible. Rather the opposite reaction happens XeF_6 + 3 H_2O $\longrightarrow$ XeO_3 + 6 HF.

Q15. In which of the following arrangements, the sequence is not strictly according to the property written against it?
    (A) B < C < O < N: Increasing first ionization enthalpy
    (B) HF < HCl < HBr < HI :Increasing acid strength
    (C) NH_3 < PH_3< AsH_3 < SbH_3: Increasing basic strength   <-- CORRECT
    (D) CO_2 < SiO_2 < SnO_2 < PbO_2: Increasing oxidizing power
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As we move down the group basicity decreases. As we go down the group size of atom increase, the availability of lone pairs decreases. Because it occupies a larger volume. Thus the basic character of hydrides decreases as follows: NH_3>PH_3>AsH_3>SbH_3.

Q1. Among the following which is the strongest oxidizing agent?
    (A) F_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) I_2
    (C) Br_2
    (D) Cl_2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: F_2 is the most electronegative element hence it readily get reduced to F^- ion so it is a very strong oxidizing agent.

Q2. The brown ring test for nitrates depends on:
    (A) reduction of nitrate to nitric oxide.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) oxidation of nitric oxide to nitrogen dioxide.
    (C) oxidising action of sulphuric acid.
    (D) the reduction of ferrous sulphate to iron.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In the ring test of nitrates, nitrate ion is reduced to nitric oxide. The reaction is as below:
$2HN{O_3} + 3{H_2}S{O_4} + 6FeS{O_4} \to 3F{e_2}{(S{O_4})_3} + 2NO + 4{H_2}O$
$[Fe{({H_2}O)_6}]S{O_4} + NO \to [Fe{({H_2}O)_5}(NO)]S{O_4} + {H_2}O$

Q3. One mole of magnesium nitride on the reaction with an excess of water gives:
    (A) Two moles of ammonia   <-- CORRECT
    (B) One mole of nitric acid
    (C) Two moles of nitric acid
    (D) One mole of ammonia
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mg_3N_2 + 6H_2O = 3Mg(OH)_2 + 2NH_3

Q4. Which of the following statements is not valid for oxoacids of phosphorus?
    (A) Hypophosphorous acid is a diprotic acid.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) All oxoacids contain tetrahedral four coordinated phosphorus.
    (C) All oxoacids contain at least one P = O unit and one P – OH group.
    (D) Orthophosphoric acid is used in the manufacture of triple superphosphate.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Hypophosphorous acid is a phosphorus oxoacid and a powerful reducing agent with molecular formula H_3PO_2. Inorganic chemists refer to the free acid by this name (also as "HPA"), or the acceptable name of phosphinic acid. It is a colorless, Monoprotic low-melting compound, which is soluble in water, dioxane, and alcohol.

Q5. Sulphur trioxide can be obtained by which of the following reaction:
    (A) S + H_2SO_4$\rightarrow{\Delta }$
    (B) H_2SO_4 + PC_3$\rightarrow{\Delta }$
    (C) CaSO_4 + C$\rightarrow{\Delta }$
    (D) FeSO_4$\rightarrow{\Delta }$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Thermal decomposition of FeSO_4 produces the following products $2FeSO_4 \to Fe_2O_3 + SO_2 + SO_3$.

Q6. Argon is used:
    (A) To obtain low temperature
    (B) In radio therapy for treatment of cancer
    (C) In high temperature welding   <-- CORRECT
    (D) In filling airships
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ar is used in high temperature welding to provide an inert atmosphere.

Q7. The function of Fe(OH)_3 in the contact process is:
    (A) To remove arsenic impurity   <-- CORRECT
    (B) To remove dust particles
    (C) To remove moisture
    (D) To detect colloidal impurity
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Fe(OH)_3 is used to remove arsenic impurities.

Q8. Of the following compounds the most acidic is:
    (A) P_2O_5   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Bi_2O_3
    (C) As_2O_3
    (D) Sb_2O_3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: More is the oxidation number greater is the acidity of the oxide. Here P is in +5 oxidation state.

Q9. Atoms in a P_4 molecule of white phosphorus are arranged regularly in the following way:
    (A) At the corners of a tetrahedron   <-- CORRECT
    (B) At the corners of the cube
    (C) At the corners of the octahedron
    (D) At the centre and corners of a tetrahedron
    Answer: A
    Explanation: in P_4 four P atoms are arranged at the corners of tetrahedron (tetrahedral structure).

Q10. Aqueous solution of Na_2S_2O_3 on reaction with Cl_2 gives______.
    (A) Na_2S_4O_6
    (B) NaOH
    (C) NaHSO_4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) NaCl
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Aqueous Na_2S_2O_3 on reaction with Cl_2 produces NaHSO_4.
Reaction is given below:
$Na_2S_2O_3 + 4Cl_2 + 5H_2O \to 2NaHSO_4 + 8HCl$

Q11. The angular shape of ozone molecules $\left( {{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)$ consists of
    (A) 1 sigma and 2 pi bonds
    (B) 2 sigma and 2 pi bonds
    (C) 3 sigma and 2 pi bonds
    (D) 2 sigma and 1 pi bonds   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: since both bonds are identical, identical in length and strength. This is due to sp^2 hybridization and delocalized pi bonding. Each oxygen has an unhybridized p-orbital, and all three overlap side to side, producing a sigma bond and a pi bond between the central oxygen atom and each of the terminal oxygen atoms. In this case, there are two sigma bonds and two pi bonds. 
Therefore, it will contain two sigma bonds and one pi bond.

Q12. Which one of the following arrangement does not give the correct picture of the trends indicated against it?
    (A) Cl_2 > Br_2 > F_2 > I_2 Bond dissociation energy   <-- CORRECT
    (B) F_2 > Cl_2 > Br_2 > I_2: Electronegativity
    (C) F_2 > Cl_2 > Br_2 > I_2: Electron gain enthalpy
    (D) F_2 > Cl_2 > Br_2 > I_2: Oxidizing power
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Correct order of Electron gain enthalpy of halogens is Cl_2 > F_2 > Br_2 > I_2. This is because of the very small size of fluorine.

Q13. Four species are listed below:
 $HCO_3^ - $
 ${{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{{\text{O}}^ + }$
 $HSO_4^ - $
 ${\text{HS}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{F}}$
Which one of the following is the correct sequence of their acidic strength?
    (A) i < iii < ii < iv   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ii < iii < I < iv
    (C) iv < ii < iii < i
    (D) iii < I < iv < ii
    Answer: A
    Explanation: i < iii < ii < iv is the order of acidic strength.
as IV is stabilised by -I effect of fluorine.

Q14. Helium is used in balloons in place of hydrogen because it is:
    (A) more abundant than hydrogen
    (B) radioactive
    (C) incombustible   <-- CORRECT
    (D) lighter than hydrogen
    Answer: C
    Explanation: He is used in balloons in place of hydrogenas because He is incombustible, but hydrogen is highly combustible gas.

Q15. Which is most easily liquefiable rare gas?
    (A) Ne
    (B) Kr
    (C) Ar
    (D) Xe   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Xe is most easily liquefiable rare gas. Xenon has a high critical temperature. Thus it is easily liquefiable.

Q1. Hybridisation in methane (CH_4) ethene (C_2H_4) ethyne (C_2H_2) involves s and p orbitals. Choose the correct hybrid orbitals in the options given below for CH_4,_ C_2H_4 and C_2H_2 respectively:
    (A) sp^2, sp, sp^3
    (B) sp^3, sp, sp^2
    (C) sp, sp^3, sp^2
    (D) sp^3, sp^2, sp   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In methane C is sp^3 hybridised because of 3 sigma bond formation. While in ethane both the C are sp^2 hybridised, and in ethyne both the C are sp hybridised.

Q2. Change in hybridisation affects the carbon’s and the organic compound’s:
    (A) bond length
    (B) bond enthalpy
    (C) electronegativity   <-- CORRECT
    (D) bond strength
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In hybridization as % of 's' character increases electronegativity also increases.
More the s character more will be the electronegativity of that atom.
Increasing order of electronegativity with %s character is sp (50%) > sp^2(33.33%) > sp^3(25%).

Q3. Condense the following complete structural formula given below. Choose the appropriate answer given below
    (A) (CH_2)_3CH (CH_3) CH(CH_3)_2
    (B) CH_3CH_2CH = CH_2CH_2CH_3
    (C) CH_3CH = CH(CH_2)_3CH_3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) CH_2C(CH_3)_3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: All the single bonds are broken and atoms are written together.

Q4. 2-bromo butane can be represented in various ways. Choose the incorrect one from the following
    (A)    <-- CORRECT
    (B) CH_2CHBrCH_2CH_2
    (C) 
    (D) 
    Answer: A
    Explanation: methyl group is represented at 3rd carbon no bromine is there on 2nd carbon

Q5. Which of the following is the correct IUPAC name?
    (A) 4, 4-Bis(methyl)-3-ethylheptane
    (B) 5-Ethyl-4, 4-dimethylheptane
    (C) 4, 4-Dimethyl-3-ethylheptane
    (D) 3-Ethyl-4,4-dimethylheptane   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: While writing IUPAC name, alkyl groups are written in alphabetical order. thus lower locant 3 is assigned to ethyl. prefix di, tri or tetra are not included in alphabetical order

Q6. Write the state of hybridisation of carbon in H_2C = O and mention the molecular geometry also.
    (A) sp hybridised carbon, linear
    (B) sp^2 hybridised carbon, trigonal planar   <-- CORRECT
    (C) sp^3 hybridised carbon, tetrahedral
    (D) sp^3 hybridised carbon, trigonal pyramidal
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Due to the presence of a double bond in the carbonyl carbon ( $>\mathrm C=\mathrm O$), carbon is sp^2 hybridised. This hybridization leads to a trigonal planar geometry which means a bond angle of 120° around the C.

Q7. The IUPAC name for
    (A) 1-Chloro-4-methyl-2-nitrobenzene   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2-Chloro-1-nitro-5-methylbenzene
    (C) 1-Chloro-2-nitro-4-methylbenzene
    (D) m-Nitro-p-chlorotoluene
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The given compound contains chloro group at position 1, nitro at position 2 and methyl at position 3. So 1-Chloro-4-methyl-2-nitrobenzene is the IUPAC name of the given compound with groups named in alphabetical order.

Q8. In $\pi$ (pi) bond formation, one of the below criteria is necessary. Choose the appropriate one.
    (A) planar orientation of the two p orbitals on adjacent atoms.
    (B) pentagonal orientation of the two p orbitals on adjacent atoms.
    (C) trigonal orientation of the two p orbitals on adjacent atoms.
    (D) parallel orientation of the two p orbitals on adjacent atoms.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Parallel orientation of p orbitals on adjacent atoms is necessary for side-ways overlapping and formation of $\pi$ bond.

Q9. In general, in the molecules containing multiple bonds, ________ provide the most reactive centres. Choose the most appropriate one.
    (A) hyperconjugation
    (B) p orbitals
    (C) $\pi$ bonds   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\sigma$ bond
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\pi$ bond formed by sideways overlapping of p orbitals/d orbitals on adjacent atoms provides the most reactive centers.

Q10. Which of the following compounds contain all the carbon atoms in the same hybridisation state?
 $H - C \equiv C - C \equiv C - H$
 $C{H_3} - C \equiv C - C{H_3}$
 CH_2 = C = CH_2
 $C{H_2} = CH - C \equiv CH$
    (A) C
    (B) A   <-- CORRECT
    (C) B
    (D) D
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In option A, all the 4 carbon atoms are sp-hybridized.

Q11. Delocalisation of σ-electrons of C - H bond of an alkyl group directly attached to an atom of unsaturated system or to an atom with an unshared p-orbital is called
    (A) Elimination reactions
    (B) Substitution reactions
    (C) Hyperconjugation   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Rearrangement reactions
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The interaction of the electrons in a sigma bond (usually C–H or C–C) with an adjacent empty (or partially filled) non-bonding p-orbital, antibonding $\sigma$ or $\pi$ orbital or filled $\pi$ orbital, to give an extended molecular orbital that increases the stability of the system is Hyperconjugation.

Q12. Hyperconjugation in an organic compound is a
    (A) temporary effect
    (B) delocalisation of σ electrons of C -C bond of an alkyl group
    (C) destabilizing interaction
    (D) stabilizing interaction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Hyperconjugation is the stabilizing interaction that results from the interaction of the electrons in a C-H $\sigma$-bond with an adjacent empty p orbital or a $\pi$ orbital to give an extended molecular orbital that increases the stability of the system. It is a permanent effect.

Q13. Covalent bonds are formed with other carbon atoms due to:
    (A) coordination
    (B) catenation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) substitution
    (D) ionisation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Catenation is the linkage of atoms of the same element into longer chains. Catenation occurs most readily in carbon, which forms covalent bonds with other carbon atoms to form longer chains and structures. This is the reason for the presence of the vast number of organic compounds in nature.

Q14. Which of the following organic compound Wohler synthesised from an inorganic compound, ammonium cyanate in the presence of heat?
    (A) HOCH(CN_2)
    (B) ammonium hydroxide
    (C) Urea   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ammonia
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The reaction can be given as starting with solutions of potassium cyanate and ammonium chloride which are mixed, heated and cooled again to get ammonium cyanate salt which on decomposition gives the urea.

Q15. Straight or branched chain compounds, for example, the below ones are called
${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}\,\mathop {\mathop {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{ - CH - C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}}\limits^{\text{|}} }\limits^{{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \,\,{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{ - }}\mathop {\mathop {\text{C}}\limits^{{\text{||}}} }\limits^{\text{O}} {\text{ - H}}$
    (A) aliphatic cyclic compounds
    (B) closed chain compounds
    (C) alicyclic compounds
    (D) aliphatic compounds   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The straight and branched chain compounds are known as aliphatic compounds (also called acyclic or open chain compounds).

Q1. Correct IUPAC name for ${{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}\,{\text{ - }}\,\mathop {\mathop {{\text{CH}}}\limits_{\text{|}} }\limits_{{{\text{C}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{5}}}} \,{\text{ - }}\,\mathop {\mathop {{\text{CH}}}\limits_{\text{|}} }\limits_{{{\text{C}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{5}}}} \,{\text{ - }}\,{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$ is ________.
    (A) 2 - ethyl-3-methylpentane
    (B) 3, 4 - Dimethylhexane   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2, 3-diethylbutane
    (D) 2 - sec-butylbutane
    Answer: B
    Explanation: 3, 4 - Dimethylhexane will be correct IUPAC name as 6 membered carbon chain will be the parent chain with methyl groups at positions 3 and 4.

Q2. Benzene and other related unsaturated ring compounds (benzenoid) such as given below are called:
    (A) Aromatic compounds   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Alicyclic compounds
    (C) Cyclic compounds
    (D) Aliphatic compounds
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Aromatic compounds follow Huckels (4n+2)$\pi$ electrons rule. They can be benzenoid or non-benzenoid. They may also be heterocyclic.

Q3. The following compound is:
    (A) Oxy cyclohextane
    (B) Tropone   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Heterocyclic compound
    (D) Aliphatic compounds
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Tropone or 2, 4, 6-cycloheptatriene-1-one is a non-benzenoid aromatic compound. The compound consists of a ring of seven carbon atoms with three conjugated alkene groups and a ketone group.

Q4. Compounds containing carbon atoms joined together in the form of a ring as following are:
    (A) Alicyclic compounds   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Heterocyclic compounds
    (C) Aliphatic compounds
    (D) Aromatic compounds
    Answer: A
    Explanation: An alicyclic compound is an organic compound that is both aliphatic and cyclic. They contain one or more all-carbon rings which may be either saturated or unsaturated, but do not have aromatic character.

Q5. The molecular formula C_3H_8O represents two alcohols: propan-1-ol and propan-2-ol. This property is called as:
    (A) Position isomerism   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Chain isomerism
    (C) Functional group isomerism
    (D) Metamerism
    Answer: A
    Explanation: propan-1-ol and propan-2-ol are positional isomers as they differ only in the position of functional group -OH. Positional isomers are isomers that have the same carbon skeleton and the same functional groups but differ from each other in the location of the functional groups on or in the carbon chain.

Q6. Propanal and propanone are
    (A) Functional group isomers   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Steroisomers
    (C) Position isomers
    (D) Chain isomers
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Two or more compounds having the same molecular formula but different functional groups are called functional isomers and this phenomenon is termed as functional group isomerism. For example, the molecular formula C_3H_6O represents both a ketone and aldehyde:$CH_3COCH_3\; and\;CH_3CH_2CHO$

Q7. What is the type of hybridisation of each carbon in the compound (CH_3)_2CO?
    (A) sp^2​​​​, sp^​​​​​2
    (B) sp^3, sp^3
    (C) sp^3, sp^2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) sp^3, sp
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The hybridisation of the C in CH_3 (all are single bonds) is sp^3 and that of C of $>\mathrm C=\mathrm O$ (double bond) bond is sp^2.

Q8. Alkyl radical (Methyl, Ethyl, Isopropyl, Tert-butyl free radical) stability in the increasing order is:
    (A) $\dot CH {\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}} < \dot C{\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}} < \dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} < \dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$
    (B) $\dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} < \dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}} C{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}< \dot CH{\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}} < \dot C{\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{3}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\dot C{\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}} < \dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} < \dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} <\dot CH {\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}}$
    (D) $\dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} < \dot CH {\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}} < \dot C{\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} \right)_{\text{2}}} < \dot C{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Tertiary radical is more stable than secondary, primary and methyl. Alkyl groups directly attached to the carbon with unpaired electron stabilise the carbocations due to inductive and hyperconjugation effects.

Q9. The nitrogen containing organic compound, when heated with copper oxide in an atmosphere of carbon dioxide, yields:
    (A) ammonium sulphate
    (B) only carbon dioxide and water.
    (C) free nitrogen in addition to carbondioxide and water.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ammonia
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the Dumas method for estimation of nitrogen in an organic compound, the nitrogen-containing organic compound, when heated with copper oxide in an atmosphere of carbon dioxide, yields free nitrogen in addition to carbon dioxide and water.
$C_xH_yN_z\;+\;\left(x+\frac y2\right)CuO\rightarrow xCO_2\;+\frac y2\;H_2O\;+\frac z2N_2\;+\left(2x+\frac y2\right)Cu$

Q10. A known mass of an organic compound is heated with fuming nitric acid in the presence of silver nitrate. This is
    (A) Feulgen method
    (B) Kjeldahl method
    (C) Carius method   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Dumas method
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The Carius method in analytical chemistry is a method for the quantitative determination of halogens in organic substances. It involves heating a known mass of an organic compound with fuming nitric acid in the presence of silver nitrate contained in a hard glass tube known as carius tube, in a furnace. The halogen present forms the corresponding silver halide (AgX). It is filtered, washed, dried, and weighed.

Q11. Carius tube is used in the estimations of which one of the following?
    (A) sulphur and oxygen
    (B) sulphur and nitrogen
    (C) halogen and sulphur   <-- CORRECT
    (D) halogen and nitrogen
    Answer: C
    Explanation: It is used in the estimation of Halogen and Sulphur. For estimation of sulphur a known mass of an organic compound is heated in a hard glass tube called a Carius tube with sodium peroxide or fuming nitric acid. For estimation of halogen, a known mass of an organic compound is heated with fuming nitric acid in the presence of silver nitrate contained in a Carius tube, in a furnace.

Q12. In the naming of organic compounds containing polyfunctional compounds, one of the functional groups is chosen as the principal functional group and the compound is then named on that basis. The order of decreasing priority for some functional groups is:
    (A) - CN, - HC = O, > C = O, - OH, - NH_2, > C = C <, - C $\equiv$ C -, -CONH_2
    (B) - C = O, - OH, - NH_2, > C = C <, - C $\equiv$ C -, -CONH_2, - CN > - HC = O
    (C) -CONH_2,-CN, -HC = O, > C = O, -OH, -NH_2,> C = C <, -C$\equiv$C-   <-- CORRECT
    (D) - HC = O, > C = O, -OH, -NH_2, > C = C <, - C $\equiv $C -, -CONH_2, - CN
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The order of decreasing priority for some functional groups is:
-CONH_2, -CN, -HC = O, > C = O, -OH, -NH_2, > C = C <, -C$\equiv$C-
Carboxlic acid > sulphonic acid > acid anhydride > ester > acyl halide > acyl amide > nitrile > aldehyde > ketones > alcohol > amine > alkene > alkyne.

Q13. If an –NH_2 functional group is present in an organic compound it is called amine. If a -CONH_2 functional group is present in an organic compound then it is called:
    (A) ether
    (B) amide   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ester
    (D) nitrile
    Answer: B
    Explanation: -CONH_2 is amide functional group. Amides are formed by conversion of a carboxylic acid into ammonium salt and then heating it.

Q14. A covalent bond when cleaved heterolytically yields:
    (A) carbonium ion
    (B) both carbonium ion and carbanion   <-- CORRECT
    (C) free radicals
    (D) carbanion
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Heterolytic cleavage produces carbonium ion and carbanion. In heterolytic cleavage, the bond breaks in such a fashion that the shared pair of electrons remains with one of the fragments. After heterolysis, one atom has a sextet electronic structure and a positive charge and the other, a valence octet with at least one lone pair and a negative charge. A species having a carbon atom possessing electrons and a positive charge is called a carbocation (earlier called carbonium ion). There is also a carbon species carrying a negative charge on a carbon atom which gets the unshared pair of electrons which is called carbanion.

Q15. Electronegativity of carbon atoms depends upon their state of hybridisation. In which of the following compounds, the carbon marked with asterisk is most electronegative?
    (A) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}-{\text{ C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}-{\text{ CH }} = {\text{ }}*{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}$
    (B) $\text{C}{\text{H}}_\text3-\text{ }\ast\text{CH }=\text{ CH }-\text{ C}{\text{H}}_\text3$
    (C) $\text{C}{\text{H}}_\text3-\text{ C}{\text{H}}_\text2-\text{ }\ast\text{C}{\text{H}}_\text2-\text{ C}{\text{H}}_\text3$
    (D) $\text{C}{\text{H}}_\text3-\text{ C}{\text{H}}_\text2-\text{ C }\equiv\text{ }\ast\text{CH}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Greater is the s character of the hybridised orbital, greater is the electronegativity of the atom. In a triply bonded C, there is sp hybridisation. In sp hybridization, the atom has maximum s character (50%). So in this case the carbon with a triple bond has maximum electronegativity.
