Q1. In which of the following, functional group isomerism is not possible?
    (A) Alkyl halides   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Alcohols
    (C) Cyanides
    (D) Aldehydes
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Two or more compounds having the same molecular formula but different functional groups are called functional isomers and this phenomenon is termed as functional group isomerism. Alkyl halides do not show functional isomerism.

Q2. The fragrance of flowers is due to the presence of some steam volatile organic compounds called essential oils. These are generally insoluble in water at room temperature but are miscible with water vapour in vapour phase. A suitable method for the extraction of these oils from the flowers is:
    (A) Distillation under reduced pressure
    (B) Crystallisation
    (C) Distillation
    (D) Steam distillation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Steam distillation is a technique applied to separate substances which are steam volatile and are immiscible with water. Essential oils are insoluble in water and soluble in steam and have high vapour pressure. Therefore, they can be separated by steam distillation.

Q3. During hearing of a court case, the judge suspected that some changes in the documents had been carried out. He asked the forensic department to check the ink used at two different places. According to you which technique can give the best results?
    (A) Distillation
    (B) Solvent extraction
    (C) Column chromatography
    (D) Thin layer chromatography   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Thin layer chromatography (TLC) is an adsorption chromatography, which involves separation of substances of a mixture over a thin layer of an adsorbent coated on glass plate. It is used to separate the pigments of the ink and will give the best results.

Q4. The principle involved in paper chromatography is
    (A) Volatility
    (B) Solubility
    (C) Adsorption
    (D) Partition   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Paper chromatography is a type of partition chromatography. In paper chromatography, a special quality paper known as chromatography paper is used. Chromatography paper contains water trapped in it, which acts as the stationary phase. Separation of components of a mixture depends upon their partitioning between water held in stationary phase (adsorbant paper) and the liquid present in the mobile phase.

Q5. In which of the following compounds the carbon marked with asterisk is expected to have greatest partial positive charge?
    (A) *CH_3 - CH_2 - CH_3
    (B) *CH_3 - CH_2 - Cl   <-- CORRECT
    (C) *CH_3 - CH_2 - I
    (D) *CH_3 - CH_2 - Br
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cl is most electronegative amongst Cl, Br and I and has more -I (inductive electron withdrawing) effect. So it causes the asterisk marked to have the maximum partial positive charge.

Q6. C_4H_10O represents methoxypropane CH_3OC_3H_7 and ethoxyethane (C_2H_5OC_2H_5):
    (A) Functional group isomerism
    (B) Metamerism   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Position isomerism
    (D) Stereoisomerism
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Metamerism arises due to different alkyl chains on either side of the functional group in the molecule. For example, C_4H_10O represents methoxypropane (CH_3OC_3H_7) and ethoxyethane (C_2H_5OC_2H_5).

Q7. The organic compound given below is one of the four options given below. Choose the most appropriate one.
    (A) benzenoid compound
    (B) aromatic heteroyclic compound
    (C) alicyclic compound
    (D) aliphatic heterocyclic compound   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The aliphatic heterocyclic compounds are the cyclic analogues of amines, ethers, thioethers and their properties are influenced by the ring strain.

Q8. The order of decreasing priority for some functional groups in the naming of an organic compound is:
    (A) - CONH_2, - CN, - HC = O, > C = O, - OH, - NH_2, - COOR (R = alkyl group), - COCl
    (B) - COOR (R = alkyl group right), - COCl, - CONH_2 , - CN, - HC = O, > C = O, - OH, - H_2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) - CN, - HC = O, > C = O, - OH, - NH_2, - COOR (R = alkyl group), - COCl, - CONH_2
    (D) - COCl, - CONH_2, - CN, - HC = O, > C = O, - OH, - NH_2, - COOR (R = alkyl group)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: COOR (R=alkyl group) > -COCl,> -CONH_2 > -CN > -HC=O> >C=O> -OH, -NH_2 is the decreasing order of priority
ester > acyl halide > acyl amide > nitrile > aldehyde > ketones > alcohol > amine

Q9. Select the nucleophile(s) among the following molecules/ions
HS^-, BF_3, C_2H_5O^-, (CH_3)_3N:, Cl^+, CH_3C^+ = O, H_2N^-:, NO_2^​​​​+
    (A) HS^-, H_2N^-:, (CH_3)_3N:, C_2H_5O^-   <-- CORRECT
    (B) CH_3C^+ =O, NO_​​​​​2^​+
    (C) BF_​​​​​3​​​​, Cl^+
    (D) Cl^+, CH_3C^+ = O
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Nucleophiles are nucleus loving species. These can be negatively charged or netural having lone pair of electrons. So among the given options nucleophiles are HS^-, H_2N^-:, (CH_​​​​​3)_3N:, C_2H_5O^-

Q10. Select the electrophile(s) among the following molecules/ions
${\text{H}}{{\text{S}}^{\text{ - }}}{\text{,}}\,{\text{B}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{,}}\,{{\text{C}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{5}}}{{\text{O}}^{\text{ - }}}{\text{,}}\,{{\text{(C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{)}}_{\text{3}}}\,{\text{N:,}}\,{\text{C}}\mathop {\text{l}}\limits^{\text{ + }} {\text{,}}\,{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\mathop {\text{ - }}\limits_{\text{3}} }}\mathop {\text{C}}\limits^{\text{ + }} \,{\text{ = }}\,{\text{O,}}\,{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{N}}\mathop {\text{:}}\limits^{\text{ - }} {\text{,}}\,\,\mathop {\text{N}}\limits^{\text{ + }} \,{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$
    (A) H_2N^-, HS^-
    (B) BF_3, Cl^+, NO_2^+, CH_3-C^+=O   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (CH_3)_3N:, HS^-
    (D) C_2H_5O^-, (CH_3)_3N:
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Electrophiles are electron loving species. These can be electron deficient neutral molecules or positively charged ions. Thus BF_3, Cl^+, NO_2^+, CH_3-C^+=O are electrophiles.

Q11. Inorganic compounds, when homolytic cleavage takes place, one of the electrons of the shared pair in a covalent bond goes with each of the bonded atoms. This results in the formation of:
    (A) free radicals   <-- CORRECT
    (B) carbanions
    (C) carbonium ion
    (D) a sextet electronic structure
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In homolytic cleavage or homolysis, the two electrons in a cleaved covalent bond are divided equally between the products. Thus, in homolytic cleavage, the movement of a single electron takes place instead of an electron pair. This process is also known as homolytic fission. Such cleavage results in the formation of neutral species (atom or group) which contains an unpaired electron. These species are called free radicals.

Q12. The following compounds are called:
    (A) aliphatic heteroyclic compounds
    (B) Alicyclic compounds
    (C) benzenoid compounds
    (D) aromatic hetrocyclic compounds.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Aromatic compounds may also have heteroatom in the ring. Such compounds are called heterocyclic aromatic compounds. Thus the given compounds are aromatic heterocyclic compounds namely furan, thiophene and pyridine respectively.

Q13. In which bond of CH_3CH_2CH_2Br the inductive effect is expected to be the least?
    (A) bond between carbon-1 and hydrogen
    (B) bond between carbon-3 and carbon-2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) bond between carbon-2 and carbon-1
    (D) bond between carbon-1 and Br
    Answer: B
    Explanation: As the distance of the functional group increases its inductive effect decreases. Carbon-3 is farthest from Br. So in the bond between carbon-2 and carbon-3 the inductive effect is the least.

Q14. To separate mixtures into their components, and also to test the purity of compounds, the popularly used technique is:
    (A) steam distillation
    (B) chromatography   <-- CORRECT
    (C) differential extraction
    (D) fractional distillation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Chromatography is used for the purpose given. In this technique the mixture of substances is applied onto a stationary phase, which may be a solid or a liquid. A pure solvent, a mixture of solvents, or a gas is allowed to move slowly over the stationary phase. The components of the mixture get gradually separated from one another.

Q15. The elements present in an organic compound are converted from covalent form into the ionic form by fusing the compound with sodium metal. This test is called:
    (A) Iodoform test
    (B) Lassaigne’s test   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Fehling’s test
    (D) Feulgen test
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Nitrogen, sulphur, halogens, and phosphorus present in an organic compound are detected by “Lassaigne’s test”. The elements present in the compound are converted from the covalent form into the ionic form by fusing the compound with sodium metal. Cyanide, sulphide and halide of sodium so formed on sodium fusion are extracted from the fused mass by boiling it with distilled water. This extract is known as sodium fusion extract.

Q1. The principle of partition chromatography is:
    (A) separation of a mixture over a column of the adsorbent.
    (B) separation of ions and polar molecules based on their affinity to ion exchanger.
    (C) separation of substances of a mixture over a thin layer of an adsorbent.
    (D) continuous differential partitioning of components of a mixture.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Partition chromatography is based on the continuous differential partitioning of components of a mixture between stationary and mobile phases. Paper chromatography is a type of partition chromatography. In paper chromatography, a special quality paper known as chromatography paper is used. Chromatography paper contains water trapped in it, which acts as the stationary phase.

Q2. Aniline is separated from aniline-water mixture using following technique:
    (A) Chromatography
    (B) Steam distillation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Fractional distillation
    (D) Differential extraction
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Steam distillation is a special type of distillation (a separation process) for temperature-sensitive materials like natural aromatic compounds. It was a popular laboratory method for purification of organic compounds.

Q3. Sodium cyanide, sulphide, and halide, (-CN, -S, and -H, coming from the organic compound) formed on fusion with sodium are extracted from the fused mass by boiling it with distilled water. This is called:
    (A) Ion extract after sodium fusion
    (B) Double distillate
    (C) Sodium fusion ion extraction
    (D) Sodium fusion extract   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Nitrogen, sulphur, halogens, and phosphorus present in an organic compound are detected by “Lassaigne’s test”. The elements present in the compound are converted from the covalent form into the ionic form by fusing the compound with sodium metal. Cyanide, sulphide, and halide of sodium so formed on sodium fusion are extracted from the fused mass by boiling it with distilled water. This extract is known as sodium fusion extract.

Q4. Geometrical isomers and Optical isomers are:
    (A) stereoisomers   <-- CORRECT
    (B) functional isomers
    (C) chain isomers
    (D) position isomers
    Answer: A
    Explanation: They are stereoisomers as they differ in the orientation of atoms in space.

Q5. When an organic compound is present in an aqueous medium, it is separated by:
    (A) steam distillation
    (B) fractional distillation
    (C) chromatography
    (D) differential extraction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Differential extraction or solvent extraction is an experimental technique where an organic compound can be isolated from its aqueous solution by shaking it with an organic solvent. The organic compound will dissolve in the organic solvent, and with the use of a separating funnel, the organic solvent and water mixture is separated. The organic compound is obtained by evaporating the organic solvent.

Q6. Acid catalysed electrophilic addition reaction to carbon-carbon double bond proceeds in two steps. The first step involves the addition of an H^+ to double bond. Name the type of intermediate formed in the first step of the following addition reaction:
${{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}-{\text{HC }} = {\text{ C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}} + {\text{ }}{{\text{H}}^ + } \to ?$
    (A) 2° Carbocation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2° Carbanion
    (C) 1° Carbanion
    (D) 1° Carbocation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In this reaction, formation of secondary carbocation takes place by the addition of H^+ to terminal carbon of carbon-carbon double bond among the two possible carbon atoms. The more stable secondary carbocation formation will take place instead of primary carbocation.

Q7. Polarisation of $\sigma$-bond caused by the polarisation of adjacent $\sigma$-bond is termed as:
    (A) Resonance effect
    (B) Hyperconjugation
    (C) Metamerism
    (D) Inductive effect   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Polarisation of $\sigma$-bond caused by the polarisation of the adjacent $\sigma$-bond is referred to as the inductive effect. This effect is passed on to the subsequent bonds also but the effect decreases rapidly as the number of intervening bonds increases and becomes vanishingly small after three bonds. The inductive effect is related to the ability of substituent(s) to either withdraw or donate electron density to the attached carbon atom.

Q8. Covalent bond can undergo fission in two different ways. The correct representation involving a heterolytic fission of ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}-{\text{Br}}$ is:
    (A) C
    (B) A
    (C) D
    (D) B   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Arrows are shown in the direction of movement of electrons. Bromine (Br) being more electronegative attracts the shared paired of electrons and results in formation of Br^- ion and ^+CH_3​.

Q9. The addition of HCl to alkene proceeds in two steps. The first step is the attack of H+ ion to the portion which can be shown as:
All of these are possible
    (A) C
    (B) B   <-- CORRECT
    (C) D
    (D) A
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since arrows are shown in the direction of movement of electrons, so the correct depiction is B.

Q10. For testing halogens in an organic compound with ${\text{AgN}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}$solution, sodium extract (Lassaigne’s test) is acidified with dilute ${\text{HN}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{3}}}.$What will happen if a student acidifies the extract with dilute ${{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{S}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$in place of dilute HNO_3?
    (A) White ppt. of ${\text{A}}{{\text{g}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{S}}$ will be formed
    (B) White ppt. of ${\text{A}}{{\text{g}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{S}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$will be formed   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ${\text{S}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}$ will be formed
    (D) Green ppt. of ${\text{A}}{{\text{g}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{S}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$will be formed
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The sodium fusion extract is acidified with nitric acid and then treated with silver nitrate. A white precipitate, soluble in ammonium hydroxide shows the presence of chlorine, a yellowish precipitate, sparingly soluble in ammonium hydroxide shows the presence of bromine and a yellow precipitate, insoluble in ammonium hydroxide shows the presence of iodine. If instead of nitric acid, sulphuric acid is used then white precipitate of ${\text{A}}{{\text{g}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{S}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$ is formed.

Q11. Delocalisation of σ electrons of C - H bond of an alkyl group directly attached to an atom of unsaturated system or to an atom with an unshared p orbital is called:
    (A) Inductive effect
    (B) Electromeric effect
    (C) Resonance effect
    (D) Hyperconjugation   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Delocalisation of σ electrons of C - H bond of an alkyl group directly attached to an atom of unsaturated system or to an atom with an unshared p orbital is known as Hyperconjugation. It is a general stabilising interaction. The $\sigma$ electrons of C- H bond of the alkyl group enter into partial conjugation with the attached unsaturated system or with the unshared p orbital. It is a permanent effect.

Q12. In which of the following representations given below spatial arrangement of group/ atom different from that given in structure A?
    (A) A and D
    (B) A and C   <-- CORRECT
    (C) B and C
    (D) A and B
    Answer: B
    Explanation: By rotation of A around vertical axis B and around horizontal axis D can be obtained. But A and C be obtained only by breaking of bonds.

Q13. Why Kjeldahl method cannot be used for the estimation of nitrogen present in DNA and RNA? Choose the most appropriate option.
    (A) DNA and RNA have phosphorous which interferes in the Kjeldahl method
    (B) Nitrogen present in rings, azo groups and nitro groups of DNA and RNA cannot be removed   <-- CORRECT
    (C) DNA and RNA have deoxyribose and ribose which interferes in the Kjeldahl method
    (D) The bases present in the DNA and RNA structures do not allow them to participate in the Kjeldahl method
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Kjeldahl method is not applicable to compounds containing nitrogen in nitro and azo groups and nitrogen present in the ring (e.g. pyridine) as nitrogen of these compounds does not change to ammonium sulphate under these conditions. So it is not used to estimate Nitrogen in DNA and RNA.

Q14. Which one of the following compounds is used in the estimation of oxygen?
    (A) silver nitrate
    (B) iodine pentoxide   <-- CORRECT
    (C) copper oxide
    (D) sodium peroxide
    Answer: B
    Explanation: I_2O_5 is used. A definite mass of an organic compound is decomposed by heating in a stream of nitrogen gas. The mixture of gaseous products containing oxygen is passed over red-hot coke when all the oxygen is converted to carbon monoxide. This mixture is passed through warm iodine pentoxide when carbon monoxide is oxidised to carbon dioxide producing iodine.

Q1. Electrophiles are electron seeking species. Which of the following groups contain only electrophile
 ${\text{B}}{{\text{F}}_{\text{3}}},{\text{ N}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}},{\text{ }}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{O}}$
 $AlCl_3, SO_3,NO_2^ + $
 ${\text{NO}}_2^ + ,{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}^ + ,{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} - \mathop C\limits^ + = {\text{O}}$
 ${{\text{C}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{H}}_5^ + , CH_3^+, NH_2^-$
    (A) (i) and (iv)
    (B) (ii) and (iii)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (i) and (iii)
    (D) (i) and (ii)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Electrophile are electron loving species which can be positively charged ions or neutral molecules which are electron deficient. (ii) and (iii) contains all the electrophiles.

Q2. In the four compounds below, which of the following pairs are position isomers?
 $C{H_3} - C{H_2} - C{H_2} - C{H_2} - \mathop {\mathop C\limits^{||} }\limits^O - H$
 $C{H_3} - C{H_2} - C{H_2} - \mathop {\mathop C\limits^{||} }\limits^O - C{H_3}$
 $C{H_3} - C{H_2} - \mathop {\mathop C\limits_{||} }\limits_O - C{H_2} - C{H_3}$
 $C{H_3} - \mathop {\mathop C\limits_| H}\limits_{C{H_3}} - C{H_2} - \mathop {\mathop C\limits_{||} }\limits_O - H$
    (A) C and D
    (B) B and D
    (C) B and C   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A and B
    Answer: C
    Explanation: B and C are position isomers as they have the same number of C atoms and same functional group -C=O but the position of carbonyl group is C-2 in B and C-3 in C.

Q3. In Carius method, the organic compound is heated with
    (A) fuming nitric acid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) phosphoric acid
    (C) iodine pentoxide
    (D) conc. sulphuric acid
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In carius method of estimation of halogens, aknown mass of an organic compound is heated with fuming nitric acid in the presence of silver nitrate contained in a hard glass tube known as Carius tube, in a furnace.

Q4. Write the state of hybridisation of carbon in the compound, $HC \equiv N$ and shape of the molecule.
    (A) sp^3 hybridised carbon, trigonal planar
    (B) sp^3 hybridised carbon, tetrahedral
    (C) sp^3 hybridised carbon, trigonal pyramidal
    (D) sp hybridised carbon, linear   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As the C is bonded to N by a triple bond so it is sp hybridized andand the molecule is linear in shape.

Q5. In sulphur estimation, 0.157 g of an organic compound gave 0.4813 g of barium sulphate. What is the percentage of sulphur in the compound?
    (A) 24%
    (B) 42.10%   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 41.6%
    (D) 11%
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Molecular mass of BaSO_4 = 137 + 32 + 64 g = 233 g
233 g BaSO_4 contains 32 g S
0.4813 g BaSO_4 contains $\frac{{(32 \times 0.4813g)}}{{233\;S}}$
So % of S = $ \frac{{(32 \times 0.4813 \times 100)}}{{(233 \times 0.157)}}$
S = 42.10%

Q6. During estimation of nitrogen present in an organic compound by Kjeldahl’s method, the ammonia evolved from 0.5 g of the compound, neutralized 10 mL of 1 M H_2SO_4. Find out the percentage of nitrogen in the compound.
    (A) 46%
    (B) 42%
    (C) 56%   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 51%
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 1 M of 10 mL H_2SO_4= 1 M of 20 mL NH_3
1000 mL of 1 M ammonia contains 14 g nitrogen
20 mL of 1 M ammonia contains $\frac{{(14 \times 20g)}}{{1000}}$ nitrogen
% of nitrogen = $ \frac{{(14 \times 20 \times 100)}}{{1000 \times 0.5}}$ = 56.0%

Q7. Which of the following is the correct IUPAC name of the given compound?
    (A) 4, 4-Bis(methyl)-3-ethylheptane
    (B) 3-Ethyl-4, 4-dimethylheptane   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 5-Ethyl-4, 4-dimethylheptane
    (D) 4, 4-Dimethyl-3-ethylheptane
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In IUPAC name, functional groups are written in alphabetical order. Locant 3 is assigned to ethyl group and the two methyl groups are present on C-4. The longest C chain has 7 C atoms so the IUPAC name is 3-ethyl-4,4-dimethylheptane.

Q8. When inductive and electromeric effects operate in opposite directions, what happens?
    (A) the inductive effect predominates.
    (B) the electomeric effect predominates.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) resonance structures are formed.
    (D) inductive and electromeric effects operate with the same magnitude.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Electromeric Effect (E effect) is a temporary effect. The organic compounds having multiple bonds (a double or triple bond) show this effect in the presence of an attacking reagent only. It is defined as the complete transfer of a shared pair of $\pi$-electrons to one of the atoms joined by multiple bonds on the demand of an attacking reagent. Polarisation of $\sigma$-bond caused by the polarisation of adjacent $\sigma$-bond is referred to as the inductive effect. When inductive and electromeric effects operate in opposite directions then electromeric effect predominates.

Q9. What does the following diagram showing Lewis structures depict?
    (A) metamerism in nitromethane (CH_3NO_2)
    (B) resonance structures of nitromethane $\left( {{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{N}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}} \right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) electron displacement effects in nitromethane (CH_3NO_2)
    (D) inductive effect in nitromethane (CH_3NO_2)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: These are resonating structures of nitromethane. It is known that the two N-O bonds of nitromethane are of the same length (intermediate between a N-O single bond and a N=O double bond). The actual structure of nitromethane is, therefore, a resonance hybrid of the two canonical forms I and II.

Q10. Nucleophile is a species that should have:
    (A) electron deficiency
    (B) a pair of electrons to donate   <-- CORRECT
    (C) positive charge
    (D) capacity to accept electrons
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A nucleophile means a nucleus loving species. It can be a neutral molecule with a pair of electron to donate or it can be a negatively charged species.

Q11. In Carius method of estimation of halogen, 0.15 g of an organic compound gave 0.12 g of AgBr. Find out the percentage of bromine in the compound.
    (A) ${\text{41}}.{\text{5}}\% $
    (B) ${\text{41}}.{\text{06 }}\% $
    (C) ${\text{24 }}\% $
    (D) ${\text{34}}.0{\text{4}}\% $   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Molar mass of AgBr = 108 + 80 = 188 g/mol
188 g AgBr contains 80 g bromine
0.12 g AgBr contains (80 $\times$ 0.12)/188 g bromine
Percentage of bromine $ = \frac{{(80 \times 0.12 \times 100)}}{{(188 \times 0.15)}} = 34.04\% $

Q12. In Duma's method for estimation of nitrogen, 0.3 g of an organic compound gave 50 mL of nitrogen collected at 300K temperature and 715 mm pressure. The percentage composition of nitrogen in the compound (Aqueous tension at 300K = 15mm) is
    (A) 18.36%
    (B) 28%
    (C) 17.46%   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 15.46%
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Volume of nitrogen collected at 300 K and 715 mm Hg= 50 mL
Actual pressure = 715 - 15 = 700 mm Hg
Volume of nitrogen at STP = $\frac {(273 \times 700 \times 50)}{(300 \times 760)}$ = 41.9 mL
22400 ml of nitrogen at STP weighs 28g
So 41.9 ml of nitrogen at STP weighs = $\frac {(28 g \times 41.9mL)}{22400}$ mL
Percentage of N_2 = $\frac {(28 \times 41.9 \times 100)}{(22400\times0.3)}$=17.46%

Q13. On complete combustion, 0.246 g of an organic compound gave 0.198g of carbon dioxide and 0.1014g of water. Determine the percentage composition of carbon and hydrogen in the compound.
    (A) 11.95% and 3.65%
    (B) 34.04% and 4.58%
    (C) 31.95% and 4.58%
    (D) 21.95% and 4.58%   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Molar mass of carbondioxide=44 g/mol
Molar mass of C=12 g/mol
44 g CO_​​​​​2 contains 12 g C
0.198 g of CO_​​​​​2 contains (12 x 0.198 g)/44 C
% of C= (12x0.198x100)/(44x0.246)=21.95%
Molar mass of water=18 g/mol
18 g water contains 2 g H
0.1014 g water contains (2x0.1014 g)/18H
% of H= (2 x 0.1014 x 100)/(0.246 x 18)=4.58 %

Q14. One among the below options which is not detected by Lassaigne’s test?
    (A) Phosphorus
    (B) Sulphur
    (C) Nitrogen
    (D) Oxygen   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Nitrogen, sulphur, halogens and phosphorus present in an organic compound are detected by “Lassaigne’s test”. Oxygen cannot be detected by this test.

Q15. In the resonance structures of CH_2 = CH - CHO given below, indicate relative stability of these structures.
    (A) II> III > I
    (B) III > I > II
    (C) I > II> III   <-- CORRECT
    (D) III>II>I
    Answer: C
    Explanation: I > II> III . (III) is unstable as O which is an electronegative atom carries positive charge. (I) is stable because of more number of covalent bonds which means it is lowest in energy.

Q1. Which of these fuels given below is not a hydrocarbon?
 Hydrogen
 LNG
 LPG
 CNG
    (A) A   <-- CORRECT
    (B) B
    (C) D
    (D) C
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Because hydrocarbons contain both C and H and hence Hydrogen is not a hydrocarbon.

Q2. Saturated hydrocarbons contain
    (A) single bonds   <-- CORRECT
    (B) triple bonds
    (C) ionic bonds
    (D) double bonds
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Saturated hydrocarbons are the compounds in which there is a single bond between the carbon atoms. They are also called alkanes and have the general formula C_nH_2n+2.

Q3. In cycloalkanes carbon atoms form:
    (A) A an open chain
    (B) A closed chain or a ring   <-- CORRECT
    (C) A open coiled chain
    (D) A zigzag chain
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Cycloalkanes contain single bond between the carbon atoms, they form ring structures and have the general formula C_nH_2n.

Q4. Which of these is not a characteristic of Aromatic Hydrocarbons?
    (A) Carbon atoms form a closed chain or ring.
    (B) They are special type of cyclic compounds.
    (C) They may contain double bonds.
    (D) Carbon atoms form a an open chain.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Aromatic hydrocarbon is not an open chain. They are ring structures. they contain one or more benzene rings either fused or isolated in their molecules.

Q5. The number of chain isomers of C_5H_12 are:
    (A) 5
    (B) 2
    (C) 4
    (D) 3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The number of chain isomers of C_5H_12 are as follows:
 n-pentane CH_3CH_2CH_2CH_2CH_3
 2-Methylbutane CH_3CH(CH_3)CH_2CH_3
 2,2-Dimethylpropane CH_3CH(CH_3)_2CH_3

Q6. In the Wurtz reaction method of preparation of alkanes, the stoichiometric coefficient of Sodium is ________.
    (A) 3
    (B) 2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 5
    (D) 1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Wurtz reaction is used for the preparation of alkanes from alkyl halides in the presence of sodium and dry ether. For example:
CH_3Br + 2Na +BrCH_3 $\longrightarrow$ CH_3CH_3 + 2NaBr
Thus two atoms of Na are used.

Q7. The number of possible conformational isomers of ethane is ________.
    (A) zero
    (B) two
    (C) one
    (D) infinite   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Conformational isomers are obtained by rotation about a carbon-carbon single bond. This results in an infinite number of momentary arrangements of atoms in space. Hence for ethane infinite number of conformations are possible.

Q8. Boiling point of alkanes are:
    (A) is independent of molecular mass.
    (B) increases with increase in molecular mass.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) is independent of branching.
    (D) decreases with increase in molecular mass.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: As molecular mass increases, the magnitude of Van der Waals forces of attraction increases and hence boiling point increases accordingly.

Q9. Halogenation of alkanes is a:
    (A) Addition reaction
    (B) Elimination reaction
    (C) Rearrangement reaction
    (D) Substitution reaction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Halogenation of alkanes is a substitution reaction because the hydrogen atoms are replaced by halogens in the presence of sunlight to give the corresponding alkyl halides. The reaction follows a free radical mechanism.

Q10. The general formula for alkenes is:
    (A) C_nH_2n+1
    (B) C_nH_2n+3
    (C) C_nH_2n-1
    (D) C_nH_2n   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Alkenes are unsaturated hydrocarbons with at least on double bond between the carbon atoms. Their general formula is C_nH_2n.

Q11. Carbon-carbon double bond in alkenes consists of:
    (A) one strong sigma $\left( \sigma \right)$ bond due to head-on overlapping of sp^2 hybridised orbitals one weak pi $\left( \pi \right)$ bond.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) one weak sigma $\left( \sigma \right)$ bond due to head-on overlapping of sp^2 hybridised orbitals one weak pi $\left( \pi \right)$ bond.
    (C) one strong sigma $\left( \sigma \right)$ bond due to head-on overlapping of sp^3 hybridised orbitals one weak pi $\left( \pi \right)$ bond.
    (D) one weak sigma $\left( \sigma \right)$ bond due to head-on overlapping of ${\text{s}}{{\text{p}}^{\text{3}}}$ hybridised orbitals one weak pi $\left( \pi \right)$bond.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Sigma bond is formed by the head-on overlap of sp^2 hybridized orbitals while the pi bond is formed by lateral or sideways overlapping of the two 2p-orbitals of the two carbon atoms. Alkenes contain 1 weak pi bond and 1 strong sigma bond.

Q12. In the alkene having IUPAC name 3-Methyl-1-butene the double bond lies on carbon atom numbered ______.
    (A) 1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3
    (C) 4
    (D) 2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: ‘1’ is written before butene which indicates that the position of the double bond is on carbon 1. The structure of the compound is CH_2=CHCH(CH_3)CH_3.

Q13. Stereoisomeric alkenes due to the different arrangement of atoms or groups in space are referred to as:
    (A) Position isomers
    (B) Constitutional isomers
    (C) Geometric isomers   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Chain isomers
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Isomers which have the same structural formulae but differ in the relative spatial arrangements of atoms or groups around the double bond are called geometric isomers. Thus geometrical isomers are a type of stereoisomers.

Q14. One of the methods of preparing ethylene is given below.This is an example of _______ reaction
    (A) Addition reaction
    (B) Substitution reaction
    (C) Rearrangement reaction
    (D) Elimination reaction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Dehydration of alcohols in the presence of alc. KOH to form an alkene is an example of elimination reaction.

Q15. The boiling point of isomeric branched chain alkene is:
    (A) same boiling point as straight chain alkenes.
    (B) same boiling point as straight chain alkenes except for optical isomers.
    (C) higher boiling point than straight chain alkenes.
    (D) lower than the boiling point of straight chain alkene.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As the surface area decreases with branching, the boiling point also decreases.

Q1. The reaction given below is used to produce polythene. This is an example of _______ reaction
${\text{n(CH = C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{)}}\xrightarrow[{{\text{Catalyst}}}]{{{\text{High}}\,{\text{temp}}{\text{./pressure}}}}\mathop {{\text{ - (C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}\,{\text{ - }}\,{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{{\text{)}}_{\text{n}}}{{\text{ - }}_{}}}\limits_{{\text{Polythene}}} $
    (A) Addition reaction
    (B) Polymerization reaction   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Substitution reaction
    (D) Rearrangement reaction
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In polymerisation reaction many monomeric units combine to form a big macromolecule.

Q2. The number of position isomers of C_5H_8 is ________.
    (A) 5
    (B) 2
    (C) 3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The position isomers of C_5H_8 are n-pentyne, 3-methyl butyne, pent-2-yne.

Q3. Thus ethyne molecule consists of:
    (A) three C - C $\sigma$ bond, two C - H $\sigma$ bonds and three C - C $\pi$ bonds.
    (B) one C - C $\sigma$ bond, three C - H $\sigma$ bonds and two C - C $\pi$ bonds.
    (C) one C - C $\sigma$ bond, two C - H $\sigma$ bonds and three C - C $\pi$ bonds.
    (D) one C - C $\sigma$ bond, two C - H $\sigma$ bonds and two C - C $\pi$ bonds.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ethyne is an unsaturated compound which belongs to the alkyne family and has the formula C_2H_2. Thus it consists of one C–C $\sigma$ bond, two C–H $\sigma$ bonds, and two C–C $\pi$ bonds.

Q4. The preparation of alkynes from vicinal dihalides is an example of ______?
    (A) Elimination reaction   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Addition reaction
    (C) Substitution reaction
    (D) Rearrangement reaction
    Answer: A
    Explanation: An elimination reaction is a type of organic reaction in which two substituents are removed from a molecule in either one or two steps. When the starting dihalide is a vicinal dihalide, the alkyne is obtained by two successive elimination reactions. 
Example :
Vicinal dihalide,$( CH_2Br-CH_2Br)$ on treatment with$alcoholic KOH$ forms a monosubstituted alkene Vinyl bromide, $CH_2CHBr$ which when reacted with sodium amide, $NaNH_2$ forms ethyne (ie. an alkyne ). The steps of conversion are,

Q5. Majority of the reactions of alkynes are examples of:
    (A) Electrophilic addition   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Nucleophilic addition
    (C) Electrophilic substitution
    (D) Nucleophilic substitution
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Alkynes have two pi bonds, hence they are electron rich species. They attract electrophiles thereby undergoing electrophilic addition reactions.

Q6. When two hydrogen atoms in benzene are replaced by two similar or different monovalent atoms or groups, how many different position isomers are possible?
    (A) 6
    (B) 5
    (C) 3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The three isomers will be ortho(i.e.1,2- or 1,4-disubstituted), meta(i.e.1,3- or 1,5-disubstituted) and para (1,4-disubstituted).

Q7. The unusual behavior of benzene is explained by:
    (A) sp^3 hybridization
    (B) sp^2 hybridization
    (C) Kekule structure
    (D) Delocalized $\pi $ electron cloud   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Resonance stabilization explains the unusual stability of benzene. There is $\pi$ electron delocalization in the ring which enhances the stability of the molecule.

Q8. Aromatic compounds are charachterized by the presence of _____ $\pi $ electrons in the ring where n is an integer (n = 0, 1, 2, ...).
    (A) 4n
    (B) (4n - 2)
    (C) (4n + 2)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (4n + 1)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Huckel rule which explains the unusual stability of cyclic conjugated polyenes (i.e. aromatic compounds) over other cyclic unsaturated compounds that does not contain (4n + 2) pi electrons.

Q9. Which of the following method is not a synthetic method for the production of Benzene?
    (A) Cyclic polymerization of ethyne
    (B) Decarboxylation of aromatic acids
    (C) By reduction of phenol
    (D) Isolation from coal tar   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since the isolation of benzene from coal tar involves the separation of benzene from other components through a physical operation "fractional distillation", it is not a synthetic method for the production of benzene.

Q10. In Friedel-Crafts alkylation reaction, when benzene is treated with an alkyl halide in the presence of a catalyst, alkylbenzene is formed. The catalyst used is:
    (A) Silver
    (B) Palladium
    (C) Anhydrous aluminium chloride   <-- CORRECT
    (D) H_3PO_4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The acid chloride or anhydride reacts with anhydrous aluminium chloride to form the acylium ion which serves as an electrophile which then attacks the benzene ring to give alkylbenzene.

Q11. Some of the polynuclear hydrocarbons having fused benzene ring system have the property of being ________.
    (A) malleable
    (B) carcinogenic   <-- CORRECT
    (C) conductive
    (D) nonflammable
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Polynuclear hydrocarbons are carcinogenic, i.e. cancer producing.

Q12. Arrange the following in decreasing order of their boiling points.
 n-butane
 2-methylbutane
 n-pentane
 2, 2-dimethylpropane
    (A) B > C > D > A
    (B) C > B > D > A   <-- CORRECT
    (C) D > C > B > A
    (D) A > B > C > D
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The boiling point depends on the molecular mass and surface area. As the number of carbon atoms increases, the boiling point increases, hence n-butane has the minimum boiling point. Among isomeric alkanes, the boiling point decreases with branching. Hence the order.

Q13. Arrange the halogens F_2, Cl_2, Br_2, I_2, in order of their increasing reactivity with alkanes.
    (A) F_2 < Cl_2 < Br_2 < I_2
    (B) Br_2 < Cl_2 < F_2 < I_2
    (C) Br_2 < I_2 < Cl_2 < F_2
    (D) I_2 < Br_2 < Cl_2 < F_2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The reaction follows a free radical mechanism in which the first step is the generation of halogen-free radical which is the fastest for fluorine. Hence the order.

Q14. The increasing order of reduction of alkyl halides with zinc and dilute HCl is
    (A) R–I < R–Br < R–Cl
    (B) R–Br < R–I < R–Cl
    (C) R–Cl < R–Br < R–I   <-- CORRECT
    (D) R–Cl < R–I < R–Br
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As we move from I to Br to Cl,atomic size decreases,it becomes difficult to release the halogen as the bond length decreases.Hence I^- is the best leaving group among halogens and reacts the fastest.

Q15. The correct IUPAC name of the following alkane is:
    (A) 3 - Isopropyl - 6 - ethyloctane
    (B) 3 - Ethyl - 5 - isopropyloctane
    (C) 5 - Isopropyl - 3 - ethyloctane
    (D) 3,6 - Diethyl - 2 - methyloctane   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Following the rules of nomenclature, the IUPAC name of the given compound is 3, 6-Diethyl-2-methyloctane.

Q1. The addition of HBr to 1-butene gives a mixture of products A, B, and C.
 CH_3- CH_2- CH_2- CH_2- Br
The mixture consists of:
    (A) A and B as minor and C as major products
    (B) B as major, A and C as minor products
    (C) B as minor, A and C as major products
    (D) A and B as major and C as minor products   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A and B both involve secondary carbocation but C involves primary carbocation and secondary carbocation is more stable than primary carbocation. Therefore A and B are the major product.

Q2. Which of the following will not show geometrical isomerism?
    (A)    <-- CORRECT
    (B) 
    (C) 
    (D) 
    Answer: A
    Explanation: This is because geometrical isomerism is not possible if three groups are same.

Q3. Arrange the following hydrogen halides in order of their decreasing reactivity with propene.
    (A) HBr > HI > HCl
    (B) HCl > HI > HBr
    (C) HCl > HBr > HI
    (D) HI > HBr > HCl   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As we move from Cl to I,the atomic size increases,bond length increases,bond strength decreases,hence it becomes easier to release halogen and hence the order.I^- is the a better leaving group.

Q4. Arrange the following carbanions in order of their decreasing stability.
 H_3C - C $ \equiv $C^-
 H - C ≡ C^- 
 H_3C - ${\rm{C}}{\mathop {\rm{H}}\limits^ - {_2}}$
    (A) A > B > C
    (B) C > B > A
    (C) B > A > C   <-- CORRECT
    (D) C > A > B
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In B, the '-' charge is on sp hybridized C atom so the negative charge is stabilised. In A, there is an alkyl group attached to sp hybridised carbon which destabilizes the negative charge. In C, the '-' charge is on a sp^3 hybridised carbon and is hence the least stable.

Q5. Arrange the following alkyl halides in decreasing order of the rate of $\beta$ - elimination reaction with alcoholic KOH
 $ {\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{ - }}\mathop {\mathop {\text{C}}\limits_{\mathop {\text{|}}\limits_{{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}} }^{\text{|}} }\limits^{\text{H}} {\text{ - C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{Br}}$
 CH_3-CH_2-Br
 CH_3-CH_2-CH_2-Br
    (A) A > B > C
    (B) B > C > A
    (C) A > C > B   <-- CORRECT
    (D) C > B > A
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A more substituted alkene is preferred in accordance with the Saytzeff's rule. Hence the order.

Q6. Which of the following reactions of methane represents its incomplete combustion?
    (A) 2CH_4(g) + O_2(g) $\to$ 2CO(g) + 4H_2(g)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) CH_4 + 2O_2 $\to$ CO_2(g) + 2H_2O(l)
    (C) $\text{2C}{{\text{H}}_{\text{4}}}+\text{ }{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}\xrightarrow{Cu,523K,100atm}\text{2C}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}\text{OH}$
    (D) $\text{C}{{\text{H}}_{\text{4}}}+\text{ }{{\text{O}}_{\text{2}}}\xrightarrow{M{{o}_{2}}{{O}_{3}}}\text{HCHO }+\text{ }{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}\text{O}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: CH_4 on complete combustion gets completely oxidized to form (CO_2 + H_2O), as per the following equation;
$CH_4 + 2O_2\to CO_2 +2H_2O$
The given reaction,
$2CH_4 + O_2\to2CO + 4H_2$
$or, CH_4 + \frac{1}{2} O_2\to CO + 2H_2$
represents incomplete combustion, because stoichiometrically,
 for complete combustion 2 moles of O_2 per mole of CH_4 is required, while the only $\frac{1}{2}$mole of O_2 per mole of CH_4 is taken to carry out its complete oxidation or combustion.
 O_2(g)is the limiting reagent for the reaction.
Thus, one mole of methane is burnt in a limited supply of oxygen, resulting in the formation of one mole of CO(g).
 ​​​CO(g)could have been further oxidized to form CO_2(g) as the final product of combustion.
 $CO(g) + \frac{1}{2} O_2(g)\to CO_2(g)$
 Hence, the given equation represents incomplete combustion of methane.

Q7. Among the following compounds one that is most reactive towards electrophilic nitration is:
    (A) Toluene   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Nitrobenzene
    (C) Benzoic Acid
    (D) Benzene
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Presence of electron releasing group like -R, -OH etc. increases the electron density at ortho and para position and thus makes the benzene ring more reactive towards electrophile. On the other hand, electron withdrawing groups like -COOH, -NO_2 etc. reduces electron density and thus reduces the reactivity of benzene towards electrophile. Thus, order of the given compounds towards electrophilic nitration is:

Q8. Which branched chain isomer of the hydrocarbon with molecular mass 72u gives only one isomer of monosubstituted alkyl halide?
    (A) Tertiary butyl chloride
    (B) Neohexane
    (C) Neopentane   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Isohexane
    Answer: C
    Explanation: (CH_3)_3CCH_3 + HX(X=Cl,Br,I) $\to$ (CH_3)_3CCH_2X
Hence a monosubstituted derivative is formed.

Q9. Ethylbenzene cannot be prepared by ______.
    (A) Clemmensen reduction
    (B) Wurtz-Fittig reaction
    (C) Friedel-Crafts reaction
    (D) Wurtz reaction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Wurtz reaction is used to prepare alkanes with an even number of carbon atoms. To prepare ethylbenzene, the Wurtz Fittig reaction has to be used.

Q10. Identify B and D in the following sequence of reactions.
    (A) Methanol, and Bromoethane
    (B) Ethyl - hydrogensulphate + aqueous KOH
    (C) Ethyl - hydrogensulphate + alcoholic KOH
    (D) Ethanol and alcoholic KOH   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The given sequence of reactions conform to following stepwise conversions:
Step (1)$ \ C_2H_5OH \overset{conc.H_2SO_4}{\underset{110^oC}\longrightarrow} \ C_2H_5HSO_4 $
Step (2)$\ C_2H_5HSO_4 \ + \ H_2O \to \ CH_3CH_2OH \ + \ H_2SO_4$
Step (3) $ C_2H_5OH \overset{PBr_3} \longrightarrow{CH_3CH_2Br}$
Step (4) $\ CH_3CH_2Br \overset{alc.KOH}{\underset{heat}\longrightarrow} \ H_2C=CH_2 + HBr$
Thus, the above sequence of reaction shows that the product 'B ' is C_2H_5OH ( i.e. ethanol ) and D is a reactant alcoholic KOH.

Q11. Ozonolysis of an organic compound 'A' produces an equimolar mixture of acetone and propionaldehyde.

    (A) 2 - Pentene
    (B) 2 - Methyl - 2 - pentene   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1 - Pentene
    (D) 2 - Methyl - 1 - pentene
    Answer: B
    Explanation: 2- Methyl -2 - pentene, when treated with ozone, forms an unstable ozonide intermediate. The ozonide when treated with$( zinc -{dust} + H_2O )$) yields an aldehyde (propionaldehyde ) and a ketone ( acetone ) as the final products The conversion reactions are represented as below.
Thus, the compound A is (2-Methyl -2 -pentene )

the bond lengths of (carbon-carbon) bond are 139 pm, which is intermediate between carbon-carbon single and carbon-carbon double bond

Q1. The synthesis of 3-octyne is achieved by subsequent stepwise reactions of sodium amide with an alkyne, and a bromoalkane. The bromoalkane and the other alkyne respectively are:
    (A) BrCH_2CH_2CH_3 and ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C }} \equiv {\text{ CH}}$
    (B) BrCH_2CH_2CH_2CH_3 and ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C }} \equiv {\text{ CH}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) BrCH_2CH_2CH_2CH_2CH_3 and ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C }} \equiv {\text{ CH}}$
    (D) BrCH_2CH_2CH_2CH_2CH_3 and ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C }} \equiv {\text{ CH}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: 3 - Octyne can be synthesized as per the following stepwise conversion reactions:
Step 1. Formation of a Sodium alkynide, by the reaction of 1 -butyne with sodium amide
$CH_3CH_2C\equiv CH +NaNH_2 \rightarrow CH_3CH_2C\equiv C Na^+ +NH_3$
1-butyne sodium amide sodium butynide
Step 2. Reaction of the alkynide ( sodium butynide) with 1 - bromobutane
$CH_3 CH_2 C \equiv C Na^+ + CH_3 CH_2 CH_2CH_2 Br $$\rightarrow$ $CH_3CH_2C \equiv CCH_2CH_2CH_2CH_3$$+ NaBr$
Sodium Butynide 1-bromobutane 3 - Octyne

Q4. The bond angle deviation in cyclobutane is ________.
    (A) 19.5^o   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 19^o
    (C) 29.16^o
    (D) 24.44^o
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The ideal bond angle in tetrahedral carbon is 109.5^o. In cyclobutane, the interior carbon to carbon bond angles is considerably less. This results in repulsions between the electron clouds causing instability of the molecule.
The deviation in bond angle in cyclobutane is calculated as -
The bond angle in cyclobutane is = 90^o
The normal tetrahedral bond angle
= 109.5^o
$\therefore$ Deviation = (normal tetrahedral bond angle - actual normal bond angle)
= (109.5^o - 90^o)
= 19.5^o
Hence, the bond angle deviation for cyclobutane is 19.5^o.

Q5. In the following sequence of reactions, the alkene is converted to compound $B$ 
${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{CH }} = {\text{ CHC}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}\mathop \to \limits^{{O_3}} {\text{A}}\mathop \to \limits^{{H_2}O,Zn} B$ 
The compound $B$--------- is?
    (A) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{COC}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$
    (B) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{CHO}}$
    (C) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{CHO}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{COC}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The given sequence of conversion steps represent Ozonolysis of 2-Butene, which follows the following path,
 Formation of an unstable intermediate/ozonide$(A)$ 
 Cleavage of the intermediate/ozonide by $(Zn+H_2O)$ to smaller molecules, giving out the compound$B$, which is CH_3 CHO ( Ethanal )
The reaction is well depicted as below,
,

Q6. The hydrocarbon which can react with sodium in liquid ammonia is________.
    (A) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}} \equiv {\text{CC}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$
    (B) CH_3CH=CHCH_3
    (C) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}} \equiv {\text{CC}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}$
    (D) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}}{\text{C}} \equiv {\text{CH}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Terminal alkynes react with Na in the presence of liquid NH_3 to form higher alkynes. The alkyne contains acidic H at the end (i.e. the H bonded to C_1 of the chain). Therefore, it is easily replaced with highly electropositive metals such as Na in liquid ammonia, to form sodium alkaline ion which can react further in the presence of a suitable catalyst to yield higher alkynes/hydrocarbons.

Q7. The treatment of CH_3MgX with CH_3C $\equiv $ C - H gives ________.
    (A) CH_3 - CH = CH_2
    (B) CH_4   <-- CORRECT
    (C) H_3C-CH_3
    (D) CH_3C $\equiv$ C - CH_3
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Terminal alkynes act as a nucleophile. The organometallic compound 'Grignard's reagent (R -Mg-X), therefore, reacts to form alkane. Thus when CH_3-Mg-Br is treated with CH_3C $\equiv$ CH we get CH_4 as per the following equation:
CH_3C $\equiv$ CH - Mg - Br $\rightarrow$ CH_3C $\equiv$ C-Mg -Br + CH_4

Q8. Benzene reacts with chlorine in the presence of sunlight and in the absence of halogen carriers to give .............?
    (A) ${{\text{C}}_{\text{6}}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{5}}}{\text{Cl}}$
    (B) ${\text{CC}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{4}}}$
    (C) $C_6H_6Cl_6$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${{\text{C}}_{\text{6}}}{\text{C}}{{\text{l}}_{\text{6}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Benzene, in the presence of sunlight and in absence of halogen carriers,
undergoes an addition reaction with Cl_2 to form benzene hexachloride,$C_6H_6Cl_6$

Q9. The general formula of a cycloalkane with one benzene ring is ________.
    (A) C_nH_2n   <-- CORRECT
    (B) C_nH_2n-2
    (C) C_nH_2n+2
    (D) C_nH_n
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Cycloalkane with one benzene ring has a formula C_6H_12.
$\therefore$ The formula becomes C_nH_2n

Q10. Cyclohexene on ozonolysis followed by reaction with zinc dust and water gives compound E. Compound E on further treatment with aqueous KOH yields compound F. Compound F is
    (A) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (B)
    (C) (D)
    (D) (C)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The following stepwise conversions reactions occuring separately in each step explain the formation of compound at option (A) ,
Step1. Treatment of cyclo hexene with ozone O_3 _ forms of an unstable intermediate "ozonide".
Step 2. Cleavage of the ozonide by (Zn + H_2O) to form compound E [ ie. Pentan 1, 5-dicarbaldehyde, (OHC - CH_2. CH_2. CH_2 - CHO) ]
Step 3 The compound E (ie. CHO - CH_2. CH_2. CH_2 - CHO) when treated with (aqueous KOH) suffers 'aldol condensation' to yield compound F as the final product.

Q11. The reagent(s) for the following conversion, is/are
    (A) alcoholic KOH followed NaNH_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) alcoholic KOH
    (C) aqueous KOH followed by NaNH_2
    (D) ZN/CH_3OH
    Answer: A
    Explanation: This is an example of elimination reaction in two steps ,
In the first step alc. KOH is used as a base forming vinyl bromide (CH_2 = CHBr) and in the second step,a stronger base NaNH_2 (sodium -amide) is used.
The stepwise conversions reactions are,
$BrC{H_2}C{H_2}Br\xrightarrow[{alc.KOH}]{}C{H_2}CHBr\xrightarrow[{NaN{H_2}}]{}C_ 2H_2$
$\mathop {BrC{H_2}C{H_2}Br}\limits_{(1,\;2 - dibromoethane)} \xrightarrow[{alc.KOH}]{}\mathop {C{H_2}CHBr}\limits_{(Vinylbromide)} \xrightarrow[{NaN{H_2}}]{}\mathop {C_2H_2}\limits_{(Ethyne)} $

Q12. Presence of a nitro group in a benzene ring:
    (A) renders the ring basic.
    (B) deactivates the ring towards nucleophilic substitution.
    (C) deactivates the ring towards electrophilic substitution.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) activates the ring towards electrophilic substitution.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: This is because the Nitro is an electron-withdrawing group, it pulls the electron density from the ring towards itself thereby decreasing the electron density in the ring and deactivating the ring towards attack by the electrophile.

Q13. The compound formed as a result of oxidation of ethyl benzene by ${\text{KMn}}{{\text{O}}_{\text{4}}}$ is
    (A) benzoic acid   <-- CORRECT
    (B) benzophenone
    (C) benzyl alcohol
    (D) acetophenone
    Answer: A
    Explanation: All alkylbenzenes (such as C_6H_5CH_3 or C_6H_5C_2H_5) on oxidation with alkaline - KMnO_4
Therefore, the oxidation of ethylbenzene with alkaline KMnO_4 yields" Benzoic - acid.

Q14. Which of the following reactions will yield 2, 2-dibromopropane?
    (A) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} - {\text{ CH }} = {\text{ C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{2}}} + {\text{ HBr }} \to $
    (B) ${\text{CH }} \equiv {\text{ CH }} + {\text{ 2HBr}} \to $
    (C) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}}{\text{CH }} \equiv {\text{ CHBr }} + {\text{ HBr}} \to $
    (D) ${\text{C}}{{\text{H}}_{\text{3}}} - {\text{ C }} \equiv {\text{ CH }} + {\text{ 2HBr }} \to $   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The reaction follows Markovnikoff’s rule of addition which states that in addition of HBr to an unsymmetrical alkene, the major product is the one in which the Br gets attached to the more substituted carbon of the double bond.

Q15. HBr reacts with CH_2 = CH-OCH_3 under anhydrous conditions at room temperature to give _________.
    (A) BrCH_2CHO and CH_3OH
    (B) H_3C-CHBr-OCH_3   <-- CORRECT
    (C) BrCH_2-CH_2-OCH_3
    (D) CH_3CHO and CH_3Br
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The product is formed through a reaction in accordance with Markovnikov’s rule (i.e. the negative part of the adding reagent goes to that carbon of the double bond which is more highly substituted).
The reaction is better understood to occur in the following two steps,
Step (1) generation of a carbocation, CH_3-C^+H-OCH_3 as per Markovnikov's rule.
Step (2) attack of the bromide ion (Br^-) over the carbocation to yield the product.
CH_3-CHBr-OCH_3.

Q1. Phenyl magnesium bromide reacts with methanol to give:
    (A) a mixture of toluene and Mg(OH)Br.
    (B) a mixture of phenol and Mg(Me)Br.
    (C) a mixture of benzene and Mg(OMe)Br.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a mixture of anisole and Mg(OH)Br.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: This is because Grignard reagents react with proton from methanol to give benzene and Mg(OMe)Br.

Q2. A gas decolourised by KMnO_4 solution but gives no precipitate with ammoniacal cuprous chloride is ________.
    (A) Ethene   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ethane
    (C) Acetylene
    (D) Methane
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Due to unsaturation, ethene decolourises KMnO_4 solution forming glycol. However, it shows no reaction with ammoniacal cupric chloride.

Q3. What would be the product formed when 1-Bromo-3-chlorocyclobutane reacts with two equivalents of metallic sodium in ether?
    (A) (A)
    (B) (C)
    (C) (B)
    (D) (D)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: This is because an intramolecular reaction takes Wurtz reaction takes place with the release of a molecule of NaCl and a molecule of NaBr.

Q4. 2-methylbutane on reacting with bromine in the presence of sunlight gives mainly ________.
    (A) 2-bromo 2-methylbutane   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1-bromo 2-methylbutane
    (C) 1-bromo 3-methylbutane
    (D) 2-bromo 3-methylbutane
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The halogenation of alkanes follows free radical mechanism with the formation of free radical intermediates. As the secondary free radical is more stable than primary free radical, hence the product is 2-bromo-2-methylbutane.

Q5. Alkyl halides react with dialkyl copper reagents to give:
    (A) Alkyl copper halides
    (B) Alkenyl halides
    (C) Alkenes
    (D) Alkanes   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Alkyl halides react with dialkyl copper reagents to give alkanes. This is Corey-House reaction and gives good yields of both symmetrical and unsymmetrical alkanes.

Q6. n-Propylbromide on treatment with ethanolic KOH is:
    (A) Propyne
    (B) Propanal
    (C) Propane
    (D) Propene   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Elimination reaction takes place, a molecule of HBr gets eliminated to form propene.

Q7. Acetylene is prepared by the action of water on:
    (A) Al_4C_3
    (B) Silicon carbide
    (C) all of these
    (D) CaC_2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The reaction of CaC_2 (Calcium carbide) with water produces acetylene (C_2H_2).
The chemical equation for the reaction of calcium\ carbide (CaC_2) with water to yield acetylene ($HC \equiv CH$) is
$CaC_2 + H_2O \to CaO + C_2H_2$
The calcium oxide (CaO) is formed as a byproduct, which simultaneously reacts with water to give Ca(OH)_2
$CaO + H_2O\to Ca(OH)_2$
Thus, the overall reaction is,
$CaC_2 \ + \ 2H_2O \to C_2H_2 \ + \ Ca(OH)_2 $

Q8. What product is obtained on electrolyzing potassium fumarate?
    (A) CH_4
    (B) C_2H_4
    (C) C_2H_2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) C_2H_6
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Acetylene can be prepared by electrolysis of a concentrated solution of sodium or potassium salt of fumaric acid. This is Kolbe's electrolytic method.

Q9. What product is obtained by heating ethylidene chloride with alcoholic KOH?
    (A) Ethyne   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Ethene
    (C) Ethane
    (D) Methane
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Ethylidene chloride is 1,1 - dichloroethane having the structural formula,
Ethylidene chloride, when treated with alcoholic KOH forms ethyne.
The reaction takes place in two steps giving vinyl chloride in the first step, which further undergoes an elimination reaction to form ethyne. as shown below,
$\mathop {C{H_3}CHC{l_2}}\limits_{(Ethylidene\;chloride)} \xrightarrow[{alcoholicKOH}]{}\mathop {C{H_2} = CHCl}\limits_{(VinylChloride)} \xrightarrow[{KOH(alc.)}]{}\mathop {HC = CH}\limits_{(Ethyne)} $

Q10. Which product is obtained by passing ethanol vapours over heated alumina?
    (A) CH_4
    (B) C_2H_6
    (C) C_2H_2
    (D) C_2H_4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: It is an example of dehydration of alcohols to give alkenes.
$RC{H_2} - \mathop {C{H_2}OH}\limits_{alcohol} \xrightarrow[{ - {H_2}O}]{{A{l_2}{O_3},623K}}\mathop {RCH = C{H_2}}\limits_{alkene} $
For example,
$\mathop {{C_2}{H_5}OH}\limits_{ethanol} \xrightarrow[{ - {H_2}O}]{{A{l_2}{O_3},623K}}\mathop {C{H_2} = C{H_2}}\limits_{ethene} $
Thus, when ethanol vapours are passed over heated alumina, the alcohol gets dehydrated to form ethene, as given above.

Q11. Ethene is obtained by electrolyzing:
    (A) All of these
    (B) Pot. Acetate
    (C) Pot. Succinate   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Pot. Fumarate
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Ethene is obtained by the electrolysis of potassium succinate by the Kolbe's electrolytic method.

Q12. Pyrolysis of coal with heavy oil in the presence of H_2 at 250 atm.and 350^0C and catalyst yields.
    (A) CH_4
    (B) C_2H_6
    (C) A mixture of low boiling hydrocarbons.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) C_3H_8
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Pyrolysis is the decomposition of a compound by the application of heat. It involves the breaking of C-C and C-H bonds resulting in the formation of lower boiling alkanes.

Q13. What does Marsh gas mainly contains?
    (A) C_2H_2
    (B) CO
    (C) H_2S
    (D) CH_4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Marsh gas which is also called methane is produced by the anaerobic bacterial decomposition of vegetable matter and the rumen of herbivorous animals underwater.

Q14. Organic compounds are found in:
    (A) both animal and vegetable kingdom   <-- CORRECT
    (B) only Animal kingdom
    (C) only vegetable kingdom
    (D) only mineral kingdom
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Compounds which are isolated directly or indirectly from living organisms like plants and animals are called organic compounds.

Q15. The organic compound can be formed by:
    (A) Plants, animals, and synthetic methods   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Plants only
    (C) Animals only
    (D) Plants and animals both
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Berzelius, a Swedish chemist proposed a theory termed as" Vital force theory ", during the 16th century. According to the theory it was considered that organic compounds are formed by living bodies such as plants and animals. The theory thus differentiated between organic compounds and the inorganic compounds. Around the year 1780attempts were made to synthesize or form organic compounds artificially by several chemists. However, this notion was rejected in 1828 when F . Wohler synthesized an organic compound, urea, from an inorganic compound ammonium cyanate.
${NH_4CNO} \overset{\Delta} \longrightarrow {H_2N.CO.NH_2}$
Since then many organic compounds could be formed by synthetic methods also.
